# Maamarim Melukatim

## Part 4

## B’s”D. Shabbos Parshas Korach, 3 Tammuz 5718

**1.** "He has set our soul in life and has not allowed our foot to slip." As my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains in his maamar titled *Zeh* for the Festival of Redemption, 12 Tammuz (the redemption actually began on 3 Tammuz), the "life" in which He has set our soul is a life that is loftier than the life of the *nefesh* (in and of itself). For the life of the *nefesh* is limited. Even though the *nefesh* is "alive in essence" (a level that transcends the diffusion of vitality that animates the body—not only the specific vitality, but even the general vitality), nevertheless, since this state of being "alive in essence" is because Hashem imprinted this nature upon the *nefesh*, this vitality too (of the level of "alive in essence") is subject to limitation. The life in which He has set our soul, however, is above nature. This is the meaning of "He has set our soul in life and has not allowed our foot to slip"—the power to ensure that our foot does not slip comes specifically from this life that is above nature.

**2.** To understand why, from the perspective of the life of the *nefesh* itself—even from the perspective of the level of "alive in essence"—it is possible for our foot to slip, and why the power to prevent this slipping comes specifically from the life that is above nature, and furthermore to understand the connection of this matter to the redemption of 12 Tammuz, we must first introduce what is written at the beginning of our Parsha: "And Korach took," which Onkelos translates as *va’yitpaleg* (and he separated/divided) Korach. Everywhere else "took" is translated as *nasiv*, but here it is translated as *va’yitpaleg*. It is stated in the *Noam Elimelech* that *va’yitpaleg* (Korach) is analogous to the firmament (*rakia*) that divides between water and water. The Tzemach Tzedek explains that this interpretation (that *va’yitpaleg* Korach is analogous to the dividing firmament) is based on the *Zohar*, which states that the dividing firmament was a dispute of the left against the right, etc., similar to the dispute of Korach against Aharon. From this it is understood that the connection of *va’yitpaleg* Korach to the dividing firmament is not only because the root of dispute (any dispute whatsoever) is from the dividing firmament, as it is stated in the Midrash: "Why is it not written on the second day 'that it is good'? Because on it, dispute was created, as it is written, 'and let it divide between water and water,'" but rather that this specific dispute—the dispute of Korach against Aharon—is a likeness of (and has its root in) the dispute of the dividing firmament. Just as the dispute of the dividing firmament is a dispute of the left against the right, so too is the dispute of Korach against Aharon; for Aharon is in the line of *Chesed* (right), and Korach, who was a Levi, was of the aspect of *Gevuros* (left).

It should be added that these two aspects of *va’yitpaleg* Korach (dispute, and the fact that he disputed Aharon) are related. The creation of dispute (the dividing firmament) occurred specifically on the second day because the first day is the attribute of *Chesed* (right) and the second day is the attribute of *Gevurah* (left), and from the side of *Gevurah*, there is room for dispute. As the *Zohar* states there: "The right is the perfection of all... in it hangs all perfection; when the left is aroused, dispute is aroused." Based on this, it can be said that the essence of Korach is dispute [as is also understood from the statement of our Sages that "anyone who holds onto dispute violates a negative commandment," as it is written, "and he shall not be like Korach and his congregation." From the fact that one who holds onto dispute (any dispute) is like Korach and his congregation, it is proven that the essence of Korach is dispute], and the fact that he disputed Aharon (*Chesed*) and wanted to make the *Gevuros* the primary element was in order to strengthen the dispute. We must understand: Korach was a clever man, and it is logical to say that his dispute regarding Aharon’s priesthood was because he erred in the ways of *avodah*. It is not understood why he wanted dispute. His disputing Aharon can be explained by the fact that Korach believed that the *avodah* of Hashem should be in the line of *Gevurah*, and therefore he disputed Aharon, whose *avodah* was in the line of *Chesed*. But according to the above—that Korach wanted to make the *Gevuros* the primary element in order to strengthen the dispute—it is not understood how Korach thought that dispute was a path in the *avodah* of Hashem. Also, it requires understanding why the translation is *va’yitpaleg* Korach, for *va’yitpaleg* is analogous to the dividing firmament, and seemingly, the very name of Korach hints at the dividing firmament, as the Tzemach Tzedek writes on the verse "And Korach took," that Korach hints at the dividing firmament, as it is written, "a firmament like the ice (*kerach*)." What is the addition of *va’yitpaleg* Korach?

**3.** This will be understood by introducing the well-known concept regarding the firmament that divides between water and water: water is *taanug*, for the fact that water causes all types of pleasure to grow is because the element of *taanug* is within it. The firmament that divides between the upper waters and the lower waters is the *parsah* (partition) through which the separation is made between the pleasures in spiritual matters (upper waters) and the pleasures of this world (lower waters). The intention of the firmament dividing between the upper and lower waters is so that through this, the lower waters will be elevated higher than they were before their descent. Through their descent below, a longing and thirst is created in them to ascend above—"the lower waters weep, 'we want to be before the King'"—and through this, they are elevated higher than they were before their descent, and even higher than the upper waters. This is what our Sages meant when they said that the fact that "it is good" is said twice on the third day is one for the work of the water and one for the work of the day. Seemingly, the work of the water is a matter of dispute, so how can it be called "good"? The explanation is that through the *avodah* of man, the clarification and elevation of the lower waters is accomplished. Therefore, on the third day, when "the waters under the heavens gathered to one place and the dry land appeared"—and dry land is the place of man—the intention of the work of the water was completed: that through the separation of the lower waters from the upper waters and their descent below, they are elevated higher than they were before their descent. Then (after the possibility for this elevation is created), the work of the water is also "good."

**4.** Based on this, it can be understood why Korach wanted dispute. Korach thought that the intention in the fact that the lower waters were separated from the upper waters and descended below was for the sake of the superiority that exists in the physical pleasures themselves, for the root of physicality is higher than the root of spirituality. [Similar to what is explained in *Torah Or* that in the upper worlds it is said, "How great are Your works," while the matter of "How many are Your works" is specifically in the lower worlds, and the concept of "many" indicates the perfection of *Ein Sof*, that while He is One, He also sustains a multitude of details.] Therefore, he wanted the *Gevuros* to be the primary element, because the fact that the lower waters weep, "we want to be before the King," is because the superiority of the aspect of revelations (*Chesed*, right) is felt in them. Since revelations are primarily in the upper worlds, the lower waters (in which there are no revelations) want to exit their existence and ascend above. But according to Korach’s error, that the intention is in the physical pleasures themselves, that the root of physicality should be revealed within them, then on the contrary, the primary superiority is in the *tzimtzumim* and *Gevuros* from which physical things are formed. But Korach erred in this, for the revelation of the root of the lower waters (physicality) themselves will be in the time to come. In order for there to be a revelation of the root of the lower waters themselves, there must first be in them the feeling of the superiority of the revelations, for through this feeling, they have the thirst and longing to ascend above, and through this, there will be a revelation of the root of the lower waters themselves. This is why "it is good" was not said regarding the work of the water until the third day, even though there is a superiority in the work of the water as it was on the second day, in that the lower waters were *separated* from the upper waters and *descended below*, because the revelation of this superiority will only be in the time to come. Now, the intention in the descent of the waters below is so that they will ascend above (as mentioned), and this matter is accomplished specifically on the third day. Similarly, this applies to the general concept of revelation (root of *Chesed*) and *tzimtzum* (root of *Gevurah*): the superiority that is in the *tzimtzum* itself will be revealed only in the time to come, and the intention in the *tzimtzum* as it is now is for the sake of the revelation.

**5.** Similarly, this applies to the *avodah* of man. Even though there is an advantage in the *avodah* of "in all your ways know Him" over the *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos*—in that through the *avodah* of "in all your ways know Him," the knowledge of *Elokus* is also within the matters of the world ("in all your ways")—nevertheless, in order for his engagement in optional matters ("your ways") to be in a manner where the matters of the world do not cause him a descent, G-d forbid, and on the contrary, in them themselves he sees Divine Providence ("know Him"), this is through the *avodah* of "let all your deeds be for the sake of Heaven." His intention in this is that he engages in optional matters so that through this he can engage in Torah and *mitzvos* [and since all his engagement in the matters of the world is for the sake of fulfilling Torah and *mitzvos*, he therefore minimizes them as much as possible and engages in them only as much as is necessary]. Then, even when he engages in the matters of the world, he sees in them a revelation of *Elokus*—"know Him."

**6.** According to the above, the precision of the language of our Sages—that "one should not *hold onto* dispute"—is also understood. *Holding onto* is precise, for the existence of the dispute itself—the fact that the lower waters were separated from the upper waters—is a creation created by Hashem. Korach’s sin was that he *held onto* the dispute, for he wanted the separation to persist (that the lower waters should remain below and not have the thirst to ascend above). It should be added that just as the intention in the creation of the dispute (the dividing firmament) on the second day is so that it will be clarified on the third day, at which time even the dividing firmament becomes "good," so too is it regarding the dispute of Korach: the intention in this (as it was from Above) was so that through this there would be peace in a manner loftier than it was before the dispute. As explained in the *drushim*, the fact that initially Moshe spoke to Korach and his congregation and tried to win them over with words of peace is because Moshe thought that just as the third day (*Tiferes*) clarified the partition and separation that was made on the second day, so too would it be regarding Korach, that Moshe [who was the third, *Tiferes*] would clarify him. [However, it was not so, because Korach did not want this, and his desire was to *hold onto* the dispute.]

Based on this, we can explain what the Targum adds: that "And Korach took" is *va’yitpaleg* Korach, analogous to the dividing firmament, even though Korach’s own name hints (as mentioned) at the dividing firmament ("a firmament like the ice"). For Korach’s name (from the word *kerachah*, whose meaning is division) points to his nature (that he was inclined toward dispute), which was created by Hashem. *Va’yitpaleg* Korach, however, is the act of dispute that he performed by his own will and choice. This is what the Targum Onkelos innovates: that "And Korach took" is *va’yitpaleg* Korach, analogous to the dividing firmament, meaning that even the *act* of Korach’s dispute, although it was by his own will and choice, is analogous to the dividing firmament created by Hashem. Just as the intention in the creation of the dividing firmament is so that it will be clarified on the third day, so too is it with *va’yitpaleg* Korach: the intention in this (from Above) is so that it will be clarified through Moshe, as mentioned.

**7.** It can be said that the reason Korach erred and thought that the intention in the dividing firmament was the separation itself is because the element of *bitul* was not within him. The matter is that what was explained above (section 3)—that the intention in the fact that the lower waters were separated from the upper waters and descended below is so that they would have the longing and thirst to ascend above—is a connection and inclusion of two opposite attributes. For from the side of *Chasadim* (the superiority of revelations), the superiority is in the upper waters, and there would be no need for the lower waters to be separated from the upper waters and descend below. And from the side of *Gevuros*, the superiority is in the revelation of the root of the lower waters themselves, and there is no need for the lower waters to have a thirst and longing to exit their existence and ascend above. The fact that the intention in the descent of the lower waters below is that they should have the thirst to ascend above is from the side of *Tiferes*, the middle line, which connects the opposites of *Chesed* and *Gevurah*, to "include the left in the right." Since the matter of inclusion is from the side of *bitul*, Korach, who was not in a state of *bitul*, could not accept this matter.

It can be said that similarly, this is regarding the *avodah* of "let all your deeds be for the sake of Heaven." The fact that even though he knows the greatness of the superiority of "in all your ways know Him"—the knowledge of *Elokus* within the matters of the world themselves—nevertheless, all his engagement in the matters of the world is only a means for the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, is through the *bitul* to fulfill the Supreme Will. Since his *avodah* is not to quench his thirst to have a revelation of *Elokus* in his soul, but rather he is surrendered and devoted to fulfilling the will of Hashem, therefore the revelation of knowing *Elokus* (also) in the matters of the world is not his primary concern, and his entire desire is in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, the fulfillment of the will of Hashem. [And through this, he will also have the revelation of *Elokus* that is in the matters of the world, as mentioned (section 5), that through the *avodah* of "let all your deeds be for the sake of Heaven," one reaches "in all your ways know Him."]

**8.** This is "He has set our soul in life and has not allowed our foot to slip." When a person engages in Torah and *mitzvos*, he is in the aspect of the head, and when he engages in the matters of the world, he is in the aspect of the foot. The power to ensure that his feet (his engagement in the matters of the world) do not slip is from the life in which He has set our soul—the life that is above nature, above the life of the *nefesh* itself, and even above the level of "alive in essence." For from the level of the life of the *nefesh* itself (including the level of "alive in essence"), it is possible that he will desire the revelation of *Elokus* that is in the matters of the world, and when his engagement in the matters of the world is for the sake of (the revelation in) the matters of the world themselves, and not for the sake of Heaven for the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, then the feet within him (his engagement in optional matters) will slip. In order that his feet should not slip, through his engagement in optional matters being for the sake of Heaven as mentioned, it is through the life that is above nature (it can be said that the vessel for this is *bitul*), which, because it is above limitation, connects the two opposites of *Chesed* and *Gevurah*. Even though he knows the superiority in the clarification of optional matters, his intention in performing optional matters is for the sake of the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*.

**9.** It can be said that this is the connection of "He has set our soul in life..." with the redemption of 12 Tammuz. It is known that through the conduct of nature, which is always in one manner, the matter of "I have not changed" is revealed (except that the matter of "I have not changed" as it is revealed in natural conduct is clothed in the limitation of nature), and through miracles, a revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is without limit, which is above being clothed in the worlds, is drawn down. The root of these two matters is *Chasadim* and *Gevuros*. The conduct of nature (*tzimtzum* and limitation) is from the *Gevuros* [it can be said that the fact that the matter of "I have not changed" is revealed specifically in natural conduct is because the root of *Gevuros* is higher than the root of *Chasadim*], and miracles (a revelation above the limitation of nature) are from the *Chasadim*. The matter of "including the left in the right" is that the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* without limit that comes through miracles is not in a manner of the overturning of nature, but rather, even though nature remains in its existence, one sees clearly that it is a miracle that is above nature. Perhaps it can be said that what is written in *Tanya*—that the matter of "He shared with it the attribute of mercy" is the revelation of *Elokus* through *tzaddikim* and signs and wonders—the intention in this is (primarily) for the signs and wonders [through the *tzaddikim*] that are clothed in nature ("He shared with it"). For the signs and wonders that are above nature are from the *Chasadim*, and nature (in which the wonders are clothed) is from the *Gevuros*, and therefore these signs and wonders are from the attribute of mercy, *Tiferes*, which connects the two opposites of *Chesed* and *Gevurah*.

This is the connection of "He has set our soul in life..." to the redemption of 12 Tammuz, for the redemption of 12 Tammuz (including also the beginning of the redemption that was on 3 Tammuz) was an open miracle that was above nature. And yet, it was not in a manner of the overturning and nullification of nature, but rather nature remained in its existence. Furthermore, even the opponents remained in their strength at that time, and nevertheless, they were forced to assist (and through their own strength) in the liberation and redemption. Through this, the partition between the lower and upper worlds was nullified, to "include the left in the right." Through this, the power was given thereafter to every single Jew to nullify the partition between engagement in optional matters and the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, so that even in optional matters, the light of Torah and *mitzvos* will shine. This serves as a near preparation for the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh together shall see that the mouth of Hashem has spoken," that even physical flesh will see *Elokus*. All this is accomplished through the signs and wonders of the *tzaddikim*, who draw down into nature a revelation of *Elokus* that is above nature, just as it was in those days, at this time.

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Korach, 3 Tammuz, 5724

"May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers; may He not forsake us and may He not abandon us." The *sicha* of the Baal HaGeulah from 3 Tammuz 5727 is well known: "We ask of Hashem, 'May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers; may He not forsake us and may He not abandon us.' May Hashem be with us, and He *will* be with us, 'as He was with our fathers.'"

One must understand: a request and a promise are different concepts (and, on the face of it, opposites). Yet, he says, "We *ask* of Hashem... that He *should* be with us, and He *will* be with us"—meaning the *request* is (not only that He should be with us, but also) that He *will* be with us. Even though the word *yehi* ("may He be") is a term of request as well as a term of promise, they are seemingly different interpretations, yet in the *sicha*, he includes both concepts together.

He continues in the *sicha* that the fact that "May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers" (*yehi* as both a request and a promise) applies even though "we are not equal to our fathers." It can be said that the source for this explanation is what is found in the Midrash: "King Solomon says before the Holy One, Blessed be He: 'A king who hires workers and they do their work well, and he gives them their wages—what praise is there for the king? When is he praised? When he hires bad workers who do not do their work, and he gives them their wages—that is a great kindness.' And thus it is written, 'May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers.'"

He explains in the *sicha* that the reason we cannot be compared to our fathers is that our fathers were *baalei mesiras nefesh* in actual practice regarding Torah and *mitzvos*. One must understand: this *sicha* was said in connection with his departure for exile in Kostroma, where the exile (and the imprisonment before it) was due to his *mesiras nefesh* in actual practice for Torah and *mitzvos* [and furthermore, the very saying of this *sicha* was an act of *mesiras nefesh* in practice], and yet he says that we are not like our fathers who were *baalei mesiras nefesh*.

Seemingly, one could say that since the Baal HaGeulah’s request, "May Hashem our G-d be with us," was (not only for himself but also) for all of Israel, including those who are (only) called by the name of Israel, he therefore said that they are not like our fathers who were *baalei mesiras nefesh* in practice. But this explanation is insufficient, because in the phrase, "*We* are not equal to our fathers," he included himself as well. And one cannot say that by including himself among those who are not *baalei mesiras nefesh* in practice, he was speaking out of humility, for the concept of humility applies only to something that is within one's relative reach.

**2.** Now, in addition to the precision required in the *sicha*, the phrase "May Hashem our G-d be with us" (in the verse itself) requires explanation. Seemingly, after saying "Hashem our G-d"—that He is *our* G-d, and especially according to what is explained in Chassidus that *Elokeinu* means *our power and our vitality*—what need is there for a request that He be "with us"? Also, one must understand the phrasing "with us... with our fathers." The term "with" (*im*) is applied to something that is secondary to the thing it is with [like "the heirs of the husband shall divide with the heirs of the father," where the heirs of the husband are secondary to the heirs of the father], and yet it says "May Hashem our G-d be *with us*... *with* our fathers," implying that Hashem our G-d is secondary to us and to our fathers.

This can be explained according to the well-known concept that the reason fear of Heaven is called an "otzar" (treasury) is because, just as a king's treasury—the king cannot create a treasury unless he gathers from others—so too, fear (the treasury of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He) is not in the hands of Heaven, as our Sages said, "Everything is in the hands of Heaven, except for fear of Heaven."

One should add that the reason the term "treasury" is used specifically for fear—even though this concept (that the Holy One, Blessed be He, seemingly "needs" the person) applies to all *mitzvos*—is because the proper fulfillment of *mitzvos* is through *ahavas Hashem* or *yiras Hashem*. One of the differences between love and fear is that *ahavas Hashem* comes through a revelation of light from above, while *yiras Hashem* comes (primarily) through the *avodah* of the person. This is similar to the fear of a mortal king: the reason the citizens fear the king is because they accepted him to be king over them, for the acceptance of sovereignty is through the people: "You shall surely set a king over you." Based on this, we can explain the phrase "May Hashem our G-d be *with us* as He was *with* our fathers," because in *yiras Hashem* (which is the beginning, essence, and root of *avodah*), the essence is the *avodah* of the person, and the revelation of light from above (Hashem our G-d) is only assisting the person—"with us."

**3.** The reason why fear comes primarily through the *avodah* of the person is that fear is *bitul*. Especially the fear of a king: "You shall set a king over you, so that his awe may be upon you," where the *bitul* of this fear is connected to being a servant of the king [for it is the nature of a servant to be in awe and fear of his master]. The *bitul* of a servant is absolute *bitul*, and therefore it comes specifically through the person. For the effect produced in a person by a revelation of light from above is like an external addition, and therefore the change it creates in him is only in his outward appearance, not a change in the person himself. In order to arrive at absolute *bitul*, the *bitul* of a servant [where the difference between a free man and a servant is in his very existence], it must be through the person himself accepting upon himself to be a servant of the King.

It can be said that the same applies to *mesiras nefesh*. Since *mesiras nefesh* is absolute *bitul*, and especially when the *mesiras nefesh* is for matters for which, according to the law (a command from above), one is not obligated to sacrifice his life, it therefore comes (primarily) not through a revelation of light from above, but through *the person* sacrificing his own life. Based on this, it is even more understandable that the request and prayer of the Baal HaGeulah (in the *sicha* of 3 Tammuz) was in the words of the verse, "May Hashem our G-d be *with us* as He was *with* our fathers," because he was speaking then about the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh*—and in that very thing, in many matters for which one is not legally obligated to sacrifice his life, it comes (primarily) from the person himself. And since in the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh* the essence is the *avodah* of the person, and the revelation of light from above is assisting the *avodah* of the person, he therefore began his request and prayer (in the words of the verse) with "May Hashem our G-d be *with us*."

**4.** The term "with" (*im*) is appropriate when there is a similarity between the two things, as in the Sages' interpretation of the verse, "And they shall stand there *with you* (*imcha*)"—"*imcha* (with you) in those who are similar to you." Even though the term "with" denotes something secondary (as mentioned in section 2), it nevertheless has a similarity to the primary. The same applies to the term *es* (with), which denotes something secondary, as in the Sages' interpretation of the verse, "*es* his flesh"—the secondary to his flesh. Nevertheless, it is similar to the primary, as in the Sages' interpretation of the verse, "And they shall bear *with you* (*etcha*)"—"*etcha* (with you) in those who are similar to you." It is explained in books of grammar that the secondary implied by the term *es* is more secondary than the secondary implied by the term *im*. Based on this, in the term *es*, the primary emphasis is that the thing (to which *es* is applied) is only secondary, while in the term *im*, the primary emphasis is on the similarity between the two things. From this it is understood that the primary emphasis in "May Hashem our G-d be *with us*" is not that Hashem our G-d is, so to speak, secondary to the person, but rather the similarity, so to speak, that exists between them. It can be said that the similarity between them is in the matter of primary and secondary. Just as the perfection of a person's *avodah* is when his *avodah* is through his own power, which is why Hashem our G-d is, so to speak, secondary to the person (as mentioned in section 2), the same is true for the other side: the perfection of a person's *avodah* is when his *avodah* [even the *avodah* through his own power, and the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh*, including *mesiras nefesh* for matters for which one is not legally obligated to sacrifice his life] is not because he wants to serve Hashem, but because he is *batel* to *Elokus*. Since his *bitul* to the Holy One, Blessed be He, is absolute *bitul*, every single *mitzvah* (even when he is not legally obligated to sacrifice his life for it) is for him in such a way that it is impossible not to fulfill it, even when its fulfillment is through *mesiras nefesh*.

One should add that through *bitul* to *Elokus*, there is also an increase in *mesiras nefesh*. When his *mesiras nefesh* is because he wants and has decided to fulfill the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He, even when it requires *mesiras nefesh*, he still leaves room for the possibility of it being otherwise, and the fact that he actually stands in *mesiras nefesh* is only because he decided so. This is not the case when his *mesiras nefesh* is because of his *bitul* to the Holy One, Blessed be He, where every *mitzvah* commanded by the Holy One, Blessed be He, is for him in such a way that it is impossible for it to be otherwise; then there is no room at all for it to be otherwise.

**5.** This is "May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers," for in the *avodah* of the fathers, the two aforementioned concepts are emphasized. They fulfilled the entire Torah before it was given, which emphasizes that their *avodah* was (not because of a command from above, but) through their own power. And yet, they were in absolute *bitul*, for the fathers are the *Merkavah* (Chariot). The *bitul* of the *Merkavah* to the Rider is absolute *bitul*. The *bitul* of the *Merkavah* to the Rider is not from the will of the *Merkavah* (that it wants to be *batel* to the Rider and a *Merkavah* to Him), but from the Rider. And since there are many levels in *bitul*, we therefore request, "May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers"—that the matter of "May Hashem our G-d be with us," our *bitul* to *Elokus*, should be as it was with our fathers: the *bitul* of a *Merkavah*.

**6.** Based on this, we can explain what the Baal HaGeulah said, "*We* are not equal to our fathers, who were *baalei mesiras nefesh* in practice," including himself in this, because the true essence of *mesiras nefesh* is when the *mesiras nefesh* is from the perspective of *bitul* (as mentioned in section 4). And since there are many levels in *bitul* (as mentioned in section 5), it is appropriate for him to say about himself (out of humility) that he lacks in the matter of *mesiras nefesh*. Based on this, we can also explain what he says in the *sicha*—that the request "May Hashem our G-d be with us" includes the interpretation of *yehi* as a term of promise ("He *will* be with us"). For the fact that prayer (request) and promise are two different things is because prayer is the request of the person, and a promise is from above. Even among *tzaddikim*, when they are an "existence" (at least in a subtle way), prayer and promise are two different things. A *tzaddik's* promise is in the mission of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and a *tzaddik's* prayer is the request of the *tzaddik* himself. This is not the case when the *tzaddik* is in such a state that even his *avodah* through his own power (which is seemingly an "existence") is in absolute *bitul*; then, even in his prayer (request), there is also the element of the promise.

One should add that he imparted a semblance of this (that even existence is in *bitul*) to those who are connected and related to him, by rooting in them *mesiras nefesh* even for matters for which, according to the law (a command from above), one is not obligated to sacrifice his life (*mesiras nefesh* from the perspective of the person), and that even the *mesiras nefesh* for these matters should be in such a way that it is impossible for it to be otherwise (*mesiras nefesh* from the perspective of *Elokus*). Therefore, the fact that the Baal HaGeulah’s request includes the element of promise is also due to the recipients.

May the promise be fulfilled: "May Hashem our G-d be with us, as He was with our fathers; may He not forsake us and may He not abandon us," and for all the children of Israel there will be light in spirituality and in physicality.

## 12 Tammuz 5717

"Hashem is for me as a helper, and I will gaze upon my enemies." The Rebbe Rayatz, the Baal HaGeulah, analyzes this verse in his maamar (delivered on the first 12 Tammuz, 5687): The literal implication of "Hashem is for me as a helper" is that there are other helpers, and the request is that Hashem should also be among them. This is difficult to understand, for all of Klal Yisrael believes with simple faith that He, may He be blessed, is the sole Helper and Savior for man in all his affairs. How, then, can one say "Hashem is for me as a helper," which implies that there are other, true helpers, and Hashem merely joins them? Furthermore, we must understand the request "and I will gaze upon my enemies" (that he should see vengeance upon his enemies). Seemingly, it would have been more appropriate to request that the enemies and haters be transformed into lovers. Even though David’s hatred was directed only toward the enemies of Hashem—as it is written, "Do I not hate those who hate You, Hashem, and contend with those who rise up against You?"—it is nevertheless written, "Let sins be consumed, but not sinners" (a concept that applies even to the enemies of Hashem, as we saw in the conduct of our Rebbes, and especially the Baal HaGeulah, who drew even those included in the category mentioned at the end of Tanya, Chapter 32, close and brought them to repentance). He should have requested that they do teshuvah; what is the meaning of the request "and I will gaze upon my enemies"?

2) To understand this, the maamar introduces what David said: "Your statutes were songs to me in the house of my dwelling." When he was a wanderer, tossed about in exile (*megurai* from the word *geirus*—exile) and filled with fear (*megurai* from the word *magor*—fear) from his enemies and pursuers, he would find pleasure and joy in the words of Torah (*chukecha*—Your statutes), which were as sweet and pleasant to him as songs and melodies. We must understand: there are many types of pleasures; why does David compare the pleasure he had in the words of Torah specifically to the pleasure of songs? Furthermore, we must understand that there are three categories of mitzvos: *mishpatim* (judgments), *eidus* (testimonies), and *chukim* (statutes). *Mishpatim* are mitzvos that are also required by logic (such as theft, robbery, fraud, and honoring parents). *Eidus* are mitzvos that serve as a sign and remembrance (such as Shabbos, Pesach, Sukkos, and tefillin), which also have a place in the intellect. Even though the intellect by itself (without the Torah’s command) would not mandate them—unlike *mishpatim*, where even if the Torah had not been given, we would learn modesty from a cat and theft from an ant—nevertheless, once the Torah has commanded them, the intellect agrees. *Chukim*, however, are mitzvos that have no reason, but are only "a statute I have enacted, a decree I have issued." We must understand why he said "Your statutes were songs to me"—it is obvious that King David’s pleasure and joy in Torah study encompassed all the laws of the Torah (including *eidus* and *mishpatim*). Why does he say "Your statutes" specifically?

3) The matter is that *zemirot* (songs) also implies praise. As it is stated in Tanya, David calling the words of Torah "songs" refers to the praise of the Torah—that David was praising the Torah by noting that the vitality of all the worlds depends on a single detail of the Torah. The connection between this interpretation and the simple meaning of "Your statutes were songs to me" is that through contemplating the greatness and praise of the Torah—that all worlds are nullified in existence relative to a single detail of Torah—he achieved that all worldly matters held no place for him. Even when he was in a state of physical distress, he would engage in Torah with great joy. In the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah, another interpretation of "Your statutes were songs to me" is explained: *zemirot* comes from the word for cutting and severing, as in "to prune (*lezamer*) the tyrants." Through King David’s Torah study, all his enemies and pursuers were nullified, as the Sages said: "Go early and late to the beis medrash, and they will be consumed of their own accord." The two interpretations can be linked: through engaging in Torah in the manner of *zemirot* as explained in Tanya—where he felt that the vitality of all worlds depends on a detail of Torah—it follows that whatever is not in accordance with Torah, and certainly whatever opposes Torah, loses its vitality. This is *zemirot* in the sense of "pruning the tyrants." Based on this, we can understand why he said "Your statutes (*chukecha*)": because these two aspects of the Torah’s *zemirot* (the praise of the Torah and the pruning of tyrants) are primarily derived from the aspect of *chukim* in the Torah.

4) The matter is that the two general divisions of mitzvos—*eidus* and *mishpatim*, which have a reason, and *chukim*, which are above reason—are two general aspects in the service of Hashem: the service of *ta'am* and *da'as* (intellect and understanding, corresponding to *mishpatim*) and the service of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke, corresponding to *chukim*). These must exist in every single mitzvah. There are two aspects to mitzvos: First, that the mitzvos are His will, a will that is above reason. This applies equally to all mitzvos. Second, that after the will is enclothed in *chochma* (of the Torah), a reason is added to every mitzvah, and through every mitzvah, a specific light and revelation is drawn down. This is the meaning of the 248 commandments being the 248 limbs of the King, where each limb is a vessel for a specific power. These reasons are from the *chochma* of the Torah as it is above. From this, there are drawn down (through the multiplicity of *seder hishtalshelus*) the reasons for the mitzvos in the *nigleh* of the Torah (the reasons for *eidus* and *mishpatim* as they are simply understood). This is why in the performance of mitzvos there must be two *kavanos*: a general *kavanah* and a specific *kavanah*. From the perspective of the will (which is above reason), there must be the general *kavanah* of *kabbalas ol* to fulfill the will of Hashem, and from the perspective of the reasons for the mitzvos, there must be the specific *kavanah* pertaining to that particular mitzvah.

5) This is why the two categories of *chukim* and *mishpatim* are two general aspects in every single mitzvah. Even the mitzvos of *eidus* and *mishpatim* that have a reason must be performed (primarily) because they are the will of Hashem, just like the *chukim*. Conversely, even in the mitzvos of *chukim*, there is the reason and specific *kavanah*—that through every mitzvah (even the *chukim*), a specific light and revelation is drawn down. Furthermore, each of these two aspects (*chukim* and *mishpatim*) is a general matter in man’s service, not only in the performance of mitzvos but in the entirety of a person’s conduct. The matter of *mishpatim* is (as explained in the maamar) to judge every matter: does it conform to the intellect and wisdom of the Torah? Even when a matter in itself has no trace of prohibition, one must weigh carefully whether it will cause a weakening in any mitzvah or custom of Israel, in which case the matter must be rejected entirely. The matter of *chukim* is the service of *kabbalas ol malchus shamayim*, which must be present not only during the performance of a mitzvah but throughout the entire day.

6) This is the meaning of "Your statutes (*chukecha*) were songs to me"—specifically *chukecha*. The intent of the verse is not to refer to the category of *chukim*, but to all mitzvos. When their performance (and study) is due to the command and decree of Hashem (in the manner of "Your statutes"—a statute I have enacted, a decree I have issued), then specifically they become "songs to me." The point is that the fact that all worlds are nullified in existence relative to a detail of Torah is primarily because the root of the Torah is in *Keter*, which is above *Chochma*. From the perspective of this level, the mitzvos and all the details of the *halachos* within them are because "so it arose in His will," a will that is above reason. In the level of Torah as it is drawn into *Chochma*, since the mitzvos and their details (from the perspective of *Chochma*) are based on reason—that in order for the *mochin* to be drawn into the worlds through tefillin, they must be in this specific manner—it is inevitable that the worlds have some value and place. Therefore, he emphasizes "Your statutes (*chukecha*) were songs to me in the house of my dwelling": when his Torah study is in a manner where he knows and feels that all the details of the Torah are because "so it arose in His will" (*chukecha*), then he feels how all worlds are nullified in existence relative to a single detail of Torah. Consequently, the words of Torah he studies are "songs" (pleasure and delight) to him even in the house of his dwelling, because all the persecutions he suffers from his enemies have no place for him. Furthermore, through this, it is drawn down in the world as well, that the enemies and pursuers are nullified—*zemirot* in the sense of "pruning the tyrants."

7) To explain this more deeply, we must first understand the concept of *eidus* (testimony). This concept, too, applies to all mitzvos (even *chukim* and *mishpatim*), similar to what was said regarding *mishpatim* and *chukim*. As the Baal HaGeulah explains in the maamar "Vayakam," "He established a testimony in Yaakov and appointed a Torah in Yisrael"—that the mitzvos (even *mishpatim* and *chukim*) are called *eidus* because they draw down and reveal the essential concealment of the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof*, which is above the concealment associated with revelation. Just as the concept of testimony in simple terms is only regarding something hidden—for regarding something revealed, testimony is not applicable, as it is already known, and even regarding something that is destined to be revealed, testimony is not needed—so too in spirituality: the *Ohr HaMemalei* (indwelling light) is something revealed that is grasped by the intellect. As is known regarding "From my flesh I behold Elokah," just as it is clear to a person that there is a soul that vivifies his body—because he feels his body is alive, he knows clearly that this is not from the body itself but that there is a soul vivifying it—so too regarding the world: by seeing a living world, one knows clearly that there is a Divine vitality vivifying the world. The *Ohr HaSovev* (surrounding light), which is above enclothement in the worlds, is "something destined to be revealed" (a concealment associated with revelation). As explained elsewhere, through grasping the *Ohr HaMemalei* that is enclothed in the worlds—which is merely an illumination (as proven by the fact that it is enclothed)—one comes to the knowledge that there is a light that is transcendent of the worlds, which is the source from which the illumination in the enclothement is drawn. This is similar to how the intellect itself necessitates that there is something above the intellect. The concept of *eidus* relates to the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof*, which is above even the *Sovev*, which is completely hidden, and regarding which no knowledge or grasp is applicable, not even the knowledge of negation. This is why all mitzvos are called *eidus*: because they draw down and reveal the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof*, which is above even the *Sovev*.

8) We must understand: if the mitzvos are *eidus* regarding the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* because they are His will—a will above reason—what is the difference between *eidus* and *chukim*? We must also understand the connection between the category of mitzvos called *eidus* (because they are a sign and remembrance, a matter of reason) and the concept of *eidus* in the totality of mitzvos (that they testify to the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* because they are a will above reason). The matter is that the *eidus* in mitzvos within man’s service is the service of *re'usa d'liba* (the desire of the heart). *Re'usa d'liba* is the desire for Elokus that comes from the essence of the soul, through which one grasps the *Atzmus*, as it is said: "No thought can grasp Him at all" (referring to the internal aspect and *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* which is above the *Sovev*, which is not grasped in any grasp, not even the grasp of negation), "but He is grasped by the *re'usa d'liba*." The service of *chukim* is the service of *kabbalas ol*. The difference between these two services is that in the service of *re'usa d'liba*, since there is a desire—even though the desire is from the connection of the essence of the soul to the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof*—it is still in the state of *metzius* (existence). Even when his desire is in *bitul*, that he does not want anything for himself at all and his entire desire is that there be a revelation of Elokus in the world and that the intent of a "dwelling place for Him in the lower realms" be fulfilled, the very essence of desire is *metzius*. The true essence of *bitul* is in the service of *kabbalas ol*, which is like a servant who has no desires at all; everything he does is due to the yoke of the master placed upon him, because of which he is *compelled* to fulfill the master’s will.

9) The difference between the service of *eidus* and the service of *chukim* is analogous to the difference between them regarding the mitzvos themselves. This is understood based on what is known: that the will of the mitzvos as it is from the *Atzmus* is an essential will that is not for the sake of any intent to be fulfilled through the mitzvos, and the purpose of the mitzvos (from the perspective of this will) is the mitzvos themselves. From this, it is understood that the fact that the mitzvos draw down and reveal the *Atzmus* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* in the world—even though the drawing down is because the mitzvos are His will above reason—since this is a matter that is *accomplished* through the mitzvos, it is analogous to reason. The true essence of the essential will of His *Atzmus* is in the mitzvos themselves. This is why the service of *eidus* is the service of *re'usa d'liba* and the service of *chukim* is the service of *kabbalas ol*. Because the *eidus* in mitzvos, since it is a drawing down and revelation, the vessel for this is desire—and even the desire that comes from the essence of the soul is a movement of drawing down and expansion (*metzius*). The vessel for the *chukim* of the mitzvos, which is a truly essential will that is above revelation, is the *bitul* of *kabbalas ol*—a *bitul* that comes from the essence that is above any matter of expansion.

10) This is "Your statutes (*chukecha*) were songs to me"—specifically *chukecha*—for his intent in this is to exclude not only the matter of *mishpatim* but also the matter of *eidus*. For in the level of *eidus*, some *metzius* still remains. And not only from the side of man—for even his desire that is above *ta'am* and *da'as* is *metzius* (as above)—but also from the side of the mitzvos that are in the level of *eidus*, since their matter is the drawing down and revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* in the world. The true and complete recognition that all worlds are nullified in existence relative to a single detail of Torah is specifically in the level of *chukim*, where the details of the Torah (from the perspective of this level) are an essential matter from their essential root in the Torah, which is above any connection to the world.

11) The maamar continues that David was punished for this because David’s Torah study was in the manner of "pruning the tyrants" (as above), and the ultimate intent is as it is written, "He did not create it for naught, but formed it to be inhabited"—to engage in the service of *birurim* (refinements) and to draw down a revelation of light in the world. This is the advantage of *tefillah* over Torah: *tefillah* is refinement and elevation—meaning that through *tefillah*, the sparks are refined, purified, and elevated upward. Torah, by contrast, is a drawing down from above, and the refinement through Torah is in the manner of "pushing away." When David wanted to perform refinements through Torah, which is in the manner of "pushing away"—"pruning the tyrants"—he was punished for it, because the ultimate intent is "to be inhabited."

We must understand: David’s Torah study in the manner of "Your statutes were songs to me" is in the level of Torah as it is from the essential will (as explained at length above). How can it be that this is not in accordance with the true intent? The explanation for this is based on what is said in the maamar at the beginning regarding "Hashem is One." The meaning of "One" (*echad*) is "unique" (*yachid*), and the reason we say "One" and not "unique" is to indicate that *Havayah* and *Elokim* are all one. The matter is that the true meaning of the unity of *Havayah* is that the unity is also from the perspective of the world. This is "Hashem is One": if it were written "Hashem is unique," the meaning would be that His uniqueness is from the perspective of the *Ohr Ein Sof* (and not from the perspective of the world). To emphasize that His uniqueness is also from the perspective of the world—even from the perspective of the world as it is created from the name *Elokim*, which conceals and hides the name *Havayah*—it is said "Hashem is One," that even the *Chet* and *Dalet* (which are the seven heavens, the earth, and the four directions of the world) are nullified to the *Aleph* (the uniqueness of the world). Since *Havayah* and *Elokim* are all one, the name *Elokim* does not truly conceal, and therefore, even the world that was brought into being from the name *Elokim* is truly nullified, and "there is nothing else beside Him." This leads to the *bitul* in the level and manner of "unique," which is above "One." Through the unification of these two matters (that His uniqueness is in the manner of "unique," and that this matter is also from the perspective of the world), there is a revelation of the power of the *Atzmus* that includes and connects the matter of "One" and "unique."

12) It should be added that the name *Havayah* ("Hashem is One") points to all three matters (One, unique, and the power of the *Atzmus* that connects them). In *Havayah* there are three matters: 1) *Havayah* from the word *mehoveh* (bringing into being)—this meaning in the name *Havayah* points to His connection to the worlds. 2) *Havayah* from the word *hayah, hoveh, v'yihyeh* (was, is, and will be)—this meaning in the name *Havayah* points to Him being above the worlds. 3) The third matter in the name *Havayah* is that *Havayah* is the "Name of the Essence"—meaning it points to His *Atzmus*. Although in *Pardes* it is written that the fact that *Havayah* is the "Name of the Essence" is only regarding the essence of the *Sefiros* (the lights enclothed in the vessels), the conclusion of Chassidic teaching is that the meaning of "Name of the Essence" is the *Atzmus* itself. Since all three matters are in the same name, it is understood that they are related to each other. That is, the unification of the two meanings in *Havayah*—*Havayah* as *mehoveh* and *Havayah* as *hayah, hoveh, v'yihyeh*—is because *Havayah* is the "Name of the Essence." Thus, through the fact that *Havayah* (which is above the worlds) is drawn into *Havayah* (as *mehoveh*), even though externally this is a matter of descent, through this specifically the "Name of the Essence" within it is revealed. Moreover, the revelation of the "Name of the Essence" of *Havayah* is primarily in *Havayah* as *mehoveh*. As explained elsewhere, the reason the name *Havayah* is the "Name of the Essence" pointing to the *Atzmus* is because the creation of *yesh me'ayin* is specifically through the power of the *Atzmus*, whose existence is from His essence.

13) Based on this, we can understand what the Rambam says (cited in the aforementioned maamar at the beginning): "The foundation of foundations and the pillar of wisdoms is to know that there is a First Being who brings into being all that exists, and all that exists from the heavens and the earth and what is between them only exists from the truth of His existence." The mitzvah of knowledge consists of three matters: that there is a First Being, that He brings into being all that exists, and that all that exists only exists from the truth of His existence. These three matters correspond to the three matters in *Havayah* mentioned above. "Foundation of foundations and pillar of wisdoms" is an acronym for *Havayah*. "First Being" is that He is prior to everything, above creation. "Brings into being all that exists" is *Havayah* as *mehoveh*. "And all that exists... only exists from the truth of His existence"—*truth* of His existence is the *Atzmus* whose existence is from His essence, for the creation of existence *yesh me'ayin* is through the power of the *Atzmus* (as above), the matter of the "Name of the Essence."

14) It can be said that this is also why *Havayah* is an acronym for "foundation of foundations and pillar of wisdoms," for foundations and wisdoms are two opposite matters. Foundations are the simple premises that are above construction and reasoning—they are the foundations of grasp. Wisdoms are the intellectual arguments that are grasped in understanding, where debate and inquiry are applicable. In man’s service, the matter of foundations is the simple faith that is above intellect, and wisdoms are the matter of grasp. It can be said that the root of the foundations is in *Havayah* as it is above the worlds (*hayah, hoveh, v'yihyeh*), and the root of the wisdoms is in *Havayah* as *mehoveh*. The power that unites the foundations and the wisdoms—that the faith above intellect should be drawn into the intellect as well—is from the name *Havayah*, the "Name of the Essence."

Based on this, we can understand why David was punished for saying "Your statutes were songs to me," because the Torah as it is from the essential will that is above reason (foundations) is analogous to *Havayah* as *hayah, hoveh, v'yihyeh* which is above the world. Therefore, the refinement that comes from this level is in the manner of "pushing away" (and not in the way of refinement), *zemirot* in the sense of "pruning the tyrants." Since the true meaning of the unity of *Havayah* is that the unity is also from the perspective of the worlds, there must be the drawing down of *eidus* and *mishpatim* of the Torah (wisdoms) so that there will be a revelation of Elokus in the world. Through this, the essence of the Torah, which is above even *chukim*—the "Name of the Essence"—is revealed.

15) This is "Hashem is for me as a helper." "My helper" refers to the sparks being refined, which are the true helpers of man (similar to what is known regarding "Man shall not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem shall man live"—that through man refining the sparks in the *domem, tzomeiach, chai, medabeir*, he is drawn additional strength in his service, for the sparks help and assist him). The meaning of "Hashem is for me as a helper" is that the sparks being refined (my helper), even though the matter of refinements is from below to above (a matter of the world), there is drawn into them a revelation of the name *Havayah* which is above *hishtalshelus*. The connection of these two matters is from *Havayah*, the "Name of the Essence." This is also "and I will gaze upon my enemies"—that even those who are enemies of David, who are enemies of Hashem, do not need to be rejected entirely, but rather one must refine the sparks within them. Through extracting the sparks from them, the evil within them is nullified. Through this, one comes to a "gazing" at Elokus—"I will gaze upon my enemies"—a tangible gazing at Elokus even in worldly matters. As it was with the Baal HaGeulah, that even the opponents, although they remained in their existence, were compelled (through the sparks within them) to act according to the intent, and there was a tangible revelation of Elokus (that is above nature) within nature. Through this, he drew the strength for those who follow in his paths to draw down a revelation of Elokus that is above nature into nature. This became a near preparation for the completion of the intent of a "dwelling place for Him in the lower realms"—that the lower realms will be a dwelling place for Him, for His *Atzmus*, in the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Chukas-Balak, 12 Tammuz 5729

### With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Chukas-Balak, 12 Tammuz 5729

"Hashem spoke to Moshe, saying... This is the statute (*chukas*) of the Torah... that they take to you a red heifer..." Rashi explains: "Take to you—it is always called by your name: the heifer that Moshe made in the wilderness." One must understand: Moshe only made the first heifer; why are all the heifers (the eight heifers made subsequently, and even the tenth heifer that Melech HaMoshiach will make) called by Moshe’s name? Furthermore, according to the well-known principle that the name of a thing indicates its essence and content, it is understood that the fact that all the heifers are called by Moshe’s name means that this (the connection to Moshe) is their essence and content. Based on this, it is even more difficult to understand why they are called by Moshe’s name, given that the actual making of the heifers was done by the Kohanim [and even the first heifer was made by Elazar the Kohen; the explanation that it is "the heifer that Moshe made" seemingly means only that it was made according to his instruction and command]. What, then, is their connection to Moshe, to the point that they are called by his name?

2) The matter is as follows: It is stated in *Likutei Torah* that the reason it is said regarding the red heifer, "This is the statute of the Torah," is because the mitzvah of the red heifer is the totality of the Torah. Therefore, just as the Torah is called by Moshe’s name, as it is written, "Remember the Torah of Moshe My servant," so too the red heifer, which is the totality of the Torah, is called by Moshe’s name. Seemingly, one could add that when *Likutei Torah* says the mitzvah of the red heifer is the totality of the Torah, it refers primarily to the *mitzvos* of the Torah [as is understood from the explanation in *Likutei Torah* there, that the reason the red heifer is the totality of the Torah is because the foundation of all mitzvos is *ratzo v'shov*, and the red heifer is the concept of *ratzo v'shov*]. Accordingly, the totality of the *mitzvos* of the Torah is connected to Moshe.

This can be explained based on what is written in *Tanya* regarding the reason Moshe Rabbeinu commanded the generation that entered Eretz Yisrael to recite the *Shema* twice daily, to accept the Kingdom of Heaven with *mesiras nefesh* (even though Hashem had promised them, "Hashem will place your fear and dread...")—it is because the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* depends on remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*. It can be said that the reason Moshe specifically commanded this to the generation that entered Eretz Yisrael is because *mesiras nefesh* is the concept of *bitul*, and since a human being is a *metzius* (the opposite of *bitul*), in order for the concept of *mesiras nefesh* to be revealed within him [and in a way that it is fixed in his heart constantly, day and night, never departing from his memory], he requires a special empowerment. This empowerment comes through Moshe, because Moshe is the concept of *bitul*, "and we are nothing." Therefore, because Moshe commanded the generation that entered Eretz Yisrael to accept upon themselves (twice daily) the Kingdom of Heaven with *mesiras nefesh*, they were given the strength to always remember their *mesiras nefesh*. This is the meaning of "it is always called by your name," because the fulfillment of the Torah and its *mitzvos* [as the red heifer is the totality of Torah and *mitzvos*] depends on remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*, and the strength to always remember the concept of *mesiras nefesh* is through Moshe, and through the *atpashuta d'Moshe* (the extension of Moshe) in every generation, down to the Rebbe, leader of our generation, the *Baal HaSimcha* and the *Baal HaGeulah*. It can be said that because the *avodah* of the leader of our generation throughout his thirty years of leadership was with revealed *mesiras nefesh*, the empowerment for remembering *mesiras nefesh* from the *atpashuta d'Moshe* of our generation is even more revealed.

**To add:** The explanation for why the mitzvah of the red heifer is the totality of the entire Torah [which is why it is said regarding it, "This is the statute of the Torah"] is because the foundation of all *mitzvos* is that they are a *chukah*. That is, the *mitzvos* are the Supreme Will that transcends intellect; therefore, their fulfillment must also be by way of *kabbalas ol*, a *chukah*—"I have enacted a statute, I have issued a decree." Based on this, it is even more understandable why the red heifer is called by Moshe’s name: in order for the fulfillment of all *mitzvos* (even those that have a reason) to be in the manner of "This is the *statute* of the Torah," it must be through the fact that the Torah (and its *mitzvos*), even after it has been clothed in *chochmah* and intellect, is called by the name of Moshe, whose essence is *bitul*—"the Torah of Moshe *My servant*." Through this, there is the empowerment for every Jew (through the aspect of Moshe within him) that his fulfillment of *mitzvos* should be with the *bitul* of *kabbalas ol*, like the fulfillment of the mitzvah of the red heifer: "This is the statute of the Torah."

3) Now, it is stated in the *Midrash* regarding the verse "that they take to you a red heifer": The Holy One, Blessed be He, said to Moshe, "To you I reveal the reason for the heifer, but to others it is a statute." One must understand: since Moshe grasped the reason for all *mitzvos*, including the reason for the mitzvah of the red heifer, how is the empowerment for the fulfillment of *mitzvos* in the manner of "I have enacted a statute, I have issued a decree" drawn down through him? Seemingly, this could be explained based on what is written elsewhere, that in every mitzvah there are two aspects: *chukim* and *mishpatim*. For all *mitzvos* (even the *eidus* and *mishpatim* that have a reason) are His Will, and Will is higher than reason—higher even than the reasons within His *chochmah*. After the Will of the *mitzvos* (even the *chukim*, and even the mitzvah of the red heifer) is drawn down and clothed in *chochmah* (of Torah), a reason is added to them. The difference between the *mitzvos* of *eidus* and *mishpatim* and the *mitzvos* of *chukim* is that in the *mitzvos* of *eidus* and *mishpatim*, the reasons within His *chochmah* were drawn down and clothed in the intellect of created beings, even into human intellect, whereas in the *mitzvos* of *chukim*, their reasons were not (to such an extent) clothed in the intellect of created beings. The reason for the mitzvah of the red heifer is in His *chochmah* (*chochmah* of *Atzilus*) and was not drawn down at all into the intellect of created beings. [The fact that Moshe grasped the reason for the heifer is because even while he was below, the aspect of *chochmah* of *Atzilus* was revealed within him.]

This is the meaning of the fact that in all *mitzvos* there are two aspects, *chukim* and *mishpatim*: from the perspective of the Will of the *mitzvos*, all *mitzvos* are *chukim*, and their fulfillment must be by way of *kabbalas ol*—"I have enacted a statute, I have issued a decree." From the perspective of the reasons for the *mitzvos*, all *mitzvos* are *mishpatim*, and their fulfillment must be (also) from the perspective of the reason. Because Moshe knew the reason for the mitzvah of the heifer, he fulfilled this mitzvah also from the perspective of the reason [unlike everyone else, whose fulfillment of the mitzvah of the red heifer from the perspective of the reason is that he contemplates that even this mitzvah has a reason]. Based on this, it is understood simply that even for Moshe, there was no lack, Heaven forbid, of fulfilling *mitzvos* in the manner of "I have enacted a statute, I have issued a decree," because this aspect of the fulfillment of *mitzvos* is from the perspective of the Will of the *mitzvos*. However, this explanation requires further clarification, because the advantage of the mitzvah of the red heifer over all *mitzvos* is that in all *mitzvos*, the reason within them elevates the Will, whereas in the mitzvah of the red heifer, for which there is no reason (in human intellect), the Will is revealed [and the meaning of "This is the statute of the Torah" is that all *mitzvos* of the Torah are a *chukah* like the red heifer]. From the fact that it is said "that they take to you," that the heifer is called by Moshe’s name, it implies that the special aspect of the mitzvah of the red heifer—that the *chukah* within it (Will higher than reason) is revealed—is also relevant to Moshe. Seemingly, since Moshe knew the reason for the heifer, what is the difference for Moshe between the mitzvah of the red heifer and all other *mitzvos*?

4) This will be understood by prefacing what is written regarding "A prayer of Moshe." It is stated in the *Zohar* that the prayer of Moshe is the "prayer of a rich man." It should be noted what the Rebbe, the *Baal HaGeulah*, said in his well-known *sicha* that the psalm "A prayer of Moshe" is connected to the redemption of 19 Kislev [as is known, the Alter Rebbe would recite a daily *Tehillim* portion as divided by the days of the month, and since the psalm "A prayer of Moshe" is the beginning of the monthly *Tehillim* portion for the 19th day of the month, he recited this psalm on the day of his redemption (19 Kislev)]. From this, it is understood that this psalm is also connected to the redemption of 12 and 13 Tammuz, the redemption of the leader of our generation, who is the successor to the *Baal HaGeulah* of 19 Kislev. [Especially in this year, in which 12 Tammuz, the birthday of the *Baal HaGeulah*, is the beginning of the *Tzaddik* year of the *Baal HaGeulah*, and in it one begins to recite the *Tzaddik* psalm in *Tehillim*, which is the psalm "A prayer of Moshe"]. Now, the essence and content of this psalm is "A prayer of Moshe" [the matters that follow in the continuation of the psalm (after the words "A prayer of Moshe, man of G-d") are matters that Moshe said in his prayer (specific matters), but the general subject of the psalm (which is also the name of the psalm) is "A prayer of Moshe"], and the prayer of Moshe is the "prayer of a rich man" (as mentioned above). From this it is understood that the connection of the psalm to the redemption of 19 Kislev and 12 Tammuz is primarily from the perspective of the general subject of the psalm—"A prayer of Moshe," the "prayer of a rich man," as will be explained in section 13.

5) This will be understood by prefacing the precision of the Rebbe (Rashab) in his *maamar* entitled "A prayer of Moshe": the concept of prayer is that one prays to the Holy One, Blessed be He, to fill one's lack, and since a rich man lacks nothing, what is the concept of the "prayer of a rich man"? It can be said that this precision relates (primarily) to the prayer of Moshe. For regarding a rich man in general, it can be said that his prayer is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, should fill his spiritual lack. This is not the case with Moshe, in whom, even while he was below, his source as it is in *Atzilus* shone in revelation, to the point that there was no partition or interruption between them—"Moshe, Moshe, the accent does not pause". It is understood that the fact that Moshe was rich in physicality is because he was rich in spirituality—meaning that even in spirituality he lacked nothing, not even a lack such as a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him. Therefore, the *maamar* is precise: what is the concept of the "prayer of a rich man"?

The *maamar* continues that the concept of a rich man is not only that he lacks nothing, but that he is influenced with an abundance of bounty. As our Sages say regarding the verse "sufficient for his need, which he lacks"—"sufficient for his need, but you are not commanded to make him rich." Since "sufficient for his need, which he lacks" includes even the lack of a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him, and yet they said "you are not commanded to make him rich," it is understood that even when one has all his needs (including a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him), he is not (yet) "rich," because the concept of a rich man is (not only that he has all his needs, but) that he is influenced with an abundance of bounty. Based on what was said above—that the fact that Moshe was rich in physicality is because he was rich in spirituality—it is understood that in addition to the fact that Moshe had no lack, Heaven forbid (not even a lack such as a horse to ride upon, etc.), because all the revelations belonging to the worlds shone within him in revelation, which are included in the two aspects of *Memale Kol Almin* (Filling all worlds) and *Sovev Kol Almin* (Surrounding all worlds), the revelation of which is the filling of the lack [the light of *Memale*, since it is the *source* for the worlds, therefore, when this light is not in revelation in the world, the world is truly lacking. And the light of *Sovev*, which is higher than the source for the worlds and only relates to the worlds, therefore, when this light is not revealed in the world, the lack of the world is like the lack of a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him. As our Sages say regarding the verse "And G-d finished on the seventh day—what was the world lacking? Rest. Shabbos came, rest came." Rest is the aspect of *Sovev* that is higher than the light clothed in the world, and yet, when this revelation was not in the world, the world was lacking. However, this lack is not that there was a lack of some detail in the world itself, for all the details of the world were brought into being by the *work* of creation (the light clothed in the world) which was completed before Shabbos. The fact that the world was lacking rest is like the lack of a horse to ride upon (which is not an essential thing for the necessity of its existence), and when Shabbos came and the light of *Sovev* was drawn down and revealed, this lack was also filled. The concept of the richness of Moshe is that in addition to the fact that the revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev* shone within him in revelation], the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than any relation to the worlds also shone within him. As explained in the *maamar*, the reason Moshe is called "rich" is because Moshe is the aspect of *Da’as Elyon* (Higher Knowledge). One of the superiorities of *Da’as Elyon* over *Da’as Tachton* (Lower Knowledge) is that *Da’as Tachton* receives from the externality of *Keter*, *Arich*—*Sovev*, while *Da’as Elyon* receives from the internality of *Keter*, *Atik*—*Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than the category of worlds. Based on this, one must understand even more the concept of "A prayer of Moshe," the "prayer of a rich man." The concept of prayer is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, should fill one's lack, and since Moshe was rich both in physicality and in spirituality, not only did he not lack (in actuality) anything, but the concept of "lack" was not applicable to him at all. What, then, is the concept of his prayer?

6) The core of the explanation for this (in the *maamar*) is that the "prayer of a rich man" is not for himself, but for *Knesses Yisrael*. As it is stated in the *Midrash* regarding the verse "A prayer of Moshe": "It is like a parable of three who came to take... from the king... The third came. The king said to him, 'What do you request?' He said to him, 'I do not request anything for myself, but such-and-such a province is destroyed and it is yours; decree that it be rebuilt...' So Moshe did not request for himself, but for Yisrael." Seemingly, this explanation requires further clarification. According to the above, the prayer that a rich man prays (for others) does not relate to his own richness [for the fact that he prays for others is because he desires their good], whereas the meaning of "prayer of a rich man" (simply put) is that his prayer is *because* he is rich.

This will be understood based on what is explained in the *maamar* that *Knesses Yisrael* is the aspect of *Malchus*, and Moshe’s request for *Knesses Yisrael* was (for Yisrael as they are, and also) for the *Sefirah* of *Malchus*. Therefore, the *Midrash* says that Moshe’s request for *Knesses Yisrael* is like the request "such-and-such a province, etc.," for a province is *Malchus*, and "it is destroyed" is the lack that occurred in *Malchus* (the concept of the diminution of the moon), and the request "decree that it be rebuilt" is that the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* should be drawn into *Malchus*, through which it will be built as an everlasting structure. For when the lack of *Malchus* is filled by drawing into it the revelation that belongs to *Malchus*, at which point it is elevated to the level as it was before the light was removed and it became lacking, then it is possible that the light drawn into it could be removed once again. In order for its structure to be an everlasting structure (where it is impossible for it to be destroyed, Heaven forbid), it must be through drawing into it the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than the light belonging to the worlds (*Malchus*), for in this light, *Tzimtzum* and removal are not applicable. This is why Moshe’s prayer is called the "prayer of a rich man"—the meaning of "prayer of a rich man" is that his prayer is *because* he is rich (as mentioned above), for the fact that Moshe prayed that the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* be drawn into *Malchus* (through which it will specifically be built as an everlasting structure) is because he was rich—the aspect of *Da’as Elyon* that receives from *Atik*, the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than the category of worlds.

7) One must understand: according to the above [that Moshe’s prayer that the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* be drawn into *Malchus* is because Moshe is *Da’as Elyon* and therefore has the ability to draw this light into *Malchus*], the drawing down of the revelation into *Malchus* by Moshe is (seemingly) by way of "from above to below." What, then, is the concept of *prayer* of Moshe (*prayer* of a rich man), given that prayer is "from below to above"? The explanation for this is that when the drawing down into *Malchus* is by way of "from above to below," then, even when the revelation is the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than the concept of *Tzimtzum*—which in general is the aspect of the essence of the light that *Tzimtzum* did not touch—nevertheless, since the fact that it is impossible for the light to be removed from *Malchus* is because *the light* is higher than the concept of *Tzimtzum*, regarding *Malchus* itself, this is not the true concept of an everlasting structure, since from the perspective of *Malchus*, it is possible for the light to be removed from it. The true concept of an everlasting structure is when the drawing down of this revelation into *Malchus* is (not only from above, but also) from the perspective of *Malchus* itself. This is the "prayer of Moshe," for prayer is the *avodah* of created beings; therefore, the drawing down through prayer is in a manner that relates to the "below" itself, to the created beings and also to the *Sefirah* of *Malchus*, the root of the created beings. However, the drawing down through prayer in general, since prayer is the *avodah* of created beings, is a drawing down that relates to the worlds. In the drawing down through the prayer of Moshe, there are both superiorities: the drawing down of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than any relation to the worlds, and yet the drawing down is drawn into *Malchus* in a way that relates to *Malchus* itself.

8) More deeply, it can be said that the advantage of the drawing down through the prayer of Moshe over the drawing down by way of "from above to below" is not only in the manner of the drawing down (that the drawing down through the prayer of Moshe relates more to the "below," as mentioned above), but also in the drawing down itself. The matter is that the reason everything created during the six days of creation requires rectification is because the intent of creation is for the sake of the *avodah* of man; therefore, the world was created in a way that its rectification would be through the *avodah* of man, through which man becomes a partner with the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the work of creation. This is also the reason why the emergence of the worlds from *Malchus* was through the *Tzimtzum* in which the light was removed from the aspect of *Malchus* [as it is written, "You made the heavens, etc.,"—*At* (You) is missing the letter *Hei*, for the fact that *Malchus* became the source to bring the worlds into being ("You made the heavens, etc.") is because the five *Partzufim* were removed from it—*At* is missing the *Hei*. It can be said that the lack that was in *Malchus*, from which the world was created, is the root and cause of the lack of the world, for everything created during the six days of creation requires rectification], so that the filling of the lack of *Malchus* would be through the *avodah* of man. To add: even though the *Tzimtzum* was only in the light that relates to the worlds, in the light of limitation (the root of *Memale*) and also in the light of the unlimited (the root of *Sovev*), [the effect of the *Tzimtzum* in the light of limitation is in the light itself, that a descent and limitation occurred in it, to the point that it became a source to bring the worlds into being, and the effect of the *Tzimtzum* in the light of the unlimited is only that it should not shine in the place of the void.
