This is what is meant by the fact that the Great Circle (the light of the unlimited) was touched by the *Tzimtzum*; the concept of the *Tzimtzum* touching it is that the light should be only there (in the circle) and not revealed outside.]—but in the essence of the light, the *Tzimtzum* did not touch at all, meaning that the *Tzimtzum* did not touch it [which is why, from the perspective of this light, it is possible for there to be revelation even in the worlds]. Nevertheless, since the intent of all revelations (even the revelation of the essence of the light that is higher than the category of worlds, higher even than (the root of) *Sovev Kol Almin*) is for the sake of Yisrael, therefore, the drawing down of this light is also through the *avodah* of man.

9) Based on this, one can explain what is written in the *maamar* that in the higher revelations there are three general levels: *Memale Kol Almin*, *Sovev Kol Almin*, and the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than *Memale* and *Sovev*. These three levels correspond to the three loves in the verse "And you shall love... with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might." The love of "with all your heart" is the aspect of *Memale Kol Almin*, for since the vitality of the aspect of *Memale* is clothed within the created beings in their internality, therefore, through contemplation, this vitality is felt even in the animal soul, and the love is "with all your heart"—with both your inclinations. The love of "with all your soul" is the aspect of *Sovev*, for since the light of *Sovev* is higher than being clothed in the worlds, therefore, through feeling the wonder of the *Ohr Ein Sof* (*Sovev*), his love for Hashem is in a manner of *mesiras nefesh* ["with all your soul"—even if He takes your soul], that he wants to exit his existence and be included in the *Ohr Ein Sof*. This love is only in the Divine soul, for the apprehension [in a manner of recognition and feeling, which is when apprehension specifically leads to love] of the wonder of the *Ohr Ein Sof* can only be in the Divine soul, whose root is in the Name *Havayah*, *Sovev*. The love of "with all your might" is in the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher even than *Sovev*, for the true unlimited is in the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* (unlike the light of *Sovev*, which has some form and limitation). Therefore, the love through the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* is "with all your might"—without limit. After explaining the connection of the three loves to the three levels mentioned above, it concludes that from this, the concept of the three levels is understood: *Memale* is clothed in the worlds, *Sovev* is higher than being clothed but relates to the worlds, and the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* is not in the category of worlds.

One must understand: seemingly, the explanation of the connection of the three loves to the three higher levels is *after* understanding the concepts of the three levels, yet the continuation of the matters in the *maamar* implies that this concept [that these three levels are the three loves] adds explanation to the three levels. One of the explanations for this is that the reason there are three levels above in which all revelations are included is because all the higher revelations are for the sake of the *avodah* of man. Since in the love of Hashem [which is the essence of *avodah*, for "there is no service like the service of love"] there are three loves—with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might—therefore, the totality of all the higher revelations is divided into three levels (*Memale*, *Sovev*, and *Ohr Ein Sof* higher than *Sovev*) corresponding to the three loves mentioned above. Since the understanding of a concept in its entirety is through explaining it from its foundation and root, therefore, the beginning of the explanation (in the *maamar*) of the three higher levels is how the three loves are within them, for this is the root and cause for the drawing down of the three levels.

10) It can be said that the reason in the internality of the matters for why the drawing down and revelation of the three aspects—*Memale*, *Sovev*, and the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof*—is through the three loves of "with all your heart," "with all your soul," and "with all your might" is because the intent of all revelations is so that through them there will subsequently be the creation of the world. Therefore, just as the creation of the world was in a manner that *all* matters within it would be rectified through the *avodah* of man, so that through this man would be a partner with the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the work of creation, so too is it regarding the higher revelations: their emergence (their drawing down) was in a manner that their revelation would be through the *avodah* of man, so that the partnership of man with the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the work of creation would be not only in the world itself, but also in the higher revelations through which the creation of the world occurred. Since the essence of the *avodah* of man is the love of Hashem—"there is no service like the service of love" (as mentioned above)—therefore, the revelation of the three levels mentioned above (in which all higher matters are included) is through the three loves of "with all your heart," "with all your soul," and "with all your might." Through the fact that the higher matters are drawn down and revealed through the *avodah* of man, an elevation is effected in them above their state as they are from their own perspective.

This is the "prayer of Moshe": the drawing down of the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* higher than *Sovev* that Moshe drew into *Malchus* was specifically through prayer. Even though, since Moshe is *Da’as Elyon* who receives from *Atik* (the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* higher than *Sovev*), he had the ability to draw this light into *Malchus* by way of "from above to below," because the drawing down of the light is through prayer—the *avodah* of man (by way of "from below to above")—the intent for which the light was emanated is fulfilled, and through this, an elevation is effected in it, and its unlimited nature is increased. The unlimited nature within it is not only as it is from its own perspective—the essence of the light in which *Tzimtzum* and removal are not applicable—but (also) as it is from the perspective of the *Atzmus* (the Essence). Therefore, the structure of *Malchus* that is created through the light as it is drawn down through the prayer of Moshe is an everlasting structure.

11) One must clarify: the elevation effected in the higher revelations through the *avodah* of man is (primarily) *when their drawing down and revelation* is through the *avodah* of man. Since the fact that the drawing down and revelation occurred through the prayer of Moshe is only regarding *Knesses Yisrael* (*Knesses Yisrael* as it is, and also the *Sefirah* of *Malchus*), but regarding Moshe, it seemingly cannot be said that the drawing down and revelation was through his prayer, for Moshe is "rich," and the concept of a rich man is that all revelations shine within him in revelation, even the revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is higher than any relation to the worlds. Accordingly, the elevation and addition effected in the light through the prayer of Moshe is seemingly only regarding others and not regarding Moshe himself. The explanation for this is that since Moshe is the shepherd of Yisrael, therefore, when something is lacking in *Knesses Yisrael*, it is as if the matter is lacking in him as well. In addition to the fact that his pain over the fact that Yisrael was lacking was extremely great, as if he himself were the one lacking, the lack of Yisrael was also his own lack. For Moshe and Yisrael are one, and in the words of Rashi, Moshe is Yisrael and Yisrael is Moshe. Therefore, even though Moshe was rich and all revelations shone within him, nevertheless, since Yisrael were lacking the revelation, and only through *avodah* (the prayer of Moshe) was the revelation renewed for them—the revelation was also renewed for Moshe through his prayer. [To add: the fact that Moshe is the shepherd of Yisrael is his primary essence. All his superiorities, including the fact that he was rich even in spirituality, the aspect of *Da’as Elyon* that receives from *Atik*, are secondary, an aspect of externality, relative to the fact that he was the shepherd of Yisrael. Based on this, it is more understandable that the revelation

## 13 Tammuz 5729

A prayer of Moshe, the man of G-d, etc. The Rebbe Rayatz explains in his well-known sicha that this psalm pertains to the redemption of 19 Kislev. [As is known, the Alter Rebbe would recite a daily portion of Tehillim according to the days of the month, and since the psalm "A prayer of Moshe" is the beginning of the daily portion for the 19th of the month, he recited this psalm on the day of his redemption, 19 Kislev.] The sicha continues, stating that David, King of Israel, had a tradition that this psalm was composed by Moshe, as the Midrash states: "Moshe recited eleven psalms, corresponding to the eleven tribes." The sicha further notes that the psalm begins with "Hashem, You have been a *maon* (dwelling place)..." and concludes with "And may the *noam* (pleasantness) of Hashem... be upon us." *Maon* and *noam* consist of the same letters. We must understand the connection between these three points: the psalm’s relevance to the redemption of 19 Kislev, the fact that Moshe composed it, and the connection between *maon* and *noam*. Furthermore, we must understand why the sicha cites the Midrash as proof that Moshe composed it, when the psalm itself states that it is a prayer of Moshe.

2. This can be explained based on the well-known principle that the redemption of 19 Kislev initiated the process of "your wellsprings shall spread outward," which serves as the preparation and vessel for the coming of Moshiach. Accordingly, the connection of this psalm to the redemption of 19 Kislev indicates (also) its connection to the future redemption. This is why, after stating that this psalm belongs to the redemption of 19 Kislev, the sicha continues by saying that Moshe composed it, for Moshe is the first redeemer and he is the final redeemer. [It emphasizes that *David, King of Israel* had a tradition that Moshe composed it, hinting that the aspect of Moshe relevant here is that Moshe redeemed Israel from the exile of Egypt, as the redemption from Egypt is the prelude to the future redemption by David, King Moshiach: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders."] It cites the Midrash that Moshe recited eleven psalms, for in the number eleven there are two concepts: One, which is before (and above) ten, is the Ohr Ein Sof that transcends the ten Sefiros—"You are *One* and not in a calculation"—and the *ten* represents the drawing down of that "One" into the ten, into all the ten Sefiros, down to the Sefirah of Malchus. On the contrary, the primary drawing down of the aspect of "One and not in a calculation" is in Malchus, for the root of Malchus is in the inwardness of Keter. All the Sefiros have their root in the externality of Keter, which is counted among the ten Sefiros, whereas the root of Malchus is in the inwardness of Keter, which is not counted among the ten Sefiros—"One and not in a calculation." However, in revelation, Malchus is below all the Sefiros, having descended to become the source for the creation of the worlds of Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah, down to this physical world. In the future, the root of Malchus ("One and not in a calculation") will be revealed within Malchus [especially as it has descended into Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah], and through this—in the worlds of Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah, down to this physical world. On the contrary, the primary revelation will be in this physical world, and through this, the intent of "a dwelling place in the lower realms" will be completed, that this lowest world, below which there is no lower, will be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed—for His very Essence.

Accordingly, we can explain why the sicha cites the Midrash "Moshe recited eleven psalms," for this hints at the connection of the psalm "A prayer of Moshe" to the future redemption, as the theme of this psalm [which is the head and beginning of the eleven psalms] is the drawing down of the "One" (One and not in a calculation) into the "ten" (into all the ten Sefiros, down to Malchus). Based on this, we can explain why the sicha continues that *maon* is the same letters as *noam*. It is explained in the discourses on "A prayer of Moshe" that *maon* is Malchus [called *maon*, from the term for a dwelling or house, similar to "his house—this is his wife"] and *noam* (delight/taanug) is Atik, and *maon* being the letters of *noam* indicates that the root of Malchus is in Atik. It can be said that the reason the sicha brings the concept of *maon* being the letters of *noam* in continuation of the concept of "eleven" is to hint that the revelation of the "One" (One and not in a calculation) into the "ten" (the ten Sefiros) will be primarily in Malchus, because the root of Malchus is in Atik.

3. The matter can be understood more specifically based on what the Rebbe (Rashab) explained in the discourse "Zeh": The Zohar states that "A prayer of Moshe" is the prayer of a rich man. This is the difference between the prayer of David and the prayer of Moshe: the prayer of David is the prayer of a poor man, and the prayer of Moshe is the prayer of a rich man. The discourse asks: The essence of prayer is that one prays to Hashem to fill his lack; since a rich man lacks nothing, what is the nature of a rich man's prayer? This requires even more explanation based on what our Sages said regarding the verse "sufficient for his need, which he lacks"—"sufficient for his need" means you are not commanded to make him rich, but "which he lacks" includes even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him. This implies that the concept of wealth is not only that he lacks nothing (even a horse to ride and a servant to run before him), but that he is endowed with an abundance of bounty. Based on this, we must understand even more: what is the nature of a rich man's prayer? It is explained in many places, and in the aforementioned discourse, that the prayer of a rich man is not for himself. As the Midrash says regarding "A prayer of Moshe": It is like three who came to take from the King... the third came, and the King asked him, "What do you request?" He replied, "I do not request anything for myself, but such-and-such a province is desolate and it is yours; decree that it be rebuilt." Thus, Moshe did not request for himself, but for Israel. Seemingly, this explanation requires further clarification. Since prayer is "service of the heart," it is understood that even when one prays for others, his prayer is such that their lack touches his own heart (the heart of the person praying) as if he himself were the one lacking (and the more their lack touches him, the greater his prayer is). Thus, even prayer for others is from the perspective that he is lacking; why then is it called the prayer of a rich man?

The point of the explanation is that the concept of wealth is not just that he has enough for his needs in an expansive way, and even more than his needs, but that he is rich in essence. The matter is that "rich" and "poor" refer to "giver" and "receiver." From this it is understood that even if one has abundant bounty, if the bounty he has is not his own but received from others, he is a poor man, a receiver. The concept of a rich man is that *from his own perspective* he has everything. [This can be connected to the saying of our Sages: "There is no poor man except in *Daas*, and no rich man except in *Daas*." For *Daas* is recognition and feeling, and the advantage that recognition and feeling have over intellect and comprehension (Chochma and Binah) is that when a person understands something, it is not that he *himself* knows the thing; he only receives the knowledge from the intellect that bestowed this knowledge upon him. The concept of recognition and feeling is that he himself recognizes and feels the thing. This is why the concept of poverty and wealth is primarily in *Daas*. Since the knowledge that comes from intellect and understanding is like acquired knowledge, but he *himself* does not know, therefore, even after he has intellect and understanding, he remains poor (lacking). It is specifically through *Daas* that he emerges from his poverty and becomes rich. It is known that the concept of strength is in *Daas*. When a person decides to do something because he recognizes and feels that it must be done, the decision is with much greater strength than a decision that comes from understanding and comprehension. The reason for this is that comprehension is via a process of debate, which leaves room for a contrary comprehension. Therefore, a decision from comprehension is not so strong. Recognition and feeling are in the essence of the logic; in the essence of the logic, there is no room for a contrary logic, and therefore the decision from recognition does not change. Accordingly, it can be said that the fact that Chochma and Binah themselves (without *Daas*) are a state of poverty is not only regarding the person [for the knowledge from Chochma and Binah is something added to the person, and the person himself is lacking the knowledge—poor], but also regarding the intellect and comprehension themselves, since in the comprehension of Chochma and Binah there is room for a contrary comprehension.] Since he is rich in essence, it is understood that no lack is applicable to him. Therefore, even though the lack of those for whom he prayed touches him deeply, and the prayer he offers for them is as if he himself were the one lacking, nevertheless, no lack is created in him, and his prayer is the prayer of a rich man.

4. This can be understood by prefacing that the concept of wealth in simple terms is, as mentioned above (Section 3) from the discourse, that a rich man has not only sufficient for his needs, but is endowed with an abundance of bounty. Accordingly, the difference between a poor man—even when he has sufficient for his needs—and a rich man is in two matters. Even in those things that the poor man also has, it is not comparable to the rich man. The poor man, from his own perspective, lacks even these things (as mentioned there), and it is only *in practice* that he has them. And the rich man is endowed with an abundance of bounty—an abundance of bounty that the poor man does not have at all. Seemingly, one must say that in spirituality, the two matters are dependent on one another. For the things he requires (sufficient for his needs) to be his not in a way that he receives them from others, but from his own perspective, is specifically through the abundance of bounty that is above the filling of the lack. The matter in *avodah* is that when a person's *avodah* is only according to his intellectual comprehension, then, in addition to the fact that the *avodah* is in measurement and limitation (sufficient for his needs), he lacks (inwardly) even this *avodah*, since from the perspective of comprehension, there is room for the opposite. In order for his *avodah* to Hashem to be in a way that leaves no room for the opposite, it is specifically through the *avodah* that is above measurement and limitation—wealth.

To explain the concept of wealth that is above the filling of the lack, the discourse prefaces that even in the filling of the lack there are two matters, as it says, "sufficient for his need, which he lacks," and our Sages said, "which he lacks—even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him." This means that "sufficient for his need" is that one must provide him with all the things necessary for everyone, and afterwards it adds "which he lacks," that one must also provide him with that which *he* lacks (a horse to ride and a servant to run before him) because it is his custom. And wealth is an abundance of bounty, even above that which he lacks. It explains that these three matters [the two matters in the filling of the lack, and wealth] exist also Above [as is known, that all matters below are drawn down from their counterparts Above]. The matter is that in the revelations Above there are three general levels: *Memale Kol Almin* (Filling all worlds), *Sovev Kol Almin* (Surrounding all worlds), and the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above *Memale* and *Sovev*. *Memale* is the light that is enclothed in the worlds and in the created beings to vivify them according to their capacity. As our Sages said, "Just as the soul fills the body, so the Holy One, blessed be He, fills the world," for just as the vitality of the soul enclothed in the body is according to the nature of the body's limbs—in every limb the vitality is according to its capacity—so too is it with the vitality of *Memale Kol Almin*, which vivifies every world and every created being according to its capacity. *Sovev* is the light that is above enclothement in the worlds, and therefore it surrounds and encompasses the worlds equally, but it relates to the worlds (which is why it is called *Sovev Kol Almin*). This is similar to the vitality of the soul itself, that the soul is alive in essence; although it is incomparably above the vitality that spreads and enclothes in the body, nevertheless it is like a source from which the vitality that spreads and enclothes in the body is drawn. This level is called *Chai Olamin* (Living of worlds). The difference between *Chai* (with a *patach*) and *Chei* (with a *tzeirei*) is that in *Chei Olamin* (with a *tzeirei*), the word *Chei* is attached to *Olamin*, meaning the vitality of the worlds—*Memale*; and in *Chai Olamin* (with a *patach*), the word *Chai* is not attached to *Olamin*, meaning the level of "alive in essence"—*Sovev*. It can be said that the reason the level of "alive in essence" (*Sovev*) is also called *Chai Olamin* is because it is like a source from which the vitality of the worlds is drawn. The discourse adds that the level of *Sovev* is also called *Chayei HaChayim* (Life of Life). For *Chayim* is the vitality that spreads and enclothes in the worlds (*Memale*), and the level of *Sovev* from which the vitality of the worlds is drawn is called *Chayei HaChayim*. This is what our Sages said, "The Vivifier of Life will give you life," for the Vivifier of Life (the level of *Chayei HaChayim*) is the source from which life is drawn.

This is what our Sages said regarding the verse "A psalm, a song for the Shabbos day"—a psalm, a song for the future to come, for the day that is entirely Shabbos and rest for the *Chai HaOlamin*. *Chai HaOlamin* (with a *patach*) is the level of *Sovev*, and in the future there will be cessation and rest even from the level of *Chai HaOlamin*, for then there will be a revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above relation to the worlds (above even *Sovev*). As it says, "He will vivify us after two days; on the third day He will raise us up and we will live before Him." It is stated in Likutei Torah that the "two days" are the two revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev*, and the "third day" is the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above relation to the worlds. This is "on the third day He will raise us up and we will live *before Him*"—the inwardness and essence of the Ein Sof. [It should be noted that the simple interpretation of "two days" and "third day" is that they are three times. The two days are this world and Gan Eden, or this world and the days of Moshiach, and the third day is the resurrection of the dead. The connection between the two interpretations is that in the two times of the "two days" are the revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev*, and in the resurrection of the dead there will be the revelation of the Essence.]

The three matters mentioned above—the two matters in the filling of the lack (sufficient for his need and which he lacks) and wealth—in the revelations Above are in the three levels mentioned. The two matters of filling the lack are the two revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev*. Since even the light of *Sovev* relates to the worlds, therefore, when this light is not revealed in the world, the world is lacking. As our Sages said regarding the verse "And G-d finished on the seventh day": "What was the world lacking? Rest. Shabbos came, rest came." Rest is the level of *Sovev* that is above the light enclothed in the world, and nevertheless, when this revelation was not in the world, the world was lacking, and when Shabbos came and this light was drawn down and revealed, the lack was filled. Therefore, even the revelation of *Sovev* is a filling of the lack. However, the filling of the lack through the revelation of *Memale* is like "sufficient for his need," and the filling of the lack through the revelation of *Sovev* is like "which he lacks—even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him." And wealth is the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above relation to the worlds.

5. Now, the difference between "sufficient for his need" and "which he lacks" (regarding a poor man in the simple sense) is not only that the bounty of "which he lacks" is a greater bounty (even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him), but also that the matter of "which he lacks" is specifically for one whose custom it is. According to the principle that all matters in the Torah are with utmost precision, we must say that the analogy of the two revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev* to the two matters of "sufficient for his need" and "which he lacks" is not only because the revelation of *Sovev* is a more sublime revelation, but also because the matter of filling the lack through the revelation of *Sovev* is specifically for one whose custom it is. The explanation for this can be said based on what is written in the discourse, that the three levels in love—"with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might"—are in the three levels mentioned. The love of "with all your heart" is in the level of *Memale*. By contemplating that the vitality of everything is G-dliness, one will come to love Hashem "with all your heart," with both your inclinations. Since the vitality of the level of *Memale* is enclothed in the created beings in their inwardness, therefore, through contemplation, this vitality is felt even in the animal soul. And the love of "with all your soul" is in the level of *Sovev*. By contemplating that the G-dly vitality enclothed in the worlds is merely a radiation that is incomparable to the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof (*Sovev*), one feels the wonder of the Ein Sof, and through this he will come to the love of "with all your soul," that his love for Havayah is in a way of self-sacrifice (even if He takes your soul), for he wants to exit his existence and be included in the Ein Sof. This love is only in the G-dly soul. There are two reasons for this. Because the comprehension [in a way of recognition and feeling, for then specifically does comprehension lead to love] of the wonder of the Ein Sof can only be in the G-dly soul, whose root is in the name Havayah, *Sovev*. This is not so for created beings, for since their root is from the name Elokim, *Memale*, it is impossible for them [even for angels, and certainly for the animal soul] to have the comprehension (in a way of recognition and feeling) of Havayah, *Sovev*. Also, because the animal soul's essence is existence, and the love of "with all your soul" is that he wants to *exit* his existence and be included in the Ein Sof, which is the opposite of the concept of existence. For the love of "with all your heart," which comes through contemplation and recognition that the vitality of everything is G-dliness, relates *to the existence* of the person who loves. [Just as a person loves himself, meaning he loves the vitality and wants the vitality to spread within him, so too, when he understands and feels that the main thing is the G-dly vitality, he wants G-dliness.] Therefore, this love relates also to the animal soul. This is not so for the love of "with all your soul," which is the desire to exit his existence and be included in the Ein Sof; it is only in the G-dly soul. Since its root is in the name Havayah (*Sovev*), and even after it descended below it is a part of the name Havayah, as it says, "For the portion of Havayah is His people," therefore it has the desire to exit its existence and be included in its root, *Sovev*. And according to the principle that the descent of the soul below is a descent for the sake of an ascent—meaning that through its descent below it will ascend to a more sublime level than it was before its descent—it is understood that the intent in the descent of the soul below is that it will ascend above its root, and this is the love of "with all your might," the self-sacrifice and annihilation in the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above even *Sovev*. Accordingly, it can be said that the fact that the filling of the lack through the revelation of *Sovev* is like "which he lacks" for one whose custom it was, is because the souls were accustomed (before their descent below) to the revelation of *Sovev*.

6. It must be understood that according to the above explanation, the fact that the revelation of *Sovev* is generally a filling of the lack is specifically regarding souls, whereas regarding created beings, seemingly, one cannot say that the revelation of *Sovev* is a filling of the lack, since it is not their custom. From the fact that the discourse cites what our Sages said, "What was the *world* lacking? Rest, etc.," it is understood that when the revelation of *Sovev* (rest) is absent, it is a lack also in the world. It can be said that since the primary intent in the descent of the soul below is (not for the ascent of the soul, but) in order to rectify [and elevate] the world, therefore, through the love of "with all your soul" of the souls as they have descended below into the world, the world is elevated to a more sublime level than it is from its own perspective, such that it becomes related to the level of *Sovev* (*similar* to the relation of souls to *Sovev*), to the point that when the revelation of *Sovev* does not shine, the world is lacking.

7. We should add an explanation to this, based on what is written in the discourse that the two matters of *Sovev* and *Memale* are the two names Havayah and Elokim. As explained in many places, the name Elokim is not only the shield and sheath that conceals and hides the light of the name Havayah, but even the light of the name Havayah as it is drawn down and contracted through the name Elokim to be a source for created beings, which generally is the light of *Memale*, is called Elokim. Based on what is written in Tanya that the creation of the world is from the name Havayah (Havayah means "bringing into being"), but if the creation were from the name Havayah itself, the world would be nullified in existence, and therefore the actual creation was through the name Elokim, one can say that similarly it is also regarding the matter of *Sovev* and *Memale*, that the primary vitality of the world is from the light of *Sovev* (Havayah), but in order for the world to be limited, the drawing down of vitality into the world is through *Memale* (Elokim). There are two matters in this. The essence of the world's vitality is from *Sovev*, but if the vitality were drawn into it from *Sovev* itself, the world would not be limited (so much) and all created beings would be equal [similar to what is explained in Tanya, that if the creation of the world were from the name Havayah itself, there would not be the division of time and place], and through the vitality (that is from *Sovev*) being drawn through *Memale* (which enclothes in every created being according to its capacity), division is created in them. Another matter in this is that even the vitality of the world (which is in limitation and division) that is drawn from the light of *Memale* is (not from its own perspective, but) from the perspective of *Sovev*.

The matter is that it is explained in the discourse (cited above in Section 4) that *Memale* is like the vitality of the soul spreading in the body, and *Sovev* is like the vitality of the soul itself, alive in essence. According to what is explained elsewhere that the fact that the vitality spreading from the soul vivifies the body is because it is attached to the soul itself, which is alive in essence [for the level of the spreading of vitality (from its own perspective) does not have the power to vivify anything, and the fact that the vitality spreading from the soul vivifies the body is because it is attached to the soul, which is alive in essence], it can be said that similarly it is regarding the matter of *Memale* and *Sovev*, that the power in the light of *Memale* (the spreading of vitality) to vivify the created beings is (not from its own perspective, but) because it is attached to *Sovev*, alive in essence. [Accordingly, one can explain what is written in the discourse (cited above in Section 4) that the level of *Sovev* is called *Chayei HaChayim* or *Chai Olamin* (with a *patach*), for it can be said that the two names *Chayei HaChayim* and *Chai Olamin* point to two matters. That it is called *Chayei HaChayim* is because from it is drawn the *vitality of Memale*, and that it is called *Chai Olamin* is because from it is drawn the power in the vitality of *Memale* to vivify the *worlds*.] We should add that the fact that in the vitality spreading to vivify the body the matter of "alive in essence" is revealed (in that it has the power to vivify the body), even though the essence is above spreading, is because the matter of "alive in essence" is (also) the essence of the spreading vitality. [Accordingly, one can say the intent in *Sovev* being called *Chayei HaChayim* is that the vitality (the essence and the substance) of the life (*Memale*) is *Sovev*.] It can be said that through the two matters in the vitality enclothed in the world—that in revelation it is limited vitality, and in inwardness it is unlimited (which is why it has the power to bring created beings into being, as mentioned)—there are counterparts to these two matters in the world. In the externality, the vitality that the world requires is only limited and small vitality [and the revelation of *Sovev* is generally wealth]. In the inwardness of the world, the inwardness of the vitality within it is felt, for the fact that it has the power to vivify is because it is attached to the level of "alive in essence." And through the level of "with all your soul" of the souls, the inwardness of the world is revealed. And through this, also the *world* lacks the revelation of *Sovev*, and through the revelation of *Sovev*, the lack of the world is filled.

8. Similarly, it is regarding the matter of wealth, the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above *Sovev*, that through the revelation of this matter in the souls of Israel, there will be in the future *a semblance* of this revelation also in the world. Accordingly, we can explain what is written in the discourse in explanation of the Midrash that Moshe's prayer was not for himself but for Israel, that the Congregation of Israel is the level of Malchus, and Moshe's request (the prayer of a rich man) for the Congregation of Israel was that the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof (wealth) be drawn down into Malchus. [Accordingly, it explains there what is written in the Midrash that Moshe's request for Israel is like the request, "Such-and-such a province, etc., decree that it be rebuilt," for a province is Malchus, and the request "decree that it be rebuilt" is that the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof be drawn down into Malchus, through which it will be built in a way of an eternal building.] This requires explanation, for Moshe's request for Israel was for Israel in the simple sense, as explained in the Midrash, and the discourse explains that Moshe's request for the Congregation of Israel is for Malchus. It can be said that through the drawing down of the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof into Israel, through this, this revelation will be in Malchus, the root of the world, and through this—in the world. To add, just as we explained above (Section 7) regarding the matter of the revelation of *Sovev* that is drawn into the world through Israel, that this is through revealing the inwardness of the vitality of the world, similarly it is regarding the revelation of the Ein Sof that is above *Sovev* that is drawn down by Israel into the world, for this is through revealing the inwardness and root of Malchus. As explained in the discourse in interpretation of "Such-and-such a province is yours," that the root of Malchus is in the Essence.

It can be said that the reason it cites in the discourse (cited above in Section 4) what is written, "He will vivify us after two days; on the third day, etc.," and explains that the two days are the two revelations of *Memale* and *Sovev* and the third day is the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof, and these three revelations are revealed in three times, is to hint that even though time is one of the parameters of the world and the vitality of the world (enclothed in it in its inwardness) is *Memale*, nevertheless, the world also relates to *Sovev* and also to the Ein Sof that is above *Sovev*. To note, similarly it is regarding place [for the parameter of the world is place and time], for the matter of place in the world is that it has levels of higher and lower, for even though the division of higher and lower in the world is from the division in the vitality enclothed in it, *Memale* [as our Sages said, "He stretched out His right hand and created the heavens, He stretched out His left hand and created the earth," for heavens (the upper worlds) are from the aspect of right, and earth (the lower worlds) are from the aspect of left, and the division of right and left is in the vitality of the aspect of *Memale*], nevertheless, the totality of all the worlds is divided into the three worlds of Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah, which are *analogous* to the three revelations mentioned. As explained in many places, matter (Beriah), the essence of existence that is above form and revelation, is analogous to the essential concealment of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof, and form (Yetzirah), the revelation of matter, is analogous to *Sovev*, which is the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof, and rectification (Asiyah), specific design, is analogous to *Memale*, which enclothes in every world and every created being according to its capacity. This is also what is written in the discourse in interpretation of the blessing "Creator of souls," that "their lack" (in the plural) are the two matters of filling the lack that are from *Memale* and *Sovev*, and "for all that You have created to vivify with them," which the Tur explains are things that come for refinement and pleasure, is the abundance of bounty of wealth that is from the revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof. It can be said that the reason it cites this interpretation in the discourse is to hint that even in the world of Asiyah (including this physical world) there are these three matters.

However, the G-dly vitality enclothed in the world (*Memale*) is in revelation in the world, and the fact that even this revelation of vitality is through the *avodah* of Israel [as explained in the discourse "This is the statute of the Torah," that the revelation of the three matters of *Memale*, *Sovev*, and the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof is through the three loves of "with all your heart," "with all your soul," and "with all your might"] is because the fact that the vitality of *Memale* is in revelation in the world means that in the world it is felt that it is alive, but it is not felt in it that the vitality within it is G-dliness, and through the *avodah* of Israel, it is felt in the world that the vitality within it is G-dliness. This revelation is also now, in this world. And the vitality of *Sovev* that is not enclothed in the world but only surrounds and encompasses it, and certainly the Ein Sof that is above *Sovev*—their *drawing down* into the world is through the *avodah* of Israel, and the revelation of these drawings down will be in the future, in the days of Moshiach (revelation of *Sovev*) and the resurrection of the dead (revelation of the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above *Sovev*), as mentioned above (Section 4).

9. The discourse explains that the fact that Moshe is called rich [and as mentioned above in Section 3, that the prayer of Moshe is the prayer of a rich man] is because Moshe is the level of *Daas Elyon* (Higher *Daas*). The matter is that *Daas Tachton* (Lower *Daas*) receives from the externality of Keter, *Arich*, and *Daas Elyon* receives from the inwardness of Keter, *Atik*. The difference between *Arich* and *Atik* is that *Arich* is the root and source of the emanated beings, the aspect of *Sovev* [as mentioned above in Section 4, that *Sovev* is like a source for the worlds], and *Atik* is the lowest level in the Emanator, the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above the parameter of worlds. Since the revelation of *Sovev* (*Arich*) is generally a filling of the lack, and the matter of wealth is specifically in the Essence of the Ohr Ein Sof that is above *Sovev* (*Atik*), therefore, also in *Daas*, the matter of wealth is specifically in *Daas Elyon* that receives from the inwardness of Keter.

According to what was explained above in Section 4, that the negation of poverty (lack) is specifically through the wealth that is above the filling of the lack, whereas when the bounty is only "sufficient for his need" [including also the matter of "which he lacks," even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him], a lack remains (inwardly) also regarding the limited bounty, one must say that even when the *avodah* is from the perspective of *Daas*, recognition and feeling, but only *Daas Tachton* that receives from *Arich*, the *avodah* is like something added to him, and the person *himself* (in his inwardness) lacks the *avodah*, meaning that there remains a place in the person where the revelation of G-dliness does not shine. For even though the matter of recognition and feeling (even of *Daas Tachton*) is that the person *himself* recognizes and feels (as mentioned in Section 3), nevertheless, since the person's

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Chukas-Balak, 12 Tammuz, 5736

### With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Chukas-Balak, 12 Tammuz, 5736

"You have given those who fear You a banner to be displayed because of the truth, Selah." The Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Baal HaGeulah and the Baal HaSimcha, brings in his maamar (d.h. Zeh) the interpretation of the Targum Yonasan: "You have given to those who fear You a *nissa* (from the word *nissayon* — trial) to be tested, because of the *kushta* (truth) of Avraham forever." Now, this verse was said by Dovid, the sweet singer of Yisroel, in the name of every single Jew. From this it is understood that all the details in this verse exist also within every single Jew. And as is also understood from the Targum’s interpretation that "because of the truth, Selah" refers to the *kushta* of Avraham, and it is known that the aspect of the *Avos* exists within everyone, for we only call the three of them *Avos*—the "head of the rocks," etc.—and especially Avraham, who is the head of the *Avos*. From this it is understood that the verse "You have given to those who fear You," etc. (the reason for which is "because of the truth, Selah") also refers to every single Jew, just as it is written: "And now, Yisroel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear," etc., for in relation to the aspect of Moshe within every person, fear is a "small matter." It can be said that this is why every Jew—even one who is called by the name Yisroel—is called "those who fear You." And this is what is meant by "You have given to those who fear You a banner to be displayed because of the truth, Selah": that the Ribono shel Olam gives every Jew a *nissa* to be tested (from the word *nissayon*), because within everyone there exists the *kushta* of Avraham.

2) The maamar continues, and it is known that Avraham Avinu opened the channel of *mesiras nefesh*. It can be said that this explains the reason why the *avodah* of trials is connected specifically with the *kushta* of Avraham. For on the face of it, the primary *avodah* of Avraham was not in the matter of "those who fear You"—the *avodah* of fear—but rather in love, as it is written: "Avraham, My lover." Regarding this, it explains that Avraham Avinu opened the channel of *mesiras nefesh*, for the *avodah* of trials is specifically through *mesiras nefesh*, because *mesiras nefesh* is the perfection of the matter of fear and *bitul*. And this is what is said after the trial of the *Akeidah*: "Now I know that you are a G-d-fearing man." Now, the fact that the *avodah* of trials is specifically through *mesiras nefesh* refers to a lofty level within it. For the general *avodah* in *mitzvos* must be founded upon the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh*, as it is brought in *Tanya*—the reason why Moshe Rabbeinu commanded the generation that entered the land to recite *Krias Shema*, etc., is because the fulfillment of *mitzvos* depends on remembering the matter of *mesiras nefesh*, etc. Likewise, the general engagement in *mitzvos* and *tefillah* for the *neshamah* is a matter of *mesiras nefesh*, since it does not contemplate the needs of the body, etc. But nevertheless, his *avodah* in the open is not a matter of *mesiras nefesh*, but rather the *avodah* of *mitzvos*, in that he fulfills the positive *mitzvos* in all their details and is careful with the negative *mitzvos* in all their details. From this it is understood that this is not the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh* as it is in itself, but rather as it is connected with the *avodah* of *mitzvos* and clothed within it, which is *avodah* according to intellect and emotion. It can be said that within the powers of the soul, this is the *avodah* from the perspective of the *makif* that is close and belongs to the *pnim* and is clothed within it, similar to the power of will that is clothed in *Chochma*, and through it in the general power of intellect and *midos*, the internal powers of man. This is not the case with the *avodah* of trials, which is through the *avodah* of *mesiras nefesh* itself; what is drawn down from this into the *avodah* of the ten powers of the soul is like a secondary effect and result of its primary essence, which is the matter of *mesiras nefesh*. It can be said that within the powers of the soul, this is the aspect of the *makif* that is far, the aspect of *yechidah* in the soul. Based on this, one can connect the two interpretations of the verse "You have given," etc., "a banner to be displayed": one, the matter of trials as per the Targum Yonasan (as above), and two, the matter of *nissim*, and "a banner to be displayed" is (similar to the language of Chazal) a *nes* within a *nes*, because the *avodah* of trials is from the perspective of the *nes* within a *nes* in the soul, the aspect of *yechidah*.

3) This is also what the maamar continues with, that the beginning of Avraham’s *avodah* was the recognition of *Elokus* from the matters of the world, as it is brought in the *Midrash*: "It is like someone who was passing from place to place and saw a palace on fire. He said, 'Can you say that this palace has no leader?' The owner of the palace looked at him, etc. So too, because our father Avraham said, 'Can you say that this world has no leader?' the Ribono shel Olam looked at him and said to him, 'I am the owner of the world.'" This can be explained: the matter of "I am the owner of the world" that was revealed to Avraham is the matter of the "Creator-spark" clothed within the "created-spark." The created-spark in which the Creator-spark is clothed is the *yechidah* in the soul, as explained in *Etz Chaim*. This recognition of *Elokus* he also publicized throughout the entire world, as it is written: "And he called there in the name of Hashem, G-d of the world." Do not read *vayikra* (he called), but *vayikri* (he caused others to call), that he caused everyone in the world to call out that there is an owner to this palace. As is explained in many places, the precision in the language "G-d of the world" (*E-l Olam*) and not "G-d of the world" (*E-l HaOlam*)—meaning, not that *Elokus* is one thing and the world is another, but that *Elokus* rules and governs the world, rather that the world and *Elokus* are entirely one, for there is nothing else besides Him. This is the connection between Avraham’s recognition of *Elokus* and his *avodah* of trials, because the *avodah* of trials is through *mesiras nefesh* that comes from the *yechidah* in the soul. This is also why the *mesiras nefesh* of Avraham was not like the *mesiras nefesh* of Rabbi Akiva, who said, "When will it come to my hand and I will fulfill it," but rather that his entire matter was to publicize His *Elokus* in the world, and if *mesiras nefesh* was needed for this, he was prepared for it. That is to say, Avraham Avinu had no existence for himself—"I am dust and ashes"—which is the matter of *mesiras nefesh* that comes from the aspect of *yechidah*. And specifically from this *bitul* he came to the greatest strength, to the point that even though "Avraham was one," and the entire world was on one side and he was on the other, nevertheless "he inherited the land," for he publicized His *Elokus* in the entire world, through which they build the world to be a dwelling place for Him in the lower realms.

4) Now, the reason why the *avodah* of trials is specifically through *mesiras nefesh* is explained in the maamar: because in a trial, the Divine spark is hidden and concealed to the greatest degree. It explains by first noting the difference between the *avodah* of *birurim* (refining) and the *avodah* of trials (for although trials are also part of the *avodah* of *birurim* for which the *neshamah* descended below, there is still a difference between them). In the *avodah* of *birurim*, the engagement is with the thing being refined, like physical food, where the spark is in the food being refined and the refinement is through the engagement with it (and so it is also with all the general needs of man, which are called by the name "eating"). This is not the case in a trial, where the manner of its refinement is not through engagement with the thing, but through the person’s engagement with himself. The matter is that the *avodah* of *birurim* is by way of war, "eat bread at the mouth of the sword." This is through the preface of *tefillah*, as it is written, "With my sword and my bow," and the Targum translates, "With my prayer and my supplication." As is explained in many places regarding the *brachos* of *Krias Shema* (which are the preface to *Krias Shema*, "and you shall love," etc., the general matter of *tefillah*), it is contemplation on the root of the animal soul and the *birurim*, etc., through which he refines them, etc. Therefore, it is *avodah* by way of war and clothing oneself in the thing being refined, contemplating its root and thereby refining it. And so it is with the general *avodah* of *mitzvos*, which is through war with the *yetzer hara*, where one must argue and fight with it using all kinds of war tactics, etc., and through contemplation in many ways how to defeat it. This is not the case in the matter of trials; the *avodah* in them is not by elevating them, but by way of rejection and *bitul*. This is similar to the difference within the *mitzvos* themselves between positive and negative *mitzvos*. The positive *mitzvos* are about action and deed, meaning that he engages with the thing through which he fulfills the *mitzvah* (with the matter and in the matter), but the negative *mitzvos* are about "turn from evil," that he turns from the evil and rejects it.

5) Now, although the manner of *avodah* of negative *mitzvos* is through rejection and *bitul*, nevertheless, in this it is equal to the *avodah* of positive *mitzvos*, for both are in the matter of an existence upon which the definition of action and the absence of action applies; it is just that in a positive *mitzvah* he is commanded regarding action, and in a negative *mitzvah* regarding the absence of action. Therefore, the engagement in negative *mitzvos* is also not only with the person himself, but also with the thing being refined. Although the primary *avodah* of negative *mitzvos* is in that he rules and governs his *yetzer* not to eat, etc., which is by way of rejection and *bitul*, nevertheless, since his *avodah* is with a thing that has an existence in physicality and matter, he has a connection—at least by way of negation—to the thing being refined. This is not the case with the *avodah* of trials, which is in a matter (in the language of the maamar) that is not a thing in and of itself, but rather a thing was set up to conceal and prevent. Therefore, the engagement of the person is with himself, to awaken the essential power within him, which is the strength to stand against the trial and not be affected by it at all, to the point that he does not enter into arguments and excuses, but only stands with the strength that "otherwise it is impossible," and he nullifies the trial entirely. Through this strength, it is truly nullified, for the truth of the matter is revealed: that it is a matter that has no existence, and its entire existence is only so that the essence of the person’s soul should be revealed—his internal will that is above clothing in vessels. This is similar to the trial of Avraham in the trial of the *Akeidah* (for the primary opening of the channel of *mesiras nefesh* by Avraham was in the trial of the *Akeidah*), where the primary trial was in the matter of alacrity (*zerizus*). As is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, the *zerizus* of Avraham Avinu stands for us forever, etc. And as Chazal said, that a great river was made before them, etc., but nevertheless Avraham was not affected and went to fulfill the mission of the Ribono shel Olam and descended into the water, etc., and through this the existence of the river was nullified, for through his strength the truth was revealed that the entire existence of the river was only to test him, etc. And likewise afterwards (in the trial of the *Akeidah* itself), when the Ribono shel Olam said to him, "I did not tell you," etc., "bring it up, bring it down." And so too was the conduct of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Baal HaSimcha and the Baal HaGeulah, when he sat in prison (as told in his *reshimos* and *sichos*), that he decided at the outset to be bold and strong without fear and not to take the situation into account at all, etc. And such was his conduct all the days he sat in prison. Through this, not only did this conduct give him the strength to stand against all the difficulties and concealments of the prison (for the concealment was not only on his physical matters, but also on his spiritual matters, as is emphasized that during his time in prison there was no possibility to engage in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and the *maayanos*), but furthermore, through this, the concealment was nullified. For although at first it seemed that they were a strong and great existence (as told in his *reshimos*), through his strength they were nullified from their existence, to the point that he was released in a manner that was open to the eyes of all. Through this, an advantage was also created in the Baal HaSimcha and the Baal HaGeulah himself, similar to what was the case in the matter of 19 Kislev, that through the imprisonment and the redemption, an elevation was created regarding Chassidus, as explained in many places. So too here, that an elevation was created in the Baal HaSimcha and the Baal HaGeulah as mentioned above, that the *avodah* of disseminating Torah was increased with greater intensity than it had been before, to the point that through this he began in practice the matter of dissemination throughout the entire world, and in a manner of "from now and forever." Similar to what is in the Gemara, that when there are three generations engaged in Torah, the Torah does not cease from his seed, because the Torah circles its inn (*achsnia*). So too in our matter, that there are already (as a result of the redemption of 12-13 Tammuz) three generations of those who study Torah and fulfill its *mitzvos*, and even more, those who cherish Torah and its *mitzvos* (through which their fulfillment of *mitzvos* is with *hiddur*). All this is because he stood with the greatest strength above all calculations, through which he nullified the trial in the most lofty manner. And since "the body follows the head," it must be so also in the *avodah* of everyone, that we should walk in the straight path which He taught us, to walk in His ways, to stand with strength so as not to be affected by any obstacles and delays in the *avodah* of Hashem, for since he goes to fulfill his mission in this world, the trial has no existence. "And Hashem your G-d is testing you to know if you love Hashem your G-d," and through strength and *mesiras nefesh*, the trial is nullified.

6) To understand all this in more detail, one must first preface the general matter of the descent of the *neshamah* below, which is a great descent from a high roof to a deep pit. For the *neshamah* before its descent below is pure, and there are several interpretations for this: one, that it refers to the world of *Atzilus*; two, *tehiro tata'ah*; three, *tehiro ila'ah*. And its descent is to the lowest point, not only to the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*—the worlds of separation in general—but to this lowest world, than which there is no lower, where the majority is evil and only a little good is mixed within it, to the point that the deeds of this world are difficult, etc. (as explained in *Tanya* in the name of *Etz Chaim*). And furthermore, that the *avodah* in this world itself is in the lowest of the low, in a place where "you descended to Egypt" and in a manner where "the *yetzer hara* is among you," where one must fight with the *yetzer hara*, and "today he tells him to do this, and tomorrow, etc., serve idols," which is the opposite of "I am" and "you shall have no other gods" (the root of the 248 positive and 365 negative *mitzvos*, as explained in *Tanya*). However, this descent is for the sake of an ascent. For although the *neshamah* did not descend to refine itself, etc., but to refine its body and its animal soul and its portion in the world (as explained in *Etz Chaim* and brought in *Tanya*), nevertheless, through the descent of the *neshamah* below, it is elevated to a level more lofty than it was before its descent, which is above even the *tehiro ila'ah*. And even more, to a level that has no value or connection to the matter of the chain of progression (*hishtalshelus*) and level and ascent, to the point that it is not even appropriate to say that it has an advantage over the chain of progression, but rather in the well-known language: "to be absorbed in the body of the King," in His very essence and being. And in the language of the *Zohar* in another place, in this aspect "they are not found with the King except for Yisroel alone" (which is above even *mitzvos*). And the ascent is through the *avodah* in *mitzvos*, for "I was created to serve my Maker," and as it is written, "He placed him, etc., to work it and to guard it," to work it—these are the 248 positive *mitzvos*; and to guard it—these are the 365 negative *mitzvos* (for wherever it is said "guard," etc., it is only a negative *mitzvah*). And for this there must be the preface of Torah, for "great is study, for it leads to action." And also the defeat of the *yetzer hara* is through Torah, as Chazal said: "I created the *yetzer hara*, and I created for it Torah as a spice," and "if this repulsive one hits you, drag him to the *beis medrash*," etc. And this is what is said: "Turn from evil and do good, seek peace and pursue it," which refers to positive *mitzvos*, negative *mitzvos*, and Torah, as explained in *Likutei Torah* in our *parsha* (Balak).

7) However, one must still understand the reason why specifically through the *avodah* of the *neshamah* below it is elevated to a level more lofty than it was before its descent, to such an ascent that is incomparable to its previous level. The matter is that the sparks in physical things have their root in the world of *Tohu*, which is above the world of *Tikkun*. As it is written: "For man does not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem does man live." The Arizal explains that the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that is in the bread is the Divine spark within it. And although in man there is also the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that gives him life, nevertheless, one needs specifically the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that is in the bread, for "everything that is higher falls lower." Like the parable of the stone found at the top of the wall: when it falls below, it falls further from the wall than the stone falling from the middle of the wall, etc. Therefore, since the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that is in the bread fell lower than the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that is in man (for bread is from the category of *tzomei'ach* [vegetable], and especially when at the time of eating it is no longer *tzomei'ach* but *domeim* [inanimate]—and furthermore, that the eating of bread is with salt, which is *domeim*—and man is *medaber* [speaking]), this itself is proof that the sparks found in the bread have their root higher than the "word that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem" that is in man, even from the "Supernal Man," the aspect of *Tikkun*. Therefore, specifically through them will man live—the man below, and (through this) the Supernal Man, as it were. To note another matter in this: it is explained in another place at length the difference between the world of *Tikkun* and the world of *Tohu*, that both were brought into being by the Supernal Will, but in the world of *Tikkun* it is in a manner of "judgment is pleasing to Me," and in the world of *Tohu* it is in a manner of "judgment is not pleasing to Me." That is to say, in the world of *Tohu* the Supernal Will exists, but it is in concealment and hiding, and in the open it is the matter of the opposite of the will, of "judgment is not pleasing to Me." Therefore, it progresses below that the matters that came into being from the world of *Tohu*, although in the open they are matters of the opposite of holiness, of "judgment is not pleasing to Me," nevertheless, even in them there are sparks of holiness, and on the contrary, specifically in them there is strength, of the lights of *Tohu*. This is what is meant by the fact that through the descent of the *neshamah* below, it is elevated to a level more lofty than it was before its descent; this is from the perspective of the refinement of the sparks of the world of *Tohu*, through which it inherits the lights of *Tohu*, which is the matter of "the heritage of the congregation of Yaakov."

8) Now, according to the rule mentioned above that "everything that is higher falls lower," it must be said that also in the sparks of *Tohu* themselves, the further down it fell, the higher the place from which its root is. From this it is understood that there is an advantage in the refinements through negative *mitzvos* over the refinements of positive *mitzvos*. For although the sparks in physical things through which one fulfills positive *mitzvos* also have their root in the world of *Tohu*, nevertheless, the fall in them is not as great, for they are matters of permission from the side of *nogah*. This is not the case in negative *mitzvos*, which are in matters that are forbidden and connected to the hands of the *chitzonim*; this itself is proof that the root of the sparks clothed within them is higher. Therefore, through the *avodah* of negative *mitzvos*, even at the beginning of the *avodah* where he does not transform the intentional sins into merits but only rejects them, a light is drawn down that is more lofty than in the *avodah* of positive *mitzvos*. As explained in *Likutei Torah*, positive *mitzvos* are connected to *Vav-Hei*, the aspect of "the revealed," and negative *mitzvos* to *Yud-Hei*, the aspect of "the hidden things belong to Hashem" (and also—*Yud-Hei* is a holy name in itself), and the difference between them is an incomparable difference. In general, this is the difference between internal light and surrounding light; positive *mitzvos* draw down internal light, which is light that is clothed in vessels, and negative *mitzvos* draw down surrounding light that the vessel cannot contain. Now, this advantage in negative *mitzvos* over positive *mitzvos* is even when the *avodah* in matters of negative *mitzvos* is only in a manner of rejection. And all the more so when the *avodah* in them is in a manner that transforms intentional sins into merits, for then he draws down a light that is incomparably higher than the light drawn down by negative *mitzvos* in a manner of rejection. And as is understood from this, the matter of "intentional sins are transformed for him into merits" is only through the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, for the regular *avodah* (the daily offerings in their order) in forbidden matters is only by way of rejection. The difference between these two *avodos* is an incomparable difference, as is understood from many places, that the difference between them is as the value of the finite to the infinite. And as it is in the matter of time, for the *avodah* of *teshuvah* is in one hour and one moment, above the measurement of time, whereas regular *avodah* is measured in the continuation and span of time (and by way of consequence, also in place).

9) Now, although the fall of the sparks in negative *mitzvos* is in matters that are forbidden and connected to the hands of the *chitzonim*, nevertheless, they have an existence, which is why the matter of *avodah* is applicable to them, at least by way of negation and rejection, as stated above. Therefore, also the light drawn down by negative *mitzvos*, although it is surrounding light, the aspect of *Yud-Hei* of the Name *Havayah*, nevertheless, even the *Yud-Hei* of the Name *Havayah* are letters of the Name *Havayah*, and letters are matters of revelation (although within the letters themselves there is a difference between the *Vav-Hei* of the Name *Havayah*, which is like internal light, and the *Yud-Hei* of the Name *Havayah*, which is like surrounding light). This is not the case with trials; they are in things that have no existence. For although the matters in which one fulfills negative *mitzvos* are matters of *kelipah*, nevertheless, there is no necessity to say that this is their entire existence against holiness. The proof is that there are many matters that are forbidden only in eating but permitted in benefit (through which it is possible to elevate them to holiness), and even those that one is compelled to benefit from. And so too there are many levels and differences in forbidden matters that do not oppose the will of Hashem in all their matters and in all their details. And furthermore, sometimes even the forbidden thing itself becomes permitted, similar to what Chazal said, that at the time of the conquest of the land (and so too in a war similar to it), even "pig’s neck" was permitted to them, which became blood and flesh of his flesh, and with this power was the conquest of the land (which is why it was permitted, as explained in the books of the commentators), meaning that it assists holiness. This is not the case in trials, whose existence is that a thing was set up to conceal and prevent the *avodah* of Hashem, and were it not for this, it would have no existence, not even in the manner of imagination. And since the fall is to the lowest of the low, in matters whose entire existence is only to oppose the will of Hashem, it is understood that their root is from a more lofty place. Therefore, through the *avodah* of trials, where the descent is to the lowest of the low, through this the person is elevated to an ascent that is far more lofty.

10) Now, all matters of holiness are drawn down specifically through *avodah* (and not in a manner of "bread of shame"), from which it is understood that the elevation in the *avodah* of trials over the *avodah* of positive and negative *mitzvos* is not only from the perspective of the root of the sparks within them, but also from the perspective of the effort and *avodah* of man in this *avodah*. For just as the *avodah* and effort in fulfilling positive *mitzvos* is not like the *avodah* in negative *mitzvos* (for in order to be careful not to transgress negative *mitzvos*, one must make fences, etc., and "sanctify yourself in what is permitted to you"), so too the effort in fulfilling negative *mitzvos* is not like the overcoming and strength and courage that must be in the *avodah* of trials. It can be said that this is what Chazal said regarding the trial of the *Akeidah*, which is the first trial mentioned explicitly in the text, "And G-d tested Avraham," that the Ribono shel Olam said to Avraham, "I have tested you with several trials and you stood in all of them; now stand for Me in this trial so that they will not say there is no substance in the first ones." That is, because in the nine previous trials there was not yet the perfection of the *avodah* and effort of trials, which is why they were not mentioned explicitly in the Written Torah, for in writing and in revelation this is not yet the perfection of the matter of trial. And through the fact that he stood in this trial, this completes and verifies all the *avodah* of Avraham (also his *avodah* from before). This is "because of the truth, Selah," and the Targum Yonasan interprets "because of the *kushta* of Avraham forever," which is the truth that was revealed through the *avodah* of Avraham. This is what is explained in the maamar, that in order to stand in a trial, the *avodah* according to intellect and emotion is not sufficient, and not even *avodah* according to intellect and emotion founded upon *mesiras nefesh*, but there must be an *avodah* whose entire matter is *mesiras nefesh*. The matter is that since the engagement in trials is in a matter that has no existence, and its existence is only that a thing was set up to conceal and prevent as mentioned above, therefore also the manner of its refinement is not through *avodah* that gives existence and takes up space for the thing being refined, but in *avodah* that nullifies it entirely. For in *avodah* according to intellect and emotion, even the intellect and emotion of holiness of the animal soul, since it is connected with argument and explanation in the intellect, this itself shows that there is a conflicting existence that he is fighting with, and therefore this *avodah* will not suffice for trials, through which there is a refinement of matters that have no existence. Rather, it is through *mesiras nefesh* with great strength, that he does not enter into any argument or calculation, and nullifies the trial entirely as if there is no existence that he needs to fight with, etc. Therefore, this *avodah* is (within the *makifim* of the soul itself) from the aspect of the *yechidah* in the soul as mentioned above, for specifically from the perspective of this aspect there is no place for any existence except for holiness, and the other matters are mere imagination, and also the existence of the imagination is only for the sake of holiness, so that through it the person will be elevated to a greater ascent, which is above even the ascent that is made through the *avodah* of positive and negative *mitzvos*, to the point that it is also above the *avodah* (in matters of negative *mitzvos*) of "intentional sins are transformed for him into merits," which is the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, and *teshuvah* from love in general.

11) Now, also in trials themselves there are several levels. For just as in the matter of *nissim* there are several levels one above the other (*nes*, *nes* within a *nes*, etc.), so too it is in trials that there are several levels one below the other, as the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, explains in his maamar *Acharei* (which is printed at the end of his *Sefer HaMitzvos*) several levels in this. In general, it is as the Rebbe (Rashab) brings in his maamar "You have given to those who fear You a banner to be displayed," the statement of the *Midrash*: "Come and see what is between the first and the last; the first were tested by the Ribono shel Olam, as it is said, 'And G-d tested Avraham,' etc., but the last are tested by the nations of the world," etc. For in the trials through the nations of the world, the concealment and hiding is greater than in ordinary trials. Therefore, in order to stand against these trials, it is through a more lofty level in *bitul* and *mesiras nefesh* itself. It can be said that this is why the primary matter of trials is specifically in the last generations, and primarily in the generation of the footsteps of *Moshiach*, where the darkness is double and redoubled, and the *avodah* is with *mesiras nefesh*. As is explained in the maamarim of our Rebbes, and especially in the maamarim of the Baal HaGeulah and the Baal HaSimcha, in the interpretation of the verse "And the man Moshe was very humble, more than any man on the face of the earth," that primarily this was because of the generation of the footsteps of *Moshiach*, where the concealments and hidings grew, and nevertheless they stand with enormous strength and study Torah and fulfill *mitzvos* with *mesiras nefesh*, and because of this (in the language of the maamar) "Moshe Rabbeinu fell down within himself." Similar to the situation as it was at the time of the imprisonment in that country, etc. And so too now, although there are no such disturbances and obstacles, G-d forbid, on the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, nevertheless there are the trials from the side of expansion and wealth, for sometimes from the side of expansion, etc., the trial is greater. For the *yetzer hara* is a master of his craft, that "today he tells him to do this," etc., and confuses the person from the *avodah* of Hashem so that at least it should not be in absolute perfection, "like one who wants to do." Through this he lowers the person from level to level, etc., at first in matters of the overcoming of the animal soul which is from *nogah*, and afterwards in matters of *shogeg* (unintentional), and afterwards, etc. And in order to stand against all these trials, the person must do his *avodah* with great strength, and in the language of *Tanya*, "he shall thunder against it with a voice of noise," etc., as Chazal said, "A person should always arouse the good inclination against the *yetzer hara*," etc., through which he nullifies its entire existence, and on the contrary, it becomes a helper, that "even his enemies will make peace with him," this snake. And from this itself, that the *avodah* of the footsteps of *Moshiach* is most difficult, this itself is proof that there are and were given the powers for this, for "I do not ask according to my strength, but according to their strength," meaning that the power is given to everyone to awaken the strength that

## 12 Tammuz 5738

"This is the day that Hashem has made; let us rejoice and be glad in it." The Rebbe, the Baal HaGeulah, brings in his maamar on the words "This is..." [which he said at the first celebration of 12 Tammuz (at the seudas hodaah) in the year 5688], that it is stated in the Midrash: Rabbi Avin said, "We do not know whether to rejoice in the day or in the Holy One, blessed be He." Shlomo came and explained: "Let us rejoice and be glad in You"—in the Holy One, blessed be He. "In You"—in Your fear, "in You"—in Your Torah, "in You"—in Your salvation. Rabbi Yitzchak said: "In You"—in the twenty-two letters that You wrote for us in the Torah; *beis* [is] two, *chaf* [is] twenty, that makes "in You" (*bach*). The maamar questions: Why does it say, "We do not know whether to rejoice in the day or in the Holy One, blessed be He"? Since "this is the day that Hashem has made" [meaning, the virtue of the day is not of itself, but rather that "this is the day that Hashem has made"], it is seemingly understood that the joy should be in the Holy One, blessed be He. Why, then, say "we do not know"? Furthermore, what are the three matters of fear, Torah, and salvation? And also, the statement of Rabbi Yitzchak, "In You—in the twenty-two letters," requires explanation, for "in You" simply means in the Holy One, blessed be He; why interpret it as the twenty-two letters?

2. The explanation of the virtue of the day (to the point that there is a *hava amina*—a preliminary thought—to rejoice in the day itself) is that the day on which a miracle occurred is an exalted day. There are two aspects to this: The day on which a miracle occurred is a "meritorious day" in its own right (even beforehand), which is why the miracle occurred on it, for "merit is brought about through a meritorious day." Furthermore, through the miracle that took place on it, it becomes a meritorious day and a day of *segulah* (even more than it was before). Moreover, on this very day, the primary elevation is in the specific time (day or night) when the miracle occurred. As the Midrash states: "When You perform miracles for us by day, we sing a song before You by day (and Devorah and Barak son of Avinoam sang *on that day*...), and when You perform miracles for us by night, we sing a song before You by night (the song shall be for you *as in the night* when a festival is sanctified)." It can be said that the distinction in the time when the miracle occurred—day or night—corresponds to the level and manner of the miracle: whether the miracle is in a manner of light and revelation (day) or in a manner of concealment (night). According to this, it is also understood that the miracle is in a manner of day, light, and revelation.

3. The explanation of this matter (the connection between the time the miracle occurred and the miracle itself) can be understood by prefacing the well-known fact that *nes* (miracle) comes from the word *harama* (lifting). Through the miracle, a lifting and elevation is effected in nature. This is what we say in the blessing, "Who performed a miracle for me in this place," for even the place, which is boundary and nature, is elevated by the *beli gevul* (limitlessness) of the miracle that is above nature. From this, it is understood that the same applies to the time when the miracle occurred, just as we say in the blessings of the miracles (of Chanukah and Purim), "Who performed miracles for our fathers in those days, at this time."
