4. Explaining this in greater detail: It is known that there are (generally) two types of miracles. Miracles that are above nature [such as the miracles of the Exodus, turning water into blood, etc., up to the miracle of the splitting of the Red Sea, where the sea was turned into dry land], and miracles that are clothed in the ways of nature. Within the latter, there are two modes: The garments of nature are in a manner where it is recognizable that they are merely a garment for the miracle clothed within them. Such are the miracles of Chanukah and Purim (and similarly the miracles of the redemption of 19 Kislev and 12 Tammuz), for although they were clothed in the ways of nature, nevertheless, the miracle within them was recognizable in revelation (to the point that "all the ends of the earth saw"). And [there are] those where the garments of nature conceal and hide the miracle clothed within them, to the point that sometimes they conceal and hide it completely, so that it is not recognizable at all that it is a miracle, and the beneficiary of the miracle does not recognize his miracle.

5. It is known that the root of nature is from the Name *Elokim* (*Elokim* in *gematria* is *hateva*—nature), which generally is the *Ohr HaMemalei* (the light that fills) that is clothed in the worlds according to their capacity, and the root of miracles is from the Name *Havayah*, which generally is the *Ohr HaSovev* (the light that encompasses) that is above the worlds. From this, it is understood that the miracles not clothed in nature have their root of influence from the revelation of *Havayah* itself, which is above being clothed in the Name *Elokim*, and the miracles clothed in nature have their root of influence from the revelation of the Name *Havayah* as it is clothed in the Name *Elokim*.

This can be understood by way of analogy to the power of will in a person (for will is a metaphor for *Ohr HaSovev*), which has two levels: a will that is above reason, and a will that is clothed in reason. Within this itself (in the will clothed in reason), there are two modes: Although it is clothed in reason, it is recognizable in revelation that in its essence it is a will (that is above reason), and that the will inclines the intellect in such a way that the intellect itself becomes as the will, and it is felt that the fact that he thinks so is (not because of the inclination of the will, but) because of the intellect. Similarly, in the analogy, the revelation of *Ohr HaSovev* has three levels analogous to the above, which are the root of the three types of miracles: a miracle completely above nature, a miracle clothed in nature in a way that the miracle within it is recognizable, and a miracle clothed in nature in a way that nature hides the miracle within it.

6. The fact that *nes* is from the word *harama*, that through the miracle a lifting and elevation is effected in nature, applies primarily to miracles clothed in nature. For in miracles above nature, the revelation of the Name *Havayah* that is above nature is in a manner where nature (which is drawn from the Name *Elokim*) is nullified by the revelation—the overturning of the laws of nature. The concept of *nes* as *harama*—that the revelation of the Name *Havayah* is in a manner where nature (drawn from the Name *Elokim*) is elevated by the light of the Name *Havayah*—is (primarily) in miracles clothed in nature. Nevertheless, from the fact that even miracles not clothed in nature are called by the name *nes* (from the word *harama*), it is understood that even through these miracles, a lifting and elevation is effected in nature. For since the overturning of nature through the miracle is only in one detail and not in the totality of the matter [like the miracle of the splitting of the Red Sea, where the change (the overturning of nature) was only in that the waters stood like a heap and a wall, but the actual substance of the water remained as it was before], it follows that even in these miracles, the revelation of the Name *Havayah* is in a state of being clothed in the nature of the totality of the matter in which the miracle occurred, and thereby a lifting and elevation is effected in it.

7. This is the meaning of "We do not know whether to rejoice in the day or in the Holy One, blessed be He," for in every miracle there are the two aspects of "the day" and "the Holy One, blessed be He." The elevation of nature through the miracle is "the day." As mentioned above (sections 2 and 3), through the miracle, a lifting and elevation is effected in the time (the day) in which the miracle occurred. And the miracle itself, whose essence is above nature, has its root of influence from the *Ein Sof* that is above the worlds (*Ohr HaSovev*) as it shines and is revealed in the world in a manner of *sovev u'makif* (encompassing)—the Holy One, blessed be He. As explained elsewhere, the fact that we call Him, may He be blessed, by the name "the Holy One, blessed be He," refers to the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is holy and separated from the worlds, as it is drawn down (*baruch* from the word *hemshech*—drawing down) into the worlds in a manner of *sovev u'makif*. We do not know whether to rejoice in the day or in the Holy One, blessed be He, because in each of them there is a virtue that is not in the other. In terms of the level of light, the miracle itself (the matter of overturning nature) is much more exalted than the elevation of nature through the miracle. For the miracle itself (overturning nature) is the revelation of *Ohr HaSovev* that is above the worlds, whereas the elevation of nature through the miracle is the revelation of *Ohr HaSovev* as it is clothed in the worlds. However, in terms of revelation, the matter of the elevation of nature is more exalted. For in the miracle itself, the revelation of *Ohr HaSovev*, a person has no grasp. That is why miracles are called *niflaos* (wonders), for a *pela* (wonder) is something not grasped by the intellect. Moreover, when a person sees a wonder, he is astonished by it, and astonishment is a matter of *bitul* (nullification). As explained elsewhere regarding the four who must give thanks, that giving thanks (for a miracle) is a matter of *bitul*. Just as in the world, the matter of the miracle is that nature is *nullified* [for since the miracle comes from the revelation of the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, which the world cannot receive, the nullification of the nature of the world is thereby effected], so too regarding the person: through the miracle, he comes to thanksgiving and *bitul*. This is not the case with the matter of the elevation of nature, where the revelation of the Name *Havayah* that is above nature is clothed in nature itself; regarding this it is written, "*Know* that *Havayah* is *Elokim*," knowledge and grasp. And since joy is specifically in *Binah* (understanding), whereas in *Chochmah* (wisdom) that is above grasp there is no joy [even though *Chochmah* is also intellect, it is a general point and not in a state of settlement; from this it is understood *a fortiori* regarding a wonder that is above intellect], therefore there is a *hava amina* to rejoice in the day. It should be added that "day" is light and revelation (as explained at length in the beginning of the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah). This is "to rejoice in the day"—the reason for the *hava amina* to rejoice in the day on which the miracle occurred (the matter of the elevation of nature) is because this matter is "day," light, and revelation (which comes through knowledge and grasp).

8. Shlomo came and explained, "Let us rejoice and be glad in You"—in the Holy One, blessed be He; "in You"—in Your fear, etc. The explanation of "in You"—in the Holy One, blessed be He (which Shlomo explained) is in the Holy One, blessed be He Himself, Who is above even the *Sovev*. As explained elsewhere, the explanation of "in You" is in You in Your Essence. The innovation of Shlomo (the wisest of all men) is that the root of miracles is from the Essence. The fact that the revelation of the Name *Havayah* that is above nature is clothed in the Name *Elokim*—in *gematria* *hateva* (nature)—(for this matter is in all miracles, even in miracles above nature, as mentioned in section 6), and even after its clothing in nature it is recognizable in revelation (even in miracles clothed in nature, like the miracles of Chanukah and Purim) that it is a miracle (the revelation of the Name *Havayah*) that is above nature, is through the power of the Essence that connects and unites two opposites.

This is the connection between the two interpretations of "Let us rejoice and be glad in You"—in You in the Holy One, blessed be He (as the Midrash interprets) and in You in Your Essence, for the connection and unification of "Holy" and "Blessed" (*Sovev* and *Memalei*) is through the power of the Essence. And since the verse "Let us rejoice and be glad in You" is brought in the Midrash in continuation of the two opinions (regarding joy in miracles), whether to rejoice in the Holy One, blessed be He (in the miracle itself, which is drawn from *Ohr HaSovev*) or to rejoice in the day (from the clothing of the *Sovev* in the *Memalei*, whereby the miracle is clothed in nature), and the innovation of Shlomo is that the joy must be "in You"—in Your Essence, which connects the two matters, therefore it says "in You in the Holy One, blessed be He" (and not "in You in Your Essence"), because the power of the Essence that is revealed in miracles is in that it unites the two aspects of "Holy" and "Blessed."

9. The Midrash continues, "In You—in Your fear, in You—in Your Torah, in You—in Your salvation." The drawing down of the Essence is through fear. As explained elsewhere, the difference between love and fear is that through love, since it is an existence and an expansion, one reaches the revelations of the *Ein Sof* (expansion), and specifically through fear, which is *bitul*, and even *bitul* that comes from the essence of the soul, one reaches the Essence. However, that one reaches the Essence through fear is in a state of concealment, and for there to be a revelation of the Essence, it is through the Torah—"Torah is light." For although the *bitul* of fear is from the essence of the soul, for the root of the souls is above the root of the Torah, nevertheless, the revelation of every matter (even of the root of the souls as they are rooted in the Essence) is through the Torah.

It should be added that since "He looked into the Torah and created the world," all influences in the world are through the Torah. And the two matters of above nature (*beli gevul*) and nature (boundary) in the world are drawn from the two matters of *beli gevul* and boundary in the Torah. As explained elsewhere regarding the verse, "Who wraps Himself in light as a garment," that the revealed part of Torah (the garment of Torah) is in measurement and limitation, and the inner dimension of Torah (the light of Torah) is without limit. And through the unification of the two matters in the Torah—that the revealed and the inner are one Torah—and especially through engaging in Torah in a way that while studying the revealed, the inner dimension of Torah (the wonders in the Torah) is felt by him in revelation, thereby the connection of above nature with nature is drawn into the world, in such a way that even in nature, the wonders of above nature will be felt in revelation.

This is "in You—in Your fear, in You—in Your Torah, in You—in Your salvation." First, there must be "in Your fear," through which one draws down the Essence; afterwards, "in Your Torah" (Torah is light), through which the revelation of the Essence is effected; and from this it is drawn down to be "in You—in Your salvation," for even though they were in a state where they required salvation, and even afterwards (since they are still in exile), the salvation is in the garments of nature, nevertheless, it is recognizable in it in revelation—in a way that "all the ends of the earth saw"—that it is a revealed miracle that is above nature.

The Midrash continues, Rabbi Yitzchak said, "In You—in the twenty-two letters that You wrote for us in the Torah." The fact that through the Torah the salvation is drawn down in the aforementioned manner is primarily in the letters of the Torah. There are two matters in this: for the connection of above nature with nature is through the power of the Essence (as mentioned), and the letters of the Torah are vessels for the drawing down of the Essence (as explained in the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah). The vitality of every single Jew is through having a letter in the Torah, and therefore, in order that there be "Let us rejoice and be glad in You" (for the matter of joy is the revelation of vitality, up to the revelation of the inner dimension of vitality), it is through the letters of the Torah, from which vitality is drawn to every single Jew.

10. It is known that "joy breaks through barriers." It is understood that the barriers broken through by joy are only the barriers of that same aspect in which the joy is. Therefore, when the joy in miracles is from the side of the revelations of *Memalei* and *Sovev* ("day" and "the Holy One, blessed be He"), which are in the category of knowledge ("we do not know"), the barriers that exist in the aspects above knowledge remain. This is not the case through the joy of "Let us rejoice and be glad in You"—in Your Essence; a "breaker" is effected, the breaking of all barriers. Thereby, even more is added to the connection of above nature with nature that is effected through the revelation of the Essence. This is "This is the day that Hashem has made; let us rejoice and be glad in it"—through the joy in this day (in the manner of "Let us rejoice and be glad in You"), even more is added to the redemption, which is in a manner even more exalted than it was the first time (as it was drawn down from above, before the joy). And since in the redemption of 12 Tammuz every single Jew was redeemed, even those who are "called by the name of Israel" (only), therefore, the addition to the redemption each year, which is effected through the joy of the redemption, is also drawn down to every single Jew, to be redeemed from all the matters that prevent and hinder the performance of Torah and *mitzvos*. And according to the known principle that all redemptions are connected to one another, for they are all called "redemption," it can be said that through the joy in the celebration of the redemption, there will be an addition also in the future redemption, where "we will rejoice in it"—in Him, in His Essence—with the coming of our righteous Moshiach, immediately.

## 13 Tammuz, 5742

"Ten who sit and occupy themselves with Torah, the Shechinah dwells among them..." and so on, even five, even three, even two, even one. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Baal HaGeulah, explains in his maamar on this subject, which was given for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz (5688), that although even one person who sits and occupies himself with Torah (and certainly two, three, or five) draws down a revelation of Elokus (the Shechinah dwells), nevertheless, the drawing down that occurs through Torah of the many (ten) is a more sublime drawing down. Just as our Sages said regarding tefillah, "The tefillah of the many is not rejected," as it is written, "Behold, Hashem is mighty and does not reject," because the many, through their tefillah, draw down the thirteen attributes of mercy, so too is it with Torah: through Torah of the many, a more sublime revelation of light is drawn down.

The explanation of the Sages' expression "tefillah of the many" [and in the maamar, the term "many" is used regarding Torah as well], even though it speaks regarding ten [and the term "many" applies even to fewer than ten, yet on the other hand, even ten is not the perfection of "many," for there is a much greater multitude], can be explained by prefacing that the reason why a matter performed before ten of Israel is the greatest form of *pirsum* (publicity)—for we find no distinction regarding *pirsum* between ten and more than ten—is because ten of Israel are like, and include, the ten types of Israel (from "your heads, your tribes," down to "the hewer of your wood and the drawer of your water"), and publicity before ten of Israel is like publicity before all of Israel. This is why ten of Israel are called "the many" (without qualification)—the greatest multitude, than which there is no greater.

2) It is explained in Tanya that the advantage of ten is in all matters of Torah and mitzvos, for there is no "matter of holiness" with fewer than ten. However, the primary advantage of ten is in tefillah. The advantage of the tefillah of the many is that it is desired and accepted forever, and since the request of tefillah is that Hashem fulfill one's petition, the advantage of the tefillah of the many over the tefillah of an individual is not that an *additional* element is added to the tefillah, but rather that it pertains to the tefillah itself. Based on this, we can say that what is stated in the maamar—that the advantage in Torah of the many is like the advantage of the tefillah of the many—means (also) that the advantage in Torah of the many is in essential matters.

Seemingly, one could explain this by saying that since "Torah is only acquired in a group," it is understood that when Torah study is in a larger group, the Torah is acquired more fully. And since the perfection of a group is in ten, because ten of Israel are like and include all ten types of Israel, as above, therefore, when Torah study is in ten, the acquisition of Torah is in perfection. But this explanation is insufficient. For the aforementioned advantage in Torah of the many is in the person occupying himself with Torah: when he learns in ten, his acquisition (that he acquires the Torah and *receives* it) is in perfection. The analogy of Torah of the many to the tefillah of the many is in the *drawing down* (the *hemshech*). As is explicit in the maamar, just as the many in their tefillah draw down the thirteen attributes of mercy, so too, through Torah of the many, a more sublime light is drawn down.

3) In order to explain the advantage of the drawing down through Torah of the many, the maamar prefaces that Rabbi Yishmael says: "The Torah is expounded through thirteen hermeneutical rules," such as *kal v'chomer*, *gezeirah shavah*, etc. It explains that through each and every rule (of the thirteen by which the Torah is expounded), new matters are revealed. The reason for this is that the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded correspond to the thirteen attributes of mercy. As per the teaching of the Maggid, when Moshe said, "O G-d (*E-l*), please heal her," where the name *E-l* is the first attribute of the thirteen attributes of mercy, Hashem said to him a *kal v'chomer*: "If her father had spit in her face..."—a *kal v'chomer* for the Shechinah—which is the first of the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded. The maamar adds that this is also the connection between the two interpretations of "He who grazes among the roses (*shoshanim*)." Either read it not as *shoshanim* but as *sheshonim* (those who study) the halachos, or: just as a rose has thirteen petals, so too the Congregation of Israel has thirteen measures of mercy. The connection between the two interpretations is that through the study of Torah (those who study the halachos), the thirteen attributes of mercy are drawn down. This is why through Torah of the many, a more sublime light is drawn down: because the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy through Torah study is primarily through Torah study of the many specifically.

One must understand what is said at the beginning of the subject, that through the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded, new matters are revealed. Seemingly, the connection of these thirteen rules to what was discussed above—that through Torah of the many a more sublime light is drawn down—is that these thirteen rules correspond to the thirteen attributes of mercy, and the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy is primarily through Torah study of the many specifically. What does it matter here that through the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded, new matters are revealed?

One can say the explanation for this is that the difference between Torah and tefillah is that tefillah is *the person* asking and praying, and the drawing down from above (that Hashem fulfills his request) is *effected* through the tefillah. This is not the case in the occupation of Torah; since the Torah one learns is the word of Hashem (which exists even before the person's occupation of Torah), the action effected through the occupation of Torah is, seemingly, that the Torah and the Ohr Ein Sof clothed within it are drawn down to the person. Based on this, there is room to say that the advantage of Torah of the many over Torah of an individual is (primarily) only regarding the person occupying himself with Torah. For although the maamar says that the advantage of Torah of the many is (not only in the person's reception, that the Torah is acquired by him more, but also) in the drawing down from above (as in section 2), that through Torah study of the many a more sublime light is drawn down, nevertheless, there is room to say that the whole matter of Torah study is that through the study, the light of the Torah (which exists even before the study) shines to the person learning it, and through Torah study of the many, a more sublime light is revealed to the person. Therefore, the maamar brings that through the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded, new matters are revealed. Just as tefillah draws down a new will, "may it be" (*yehi ratzon*), so too in Torah: through Torah study according to the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded, new matters are revealed. The reason for this is that the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded correspond to the thirteen attributes of mercy, which are above Torah. For Torah is the wisdom of Hashem, the beginning of *hishtalshelus*, and the thirteen attributes of mercy are above *hishtalshelus*. Through the person learning Torah according to the thirteen rules, he draws into the Torah (*hishtalshelus*) the thirteen attributes of mercy that are above *hishtalshelus*, and thereby new matters are drawn into the Torah. This is why through Torah study of the many, a more sublime light is drawn down from above, because the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy through Torah study is primarily in Torah study of the many specifically—meaning that the level of the thirteen attributes of mercy drawn down through Torah study of the many is a more sublime level.

4) The maamar continues with another advantage of the tefillah of the many: that the drawing down from above through the tefillah of the many is not according to the measure of their *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below). In addition to the fact that the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the tefillah of the many reaches higher, which is why it draws down a more sublime drawing, the tefillah of the many draws down a drawing from above that is not according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata*, nor even according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many. This is what our Sages said, that the tefillah of the many throughout the year is like the tefillah of an individual during the Ten Days of Repentance. Just as the drawing down through the tefillah of an individual during the Ten Days of Repentance is not according to the measure of his elevation [which is why it is specifically during the Ten Days of Repentance, because they are a time of favor], so too is the drawing down through the tefillah of the many (throughout the year)—it is not according to the measure of the elevation (nor even according to the measure of the elevation of the many). And similarly it is in Torah of the many, that the drawing down through Torah study of the many is not according to the measure of the study of the many.

One must understand that even in the explanation (at the beginning of the maamar) that the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many draws down a more sublime light, it explains that the drawing down through the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many is the thirteen attributes of mercy, and the thirteen attributes of mercy are above *hishtalshelus*, and a drawing down that is above *hishtalshelus* is not according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata*. Nevertheless, it adds later (another matter) that the drawing down through the many is not according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many. The point of the explanation here is that the intention in adding that the drawing down through the many is not according to the measure of their *is'arusa d'lesata* is that the drawing down through the many is not only that the drawing is greater than the *avodah* [for this matter is in every drawing down that is above *hishtalshelus*], but also that the drawing is (primarily) from the side of above, *similar to* an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) from its own side, which is drawn from a place that an *is'arusa d'lesata* cannot reach.

One can say that this is similar to the matter of "I labored and I found," that the knowledge coming through labor is in the manner of a "finding" (*metzi'ah*)—not according to the measure of the labor—and there are two modes in this. The success in the knowledge and understanding of the subject he labored over is similar to the advantage of the tefillah of the many, where the drawing down is above *hishtalshelus* (above order and gradation), but (only) from that place to which the *is'arusa d'lesata* reached. And that the success in the knowledge of Torah coming through the labor of the person is in a place he did not labor in at all—"he labors in this place, and his Torah labors for him from another place"—is similar to the second matter of the tefillah of the many, that the drawing down through the *avodah* (tefillah) is similar to an *is'arusa d'le'eila* from its own side, which an *is'arusa d'lesata* (even the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the tefillah of the many) cannot reach. Yet, this drawing down comes through the tefillah of the many, similar to how even when his Torah labors for him in another place, it is through the labor of the person.

5) One can say that the distinction between these two matters is also in their root, in the thirteen attributes of mercy. The matter is that the number thirteen (the *tikkunei dikna*) is twelve plus one. Twelve is the twelve oxen (in *Beriah*), and the one (added to the twelve) is the sea that stands upon them (*Malchus* of *Atzilus*). And higher still, twelve is the twelve diagonal boundaries in *Atzilus*, and the one (added to the twelve) is above *Atzilus*. One can say that the fact that thirteen is above *hishtalshelus* is because through the one that is added to the twelve, the twelve also become above *hishtalshelus*. One can say there are two modes (levels) in this. That the one is drawn into the twelve as they are in their place; in this mode, even after the one is drawn into them, they are a boundary (*diagonal boundaries*), only that through the one that is above *hishtalshelus* being drawn into them, they have an unlimited power. And another mode: that the twelve are elevated and included in the one, whereby they emerge from their limitation and become in the category of "unlimited." One can say that this is what is meant by "one" (*echad*) having the *gematria* of thirteen—that all thirteen are one.

One can say that the two matters in the drawing down through *avodah* (tefillah or Torah study) of the many—that the drawing down is not by gradation (above *hishtalshelus*), and that through their *avodah* is drawn down even from a place where it is impossible for an *is'arusa d'lesata* (even the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many) to awaken—are in the two aforementioned levels. In the level of thirteen where the one is drawn into the twelve, since twelve is a boundary, the drawing down from there is through *is'arusa d'lesata*. Only that through the one drawn into the twelve, the drawing down is not by gradation (similar to "I labored and I found"). And in the level of thirteen where the twelve are included in the one and all thirteen are unlimited, the drawing down from there is similar to an *is'arusa d'le'eila* from its own side.

6) One can connect this with the Festival of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, for on 12 Tammuz [the birthday of the Baal HaGeulah] he was informed that the order for his release had arrived, and the actual release was on 13 Tammuz. One can say that the fact that on 12 (Tammuz) he was informed about the release is the matter of twelve as the one is drawn into it. And since twelve as it is in its place, even when the one is drawn into it, is a boundary, therefore on the 12th it was still before the actual redemption. For the matter of redemption is above measurement and limitation [and especially according to what is explained in the letter of the Baal HaGeulah (which serves as a preface to the maamar "Ten who sit and occupy themselves..."), that Hashem redeemed not only him, but all of Israel, including even those who are called by the name of Israel (only). And to add, that this includes the generations that follow, for the redemption of 12-13 Tammuz is a continuous action, which draws down redemption for all of Israel throughout all the generations—redemption regarding their Torah study and performance of mitzvos, and also redemption regarding their material matters, children, life, and sustenance, that they should all be "abundant," above measurement and limitation. And furthermore, that it (the redemption of 12-13 Tammuz) is also a preface and preparation for the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when the true matter of "above measurement and limitation" will be], and the actual redemption was on the 13th, the *gematria* of "one," where the twelve are elevated in the one, above limitation.

7) The maamar continues that although Torah is a drawing down from above to below, nevertheless, even in Torah there must be *avodah* and labor, and there are two matters in this. That for Torah study to be as it should be, it is through [the preface of] the *avodah* of tefillah, for "whoever says I have only Torah, even Torah he does not have." And that Torah study itself must be with *avodah* and labor. In this there are two matters: the labor in understanding the Torah, "I labored and I found," and the labor in Torah to change one's nature and habit, as our Sages said, "He who studies his chapter one hundred times is not comparable to he who studies his chapter one hundred and one times," for then specifically is he called "a servant of G-d." One must understand: the matter of *is'arusa d'lesata* in Torah is seemingly primarily in the labor that must be in the Torah study itself, yet the order in the maamar is that first it explains that for Torah study to be as it should be, there must be the *avodah* and labor of tefillah, and afterwards it says (as an additional matter) that there must be labor also in Torah study itself. It should be noted that in Tanya, too, it speaks of these two matters: the labor in Torah and the labor in the *avodah* of Hashem in general, for the primary *avodah* is the *avodah* of tefillah. The order of matters in Tanya is that first it brings the verse, "Then you shall return and see... between one who serves G-d and one who does not serve Him," for regarding this verse it is in the Gemara that "a servant of G-d" is one who studies his chapter one hundred and one times—a change of the nature of habit in Torah study—and this statement of our Sages is the source for what is explained there, that even the performance of all mitzvos [and especially the *avodah* of tefillah] must be in this manner. From this (that the order of matters in the maamar is the opposite of the order in Tanya), it is proven even more that the order of matters in the maamar is intentional.

8) This will be understood by prefacing the explanation of the precision (in the maamar) "although Torah is a drawing down from above to below." The explanation of this in simple terms is that since Torah is a drawing down from above to below, there is no need for the many. For in tefillah, where the drawing down is through the *avodah* of the below, the *avodah* of the below must be an *avodah* of the many, whereas in Torah, which is a drawing down from above, there is no difference if the below is many or one. According to what is known, that the reason why through tefillah a new will is drawn down is because of the greatness of the elevation of *man* (the arousal from below), "Your handiwork yearns," one can say that the intention in the precision that Torah is a drawing down from above to below is also the opposite: that since Torah is a drawing down from above, even through Torah study of the many, it is impossible for there to be a drawing down as sublime as the drawing down through tefillah (of the many).

Based on this, one can explain the order of matters in the maamar: first it explains the *avodah* and labor of tefillah that must be for the sake of Torah study, and afterwards the *avodah* and labor in Torah study itself, because the primary *avodah* and labor is the *avodah* of tefillah, which is why it is called "avodah" without qualification. For the matter of *avodah* is the change of nature and habit, and this is done primarily through the *avodah* of tefillah. And especially through the *Amidah* prayer, where the person praying is "like a servant before his master," in total *bitul*. Therefore, the maamar prefaces the *avodah* and labor of tefillah that is for the sake of Torah study, because the *avodah* and labor of Torah study (by itself) does not have the power to draw down a drawing not according to the measure of the *avodah* at all. And the fact that through Torah study (of the many) a drawing down is effected not according to the measure of the *avodah* at all, like the drawing down through tefillah (of the many), is primarily through the *avodah* of tefillah that is for the sake of Torah study. However, this explanation is insufficient, for in Torah, the drawing down not according to the measure of the elevation comes in the knowledge and understanding of Torah, where his success in the knowledge and understanding of Torah is not according to the measure of his labor; therefore, there must also be the labor of changing nature and habit in Torah study itself, whereby his study becomes a vessel for the drawing down through the *avodah* of tefillah (that is for the sake of Torah study).

One should add in the explanation of the connection of "the one who studies his chapter one hundred and one times" (the labor of changing nature and habit in Torah study) to the thirteen attributes of mercy, that through the study the one hundred and first time, even the study of the one hundred times before it becomes in the manner of *avodah*. Similar to what was explained above (section 5) regarding the number thirteen, that through the addition of the one, an elevation (a change or at least an addition) is effected in the twelve.

9) Based on this, one can explain that in the teaching of the Maggid brought in the maamar as above, that through Moshe mentioning the name *E-l* (the first attribute of the thirteen attributes of mercy), Hashem said to him a *kal v'chomer* (the first of the thirteen rules by which the Torah is expounded), it is precise that Moshe *in his tefillah* said, "O G-d, please heal her." One can say that the precision "in his tefillah" is to hint that the primary drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy that are above *hishtalshelus* is in tefillah, and thereby comes afterwards the drawing down also in Torah. This is also the reason why the matter of the drawing down not according to the measure of the elevation through Torah (of the many) is learned from the drawing down through tefillah (of the many), because the primary (and source of the) matter is in tefillah, and thereby it is drawn afterwards also into Torah.

To add, that this matter (that through tefillah it is drawn afterwards also into Torah) is also hinted at in the two chapters of Psalms corresponding to the birthday of the Baal HaGeulah in this year. For in Psalm 102 [which corresponds to the completion of the 102nd year], it begins with "A prayer for the afflicted..." and in the continuation of the psalm it says, "This shall be written for the final generation," which refers to Torah, which is eternal. And similarly in Psalm 103 [which corresponds to the 103rd year, beginning from the birthday], which begins with "Bless Hashem, O my soul," which is a tefillah of praise and thanksgiving, and in the continuation of the psalm it says, "Bless Hashem, you His angels, mighty in strength, who perform His word, to hear the voice of His word"—first "perform" and then "hear," the preface of "we will do" to "we will hear," which was a preparation for the receiving of the Torah.

10) It is known the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that everything a person sees or hears is an instruction in the *avodah* of Hashem. The Maggid adds that everything one sees and hears and every incident that happens to a person is for the sake of the *avodah* of Hashem. The explanation of this is that even every incident is by Divine Providence, and the fact that it is called an "incident" (*mikreh*) is because below in this world it is in the manner of an incident. Similar to what is written, "If a bird's nest happens to be (*yikareh*) before you," and our Sages said, "excluding that which is prepared," for although all matters are by Divine Providence, and furthermore, they are prepared from the primordial thought of *Adam Kadmon*, nevertheless, the verse says "if it happens to be" (*yikareh*), excluding that which is prepared, because there are matters whose intention is completed by the fact that even below they are in the manner of "prepared," and there are matters whose intention is completed by the fact that below they are in the manner of an "incident," for "it happens to be." From this it is understood *a fortiori* regarding the matters in Torah, that all its details, even when they appear externally to be only by the way (in the manner of an incident), are an instruction.

Based on this, one can say that the fact that the rule of the thirteen rules in Torah that was drawn from the thirteen attributes of mercy in tefillah is the rule of *kal v'chomer* is to teach that although the primary drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy is in tefillah and thereby comes the drawing down also in Torah, nevertheless, there is an advantage in the drawing down in Torah over the drawing down in tefillah, in the manner of a *kal v'chomer*, for although the "severe" is learned from the "light," nevertheless, it is "severe" relative to the "light." And as is explained in the maamar, that the fact that we learn the drawing down not according to the measure of the elevation through Torah of the many from the drawing down through tefillah of the many is a study in the manner of *a fortiori*, *kal v'chomer*.

The matter is that the distinction between Torah and tefillah is similar to the distinction between blessing and tefillah. In tefillah, the one praying is below and *asks* that they bestow upon him from above, and in blessing, the one blessing [the one who has the power to bless, like the Kohanim who were given the power to bless] is above the source from which the blessing is drawn and commands that the drawing down be below. Like the expression in the Priestly Blessing, "Hashem shall bless you," which is a language of command. And similarly it is in the drawing down of the influences through Torah. Since the "crown of Torah" is ownerless for all, it is in the power of every one of Israel to merit it through Torah study in a way that it becomes *his* Torah (the one learning), and he becomes, as it were, the master over the Torah, and certainly over the drawing down of the influences through the Torah.

Another advantage in the Priestly Blessing is that the drawing down of the Priestly Blessing is from above *hishtalshelus*. For blessing in general is to draw down what is already in the source and not something new, for in this matter there is an advantage in tefillah over blessing, that through tefillah a new will is effected. And in the Priestly Blessing there are both advantages: that the drawing down is from above *hishtalshelus*, and in the manner of a command. And so it is in the drawing down through Torah, that it has both advantages: that the drawing down is from above *hishtalshelus* and in the manner of a command. And this is the advantage in the drawing down through Torah (of the many) over the drawing down through tefillah (of the many), that the drawing down through Torah is in a manner that he is the master over the drawing.

11) Although the Priestly Blessing is a mitzvah in its own right, the Sages established it within tefillah. From this it is understood that although tefillah is from below to above, nevertheless, through tefillah one reaches the drawing down of the Priestly Blessing, which is from above to below. Based on this, one can add to the study of the *kal v'chomer* that just as tefillah and the Priestly Blessing, although they are different matters—for tefillah is a request (from below to above) and the Priestly Blessing is a command (from above to below)—nevertheless, through tefillah one reaches the Priestly Blessing, so too it is in Torah and tefillah: although the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy that are above *hishtalshelus* through Torah study (by itself) is below the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy through tefillah (as in section 8), nevertheless, through Torah study, the drawing down through tefillah (which is above the drawing down of the thirteen attributes of mercy of Torah) is also drawn down (afterwards).

One should add that this study is also in the manner of *kal v'chomer*. For tefillah is from below to above and the Priestly Blessing is from above to below, and nevertheless through tefillah one reaches the Priestly Blessing; so regarding Torah and tefillah, where even the drawing down of Torah (by itself) is the thirteen attributes of mercy that are above *hishtalshelus*, and only that this drawing down is below the drawing down of tefillah, the fact that through Torah the drawing down of tefillah is also drawn down is *a fortiori* and *kal v'chomer*. One can say that through the fact that Torah is *his* Torah—the person occupying himself with Torah, who is, as it were, the master over the Torah—thereby he becomes the master also over the level of the drawing down of tefillah that is drawn into the Torah. This is why the study of Torah and tefillah is in the measure of *kal v'chomer*, for the drawing down in tefillah through Torah has an advantage over the drawing down in tefillah by itself.

12) One should add that through the maamar "Ten who sit and occupy themselves with Torah," which was given by the Baal HaGeulah to be studied on the Festival of Redemption, he made everyone a messenger of the Baal HaGeulah to occupy himself with this matter, and gave him a special empowerment to succeed in this—success in establishing *shiurim* in public, and success in all the matters (explained in the maamar) that are drawn down through the occupation of Torah of the many.

And all this is in the manner of the Priestly Blessing, for the drawing down of the blessing is in the manner of speed, as explained in *Likkutei Torah* on the verse "And behold, the staff of Aharon had blossomed... and it yielded almonds," and through the good almonds of the staff of Aharon, the bitter almonds of the "Three Weeks" will be transformed into joy and gladness, in the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, literally.

## 15 Tammuz, 5742

"Ten who sit and occupy themselves with Torah, the Shechinah rests among them." My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Baal HaGeulah, explains in his maamar titled *Zeh*, delivered for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz (5688), that although even one person who sits and occupies himself with Torah draws down a revelation of Elokus—as the Mishnah continues, "and from where [do we know that even] five... even three... even two... even one..."—nevertheless, the drawing down that occurs through the Torah of the many is a more sublime drawing. Just as our Sages said regarding prayer, "The prayer of the many is not rejected," because through the prayer of the many, the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy that are above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* are drawn down, and furthermore, the drawing from above that comes through the prayer of the many is not according to the measure of their *is'arusa d'lesata* (nor even according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the many)—so too is it with Torah. Through the study of Torah by the many, the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy that are above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* are drawn down. [Although the drawing of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy through Torah study is due to the *superiority of Torah*, as the thirteen hermeneutical rules by which the Torah is expounded correspond to the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy—from which it is understood that the drawing of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy occurs even when one person sits and occupies himself with Torah—nevertheless, the drawing of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy through Torah study is primarily through the study of Torah in public, meaning that the level of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy drawn through Torah study in public is a more sublime level.] Furthermore, the drawing that comes through the study of Torah by the many is not according to the measure of the study of the many.

2) It can be said that the analogy of Torah to prayer is also hinted at in the aforementioned Mishnah: "And from where [do we know that even] one... [it is said], 'In every place where I cause My name to be mentioned, I will come to you and bless you.'" "In every place..." refers to the Beis HaMikdash [the place where the Shechinah comes, "I will come to you"], where permission was granted to mention the *Shem HaMeforash* ["I cause My name to be mentioned"], and the Beis HaMikdash is associated with the pillar of *avodah*, *korbanos*, and prayer. [To add: the Priestly Blessing, in which they would mention the *Shem HaMeforash* as it is written in the Beis HaMikdash, was also after the offering of the *Tamid* of the morning (the beginning of all *korbanos*), and even now, the Sages established the Priestly Blessing within prayer, and within the prayer itself—in the *Avodah* blessing]. The Mishnah cites this verse regarding the resting of the Shechinah through Torah study, from which it is implied that Torah and prayer are related to one another, specifically in this regard.

**To add:** The interpretation that "In every place where I cause My name to be mentioned..." refers to the Beis HaMikdash, where permission was granted to mention the *Shem HaMeforash*, is the *peshuto shel mikra* (*Torah Shebichtav*), while the interpretation that "I cause My name to be mentioned" refers to Torah study is according to the *drash* of our Sages (*Torah Shebaal Peh*). According to the known principle that all matters of *Torah Shebaal Peh* are drawn from *Torah Shebichtav*, it can be said that the fact that the study of even one person who sits and occupies himself with Torah causes the Shechinah to rest is derived from the verse "In every place where I cause My name to be mentioned...", which simply refers to the Beis HaMikdash associated with the pillar of *avodah*. This is because the essence of the resting of the Shechinah in the manner of "I will come to you"—the drawing of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* ("I will come," I Myself)—is through the line of *avodah*, the *ha'alaah* from below to above. As is explained in *Tanya*, the reason that through prayer the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is drawn down [through which a change is effected in the created beings, to heal the sick and bless the years] is because of the great elevation of the *ha'alaas man*. And through prayer, this drawing subsequently comes into Torah as well.

According to what is stated in the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah (cited above in section 1) that through prayer and through Torah one draws down the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy that are above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* primarily through the prayer of the many and the Torah of the many, to the extent that the drawing through the prayer of the many and the Torah of the many is not according to the measure of the *is'arusa d'lesata* (of the many), it is understood that the aforementioned matter—that the drawing above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* in Torah is through prayer—is emphasized even more in the drawing that comes through the many. As was explained above (in the maamar of 13 Tammuz), the reason that the matter of the drawing not according to the measure of the *ha'alaah* through the Torah of the many is learned (in the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah) from the drawing through the prayer of the many is because the essence and source of this matter is in prayer, and through this, it is subsequently drawn into Torah as well.

3) Although the superiority of *ha'alaas man* exists seemingly in Torah as well, as explained in the maamar of the Baal HaGeulah that in Torah too there must be *avodah* and exertion, nevertheless, the essence of the drawing that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is through the *ha'alaas man* of prayer specifically. The point of the explanation is that the superiority of man's *avodah* (*ha'alaas man*) through which the *Ohr Ein Sof* above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is drawn down is (primarily) when the *avodah* is in *bitul*, and the matter of *bitul* is in the *avodah* of prayer. Since the exertion in Torah study is for the purpose of understanding and grasping what one is learning, the exertion in Torah—even the exertion of "reviewing his chapter one hundred and one times," although this exertion is not (only) for the sake of understanding Torah but to change his nature and habits—is not the true essence of *bitul*, because even the study of the one hundred and first time is with understanding and grasp. The essence of *bitul* is in the *avodah* of prayer, where the person praying is like a servant before his master. It can be said that even the *avodah* of prayer that is for the sake of Torah study (for "anyone who says I have only Torah, even Torah he does not have"), since the prayer is for the sake of Torah—whose essence is understanding and grasp—is not the true essence of *bitul*. Therefore, the essence of the drawing that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (and certainly the drawing not according to the measure of the *ha'alaah*) is through the *ha'alaas man* of prayer, and through this, it is subsequently drawn into Torah as well. For through the *avodah* that is in Torah [the *avodah* of prayer that is for the sake of Torah, and below that—the *avodah* of reviewing his chapter one hundred and one times to change his nature and habits, and below that—the exertion in *understanding* Torah], the Torah that he learns becomes a vessel for the drawing that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* that comes through prayer.

4) This matter (that through prayer it is subsequently drawn into Torah as well) is also hinted at in the two chapters of *Tehillim* associated with the birthday of the Baal HaGeulah in this year (5742): Chapter 102, which they finished saying on the eve of the birthday, and Chapter 103, which they began saying on the birthday. Psalm 102 begins with the matter of prayer—"A prayer for the afflicted...", and within the prayer itself—a prayer in the ultimate *bitul*: "A prayer for the afflicted when he faints and pours out his speech before Hashem." This is according to the known teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, that the prayer of the afflicted is that he pours out his speech before Hashem. That he does not ask for anything (not even spiritual matters) and his only request is to pour out his speech before Hashem is because of the greatness of his *bitul*. [It can be said that this matter (that he does not want or ask for anything, not even spiritual matters, and only to pour out his speech before Hashem) is similar to the love of "Whom have I in heaven, and besides You I desire none," and in the words of the Alter Rebbe: "I want nothing at all; I do not want Your Gan Eden, I do not want Your Olam Haba... I want nothing but You alone." It can be said that because the Alter Rebbe said "I want nothing but You alone," and especially after this was publicized by the Tzemach Tzedek, the power was given to everyone who follows in his footsteps (who "holds onto the door handle") that in practice, at least, it should be for him something of this nature. Especially through studying the Torah of the Alter Rebbe (and certainly through studying this specific matter), through which one unites in a wondrous union with the Torah of the Alter Rebbe, and through this—with the Alter Rebbe himself.] Further in the Psalm it says, "This shall be written for the last generation...", which refers to the Torah, which is eternal. It can be said that the connection between the two matters is that the eternity of Torah in man's *avodah* is that the Torah he learns is *engraved* in his mind and heart, for then specifically it is impossible for there to be any change (eternity). And for his Torah study to be in the manner of engraving, it is through the preceding *avodah* of prayer. The point of the explanation is that the matter of the engraving of Torah is (primarily) in the Torah as it is in its root, in the level of *Keter* that is above *Chochma*. After it is drawn down and clothed in *Chochma* [from above, and certainly after it descends and is clothed in the intellect of man], it is in the manner of writing. And for Torah study in understanding and grasp to be in the manner of engraving, it is through drawing down the root of Torah (*Keter*) into the Torah below. It can be said that this is what is meant by "This shall be written for the last generation"—"shall be written" is in the future tense—that in order for the Torah he learns to be for him in the category of eternity (for the last generation), he must reach the level of the engraving of Torah that is above the level of writing, and draw from there the level of the writing of Torah, "shall be written" in the future tense. This is the connection of "This shall be written for the last generation" to "A prayer for the afflicted...": through the preceding *bitul* of prayer, and especially when the prayer is in the ultimate *bitul*, that his prayer is to pour out his speech before Hashem, through this he draws down a revelation of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, and this drawing subsequently comes into his Torah study as well: "This shall be written for the last generation."

5) Similarly in Psalm 103, which begins with the matter of prayer—"Bless Hashem, O my soul," which is a prayer of praise and thanksgiving, and within the prayer itself—a prayer in the ultimate *bitul*. The praise and thanksgiving of David to the Holy One, Blessed be He ("Bless Hashem, O my soul") was for every single event, as it is in the Gemara that David lived in five worlds and in every world he said a song (five "Bless Hashem, O my soul"). It can be said that all the events of a person are divided into five types (five worlds), and David said a song to the Holy One, Blessed be He, for all events, for saying a song to the Holy One, Blessed be He, even for matters that are the opposite of good as they appear and are revealed, is because of the greatness and intensity of *bitul*. Further in the Psalm it says, "Bless Hashem, His angels, mighty in strength, who perform His word, to hear the voice of His word"—first "perform" and then "to hear," the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma* which was a preparation for receiving the Torah. It can be said that the connection between the two matters is that the *bitul* of the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma* is not only regarding the fulfillment of *mitzvos* but also in Torah study. For through the fact that before the giving of the Torah they preceded *naaseh* to *nishma*, the power was given to every Jew that his Torah study should be in *bitul*, in the manner of "My tongue shall answer Your word," like one who answers after the speaker, to the extent that his speech (in Torah) is not dependent on his will and his choice, and to the extent that his *bitul* when he occupies himself with Torah is like the *bitul* of "with every word their souls departed." This is the connection of "(perform His word) to hear the voice of His word" to "Bless Hashem, O my soul," for through the *avodah* of prayer, and especially when the prayer is that he says a song for every event (five "Bless Hashem, O my soul"), the *bitul* of prayer is drawn down into his Torah study as well.

**To add** in explaining the connection of "(perform His word) to hear the voice of His word" to the five "Bless Hashem, O my soul": the main innovation in the *bitul* of Torah study is in *Torah Shebaal Peh*, that its study must be with understanding and grasp [for when one does not understand the meaning, it is not considered study] and nevertheless the study is in *bitul*. It is similar to "with every word their souls departed," for although every word is a specific word (for the matter of division belongs to the understanding and grasp of Torah), nevertheless, with every word their souls departed. This is the connection of "to hear the voice of His word" to the five "Bless Hashem, O my soul," for the innovation in the *bitul* of the five times "Bless Hashem, O my soul" (in Psalm 103) over the *bitul* of "pours out his speech before Hashem" (in Psalm 102) is that the *bitul* of "pours out his speech before Hashem" is that nothing matters to him (for his only request is to speak with the King), and the *bitul* of the five "Bless Hashem, O my soul," where he says a song for all events (even for matters that are the opposite of good as they appear and are revealed), is that even the matters associated with his existence are in ultimate *bitul*. And through this *bitul* in prayer, it is subsequently drawn into his Torah study as well, so that even the study in understanding and grasp is in *bitul*.

6) The maamar of the Baal HaGeulah continues (after explaining the two matters of prayer and Torah) that the creation of the world is for the sake of the Jewish people and for the sake of Torah, as it is written, "In the beginning (*Bereishis*) G-d created..."—*Bereishis* is *bei reishis* (two beginnings), for the creation of the world is for the sake of the Jewish people, who are called "beginning," and for the sake of Torah, which is called "beginning." The intent of the creation of the world is that the Jewish people should study Torah as it was given below in this world specifically. It can be said that the connection of the two "beginnings"—the Jewish people and Torah—to what was explained previously regarding prayer and Torah is that prayer is the *avodah* and *bitul* of man (the Jewish people), and therefore the two matters of prayer and Torah belong to the two "beginnings," the Jewish people and Torah. And what is said in the maamar, "that the Jewish people should study *Torah*," can be said because the matter of prayer is *ha'alaah* from below to above (exiting the world), and the intent of the creation of the world is that a revelation of Elokus should be drawn into the world. Therefore, when speaking about the intent of the creation of the world, it also says regarding the Jewish people, "that the Jewish people should study *Torah*." Based on this, one can also explain what is brought in the maamar (continuing the matter that the intent of the creation of the world is that the Jewish people should study Torah) from what our Sages said: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, made a condition with the works of creation: if the Jewish people fulfill My Torah..." and it explains that "if the Jewish people *fulfill* My Torah" is the fulfillment of *mitzvos* [and the phrasing "if the Jewish people fulfill My *Torah*" is because the fulfillment of *mitzvos* must be according to the Torah specifically], because the fact that the world was created for the sake of Torah is (in the language of the maamar) that all *matters of the world* should be according to Torah, and the action of Torah in the world is through the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* of the Torah. 

7) Now, after the maamar explains that the creation of the world is for the sake of the Jewish people and for the sake of Torah, and that the existence of the world is through the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* of the Torah, it continues with an explanation of the difference between the Torah study of an individual and the Torah study of the many, that through the Torah of the many a more sublime light is drawn down. It adds that this is understood *a fortiori* from the fact that through the prayer of the many the drawing is not according to the measure of the *ha'alaah*. From the order of the matters in the maamar, it is implied that the fact that the learning of the drawing through Torah from the drawing through prayer is in the manner of *a fortiori* belongs to what was explained previously regarding the intent of the creation of the world. The explanation for this can be said to be that the intent of a "dwelling in the lower worlds" is that the making of the dwelling (the drawing of the revelation of Elokus into the world) should be through man. And since the *avodah* of prayer is *ha'alaah* from below to above, and the drawing through prayer is from *above*—it is only that it comes *through* prayer (man's *avodah*) —therefore there is an advantage in the drawing through Torah [that the Torah study of man draws down a revelation of Elokus into the world] over the drawing through prayer. According to the known principle that the true matter of "no comparison" is specifically regarding the *Atzmus*, it can be said that the matter of the drawing not according to the measure of the *ha'alaah* is primarily in the drawing through Torah, because in this drawing the intent of a "dwelling in the lower worlds"—the intent of the *Atzmus*—is fulfilled. Based on this, one can explain the order of the matters in the maamar: that the learning of the drawing through Torah from the drawing through prayer is in the manner of *a fortiori* comes (specifically) after the explanation of the intent of creation, because in the drawing through Torah there are two matters: the drawing through Torah from the side of the superiority of Torah itself—this drawing is below the drawing through prayer (as mentioned above in section 3), and the drawing through Torah from the side that through it a revelation of Elokus is drawn into the world through the *avodah* (study) of man—this drawing is above the drawing through prayer, as mentioned above. Therefore, after the explanation of the intent of creation [and that this intent is fulfilled through Torah], it adds that the learning of Torah from prayer is in the manner of *a fortiori*, that there is an advantage in the drawing of Torah over the drawing of prayer.

8) This can be connected with the maamar titled "Hashem is for me among my helpers, and I will see [my desire] upon those who hate me," which the Baal HaGeulah said on the first 12 Tammuz (5687). One must understand the phrase "Hashem is for me among my helpers," for the implication of the language is that there are several helpers (*ozrai*—plural) and the request is that Hashem should also be among the helpers, yet all Jews believe with simple faith that He, blessed be He, alone is the Helper and Savior of man in all his matters. Furthermore, it is not understood, for the implication of the phrase "Hashem is for me among my helpers" is that the main ones are the helpers (plural) and the request is that Hashem should join them. Also, one must understand the phrase "and I will see [my desire] upon those who hate me" (that he will see vengeance upon his enemies), for seemingly he should have requested that they do *teshuvah* and become lovers. Especially since David himself said, "May sins cease, but not sinners." [Furthermore, it is not understood that he says "and I will *see* upon those who hate me," for the sense of sight is one of the most sublime senses, to the extent that one of the innovations that will be in the future is "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh shall *see*..." and similarly regarding the giving of the Torah, one of the main superiorities of the giving of the Torah is "You have been *shown* to know..." and nevertheless David requested "and I will *see* upon those who hate me," that his sight should be in the vengeance of his enemies.] Also, one must understand the connection of "and I will see upon those who hate me" to "Hashem is for me among my helpers."

The point of the explanation (in the maamar) is that "my helpers" refers to the sparks that are clarified through the *avodah* of man, which are the helpers of man. The request "Hashem is for me among my helpers" is that through the *avodah* of clarifying the sparks (the helpers), "Hashem" should be for me, that a revelation of the name *Havayah* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* should be drawn down to him. It can be said that because the drawing of the revelation of the name *Havayah* to man ("Hashem is for me") is through the clarification of the sparks ("among my helpers"), the revelation is in an internal manner. For the revelation that is drawn to him from above by way of *is'arusa d'le'eila* from its own side is in the category of *makif*, and therefore it has no permanence. And similarly regarding the drawing that is drawn to him through his request in prayer. Therefore he says "Hashem is for me *among my helpers*," that the drawing of the revelation of the name *Havayah* to him is not by way of "bread of shame," but that this (as if) comes to him for his *avodah* in the *avodah* of clarifications, the ultimate intent of creation. Through this, "Hashem is for *me*" is effected, that he unites with the revelation, which is why the revelation is a permanent thing forever, for wherever it is said "for me," it never moves forever. 

9) The verse continues, "and I will see [my desire] upon those who hate me," for in the clarification of the sparks there are two matters in general: the clarification of the sparks in *Kelipas Nogah* through the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*, and the clarification of the sparks in the *Gimel Kelipos HaTemei'os* through the *avodah* of *teshuvah*. Therefore, "in the place where *baalei teshuvah* stand, even perfect *tzaddikim* cannot stand," because the root of the sparks that fell into the *Gimel Kelipos HaTemei'os* that are clarified by the *baal teshuvah* is higher than the root of the sparks that fell into *Kelipas Nogah* that are clarified by the *tzaddikim*. Similarly in the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* ("And Your people are all *tzaddikim*"), there is an advantage in the clarification of "matters of permission" through the *avodah* of "all your deeds shall be for the sake of Heaven" over the clarification of physical matters through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. For since "matters of permission," even when one does them for the sake of Heaven, remain "matters of permission" (*your* deeds), therefore, through the clarification of "matters of permission," the intent of a "dwelling in the lower worlds" is fulfilled more—a "lower world" than which there is no lower. Therefore, the elevation that is effected in the *neshamah* through its descent below [for the main elevation is through this, that in its descent below it fulfills the intent of a "dwelling in the lower worlds"] is primarily through the clarification of "matters of permission." This is "and I will see [my desire] upon those who hate me," that through the clarification of the sparks in "those who hate me"—the sparks in forbidden matters, and similarly the sparks in "matters of permission," which are also included in "those who hate me" according to the known teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse "If you see the donkey of your enemy"—they come to a "seeing" in Elokus, "and I will see." 

10) It is explained in many places that the *avodah* of *tzaddikim* is within themselves, and the matter of *teshuvah* is that man also acts upon something outside of himself and illuminates the world. Based on this, it can be said that the matter of "I will see" in general is in addition to the clarification of "matters of permission" ("upon those who hate me"), but also through studying Torah with others. As is implied in the maamar (of 12 Tammuz 5687) that what our Sages said, "He who comes to purify is assisted," the implication of the language "to purify" (*l'taher*—and not *l'hitaher*, to purify oneself) is to purify others, is because the help and assistance of the sparks being clarified ("they assist"—plural, similar to "among my helpers") when he comes to purify others is in a more sublime manner.

Based on this, one can add another matter regarding the superiority of "ten who sit and occupy themselves with Torah," for since "their opinions are not the same," each of the ten has his own explanation (of the matter they are studying), and through studying together and each one saying his explanation to the participants in the *shiur*, there is also the superiority of occupying oneself with Torah with others. Another matter in this: through ten Jews occupying themselves with one matter, in Torah or in prayer or in the fulfillment of a *mitzvah*, a new matter is added to them—the matter of the *tzibbur*, a light that rises above them all. 

11) The language of our Sages is "He who *comes* to purify is assisted." That when he comes to purify others, the assistance is immediately *when he comes* to purify. From this it is understood that all those who have dedicated themselves to fulfilling the mission of the Baal HaGeulah in general, and specifically in the mission to establish *shiurim* in public, through the dedication itself ("throwing oneself into the work," even before the actual deed), assistance and additional strength are drawn down to succeed even more in fulfilling the mission. May it be His will that through the dedication and giving to fulfill the mission of the Baal HaGeulah, and especially *az m'halt shoin in miten* (now that we are already in the middle), and "Hashem is for me" (for each of those involved in this) "among my helpers" to finish the mission in ultimate perfection, we will merit immediately the true and complete *Geulah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. And since we are currently in a "meritorious day"—the third day on which "it was good" was doubled, and the fifteenth day of the month of *Geulah* in which "the moon is in its fullness" (the perfection of the month of *Geulah*), the merit of the meritorious day will hasten even more the *Geulah*, speedily in our days, literally.

## 4 Tammuz, Parshas Pinchas, 16 Tammuz, 5735

### 4 Tammuz, Parshas Pinchas, 16 Tammuz, 5735.

"But the land shall be divided by lot"—the division of Eretz Yisrael, after they had conquered the land of Canaan and transformed it into Eretz Yisrael. Even while Bnei Yisrael were still in the desert (before they entered Eretz Yisrael), it was said of it: "A land which Hashem your G-d seeks out; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year". It is explained that the division of Eretz Yisrael was done by lot, and this was supplemented "by the word of Hashem", which Rashi explains was through Ruach Hakodesh. Furthermore, there was another aspect to the division of the land: "To the larger group you shall increase its inheritance, and to the smaller group you shall decrease its inheritance", which is a matter based on intellect. For the simple explanation of "to the larger group you shall increase," etc., is as Rashi explains [and the explanation of Rashi on the Torah is the *peshuto shel mikra*—the plain meaning of the verse]: that to a tribe which was numerous in population, they gave a larger portion, so the portions were not equal, etc. This division was based on intellect. [And although the Ramban disagrees with this, and there are other interpretations of Rashi, the Ramban interprets Rashi’s intent as being the plain meaning. And even according to the Ramban, and those commentators who interpret Rashi’s words according to the Ramban’s view, the very fact that according to their interpretation the verse needed to negate a division based on intellect proves that this division has a connection to intellect. But the main point discussed here is the plain meaning of the verse and the plain meaning of the explanation of Rashi and the Sifri: that the division was according to the number of people, which is a division based on intellect.] Thus, we find that in the division of the land there were three aspects: by lot, by Ruach Hakodesh, and by intellect, which is also understood by the intellectual soul.

2. The concept of the division of the land by lot is explained by the Tzemach Tzedek, based on a statement of the Alter Rebbe regarding what Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai said: "I do not know by which path they are leading me". Seemingly, this is puzzling; did Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai not walk four amos without Torah and without tefillin, and did he not study and teach Torah for eighty years, etc.? What room was there for doubt as to which path they were leading him? The Alter Rebbe explains that this is from the perspective of the essence of the soul, meaning from the level of the soul that is above *taam v'daas* (intellect). Therefore, Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai said "I do not know," etc., even though he engaged in Torah, etc., because his engagement in Torah was a matter belonging to *taam v'daas*, and there is no proof from that regarding the level that is above *taam v'daas*. And this level, too—since there is the matter of reward and punishment involved in it (as is understood from the very fact that Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai said "I do not know by which path they are leading me")—proves that there is a possibility, ability, and permission granted to every person also regarding this level of the soul. This means that there is an *avodah* that acts even upon the essence of the soul, through which it will be as it should be. This level of the soul, and the *avodah* pertaining to this level, is called by the name *goral* (lot). Based on this, the Tzemach Tzedek explains the matter of the division of the land by lot.

3. Regarding the explanation of the connection between these three things (the *goral* in the soul, in the *avodah* of man, and in the division of the land): all things in the world exist within Yisrael. Especially the portion of the world that specifically belongs to Yisrael, as our Sages say: When He created the world, He divided the lands, etc., and He chose Eretz Yisrael, etc., and He chose Yisrael for His portion, etc. Let Yisrael, who came to My portion, come and inherit the land that came to My portion. Therefore, the Ribono shel Olam gave the entire land of Canaan to Avraham Avinu, to him and his seed after him, as an eternal possession. From this it is understood that the things in Eretz Yisrael are in accordance with the things in Yisrael, and conversely, that the things in Yisrael are in accordance with the things in Eretz Yisrael. And since regarding Eretz Yisrael—in the conquest of the land of Canaan to make it Eretz Yisrael—there were the three things of lot, Ruach Hakodesh, and intellect (which is the matter of "to the larger group you shall increase," etc., and "to the smaller group you shall decrease," etc.), it is understood that these three things exist within Yisrael, meaning in the spirituality of Yisrael [and this matter of "larger" and "smaller" also exists (in the division of Eretz Yisrael) regarding the body (which is secondary), so how much more so does it exist regarding the spiritual, the *neshamah*, which is the primary thing]. And since the purpose of Yisrael is as our Sages say, "I was created to serve my Creator," it is understood that all three of the aforementioned things exist also in the matter of "serving my Creator," in the *avodah* of Hashem.

4. The matter is as follows: It has been explained in the *maamarim* of the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz (as these days come in continuation of the days of redemption), that in Yisrael there are three levels. As they are in the level of "a garden spring," as they are in the level of "a well of living waters," and as they come (through "Rise up, O well, answer to it") to the level of "streams from Levanon." And "streams" (*nozelim*) is from the word *mazal*, for *mazal*, whose nature is above *chochmah* and *binah*, is the matter of *goral*, as explained in many places. It is explained therein that "a garden spring" refers to the *neshamos* as they are above, before they descended below. Then they are called by the name "daughters of Yerushalayim," for Yerushalayim indicates the perfection of *yirah* (awe), as it is stated in Tosafos that Yerushalayim is named for *yirah* and for *shalem* (perfection), and therefore we do not place a *yud* in Yerushalayim (between the *lamed* and the *mem*). Therefore, the *neshamos* as they are above are called by the name "daughters of Yerushalayim" because then they are in the perfection of *yirah*. "A well (of living waters)" refers to the *neshamos* as they have descended below and are clothed in physical bodies, similar to a well that is found in the depths of the earth, etc. However, this descent is for the sake of an ascent, for through the *avodah* of the *neshamah* below, it is specifically elevated to a level higher than it was before its descent. And this is "I am black and comely, O daughters of Yerushalayim"; the *neshamos* that descended below to be clothed in a body and *nefesh habahamit* say to the *neshamos* above, which are called "daughters of Yerushalayim": even though "I am black," because through its descent into this lowest world—than which there is no lower in terms of the concealment of His light—it becomes in a state of blackness, which is the total absence of light; nevertheless, through the fact that "I am black," specifically through this, "I am comely," for it is elevated more than it was above when it was called "daughters of Yerushalayim." For just as a well, through its waters passing through the veins of the earth that hide and conceal the water, undergoes a purification, etc., until they become "living waters," which is a higher elevation than the level of a "spring," and as it is stated in the Mishnah that specifically "living waters" (unlike a spring) purify the three severe impurities, even up to the impurity of a corpse, which is the *avi avos hatumah*—similarly, it is also regarding the *neshamah*.
