Through its descent below and its clothing in the body and *nefesh habahamit* that hide and conceal the light of the *neshamah*, when it is revealed from the covering and concealment through the *avodah* of "The princes dug it, the nobles of the people delved it"—for the matter of digging and delving is the removal of the concealment and hiding of the body and *nefesh habahamit* that hide and conceal the light of the *neshamah* (similar to the digging and delving of a well, which is the removal of the earth, etc., that hides and conceals the water)—there are two aspects in this *avodah*. First, the matter of *hisbonenus* (contemplation), which is called "princes"; second, the matter of the *midos* (emotions) in the heart, which are called "nobles of the people". Through them, one comes to "turn from evil and do good" in practice. Through this specifically, the *neshamah* is elevated higher than it was before its descent, for they become the level of "living waters" (which is higher than the level of "a garden spring"), until through this specifically it comes to the level of "streams from Levanon." This is "I am black and comely"—that specifically through "I am black" comes "I am comely." However, the strength that the *neshamah* in the body has for this *avodah* is drawn to it from its root above. This is the statement to the "daughters of Yerushalayim": "I am black and comely, O daughters of Yerushalayim," meaning that the strength for the *neshamah* in the body to clarify the blackness, etc., and to be "comely" is through the assistance that is drawn (to the *neshamah* in the body) from its root above, which is called "daughters of Yerushalayim."

5. With this it is understood why the song "Rise up, O well, answer to it" was said by Yisrael at the end of forty years, even though the well was given to them from the beginning of the forty years (as mentioned in Rashi on the Torah). For Yisrael who were in the desert, even though they were a "generation of knowledge" (*dor deah*)—and as is explained at length in Kabbalah regarding the greatness of their elevation, that they were *neshamos* of the World of Thought, meaning that even while they were below they were in the level of the World of Thought—nevertheless (from this very fact) they did not have the elevation of the level of "a well of living waters" and "streams from Levanon," because this elevation is achieved specifically through the clarification of physical things. This is why the song "Rise up, O well, answer to it" was said by the generation that entered the land specifically (at the end of forty years, before entering the land), because the matter of Eretz Yisrael is the matter of clarifying physical things specifically, through which the aforementioned elevation is achieved: "The land is very, very good". And since the generation that entered the land stood with *mesiras nefesh* and the desire to enter the "good and spacious land," and especially at the end of forty years, when they already had all the preparation needed for this, and even had already conquered the land of Sichon and Og, which is the beginning of the matter of entering Eretz Yisrael (not just a preparation and introduction to the entry, but also the beginning of the entry; for the land of Sichon and Og is equal to Eretz Yisrael regarding several laws), therefore, specifically at the end of forty years, these miracles occurred that moved Yisrael to say the song "Rise up, O well," etc.

6. The aforementioned singing of the song came through the journeys of Bnei Yisrael (as it is written before that: "From there they traveled and camped across the Arnon," etc., "Therefore it is said," etc.). This is similar to how the entirety of the matter of Torah and *mitzvos* is specifically through a journey, as it is written at the Giving of the Torah: "And Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai" (the journey of Hashem), "And to Moshe He said, 'Ascend to Hashem'" (the journey of Bnei Yisrael). It is the same in the *avodah* of every individual of Yisrael, that the beginning of the *avodah* is "Go for yourself from your land, from your birthplace, and from your father's house"—the departure from one's nature, habits, and coarseness (as explained in *Hemshech* 5666 regarding the details of "your land, your birthplace, and your father's house"). Through this specifically, "And I will bless you and make your name great, and you shall be a blessing," until "And in you shall be blessed all the families of the earth." This is also true regarding the revelation of the future redemption, when the matter of "And in you shall be blessed all the families of the earth" will be in revelation and in ultimate perfection, as it is written: "Then I will turn to the peoples a clear language, that they may all call upon the name of Hashem, to serve Him with one shoulder." The revelation of the future redemption is specifically through the preceding exile. Similar to the song "Rise up, O well," etc. (at the beginning of the entry to the land), which was specifically through the matter of the journeys as mentioned above, so too is it regarding the song "Sing to Hashem a new song" [Tehillim 96, which is the psalm of the Master of the Redemption that was begun on 12 Tammuz], which refers to the song in the future redemption [which is why it says "a new song" (*shir chadash*), in the masculine form, because the future redemption is a complete and eternal redemption after which there is no exile], which comes specifically through the preceding exile. For the matter of exile is (similar to) a development from the matter of "And He drove him out" due to the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, and before that the matter of the "diminishing of the moon". This descent was with prior intent (as the Mitteler Rebbe explains at length regarding the matter of "He is awesome in deed toward the children of men"), so that through the descent there would be afterwards the ultimate elevation and perfection in Yisrael, through which there would automatically be the ultimate elevation and perfection in the entire *Seder Hishtalshelus*, starting from this lowest world, than which there is no lower. Like the parable of the lever: when one wants to lift a house or the like, one must grasp the lever at the lowest part of the house, and through lifting the lowest part specifically, the entire house is lifted. In the same way, it is also regarding the ascent of the worlds, that through the ascent of this lowest world specifically, an ascent is made in all the worlds, an ascent of incomparable nature, similar to what is explained in the *Hemshech* of the *Yom HaHillula* (of the Master of the Redemption), that the matter of "below to no end" belongs to the matter of "above to no end."

7. Based on the above, one can understand the statement of the Master of the Redemption that only the body went into exile, not the *neshamah*. Seemingly, it is stated in the Gemara that exile confuses understanding and comprehension, and how much more so regarding understanding and comprehension in a way of "deriving a ruling from the study," and if so, exile seemingly affects the *neshamos* as well. But one of the explanations for this is based on what is stated in Maseches Eruvin: "Since it is written regarding them, 'At the word of Hashem they would camp and at the word of Hashem they would travel,' it is as if it were established for them." Since the camping is "at the word of Hashem," therefore (even though it is only for a time) it is considered to be judged as permanent. It is the same regarding the time of exile: since it is "at the word of Hashem", therefore the *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos* during the time of exile is in a manner of permanence and eternity. This matter is not a decree, but can also be explained *intellectually* by the Divine soul, according to what is explained in Tanya that the *yichud* (unification) created by Torah study and the performance of *mitzvos* is eternal forever and ever, meaning that this eternal *yichud* (which is above) is also below. This matter can also be explained in the intellect of the *nefesh habahamit* [for the purpose of Torah study is that through the intellect of the Divine soul, the intellect of the *nefesh habahamit* will also be unified in a wondrous unification, etc.]. Since the supreme intent in the descent is for the sake of an ascent, it is simple that the One who caused the descent is the Master of the house, both over the descent and over the ascent, and it is understood that the matter of "descent for the sake of an ascent" is in ultimate perfection, meaning that every detail in the descent is only for the sake of the ascent. And since He, may He be blessed, is the essence of good and it is the nature of the good to do good—to the point that we use the term "nature," *kiviyachol* (as it were)—it is understood that the reason He chose such a great descent is because this is the only way through which it is possible to arrive at this great ascent. Through this contemplation, one also acts upon the *nefesh habahamit* so that it will be in a state of *menuchas hanefesh* (tranquility of soul). Then, not only is the Divine soul not in exile, but the *nefesh habahamit* is also not in exile, for the powers of the *nefesh habahamit* (including the power of intellect) are also in their ultimate perfection. From this perspective, one can have understanding and comprehension in Torah, even to the point of "deriving a ruling from the study" (even during the time of exile), because even from the perspective of his *nefesh habahamit*, he is in a state of *menuchas hanefesh*.

8. Even when one has not reached the aforementioned level, because the explanation that the descent into this lowest world—than which there is no lower, and especially the descent in the "footsteps of Mashiach" (in the lowest world itself), which is a very great descent as explained in the Shas and as we see this tangibly with physical eyes—is only for the sake of the ascent, and therefore it is not a true descent, has not yet been absorbed into his intellect; nevertheless, since he desires and anticipates being at the level of the ascent, through this very fact he is at that level, as the Baal Shem Tov says that where a person’s thought and desire are, there he is. However, since there are external matters that confuse and conceal, the advice given is: "One should not stand to pray except with *koved rosh* (seriousness/reverence)". Prayer is the matter of connection [for this is what they said: "Would that a person pray the entire day", meaning that the entire day should be in such a connection as during prayer, "Know before Whom you are standing"], and the preparation is the matter of *koved rosh*, for through *koved rosh* the confusing things are nullified. Especially according to the teaching of the Maggid that the intent of *koved rosh* is the *koved* (heaviness/seriousness) of the "Head of all heads," and this feeling comes through the contemplation that the *neshamah* is a "part of G-d from above" [in the teaching of the Maggid there, the phrase "part of G-d from above" is cited, without the addition of the word "literally." In this we see the innovation of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in the book Tanya, which is the Written Torah of Chabad Chassidus]. Through this, all the concealing and hiding things are nullified, and immediately his thought is revealed [where he is, as mentioned above], for from the perspective of his thought, he is at the level of the ascent. And from the level of thought—for the essence of this thought is at the level of the soul that is above *taam v'daas*, because this thought is the very essence of man, as it is stated in *Tikkunei Zohar*: "What (*Mah*) is man? Thought (*Machshavah*) is *Mah*... for he is man, thought"—from the level of the soul that is above *taam v'daas*, it is drawn afterwards also into his intellect, so that in his intellect, too, the explanation is absorbed that since "at the word of Hashem they would camp, it is as if it were established for them," and this is drawn afterwards also into action in practice.

9. Similarly, it is also regarding the entirety of the matter of *avodah*, which has three modes: The *avodah* regarding "turning from evil and doing good" in practice, where the action is the primary thing, and similarly "to the larger group you shall increase," etc., and "to the smaller group you shall decrease," etc., for the *avodah* of each person is according to the nature of his portion in the world that was given to him, in which he must act in the two lines of "turning from evil and doing good." Higher than this is the *avodah* that is according to Ruach Hakodesh, and this includes two matters. As is known, Ruach Hakodesh is the level of *Malchus*, which is the tenth *sefirah*, and sometimes it is explained (in the *maamar* "U'shavtem" from the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*) that Ruach Hakodesh is the level of *Chochmah*, from which one draws the Ruach Hakodesh of the level of *Malchus* [similar to the well-known explanation of "Reshis," that in "Bereshis" there are two *Reshis* (Chochmah and Malchus) that become one word], in which all ten *sefiros* are included, meaning that the matter of Ruach Hakodesh also includes the levels and stages in between of *Chochmah* and *Malchus* in the soul. And higher than this is the *avodah* of *goral* (lot), and in this too there are two matters, as the Tzemach Tzedek explains two interpretations regarding the matter of the *goral*: 1) *Emunah* (faith), 2) *Bitul* (nullification) that is above intellect. These two modes are two extremes; the matter of *Emunah* is primarily in the *sefirah* of *Malchus*, which is below and the "end of all levels," and the *Bitul* that is above *taam v'daas* is from the perspective of the essence of the *neshamah* that is above intellect. Through this *Emunah* or this *Bitul*, no doubt remains as to which path they are leading him, and it is a clear thing that they are leading him to all good, and to the ultimate perfection of good, until he merits "You shall see your world in your lifetime", for the level of "But the land shall be divided by lot" is revealed to him, below ten *tefachim*, *neshamah* in body.

10. Just as in the division of Eretz Yisrael upon entering Eretz Yisrael for the first time there were the three aforementioned things ("But the land shall be divided by lot," "at the word of Hashem" through Ruach Hakodesh, and "to the larger group you shall increase," etc., and "to the smaller group you shall decrease," etc.), and through these three things they divided the land in a way that everyone had his vine and his fig tree, and Bnei Yisrael were in rest and tranquility, "each under his vine and under his fig tree"—so too will it be now through our actions and our *avodah*, and even with greater intensity and strength than it was then. Since there was a very great descent in the "footsteps of Mashiach," and especially the imprisonment and exile of the general *neshamos*, the *Nesi'ei Yisrael* (leaders of Yisrael), and even the imprisonment and exile of the *Nasi* of Yisrael of our generation (before 12-13 Tammuz), through his redemption—which the Ribono shel Olam redeemed not only him, but also all those who love our holy Torah, the observers of *mitzvos*, and also those who are called by the name Yisrael—this redemption is a close preparation, a channel, and a vessel to draw down the general redemption of all Bnei Yisrael wherever they are. There will be once again the conquest of Eretz Yisrael, in a way of "And I will grant peace in the land," etc., and "I will lead you upright," through the three modes of *avodah*: *goral*, Ruach Hakodesh, and "to the larger group you shall increase," etc. And the main thing and the foundation—through the decision with strength and *mesiras nefesh*, as the Master of the Celebration says that the matter of *mesiras nefesh* is the decision "like this and not otherwise." And when a Yid says that he decides so, it makes no difference what his situation and standing were the moment before. As the Rambam rules, immediately when he says "I want," his true will is revealed—that every one of Yisrael wants to fulfill the will of the Creator and do everything that depends on him so that the will of the Creator will be fulfilled.

**Through this**, the will of the Creator (who is the essence of good and it is the nature of the good to do good) will also be fulfilled: to take every one of Yisrael out of exile wherever he is, in a way of "And you shall be gathered one by one, O Bnei Yisrael". This manner shows the greatness of the affection, the greatness of the love, and the greatness of the *hashgacha pratis* (Divine providence) upon every one of Yisrael, and He will lead us upright to our land very soon with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## Monday, Parshas Pinchas, 19 Tammuz, 5728

**"Be strong and be a man"**. It is well known that the *maamar* delivered by the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.a.* on the seventh day of the Bar Mitzvah celebration of his only son, the Rebbe, 19 Tammuz 5653 [this *maamar* being the conclusion and seal of the *Hemshech* *Tefillin D’Mari Alma* which he began on 12 Tammuz, the day of the Bar Mitzvah], began with this verse. The connection of this verse ("Be strong and be a man") to a Bar Mitzvah is, on the surface, based on the well-known fact that a thirteen-year-old is obligated in *mitzvos* specifically because he is then called by the name *ish* (man). Yet, one must understand: since a thirteen-year-old becomes a man (by nature), what is the emphasis in saying (at a Bar Mitzvah celebration) "Be strong and be a man"? Furthermore, one must understand that the virtue of a thirteen-year-old is that he then becomes a *bar daas*, for *daas* is in the *mochin*. This is especially true according to what is explained in the *maamar* entitled *Ita B’Medrash Tehillim* 5653 [which is one of the *maamarim* that the Rebbe repeated at his own Bar Mitzvah celebration], that the virtue of a thirteen-year-old is that he then possesses the *etzem* of the *mochin*. What, then, is the precision in calling a thirteen-year-old by the title *ish*, which denotes the *midos*?

**b)** In the part of the *Hemshech* delivered at that time, the superiority of Yosef over Yaakov is explained: the *hemshech* through Yaakov is in *Atzilus*, while through Yosef the *giluy* is drawn (also) into *Biya*. [It may be said that the fact that the *maamar* "Be strong and be a man" speaks of the praise of Yosef—the first name of the Bar Mitzvah boy—is also to arouse him to the special *avodah* of Yosef: to draw the *giluy* down to the very lowest levels.] To explain the greatness of Yosef’s elevation, the *maamar* first explains the greatness of Yaakov, so that through this, one will understand the greatness of Yosef’s elevation, which is even higher. It explains this by prefacing with the verse, "You are Hashem alone, You made the heavens... and You give life to all of them," which are three levels. "You are Hashem alone" refers to the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum* [and it details three matters here: "You," "are," and "Hashem." "You" is the *etzem* of the *Maor*; it uses the term "You" (second person) because the *etzem* is everywhere in *giluy*, for the name of Heaven is common in everyone’s mouth. "Are" and "Hashem" are two levels in the *Ohr*: the *etzem* of the *Ohr* ("are") and the extension of the *Ohr* ("Hashem"), as explained in the *maamar*. It says "alone" regarding this, meaning there is nothing here besides the *etzem*, for the totality of the *Ohr* before the *Tzimtzum*—even the *Ohr* pertaining to the worlds ("Hashem")—is included in His *etzem* and is not in a state of *metzius*]. "You made the heavens..." is the *Ohr* as it becomes a source for the creation of the worlds. Therefore, it is written *es* (את) *asisa* (עשית) *es* (את) *hashamayim*—the word *es* is missing the letter *hei*, because the *Ohr*, even the *Ohr* pertaining to the worlds ("Hashem") as it is before the *Tzimtzum*, is not in the category of being a source for the worlds. For it to be a source for the worlds, it must be through the *Tzimtzum*, where all the *Ohr* is concealed and only a short, constricted *Kav* is drawn. This is "You made the heavens"—*es* is missing the *hei*, because the fact that the *Ohr* becomes a source for the worlds is through it being diminished and reduced (the *es* is missing the *hei*). "And You give life to all of them" is the *Kav* through which *chayus* is drawn to the worlds after they have been created. That is to say, the *Kav* contains two aspects: it is a short and constricted line, and from this perspective, it brings the worlds into being (*metzius* of the worlds); and its extension is from the *Ohr* before the *Tzimtzum*, and from this perspective, it draws *chayus* into the worlds (*giluy Elokus*). This is why "You" here ("And You give life to all of them") is spelled with a *hei*, just like the first "You" ("You are Hashem alone"), because this aspect of the *Kav*—that it gives life to all—is because the *giluy* of the *Ohr* before the *Tzimtzum* is drawn into it.

It may be said that this is why the *maamar* brings (following the statement that "And You give life to all of them" refers to the drawing of the *Kav*) the language of the *Tikkunei Zohar*: "And that flow is like the soul to the body, which is life to the body," in order to emphasize that the intent of "And You give life to all of them" here is not regarding the creation (*al tikrei mechayeh ela mehaveh*), but regarding the *chayus*, just as the soul gives life to the body. This is why the *Kav* is the *berich hatichon* (middle bolt), which bolts and connects the level of "You are Hashem alone" with the level of "You made the heavens," so that even in the worlds that were created through the *Tzimtzum* (the *es* missing the *hei*), the *giluy* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* *habli-gvul* (limitless) from before the *Tzimtzum* ("You are Hashem alone") will be drawn into them.

**c)** The fact that through the *Kav*, the *giluy* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* from before the *Tzimtzum* is drawn into the worlds, indicates that it possesses an advantage even over the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum*. For the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum* was *concealed* by the *Tzimtzum*, and the concealment caused by the *Tzimtzum* exists even in the *Ohr* *habli-gvul* (which is above the *Ohr* that pertains to the worlds), except that the concealment in this *Ohr* is that it is hidden and included in its source and does not shine in *giluy* in the worlds. [The fact that it is explained in many places that the *Tzimtzum* does not conceal the *Ohr* *habli-gvul* refers to the *Ohr* itself (that in His knowledge, it shines in *giluy* even in the place of the *chalal*), but regarding the worlds (which were created from the *Tzimtzum*), the *Tzimtzum* caused the *Ohr* (*habli-gvul*) not to be felt in the worlds]. The fact that through the *Kav*, the *giluy* is drawn into the worlds (so that the *giluy* is felt even in the worlds) indicates that it has an advantage over the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum*, even over the *Ohr* *habli-gvul*. As the *maamar* explains, the fact that the *Kav* pierces the darkness of the *Tzimtzum*—and every piercing is due to strength—is because the root of its extension is even higher than the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum*. The explanation for this is that the reason the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum* cannot come into *giluy* in the worlds created from the *Tzimtzum* is because the *Ohr* (which is *giluy*) and the *Tzimtzum* (which is concealment) are opposites. The fact that through the *Kav*, the *giluy* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* from before the *Tzimtzum* is drawn, is because the root of the *Kav* is from the *Tiferes* that is concealed, which includes and connects the opposites: *giluy* and *Tzimtzum*.

Based on this, we can explain that the three matters in the verse ("You are Hashem alone," "You made the heavens," and "You give life to all of them"), which all begin with the word "You"—where "You" denotes the *etzem* (as mentioned in section b)—are three modes of the *giluy* of the *etzem*. "You are Hashem alone" is the *giluy* of the *Ein Sof* and the *habli-gvul* of the *etzem*, which is present everywhere and besides which there is no *metzius*—"You are Hashem *alone*". "You made the heavens..." is the *giluy* of the power of limitation within the *etzem* (the ability not to shine), and higher still—the matter of His *metzius* being from His *etzem*, as is known that the creation of *yesh* ("You made the heavens") is only through the power of the *etzem*, whose *metzius* is from His *etzem*. And "You give life to all of them" is the *giluy* of the simplicity of the *etzem*, which is not defined by the definitions of *giluy* and concealment, and therefore it connects both as one.

This is the meaning of "And You give life to all of them"—"And You" with an additional *vav*, which denotes the *giluy* of the *etzem* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* in the middle *Kav* (*Tiferes*), which connects the two opposites of *Chesed* and *Gevurah*. As is known regarding "the Great, the Mighty, and the Awesome", which correspond to the three *kavim* (*Chagas*): the fact that "and the Awesome" is written with an additional *vav* is because in *Tiferes* there is the *giluy* of the *etzem* of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the division of the *kavim* (*E-l Elyon*), and through this, it connects the two opposites of *Chochmah* and *Gevurah*. This is also one of the explanations for why Yaakov (*Tiferes*) is the letters of *yivaka* (יבקע—will break forth), as in "Then your light will break forth (*yivaka*) like the dawn", for the fact that the *Ohr* (the *Ohr* of the *Kav*) breaks through the darkness of the *Tzimtzum* (and is drawn even into the worlds created from the *Tzimtzum*) is because the root of its extension is from *Tiferes* (the concealed), the *midah* of Yaakov.

**d)** It is known that the extension of the *Kav* terminates in *Atzilus*, as explained in the *maamar*, that Yaakov (the letters of *yivaka*, the breaking forth of the *Kav*) is the *berich hatichon* that bolts from one end to the other—from the end of the heavens above to the end of the heavens below. The end of the heavens below is the end of *Atzilus*. For the *giluy* to exist also in *Biya*, it is through Yosef, as it is written, "And Yosef was the ruler over the land," for through Yosef, the *giluy* is drawn into the land, *Biya*. This is "These are the generations of Yaakov: Yosef", for Yosef draws the *giluyim* of Yaakov so that they shine in *Biya*. This is similar to the difference between the Patriarchs and the Giving of the Torah (for Yosef is associated with the Giving of the Torah, because the Giving of the Torah was through Moshe, and "Moshe took the bones of Yosef with him"), for the extension through the performance of the *mitzvos* of the Patriarchs was in *Atzilus*, and at the Giving of the Torah, it was innovated that the *giluy* would be drawn also into *Biya*. The fact that the *maamar* says that Yosef draws the *giluyim* of *Yaakov* to shine in *Biya* implies that Yosef drawing the *giluy* into *Biya* is because Yosef is the "generations of Yaakov," meaning that through him, the *pnimiyus* of Yaakov—the letters of *yivaka*—is revealed. For from the perspective of the *inyan* of breaking forth (for the true *inyan* of breaking forth is that it has no measurements or limitations), it is possible for the extension to reach even into *Biya*, except that this *inyan* of Yaakov (*yivaka*) is revealed through Yosef.

This can be understood based on the well-known fact that the reason the extension of the *Kav* terminates in *Atzilus* is because the intent of the extension of the *Kav* is that the *Ohr* should be in a state of *hislabshus* (enclothement), and the *hislabshus* of the *Ohr* can only be in matters (*keilim* and worlds) that are *Elokus*. For the extension and *giluy* of the *Kav* to be in *Biya*, it is through the extension of the *Ohr Sovev*, which in general is the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum*, and within the *Ohr* from before the *Tzimtzum* itself—the *Ohr* *habli-gvul* (which is above the *Ohr* that shines to the worlds). The explanation for this is that the *Ohr* *habli-gvul*, since the *Tzimtzum* does not conceal it, shines in *giluy* (even after the *Tzimtzum*) everywhere, even in *Biya*, except that this is only in His knowledge, and in the worlds, it is not felt (as mentioned in section c). Through it shining in the *Kav* from the *Ohr* before the *Tzimtzum*, the *Kav* itself is made in such a way that it is drawn and revealed even in *Biya*.

Based on this, we can explain the difference between the breaking forth of Yaakov—the letters of *yivaka* (as it is from its own perspective)—and the breaking forth of Yaakov—the letters of *yivaka*—as it is revealed through Yosef. The breaking forth of Yaakov (from its own perspective) is the breaching and nullification of the definitions of *giluy* and *Tzimtzum* [by revealing the simplicity (*Tiferes* the concealed) which is not defined by these definitions], and through this, the *giluy* is drawn (also) into the worlds that were created from the *Tzimtzum*. But the definitions within the *giluy* itself still remain: the distinction between the *giluy* in the category of *Sovev* and the *giluy* in the category of *hislabshus*. The *giluy* in the category of *Sovev* is everywhere, while the *giluy* in the category of *hislabshus* has measurement and limitation, as it can only be in matters that are *keilim* for *giluy*. The breaking forth of Yaakov—the letters of *yivaka*—as it is revealed through Yosef, is the breaching and nullification even of the definitions within the *giluy* itself, so that even the *giluy* in the category of *hislabshus* can be everywhere.

**e)** Based on this, we can also explain what is said in the *maamar* that the reason the *giluy* in *Biya* is specifically through Yosef is because Yosef is the level of *Yesod* (the completion of the *hashpaah*), and the essence of *taanug* and joy is in the completion of the *hashpaah*, as explained there at length. Therefore, it is specifically through Yosef that the *giluy* is drawn into *Biya*. One must understand what the connection is between the *inyan* of *giluy* in *Biya* and the *taanug* and joy in the completion of the *hashpaah*, and why the *taanug* and joy in the beginning and middle of the *hashpaah* are not sufficient (for this *giluy*). The explanation for this is that the virtue of the *taanug* and joy in the completion of the *hashpaah* [where the intent here of "completion of the *hashpaah*" is that the *shefa* was received *k’tov* (well) by the recipient] is that the *taanug* reaches the *etzem* that is above the root of the *hashpaah*. As is known regarding the concept of "the end of the act is in the initial thought", the end of the act is the receiving of the *hashpaah*, and this reaches the "initial thought," meaning the beginning that is before (and above) the beginning of the thought—the root of the *hashpaah*. Therefore, specifically through the *taanug* and joy in the completion of the *hashpaah*, the breaching and nullification of the definitions of *giluy* (the *hashpaah*) occurs, and through this, even the *giluy* in the category of *hislabshus* (the *giluy* of the *Kav*) is revealed even in *Biya*.

**f)** The *maamar* continues that this is what is said in the *Shelah* that Yaakov is *Tefillin* of the head and Yosef is *Tefillin* of the hand. For through *Tefillin* of the head, the connection (*Tefillin* from the word *hitchabrus*—connection) of the *Ohr Ein Sof* the *Matzil* with the *Netzalim* is made, which draws additional *Ohr* into *Abba*, *Imma*, and *Ze’er Anpin* of *Atzilus*. And through *Tefillin* of the hand, which is in *Malchus* [as it is written, "And you shall bind them as a sign upon your hand (*yadcha*), a weak hand (*yad keihah*)," for the weak hand is *Malchus*], the connection of the *Ohr Ein Sof* (also) with the created beings is made. [This is why *Tefillin* of the head is called *pe'er*, like an ornament with which a person adorns himself, and *Tefillin* of the hand are only a garment, because *Biya* are garments, and the *Eser Sefiros* of *Atzilus* are called *tikkunim*, for *tikkunim* are like ornaments]. This is why Yaakov is *Tefillin* of the head and Yosef is *Tefillin* of the hand, for Yaakov is the *berich hatichon* that bolts and connects the *Ohr Ein Sof* with the *Netzalim*, and Yosef is the connector [“*Ben poras Yosef*”, *poras* is the letters of *tofer* (sews), sews and connects] of the *Ohr Ein Sof* with the created beings.

One must understand: since for there to be an extension in *Biya*, there must first be the extension in *Atzilus*, why do we put on *Tefillin* of the hand before *Tefillin* of the head? The explanation for this is based on the well-known fact that the *mitzvos* of the *Ribono shel Olam* that are performed through the Jewish people fulfilling the *mitzvos* are higher than the *mitzvos* of the *Ribono shel Olam* as they are from His own perspective. One may add that in the *mitzvah* of *Tefillin*, this matter is even more so. For since "What is written in the *Tefillin* of the Master of the World... and who is like Your people Israel, one nation on earth," for the *Ribono shel Olam* praises Himself with the praise of the Jewish people—in this, the *avodah* of the Jewish people, the putting on of *Tefillin* by the Jewish people, is even more relevant. Therefore, we put on *Tefillin* of the hand before *Tefillin* of the head, because the virtue of *avodah* is primarily in the *avodah* of *Yichuda Tata’ah* (*Biya*), and therefore the *avodah* of *Yichuda Tata’ah* reaches higher than the *avodah* of *Yichuda Ila’ah* (*Atzilus*). The addition made to the *Tefillin* of the Master of the World [the extension of *Ohr Ein Sof* in *Atzilus* (*Tefillin* of the head) and *Biya* (*Tefillin* of the hand] through the putting on of *Tefillin* by the Jewish people is primarily through the putting on of *Tefillin* of the hand.

The fact that through the performance of the *mitzvos* by the Jewish people an elevation is added to the *mitzvos* of the *Ribono shel Olam* is because the Jewish people "arose in thought", an essential thought that is above all *giluyim* (even from the *giluy* of *Chafetz Chesed*, which is the root and cause of all *giluyim*). Therefore, through the *avodah* (performance of *mitzvos*) of the Jewish people, an elevation is added to the *mitzvos* of the *Ribono shel Olam*. Based on this, we can say another reason why the addition to the *Tefillin* of the Master of the World is primarily through the putting on of *Tefillin* of the hand: because the extension in *Biya* (*Tefillin* of the hand) reaches the *etzem* that is above the root of the *hashpaah* and *giluy* (as mentioned in section e), which in general is the level of the essential thought mentioned above.

**g)** This is "Be strong and be a man." The fact that a thirteen-year-old becomes a man by nature is a matter that is from above, from the fact that the *Ribono shel Olam* implanted nature in creation. Since the primary virtue of any matter is when it comes through the *avodah* of man (as discussed at length above), therefore it must be "Be strong and be a man," that he should become a man (also) through his *avodah*. Based on this, we can also explain the precision of "Be strong and be a *man* (*ish*)," for *ish* denotes the *midos*, even though the virtue of a thirteen-year-old is in the *mochin*, that he possesses the *etzem* of the *mochin* which is above the *inyan* of the *midos*. For the virtue of the *avodah* of man that reaches the essential thought is primarily in the *avodah* of drawing the *etzem* of the *mochin* (which is above the *inyan* of the *midos*) into the *midos*, similar to what was explained above regarding Yosef, who draws the *giluy* of *Atzilus* (which is above the root of the created beings) into *Biya*.

One should connect all this with the *avodah* of the Rebbe, the Yosef of our generation, for the *maamar* entitled "Be strong and be a man" was delivered at the conclusion and seal of his Bar Mitzvah celebration, and his primary *avodah* was "May your springs spread outward," so that even in the outermost *chutza*—the lowest level, below which there is no *chutza*—there should be drawn (in addition to the waters drawn from the springs, also) the springs themselves. This (the spreading of the springs outward) is the preparation and the *keli* for the imminent arrival of our righteous Moshiach.

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5722

### B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5722

"The glory of this latter House shall be greater than the former," and there are two interpretations of this. The simple interpretation is that "this latter House" refers to the Second Beis Hamikdash, which was greater than the First in its structure and in the years it stood. However, in the Zohar it is stated that "this latter House" refers to the Third Beis Hamikdash, which will be built speedily in our days, which will be greater than both the First and the Second—for both of them are included in the "former," as neither of them possessed permanence, whereas the Third House will exist with eternal permanence. This is what our Sages meant when they said: "Not like Avraham, of whom it is written 'a mountain,' nor like Yitzchak, of whom it is written 'a field,' but like Yaakov, whom he called a 'house.'" The First House corresponds to Avraham, the Second to Yitzchak, and the Third to Yaakov. It is explained in Likutei Torah that the connection of the Third House to Yaakov is because Yaakov’s attribute is *emes* (truth), and *emes* is something in which there is no possibility of interruption or change.

b) Now, although the aforementioned statement of our Sages ("Not like Avraham...") speaks of the Beis Hamikdash, the language in Likutei Torah there is that there are three *geulos*: the first *geulah* in the merit of Avraham, the second *geulah* in the merit of Yitzchak, and the third *geulah* in the merit of Yaakov. It explains there that the third *geulah* is an eternal *geulah*. The simple explanation for this is that one of the foundations of the *geulah* is the building of the Beis Hamikdash. Through the addition of greatness to the Beis Hamikdash, the *geulah* becomes more elevated. Therefore, Likutei Torah links the greatness of the third *geulah* with the greatness of the Third Beis Hamikdash.

One may add that the reason Likutei Torah speaks of the greatness of the third *geulah* is because the third *geulah* is even more elevated than the greatness of the Third Beis Hamikdash. This is understood from the fact that the *geulah* (the ingathering of the exiles) will take place *after* the building of the Beis Hamikdash. Yet, even this greatness comes about through the Third Beis Hamikdash (which is why it is learned in Likutei Torah from the greatness of the Third Beis Hamikdash), because the building of the Third Beis Hamikdash will include all the matters and greatnesses that will occur thereafter. Based on what is written in the Zohar regarding the order of events that will occur in the future—that *techiyas hameisim* is the last of all—it can be said that the revelation of the greatness of the Third Beis Hamikdash (the *emes* in which there is no interruption or change) will be primarily in *techiyas hameisim*, when there will be eternal life. This can be connected to the verse, "He will revive us after two days; on the third day He will raise us up, and we will live before Him." There are two interpretations of "on the third day": that it refers to the Third Beis Hamikdash, and that it refers to *techiyas hameisim*. The connection between these two interpretations is that in *techiyas hameisim*, the greatness of the Third Beis Hamikdash will be revealed.

c) This can be understood by prefacing the statement of our Sages: "A lion arose in the sign of the lion and destroyed Ariel (the Beis Hamikdash), so that a lion might come in the sign of the lion and build Ariel." From this it is understood that what is said, "The glory of this latter House shall be greater than the former," applies even if the First Beis Hamikdash had not been destroyed and had possessed eternal existence. Therefore, "a lion arose... and destroyed Ariel" so that "a lion might come and build Ariel," which would be greater than the first (even if it had possessed eternal existence). This is similar to the greatness of *baalei teshuvah* over *tzaddikim*, for the *avodah* of *tzaddikim* (even *tzaddikim* who have no *yetzer hara*, and whose *avodah* is therefore in a manner of eternal existence) reaches within *seder hishtalshelus*, while the *avodah* of *baalei teshuvah* is above *hishtalshelus*. This is the meaning of "a lion arose and destroyed Ariel so that a lion might come and build Ariel." It is known that "a lion will come" (this is Hashem, as it is written, "A lion has roared, who will not fear?") is the revelation of the *Keter* that is above *hishtalshelus*. One may add that even according to the statement of our Sages that when they ascended from Bavel it was fitting for this (the Third Beis Hamikdash) to be built, nevertheless, the Third House that will be in the future (after the Second House) will be greater. For even though when they ascended from Bavel (after the destruction of the First House and the *tikkun* for it) they were like *baalei teshuvah*, *teshuvah* has many levels. Therefore, there was also the destruction of the Second House, so that through the *avodah* in the *galus* after the destruction of the Second House, they would reach the perfection of *teshuvah*, and thereby the glory of this latter House would be in the ultimate perfection.

Based on this, we can explain what our Sages said regarding the verse, "Hear the word of Hashem, O house of Yaakov": "Hear the words of Torah before you hear the words of prophecy; hear the words of prophecy before you hear the words of rebuke..." and it concludes: "Hear your bodies before your bones hear; the dry bones, hear the word of Hashem." Seemingly, when it says "Hear the words of Torah before you hear the words of prophecy," it is because the words of prophecy are to command regarding the words of Torah, and therefore, if they had heard the words of Torah, they would not have needed the words of prophecy. Similarly, regarding the words of prophecy themselves, if they had heard the words of prophecy of the earlier prophets—which command regarding the words of Torah not in a manner of rebuke—they would not have needed the words of rebuke (and similarly regarding the matters that followed). But the conclusion, "before your bones hear," is not understood: how can it be said that if they had heard the words of Torah or the words of rebuke, they would not have merited *techiyas hameisim*, G-d forbid? The explanation is that through the descent of not hearing the words of Torah, etc., *techiyas hameisim* will be in a more elevated manner, similar to the Third Beis Hamikdash, which will be greater because it will be after the descent of the destruction of the Second House.

d) The explanation of the greatness of the Third House over the First and Second (even over the Second as it was fitting to be in the form of the Third) can be understood by prefacing the greatness of the Beis Hamikdash (in general), which includes the greatness of the place of the *Mikdash*. For the place of the *Mikdash* (even before the building of the Beis Hamikdash) is more elevated than the place of the entire world, as it is written, "How awesome is this place; this is none other than the house of Elokus," and Onkelos translates this as "there is no common place here." The place of the entire world is a "common place" because it was created through the ten *maamaros*, which are called "common words," while the place of the *Mikdash* is not a "common place" [even though the place of the *Mikdash* was also created through the ten *maamaros*. On the contrary, the beginning and essence of the creation from the ten *maamaros* was the creation of the *Even Shetiyah* in the *Mikdash*, and from it the entire world was founded], because in the ten *maamaros* it says "And Elokim said," whereas in the place of the *Mikdash* there was a revelation of the name *Havayah*, as it is written, "Indeed, *Havayah* is in this place."

This requires explanation, for seemingly, the greatness of the place of the *Mikdash* over the place of the entire world is in the revelation that was in the Beis Hamikdash, not in the place itself, for the place of the *Mikdash* was also created through the ten *maamaros* ("common words"), and the meaning of "there is no common place here" is that the place itself is not a common place. The point of the explanation is based on what is written in Tanya, that the existence of the world is from the name *Havayah* (*Havayah* is from the word *mehoveh*—bringing into being), but if the existence were from the name *Havayah* itself, the world would be nullified in its existence, and therefore the actual existence was through the name *Elokim*. The existence of the place of the *Mikdash* was in a manner where the name *Elokim* does not conceal the name *Havayah*. This is "there is no common place here," because in the place of the *Mikdash*, the existence was felt in revelation as it is from the name *Havayah*.

The matter is that the existence from the name *Elokim* is by way of *hislabshus* ("In the beginning *Elokim* created"), and the existence from the name *Havayah* is in a manner of "automatically" ("Praise the name of *Havayah*, for He commanded and they were created"). The difference in the manner of existence (whether the existence is "automatically" or by way of *hislabshus*) indicates the relationship of the thing being brought into existence to the source that brings it into existence. When the thing being brought into existence is close to the one bringing it into existence, its existence is "automatically." Just as with cause and effect: since the effect is in proportion to the cause, the existence of the effect from the cause is "automatically" [like intellect and emotions; since the emotion is in proportion to the intellect, through contemplation, the emotion that corresponds to the contemplation comes about automatically]. Similarly, it is like light and the luminary: since the light is a revelation of the luminary, the emergence of the light from the luminary is "automatically." But when the thing being brought into existence is at a distance from the one bringing it into existence, its existence is by way of *hislabshus*, where the one bringing it into existence engages and exerts effort to bring the thing into existence.

[The reason for this is that in existence that is "automatically," the primary emphasis is the revelation of the source. Therefore, even though in cause and effect (where the existence of the effect from the cause is "automatically"), the effect is not a revelation of the cause but an entity unto itself, nevertheless, the cause is felt within it. Like intellect and emotions, where the intellect is felt in the emotions. But in order to bring into existence something that is at a distance from its source, it must be by way of *hislabshus*. For the matter of *hislabshus* is (not that the source is revealed, but on the contrary) that it clothes itself (and engages) to bring into existence a new thing. Therefore, the thing brought into existence through *hislabshus* is at a distance from its source, in such a way that its source is not felt within it. It can be said that this is similar to the matter of *koach* and *po'al* (potential and action). The reason that the extension of the action from the *koach* is not "automatically" but through *hislabshus* (where the *koach* *acts* to produce the action) is because the action is at a distance from the *koach*. It is known that the action is a novelty relative to the *koach*. Since the *koach* is spiritual and the action is physical, the extension of the action from the *koach* is (like) a new existence (*similar* to *yesh me'ayin*). The matter of *koach* is that it has the power to act to produce a new thing. From this it is understood that the fact that one knows the *koach* from the action is *through* the action that one knows the *koach*. But in the action *itself*, the *koach* is not felt. Since the *koach* is spiritual and the action is physical, the spiritual *koach* is not revealed in the physical action. One may add that the fact that the *koach* is not felt in the action is not only from the side of the action (which is incomparable to the *koach*) but also from the side of the *koach*. Since the action of the *koach* is to create a new thing that is not in its proportion (as above), the extension of the *koach* to act is a hidden extension [for the action of a new thing that is not in proportion to its source is through the concealment of the source. For only after the revelation of the source is stopped is it possible for there to be a thing that is not in its proportion]. Therefore, the action coming from the *koach* is in a manner where the *koach* is not felt within it.]

Similarly, above, the existence from the name *Elokim*, which is by way of *hislabshus*, is in a manner where the *koach* that brings into existence is not felt in the created beings. Therefore, the created beings that came into existence from the name *Elokim* are an *yesh* (an independent reality), and their *bitul* is only *bitul hayesh*. But the existence from the name *Havayah*, which is "automatically," is in a manner where it is in revelation in the created beings. Therefore, the *bitul* of the created beings that came into existence from the name *Havayah* is *bitul bimtzius*.

e) It is known that when two (or more) parables are brought in the discourses of Chassidus for a certain matter, it is because no single parable corresponds to the *nimshal* (the concept being explained) in *all* details. Therefore, they bring two (or more) parables, each of which explains *some* details of the *nimshal*. So it is in our case: the reason they bring two parables for the fact that in existence that is "automatically," the thing being brought into existence is close to the one bringing it into existence—the parable of cause and effect and the parable of light and the luminary—is because in the *nimshal*, even in the existence that is "automatically," a new thing is brought into existence that is not in proportion to the source bringing it into existence. This is also understood from the fact that even in the existence from the name *Havayah*, it is written "for He commanded *and they were created*," for the term "creation" indicates existence *yesh me'ayin*, and *yesh me'ayin* is incomparable. The fact that the existence from the name *Havayah* is in a manner where it is in revelation in the created beings that came into existence from it (as in section d), the intention of this is that it is felt in them that they are not an independent reality, and their entire reality is that the Divine light brings them into existence *me'ayin l'yesh*. Through this feeling, they are nullified to their source. But it is not that it is in revelation in the created beings themselves (their essence and greatness). Since the created beings are incomparable to it, it is impossible for a light that is not in their proportion at all to be revealed in them, similar to how it is impossible for the revelation of the spiritual *koach* to be in a physical action (as mentioned there). [To add: in *koach* and *po'al*, since the essence of *koach* is to act and its action is by way of *hislabshus*, therefore, in the fact that the *koach* *acts* to produce the action, the *koach* is revealed (only it is not revealed in the action itself). This is not so in the existence from the name *Havayah*; since the existence from the name *Havayah* is "automatically," which indicates that it is wondrous/transcendent to the matter of existence, it is not revealed even through the *existence* of the created beings, since it is transcendent to the matter of existence.] Therefore, the parable of cause and effect does not correspond to the *nimshal*, because in cause and effect, the closeness of the effect to the cause is that the effect is *in proportion* to the cause, and the revelation of the cause is in the effect itself. [Like intellect and emotions, which are cause and effect, where in the emotion itself the intellect that gave birth to it is recognizable. When one is aroused to love for something because one has understood and grasped with one's intellect that the thing is good for one, it is felt in the love itself that one's love for the thing is from the good within it. And the manner of the love is like the manner of the good of the thing.] In order to explain that even when the thing being brought into existence is incomparable to the source bringing it into existence, it is nevertheless close to its source, this is done through the parable of light and the luminary. For even though the light is only an illumination that is incomparable to the luminary [which is why the luminary is not revealed in the light; through the light one knows only the existence of the luminary, not its essence], nevertheless, it is close to the luminary, for its source is felt within it and it is nullified to it.

However, even the parable of light and the luminary is not sufficient, because in light and the luminary, the closeness of the light to the luminary and its nullification to it is in a manner where the light is not an independent reality at all, and its entire essence is that it is a revelation of the luminary. This is not so in the *nimshal*; even in the existence from the name *Havayah*, it is written "for He commanded *and they were created*," for the matter of creation is (not a spreading out and revelation of the source, but) the bringing into existence of a thing. This is also understood from what is written in Tanya, that even if the existence were from the name *Havayah* not through the *tzimtzum* of the name *Elokim*, the created beings would come into existence *me'ayin l'yesh* (only then they would be nullified in the ultimate sense, like the nullification of the sun's radiance in the sun). In order to explain that even the existence of a thing is in closeness to its source, this is done through the parable of cause and effect. For even though the effect is a reality and not a revelation of the cause, nevertheless, it is in closeness to the cause.

It can be said that the reason the parable of cause and effect is brought *before* the parable of light and the luminary is because the main novelty in the fact that the created beings that come into existence from the name *Havayah* are nullified to *Havayah* is that even though they are created beings (a reality of a thing), nevertheless, the light of the name *Havayah* is felt in them in revelation, and this matter is understood specifically from the parable of cause and effect. However, in order to explain that the revelation of the source exists even in a thing that is incomparable to the source, they add the parable of light and the luminary.

f) It is known that the fact that the world is defined by the parameters of place and time is because its existence is through the name *Elokim*. If it were to come into existence from the name *Havayah* (*Hayah, Hoveh, V'yihyeh* as one), it would not be defined by the parameters of place and time. This is what is written regarding the Beis Hamikdash: "Indeed, *Havayah* is in this place," because in the Beis Hamikdash, the place was above the parameter of place; "the place of the Ark is not of the measurement." However, the revelation that shone in the Beis Hamikdash was the revelation of the name *Havayah* as it shines in the name *Elokim*. For the name *Havayah* as it is from its own side is above the parameter of place, and the fact that the Holy of Holies was a measured and limited place (twenty cubits by twenty cubits), and the Ark was also in a measurement of place (two and a half cubits its length and a cubit and a half its width), and nevertheless "the place of the Ark is not of the measurement," is the matter of the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim*. One must understand: since even in the existence from the name *Havayah*, a new thing is brought into existence that is incomparable to the source bringing it into existence [and the revelation of the name *Havayah* in the world that came into existence from it is only in the matter of *bitul*, that it is felt in them that their reality is only that the Divine light brings them into existence every moment], then even in the world as it came into existence from the name *Havayah*, there should seemingly be the limitation of time and place.

It can be said that the explanation for this is by prefacing that from the fact that we say *Havayah* is *Hayah, Hoveh, V'yihyeh* (as one)—and *Hayah, Hoveh, V'yihyeh* is the matter of time—it is understood that even the world as it comes into existence from the name *Havayah* has the matter of time, but the time in this world is in a manner where the past, present, and future are as one. Similarly, it is with place; even the world as it comes into existence from the name *Havayah* has the matter of place, but the six extremities of place are as one. Based on this, it can be said that the reason the time and place of the world as it comes into existence from the name *Havayah* are not in limitation and division (even though the world as it comes into existence from the name *Havayah* is also incomparable to the source bringing it into existence) is because of the *bitul* within it. Since the essence of the past, present, and future (and likewise the essence of the six extremities) is not their reality, but that *Havayah* brings them into existence, therefore they do not contradict one another and are as one.

Based on this, it must be said that what is explained in many places that the place of the Holy of Holies is from the name *Elokim* (even though this place was also above the parameter of place) is because the place of the Holy of Holies (twenty cubits by twenty cubits) was in a manner of division, where every cubit is in a different place, and the division of place is from the name *Elokim*. This is "the place of the Ark is not of the measurement," which is the matter of the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim*, that the limitation and division of the place of the Ark is from the side of *Elokim*, and the fact that it was "not of the measurement" is from the side of the revelation of the name *Havayah* that shone in revelation in the place that came into existence from the name *Elokim*—the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim*.

g) One must understand: the fact that from the side of the name *Elokim* is the division of place and time is because time and place as they come into existence from the name *Elokim* are a reality. When it is felt in the six extremities of place and in the past, present, and future of time that their essence is *that Elokus* brings them into existence, they are all as one (as in section f). How is it possible that in the place of the Ark (a place that is in division, which indicates that it is a *reality*) there should be the revelation of the name *Havayah* ("not of the measurement")? The point of the explanation is that the *tzimtzum* and concealment of the name *Elokim* is only relative to the created beings, but relative to the name *Havayah*, it does not conceal at all. Therefore, even after the *hislabshus* of the name *Havayah* in the name *Elokim*, through which the world becomes a reality, nevertheless, the reality does not conceal relative to it. And even in the reality (which was made through the concealment of the name *Elokim*), through which the division of place and time was made, the revelation of the name *Havayah* shines, for the essence of the world is that *Havayah* brings it into existence. As is known the parable of the teacher and the student: when the student is incomparable to the teacher, the teacher must conceal the essence of his intellect and let only the externality remain, and the externality also must be limited and concealed in garments, explanations, and parables. The *tzimtzum* and concealment is only relative to the student and not relative to the teacher. The teacher sees the essence of his intellect even in the externality and even in the garments and parables.

[To add: in the parable of the teacher and the student, the fact that relative to the teacher the *tzimtzum* does not conceal is *after* the *tzimtzum*, the internal aspect of the intellect shines for him even in the externality and even in the garments and parables. This is not so above; the fact that the *tzimtzum* is not as it literally seems (i.e., that the *tzimtzum* does not conceal relative to *Ohr Ein Sof*) is two matters: that after the *tzimtzum*, *Ohr Ein Sof* shines in actual revelation in the place of the *chalal* just as before the *tzimtzum*, and that even at the time of the *tzimtzum*, the *tzimtzum* does not conceal relative to it, as explained at length in the discourses. Based on this, it is understood even more that even in the reality that was made through the concealment of the name *Elokim*, the revelation of the name *Havayah* shines, for in the parable of the teacher and the student, the *tzimtzum* itself is a concealment even relative to the teacher, for at the time of the *tzimtzum*, the intellect is concealed even for the teacher. Therefore, even after the *tzimtzum*, when the teacher sees the essence of his intellect even in the garments and parables, this does not belong to the garments themselves. This is not so above; even the *tzimtzum* itself does not conceal relative to *Ohr Ein Sof*, and therefore, the revelation of the name *Havayah* shines even in the reality itself. Based on this, the phrase "there is no common place here" *that the place of the Mikdash* is not a common place [and similarly the phrase "the place of the Ark is not of the measurement," *that the place* is not of the measurement] is understood even more, because the revelation of the name *Havayah* is in the place itself.]

h) The explanation of the matter of "there is no common place here" in greater depth will be understood by prefacing that in the matter of the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim*—*Havayah* and *Elokim* are all one—there are two general explanations. That even the name *Elokim* (*tzimtzum*) its essence is to reveal, for in order for the revelation of the name *Havayah* to be drawn down below, it is through the *tzimtzum* and concealment of the name *Elokim*. And another explanation: that the two names *Havayah* and *Elokim* are the names of the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is above both of them, but it so arose in His will, may He be blessed, that His revelation should be in the two lines of *bli gevul* and *gevul* (revelation and *tzimtzum*). Based on this, one can add an explanation in the fact that above, even the *tzimtzum* itself does not conceal relative to *Ohr Ein Sof* (in addition to the explanation in the discourses), that since even the *tzimtzum* of the name *Elokim* is one with *Havayah*, it is impossible for it to conceal relative to it. Based on this, one can explain in greater depth the phrase "there is no common place here" *that the place of the Mikdash* is not a common place [and similarly, the place of the Ark is not of the measurement], that the revelation of that which is above place that shone in the place was from the side of the place itself.

i) It can be said that the revelation of this matter of "there is no common place here" will be in the Third House. The matter is that the First and Second Houses are in the four letters of the name *Havayah* which hint at the ten *Sefiros* [the First House is *Hei Ila'ah* (Binah) through which is the revelation of the *Yud* (Chochma), and the Second House is *Hei Tata'ah* (Malchus) through which is the revelation of the *Vav* (Ze'er Anpin)], and the Third House is *Keter*, as mentioned above (section c) that "a lion will come" is the revelation of the *Keter* that is above *hishtalshelus*.

Now, in the ten *Sefiros*, the revelation and concealment within them (*Oros* and *Keilim*) are two matters, and the fact that the two matters of revelation and concealment are the names of the Holy One, Blessed be He, *who is above both of them*, is through the revelation of the *Keter* that is above *hishtalshelus*. For just as the matter of the division of the *Sefiros* (Chochma, Binah, etc.) is (primarily) in the revealed *Sefiros* of *Atzilus*, whereas the hidden ten *Sefiros* in *Keter* are included as one, similarly it is also in the matter of the division of *Oros* and *Keilim* (revelation and concealment), that in the hidden ten *Sefiros*, they (the *Oros* and the *Keilim*) are in unity. Based on this, it can be said that the true matter of "there is no common place here," that even the place itself will be like a vessel for the revelation of that which is above place, will be in revelation in the Third House. For then it will be drawn down in revelation even in the names *Havayah* and *Elokim* as they are in *hishtalshelus* [and through this, even in the two matters of above place and place, even as they are below in this physical world] that both of them are the names of the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is above both of them, and all is one.

Based on this, what is said in many places (cited above in section a) that the greatness of the Third House is that it will exist with eternal permanence is understood. For seemingly, since the matter of eternity could have been in the First House (as mentioned above in section c), how can it be said that this is the greatness of the Third House? The explanation is that the eternity that could have been in the First House is (primarily) from the side of the revelation of that which is above time, and the novelty in the eternity that will be in the Third House is that even time will be a vessel for this. This is the greatness of the Third House: that it will exist with eternal permanence, for the true matter of *bli gevul* (eternity) is that the eternity is not only from the side of the extension from above, but that the below is a vessel for this, and this "eternity" is only in the Third House.

j) Through the revelation of the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim* (in the aforementioned manner) that will be in the Beis Hamikdash (the Third), where even the place (that came into existence from the name *Elokim*) is a vessel for the revelation of *Havayah* that is above place, a semblance of this revelation will be drawn down also in the entire world. This revelation will be primarily in the *geulah* after the building of the Beis Hamikdash. The reason that the future *geulah* will be an eternal *geulah* after which there is no possibility of *galus* is because the world will be a vessel for the *geulah*. As explained in Likutei Torah, the third *geulah* is in the merit of Yaakov, whose attribute is the attribute of *emes* in which there is no possibility of change, for the true matter of *bli gevul* (the attribute of *emes*) is that the below is a vessel for this. Similarly, it is in the matter of the ingathering of the exiles (of the *geulah*), which will be in all six extremities (of place): "I will bring your seed from the east, and gather you from the west; I will say to the north, 'Give,' and to the south, 'Do not withhold; bring My sons from afar, and My daughters from the ends of the earth," for it can be said that "afar" and "ends" correspond to the two extremities of above and below. It can be said that the ingathering of the exiles from all six extremities will be in a manner where the six extremities will assist in this.

Now, although the revelation that will be drawn down in the world will be only a semblance of the revelation in the Beis Hamikdash itself, nevertheless, there is an advantage in the extension in the world. For the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim* in the Beis Hamikdash itself, since "there is no common place here," it is not so recognizable that the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim* is also from the side of the name *Elokim*, and the revelation of this matter (that the *yichud* is also from the side of the name *Elokim*) is primarily through drawing down a semblance of the revelation of the Beis Hamikdash into the world, a "common place." Based on this, one can explain the advantage of the *geulah* over the Beis Hamikdash [which is why the *geulah* will be after the building of the Beis Hamikdash, as in section b], for the extension of the revelation of the Beis Hamikdash into the world will be (primarily) in the *geulah*, as mentioned.

k) The essence of the revelation of the *yichud* of *Havayah* and *Elokim* (that the *yichud* is also from the side of *Elokim*) will be in *techiyas hameisim* after the ingathering of the exiles, the last of all. For the revelation that will be in the world (*geulah* from *galus* and the ingathering of the exiles) is a limited revelation (relative to the revelations that will be in the future), and as mentioned, it is only a semblance of the revelation of the Beis Hamikdash. In *techiyas hameisim*, when there will be the vitality of the body from the *Sovev* [more elevated than the vitality of the *neshamah*, which is why the *neshamah* will be nourished by the body], there will be two greatnesses: the revelation of *bli gevul* (*Sovev*), and this revelation will be in the body, whose root is from the name *Elokim*.

l) This is "the glory of this latter House shall be greater than the former," for even though in the future *geulah* there will be many matters, up to *techiyas hameisim* which is the last of all, nevertheless, the primary emphasis is on the glory of this latter House, for the root of all matters will be in the Beis Hamikdash, and from it they will be drawn down into the world (as in section b).

This is also one of the reasons that the first action of Moshiach (after he is in the status of Moshiach) is the building of the Beis Hamikdash, for this is the root of all matters that follow.

## Tuesday, Parshas Devarim, 5 Menachem-Av, 5725

"He will swallow up death forever, and Hashem Elokim will wipe away tears from off all faces." Admur Maharash explains in his maamar beginning with the word *Zeh* that the reason death will be swallowed up forever in the time to come is because at that time, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth." This can be understood by first noting the reason explained in the verse (below) that death came into the world through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge—meaning that death and the sin of the Tree of Knowledge are connected to one another. The matter is that through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, a mixture of good and evil was created. The existence of evil was present even before the sin, but at that time, the evil was separated from the good. As is known, at the beginning of creation, the dwelling place of the kelipos was below the worlds of holiness. Through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, a mixture of good and evil was created (throughout the entire world), where evil is mixed into the good and good into the evil, to the point that there is no good without evil and no evil without good. This is the meaning of the verse, "And now, lest he put forth his hand and take also of the Tree of Life, and eat, and live forever." Seemingly, the creation of man was originally intended for him to live forever, and the reason he was commanded not to eat from the Tree of Knowledge was so that he would not die (as it is written, "But of the Tree of Knowledge... you shall not eat of it, for in the day that you eat thereof you shall surely die"). So what would be the harm if he ate from the Tree of Life and lived forever? Admur HaZaken explains that since evil became mixed into man through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, therefore, "and now" (after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge), there is reason to fear that he might "put forth his hand... and live forever," for if he were to live forever, the evil mixed within him would also have eternal existence. Based on this, one can say that the fact that death entered the world through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge is so that the evil would not have existence, as mentioned above.

It can be said that the death in the world caused by the sin of the Tree of Knowledge is a result of the sin itself. The matter is that the essence of vitality is found only in holiness, whereas evil and impurity (the opposite of holiness) are death. Therefore, since spiritual death—evil—was mixed into man through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, physical death also evolved from it. This is also why in the time to come, "He will swallow up death forever," for since the evil—the spiritual death—will be nullified at that time, the physical death will naturally be swallowed up as well.

2. The reason why it is specifically in the time to come that evil (spiritual death, and consequently physical death) will be nullified is that at that time there will be a revelation of an extremely lofty light, in relation to which all opposing forces are naturally nullified. It is explained in the maamar that even when the Beis Hamikdash was standing—especially during the time of the First Temple, and even more so in the days of Shlomo, when the moon was in its fullness—there was a revelation of an extremely lofty light. By virtue of this revelation, all the nations were nullified before him without any war at all (which is why he is called Shlomo, for there was peace in his days). Nevertheless, the revelation in the days of Shlomo was such that there was still a place for the nourishment of the *chitzonim*, except that their nourishment at that time was only from the "back" (*acharayim*) of holiness, and they had no hold on the "inner" (*pnimiyus*). (It can be said that the fact that there was still a place for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* in the days of Shlomo is also evident in the nature of the nullification of the nations before him. Like the Queen of Sheba: even while she was in her own land, merely hearing the fame of Shlomo caused a degree of nullification in her, which is why she came to Shlomo. And especially after she came to him and saw his wisdom, etc., which caused her to be nullified before him to the point that "there was no more spirit in her." Nevertheless, even then she was a queen, and furthermore, Shlomo even honored her with great honor.) This is in contrast to the revelation of the time to come, which will be in a manner where there will be no nourishment for the *chitzonim* at all (not even from the aspect of *acharayim*), and the evil will be completely nullified—"He will swallow up death forever."

3. The explanation of the difference between the revelation in the days of Shlomo (where there was still a place for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* from the aspect of *acharayim*) and the revelation of the time to come (where there will be no nourishment for them at all) is explained in the maamar as being analogous to the difference (in a person’s *avodah*) between the *avodah* of "turn from evil" and the *avodah* of "loathing evil." "Turn from evil" means that one pushes away the evil, but he does not essentially hate the evil. Consequently, even though he actually pushes away the evil, he still leaves room for it, and in a hidden way, he still has some trace of love for the evil, as explained in Tanya regarding the level of a *tzaddik she'eino gamur*. In contrast, when one "loathes evil"—meaning he loathes evil completely (the level of a *tzaddik gamur*)—he does not give any room to the evil; on the contrary, he hates the evil and loathes it with absolute hatred and loathing. Similarly, this is the difference between the revelation in the days of Shlomo and the revelation of the time to come: the revelation in the days of Shlomo, although all opposing forces were nullified before it (similar to how one pushes away evil in the *avodah* of "turn from evil"), nevertheless still left room for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* (at least from the aspect of the *acharayim* of holiness). In contrast, the revelation of the time to come is like one who loathes evil with absolute loathing, in which there is no room at all for anything that is the opposite of holiness.

It should be added that according to what is explained in Tanya, that the magnitude of hatred for the *sitra achra* and the loathing of evil is proportional to the magnitude of the love for Hashem, the difference between "turn from evil" and "loathing evil" is (not only regarding the manner of negating the evil, but also) in the magnitude and manner of one's love for Hashem. Based on this, the comparison of this difference (between "turn from evil" and "loathing evil") to the difference between the revelation in the days of Shlomo and the revelation of the time to come is clarified: the difference between them in the manner of negating evil (that in the revelation of the days of Shlomo there is still room for the nourishment of the *chitzonim*, whereas in the revelation of the time to come there is not) is due to the difference in their level and manner of *light and revelation*.

4. It is known that all the revelations of the time to come depend on our deeds and our *avodah* now. From this, it is understood that the fact that in the time to come there will be a revelation that gives no room for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* ("He will swallow up death forever") is, as explained in the maamar, because through the fact that the Jewish people hate the evil with absolute hatred, this causes "And Esau I have hated" to be realized Above with absolute hatred. And by virtue of this hatred, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," and "He will swallow up death forever." Now, since Hashem saw that the *tzaddikim* are few (and especially since hating evil with absolute hatred is the level of a *tzaddik gamur*), and even regarding the level of a *beinoni*, the saying is known, "If only I were a *beinoni*," and the matter of "He will swallow up death forever" will apply to all of Israel—it is understood from this that this *avodah* (to hate evil with absolute hatred) can also be achieved by *beinonim*, and even by those below the level of a *beinoni*. For every Jew has special times—during *tefillah*, or during the study of Torah, or when he performs a *mitzvah* that he is particularly careful with, or even when he engages in mundane matters for the sake of Heaven, and certainly when he does so in the manner of "In all your ways know Him"—at which time he surrenders his entire existence to *Elokus*, and thereby he is no longer associated with the "filthy garments," just like a *tzaddik gamur*. And since this unification Above is eternal, forever and ever, the revelation that gives no room at all for the nourishment of the *chitzonim* is drawn down through it—"He will swallow up death forever."

5. This is "He will swallow up death forever": as long as the *birurim* (refinements) are not yet complete and the good and evil are mixed together (including the time when the Beis Hamikdash was standing, and even in the days of Shlomo when the moon was in its fullness), there is the matter of death, so that the evil will not have existence, as mentioned above.
