This is also the reason why even *tzaddikim* will return to their dust one hour before the resurrection of the dead (although no worm rules over them, and until this hour they existed for hundreds and thousands of years, nevertheless, before the resurrection they will return to their dust), because since a mixture of evil was created throughout the world through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the bodies of the *tzaddikim* will also require refinement. This is in contrast to the time to come (after the resurrection), when "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," there will be no death, and the body will live an eternal life. For even according to the opinion that the verse, "For the youth of one hundred years shall die," is to be taken literally, it refers only to the nations of the world; whereas regarding Israel, "He will swallow up death forever." Furthermore, even the death that will occur (according to this opinion) among the nations of the world is not actual death, but a "fall," for "whoever falls from his level is called dead." As explained in the maamar, through the sparks of holiness that were swallowed within them being refined and ascending Above, the evil within them (i.e., their physical body, which is called evil in relation to the sparks of holiness within it) will fall below. This applies to the nations of the world; in contrast, among the Jewish people, the body will also be elevated, so that the body will also be nourished by spirituality like the *neshamah*. And more than that, at that time the body will be above the *neshamah*—"a woman shall encompass a man." And all this will be in actuality and in revelation below ten *tefachim*, in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

## Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness

**1.** "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness". This verse appears at the beginning of the Book of Yeshayahu, whose subject matter—as his name implies (Yeshayahu, from the word *yeshuah*—salvation) —is entirely one of consolation, as the Gemara states. Even those passages in the prophecies of Yeshayahu that seemingly do not appear to be salvation are, in truth, also salvation and consolation. As explained in Kabbalah, these are aspects of "sweetened *gevuros*." Since the future salvation (Geulah) will come about through the sweetening of the *gevuros*, Yitzchak will be the primary figure [as the Gemara states, that in the future they will say to Yitzchak, "For you are our father," because Yitzchak represents the *gevuros*]. Therefore, the salvations in the Book of Yeshayahu include both salvations that are in the category of revealed *chasadim*, and salvations that are in the category of sweetened *gevuros*—*gevuros* that are transformed into *chasadim* (which are higher than revealed *chasadim*). The same applies to the prophecy at the beginning of the book, which contains both aforementioned types, and concludes with "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness," as will be explained.

**2.** It is explained in the *maamarim* on the verse "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness" (by the Alter Rebbe and our Rebbes, his successors), that this verse speaks of two categories. "Zion"—the aspect of Zion, although it is in *galus* and therefore requires redemption, is nevertheless not in a state of "captivity" (*shevi*), and therefore its redemption from *galus* is through "justice" (*mishpat*). And "those who return to it" (*shevi'ah*)—these are the actual captives, and their redemption from captivity is specifically through "righteousness" (*tzedakah*). The explanation of these two categories within a person refers to the *neshamah*, which is the essence of the person (as stated in Tanya, Chapter 32), for "you are called *adam* (man)" because you are "like the One Above" (*adamah l'elyon*). The *neshamah* exists as it is above its enclothement in the body—the essence of the *neshamah*, the inner heart, etc.—and the part of the *neshamah* that enclothes itself in the body, which generally consists of the revealed faculties of the *neshamah* that are in a state of enclothement, called the "foot" of the *neshamah*. Concerning this it is said, "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness": "Zion" refers to the essence of the *neshamah*, the aspect of the inner heart; in this aspect, the concept of captivity and subjugation to the *sitra achra* does not apply, *chas v'shalom*, only the concept of *galus*. Not so with the faculties of the *neshamah* that are in a state of enclothement in the body, where the concept of captivity does apply. Concerning this it says, "and those who return to it with righteousness," meaning that even the faculties of the *neshamah* (that are in a state of enclothement in the body) which are truly captive to the *sitra achra*, will be redeemed through *tzedakah*.

**3.** To explain the concept of the inner heart (called "Zion"), the aforementioned *maamarim* cite the verse, "And these words... shall be upon your heart," and our Sages' teaching, "Every day they should be in your eyes as new." One must understand how this is possible [for this requirement that "every day they should be in your eyes as new" must be true (like all matters of the Torah of Truth), and since Hashem only demands according to one's capacity, it is proven that it is within a person's power to reach this. Seemingly, since a person is limited and subject to change, how can he reach the state where every day they are in his eyes as new?]. The explanation (as understood from the aforementioned *maamarim*) is that this is due to the aspect of the inner heart, which is above the realm of change. Therefore, when the inner heart is as it should be (meaning, when it is revealed), it also influences the faculties of the *neshamah* that are enclothed in the body, and also the garments of the *neshamah*—thought, speech, and action—so that in them, too, the words of Torah will be as new. For through the revelation of the inner heart, the revealed faculties of the *neshamah* are also in their state of perfection. This is why Yisrael are called (in this verse) by the name "Zion" [as the Tzemach Tzedek says, that the interpretation (of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice") that Zion refers to the city (or the entirety of Eretz Yisrael) is somewhat forced. He explains that Zion refers to the people of Yisrael], for "Zion" (*Tziyon*) is a term for a sign (*siman*). When the aspect of the inner heart shines in a person, he is in the state of "Zion," a sign (as in, "I am merely a sign"), meaning that his entire existence is only a sign of the matters above.

**4.** The aforementioned interpretation (of the Tzemach Tzedek) that Zion refers to the people of Yisrael is understood there to be based on the statement of the Yerushalmi regarding the verse, "I have placed My words in your mouth and covered you with the shadow of My hand, to plant the heavens and to establish the earth, and to say to Zion, 'You are My people.'" We have searched the entire Scripture and have not found that Yisrael are called "Zion" except for this (verse), "and to say to Zion, 'You are My people.'" The Tzemach Tzedek explains that through the three things in this verse (according to the interpretation of the Yerushalmi there)—"I have placed My words in your mouth," this is Torah [the word of Hashem is *halacha*, which is Torah]; "and covered you with the shadow of My hand," this is *gemilus chasadim* [which is the totality of all the *mitzvos*, and the *mitzvos* are the aspect of garments, "covered you"]; "to plant the heavens and to establish the earth," these are the *korbanos* [for through the *korbanos*, the laws of heaven and earth are sustained. And through the *korbanos* (and *tefillah*) the union of *Ze'er Anpin* and *Nukvah*, called heaven and earth, is effected]—through the fulfillment of these three things, Yisrael are in the state of "Zion." That is, when these three things are in their perfection (as they are hinted at in this verse), the study of Torah is in a state of absolute *bitul*, to the point that the speech does not come from himself, but rather the word of Hashem speaks through him, similar to how the *Shechinah* speaks from the throat (of Moshe). This is "I have placed My words in your mouth," that the word of Hashem is what speaks in his mouth. Likewise, his fulfillment of the *mitzvos* is in a state of *bitul*, where his own existence is not felt, but rather he is covered ("covered you") in the shadow of My hand (the hand of Hashem), which is the aspect of the *mitzvos* as they are the *mitzvos* of Hashem. And all the more so is this true in the line of *avodah*, that his *avodah* is "to plant the heavens and to establish the earth". (Similar to what is stated in the Zohar, that by engaging in words of Torah, one creates "new heavens and a new earth" from that word. This means that his Torah speech is like the speech of Hashem: "Just as I, with My speech, created heaven and earth, so too do you.") Through the fulfillment of the three aforementioned things in this manner, the Community of Yisrael is called by the name "Zion," for they are not an independent existence, but rather their existence is that they are a sign of the matters above.

**5.** However, when there is a lack in the *avodah* of the three lines, due to our sins, then even though the sin is on the part of the *neshamah* that is enclothed in the body, it nevertheless affects the essence of the *neshamah* as well. As it is written, "Return, O Yisrael, unto Hashem your G-d, for you have stumbled in your iniquity." The one who stumbles in practice is the "foot," and "Yisrael" is an acronym for *li rosh* ("I have a head"), the head of the *neshamah*. It says "Return, O Yisrael," because the stumbling of the "foot" of the *neshamah* affects even the aspect of the *neshamah* above. Like the analogy of a person who stumbles with his foot, which causes his head to fall as well. This is the concept of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice," that the aspect of Zion—the essence of the *neshamah* called Zion—must undergo redemption from the things that cover it, which prevent the revelation of the *neshamah* in the body. This means that the redemption required for the aspect of Zion is not a redemption from "captivity," for in the essence of the *neshamah*, the concept of captivity does not apply, *chas v'shalom*, as it is written, "And My glory I will not give to another," for "My glory" refers to the aspect of the inner *Malchus*, and in a person, this is the inner heart, the inner *neshamah*, and even the essence of the *neshamah*. This aspect "I will not give to another." The redemption needed in the aspect of Zion is only the emergence from the things that cover it, as mentioned [see what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* and in the *maamarim* on the verse "Redeem my soul in peace," regarding the redemption of the general *Shechinah* from *galus*, and regarding the redemption of every individual spark from the *Shechinah* within the soul of every Jew, specifically "in peace"]. This redemption is through "justice," meaning through Torah, for through engagement in Torah, the aspect of the inner heart is revealed. But in order to redeem the faculties of the *neshamah* (that are in a state of enclothement in the body) from *galus*, which are truly captive, one needs *tzedakah* specifically, and "those who return to it with righteousness." By redeeming them from captivity, an "advantage of light" is created in the ultimate perfection. Like the analogy of a king's son who, when he is always in his father's house, the joy is not as intense; not so when the king's son has been in captivity and grinding in the prison house, etc., and then goes free to the house of his father the king—then the joy is greatly magnified, and both rejoice with a great and immense joy. This is similar to the well-known concept regarding the greatness of the joy that will be in the future during the time of the Three Weeks, and especially during the nine days, and especially during the days of the Seventeenth of Tammuz and Tisha B'Av, that the joy of these festivals [the fact that these days will be transformed into gladness and joy and good festivals] will be a greater joy, with more intensity and strength, than the joy of the festivals in the regular manner.

**6.** The essence of the matter, and the reasons why the redemption of the aspect of the essence of the *neshamah* is through "justice," which is Torah, and the redemption of the aspect of the faculties of the *neshamah* that have fallen into captivity is through *tzedakah*, which is the totality of the *mitzvos*, is because Torah and *mitzvos* themselves are also analogous to these two matters. For Torah, even as it has descended below, and even when it is studied by a person who is not pure, is as it is above—the word of Hashem—as our Sages expound on the verse, "Is not My word like fire?" And since Torah is not in a state of enclothement, the concept of captivity does not apply to it, *chas v'shalom*. It is only that the concept of redemption still applies to it, because due to the things into which it has descended (even though it is not enclothed in them), it is possible for it to be in a state of concealment. However, the *mitzvos*, since they are enclothed in physical things—*tzitzis* in physical wool, *tefillin* in physical parchment, etc., and even the *mitzvos* of the duties of the heart must be felt in the physical brain and heart—therefore the concept of captivity applies to them, as explained elsewhere regarding the verse, "I rejoice over Your word as one who finds great spoil," that in *mitzvos* it is the concept of "spoil," meaning that they plunder and extract from the *sitra achra*.

**7.** The two aforementioned matters (the aspect of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice" and the aspect of "those who return to it with righteousness") exist in all three categories of *Olam* (world), *Shanah* (year), and *Nefesh* (soul). In the category of *Nefesh*, they exist both in every individual Jew and in the totality of Yisrael [for since every Jew is a "full world", it is understood that the matters that are in every Jew also exist in the totality of Yisrael, and the matters that are in the totality of Yisrael also exist in every Jew]. Every Jew, through his *avodah* in the line of Torah, is in the state of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice," and through his *avodah* in the line of *mitzvos*, he is in the state of "those who return to it with righteousness." The same applies to the totality of Yisrael, who are divided into two types: Yissachar and Zevulun, masters of Torah and masters of good deeds. The masters of Torah are in the state of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice," and the masters of good deeds are in the state of "those who return to it with righteousness." In a more general sense, this is the distinction between *tzaddikim* and *baalei teshuvah*. In *tzaddikim*, the concept of captivity does not apply, *chas v'shalom*, for "no evil shall befall the *tzaddik*", and all the more so in *tzaddikim* who are in the state of "my heart is hollow within me". Yet, even in them, the concept of redemption applies, similar to how sometimes a *tzaddik* is caught in the iniquity of the generation, or similar to what is said regarding Moshe, "Go, descend, for your people have corrupted," that because "your people have corrupted," a descent occurs in him as well. But nevertheless, since the descent (and even when he is caught in the iniquity of the generation) is only due to matters outside of him, even then he is not in captivity, *chas v'shalom*, for the essence of the *tzaddik* is merely a sign (of *Elokus*), as it were, just as *Elokus* is below, for his existence (the *tzaddik*'s) is that he is the messenger of the "Man Above," and the messenger of a person is like him exactly. Therefore, even when he is in a state of descent, etc., his redemption is through Torah. Because in Torah, this matter (that even below it is *Elokus* in revelation, as mentioned above regarding "Is not My word like fire") is more revealed. Not so the *baal teshuvah*, whose *avodah* is to extract the sparks that have fallen and been taken captive by the *sitra achra* (and analogous—in holiness—to what is said, "and he took captive some of them"); therefore, the redemption must also be analogous to this. This is "and those who return to it with righteousness," that their redemption is in the line of *tzedakah*, which is the totality of the *mitzvos* [for the entire body is included in the right side], for the *avodah* of the line of *mitzvos* is in the manner of "captive" and "spoil." Similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, that the main *avodah* of Hashem in these times, in the footsteps of Mashiach, is the *avodah* of *tzedakah* (and not like in the time of the Shas, where Torah study was the main *avodah*), because in order to raise the "fallen Sukkah of David" to the level of feet and heels, which is the level of *Asiyah*, there must also be *avodah* in the level of *Asiyah* specifically, which is the act of *tzedakah*.

**8.** Similarly, this applies to the category of *Olam* (place), which also has these two matters. The World of *Atzilus* is refined, and regarding the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*, it is said, "and from there it separated," and specifically in the "world of separation," the World of *Asiyah*, is the *avodah* of practical *mitzvos*. Similarly, Eretz Yisrael, upon which "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are on it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year", not so the lands of the nations, whose soil is impure and whose air is impure. Therefore, in order to make the lands of the nations into Eretz Yisrael, there must be the greater *avodah* of "those who return to it with righteousness." Similarly, this applies to the category of *Shanah* (time), which also has these two types. Generally, this is the distinction between the summer time and the winter time, as explained elsewhere, that in the summer time the *avodah* is easier than in the winter time, for in the summer days the sun shines and it is the aspect of the Name *Havayah* (and the holidays in the summer are more frequent). As it is stated in the Midrash, "Because they go from summer to winter, etc., to a distant place, etc., there is no time for them to go and come." This means that the *avodah* in the winter time is distant, more difficult than in the summer time. Similarly, this is the distinction between "meritorious days" and days that are the opposite of merit. The *avodah* in the days that are the opposite of merit is in the manner of "those who return to it with righteousness," that Yisrael (through their *avodah*) transform these days into gladness and joy, in the future redemption that is coming very soon. This matter (the transformation of these days into gladness and joy) is accomplished through the *avodah* of the line of *teshuvah* specifically, for the concept of *teshuvah* is the transformation of darkness into light, which is the superiority of the *avodah* of the *baal teshuvah* over the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*. This is also the connection of the future redemption to the concept of *teshuvah* specifically [that Yisrael perform *teshuvah* (and through this specifically) they are immediately redeemed, to the point that the elevation of the future redemption is that Mashiach comes to bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*], for the novelty of the future redemption is the concept of transformation.

**9.** According to the above, it will be understood why this verse speaks only of the two matters of Torah (justice) and *tzedakah*, even though there are three lines. For the intention regarding Torah (justice) and *tzedakah* (in this verse) is to the two general types that exist in all the categories of *Olam, Shanah,* and *Nefesh* (and similarly—the matter of lights and vessels, the Name *Havayah* and the Name *Elokim*, etc.). And in each one, there must be *avodah* in all three lines. For the redemption from *galus* [both in these matters [masters of Torah and *tzaddikim* (Nefesh), Eretz Yisrael (Olam), and meritorious days (Shanah)], whose redemption from *galus* is in the manner of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice" (Torah). And in these matters [masters of good deeds and *baalei teshuvah*, lands of the nations, and days that are the opposite of merit], whose redemption is in the manner of "those who return to it with righteousness"] is through *avodah* in all three lines specifically. As our Sages say, "Anyone who engages in Torah, *gemilus chasadim*, and prays with the community, etc., it is as if he redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world," for the redemption of Hashem and Yisrael from among the nations is through *avodah* in all three lines (and in the manner of "community"). As explained above regarding the aspect of Zion, that Yisrael being in the state of Zion is through their *avodah* in all three lines [and more than that, through the fact that all three lines are in perfection]. And what is said, "Zion shall be redeemed with justice" (Torah), is because the redemption of the aspect of Zion (in all three categories of *Olam, Shanah, Nefesh*) is primarily through Torah. Similarly, this is also the case regarding "those who return to it with righteousness," that the redemption of the "captives" (in all three categories of *Olam, Shanah, Nefesh*) is through *avodah* in all three lines specifically. And what is said, "those who return to it with righteousness" (specifically), is because their redemption (of the "captives") is primarily through *tzedakah*. In addition to this, even in the matter of the *mitzvos* themselves (*tzedakah* being the totality of the *mitzvos*, as mentioned), there are all three lines: the *halacha* regarding it, which is the matter of Torah; the action in the physical thing, which is the line of *gemilus chasadim*; the elevation of the physical (with which one performs the *mitzvah*), which is the line of *avodah*, for regarding *korbanos* it is said "a pleasing aroma," and "aroma" is the concept of elevation from below to above. Likewise, *tefillah* (which corresponds to *korbanos*) is referred to as "a ladder set on the ground and its top reaches the heavens." In addition to the well-known fact that in every *mitzvah* there are the three matters of thought, speech, and action, which are the three lines. According to the above, the order of these three things (in the aforementioned statement of our Sages) will also be understood: Torah, *gemilus chasadim*, and prayer (not in the usual order), for in the general matter of "redeemed Me and My children from among the nations," it is through engagement in Torah and *gemilus chasadim*—"Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness"—but in every matter (and especially in the matter of redemption from *galus*) there must be all three lines, and "prays with the community".

**10.** This is "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with righteousness," which is the verse established in the *Haftorah* of the Shabbos before Tisha B'Av (for "from Shabbos, all the days are blessed" —including Tisha B'Av). This is analogous to the conduct of Hashem, who "prepares the cure before the affliction", for Hashem's cure is in such a way that from the beginning, "I will not place upon you", and through this, they effect the redemption of every Jew, both in his *neshamah* and in his body and animal soul. The redemption of the *neshamah* is (generally) in the manner of "Zion shall be redeemed with justice," and the redemption of the body and animal soul is in the manner of "those who return to it with righteousness" [as understood from what is explained in Tanya, that the *neshamah* itself does not need correction at all, and its descent below is only in order to correct the body and animal soul]. And in order for Torah and *tzedakah* (to ascend above, and through this) to effect the redemption in practice, it is through *tefillah*, the line of *avodah*, as mentioned.

**11.** Through the *avodah* in all three lines, in previous generations it was effected as if "He redeemed Me" (with the *kaf* of comparison), and this is similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding individual redemption. Not so now, when "behold, he stands behind our wall," and as is known from the *sicha* of the Master of the Redemption (of 12 Tammuz), that all the clarifications have already been completed and one only needs to "polish the buttons". Now, through engagement in Torah, *gemilus chasadim*, and prayer with the community, there will be "He redeemed Me," etc., in reality, and in the manner of "Redeem my soul in peace," for the true matter of "redeem in peace" will be specifically with the coming of Mashiach, as the Mitteler Rebbe explains. This is also what the Alter Rebbe wrote (in his *Iggeres HaKodesh* upon his return from P.B.): "And when I read in the Book of Tehillim the verse 'Redeem my soul in peace,' etc., I went out in peace from the G-d of peace." For it is known that the main matter of "may your springs spread outward" began after P.B. Therefore, he went out in peace when he read the verse "Redeem my soul in peace," because the (main) matter of "redeem in peace" is in the future redemption (as mentioned), and "may your springs spread outward" is the preparation for this, for the Master is coming.

Through this, he opened and paved the way, so that everyone can (and therefore must) engage in this preparation and bring the redemption by doing what is dependent upon him, as per the ruling of the Rambam, that through one action (whether in deed, speech, or thought) he tips himself and the entire world to the scale of merit and causes for himself and for them salvation and rescue, so that "Redeem my soul in peace" is effected—"He redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world"—very soon and in our days, in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## Shabbos Parshas Devarim, Shabbos Chazon, 5735

"Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with tzedakah". The Alter Rebbe and the Tzemach Tzedek (as well as our Rebbes who followed them) explain that "Zion" refers to the level of the inner heart. It is called "Zion" (*Tziyon*) as a term for a sign (*siman*), because the inner heart is a sign and indication of what is Above. On this level, it is impossible for there to be captivity, G-d forbid; it only requires redemption. This redemption is through "justice" (*mishpat*), which is Torah, as the Targum translates the phrase *k'mishpat harishon* as "like the former halacha." "Those who return to her" (*shaveha*) refers to the revealed powers of the soul that are clothed within the body—the level of the "foot" of the soul—which are truly in a state of captivity. Their redemption from captivity is specifically through *tzedakah*, which is the performance of *mitzvos*, as explained at length previously (in the *maamar* beginning *Tziyon B'mishpat*).

12) Now, according to this interpretation, *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh* (redemption through Torah) is superior to *shaveha bitzedakah* (redemption through *mitzvos*), in accordance with what is explained in many places that Torah is higher than *mitzvos*. However, in the Tzemach Tzedek’s *Reshimot* on the Prophets, regarding the verse "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with *tzedakah*," he brings an interpretation that "those who return to her" (*shaveha*) refers to "bringing the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*." In this view, "Zion" refers to the *tzaddikim*, and the "returning of Zion" is the act of bringing the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*. The redemption of the *tzaddikim* is through Torah, whereas bringing them to *teshuvah* is accomplished specifically through *tzedakah*. According to this interpretation, *shaveha bitzedakah* is higher than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh*, and furthermore, it is an incomparably higher level. This is also understood from the fact that bringing *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah* is accomplished specifically by Mashiach, as the saying goes, "Mashiach comes to bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*." The level of Mashiach’s soul is incomparably higher than the levels of other souls. As is known in the writings of the Arizal, the level of soul attained by the greatest of Israel until Mashiach is only within the levels of *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah*, whereas Adam HaRishon attained *chayah*; Mashiach, however, will attain *yechidah*—the *yechidah* that is the collective soul of all of Israel. The superiority of the level of *yechidah* over the levels of *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah* is an incomparable superiority. This is also understood from the fact that it is called *yechidah*, from the word *yachid* (singular/unique), a title indicating that it has no value in comparison to the levels of *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah*. As is known, there is a difference between *yachid* and *echad*: *Echad* (one) implies that it has a value relative to something else [for even though the title *echad* is not like the title *rishon* (first)—which necessitates a second—nonetheless, the very fact that one must say "and there is no second" proves that it is possible for there to be a second relative to it, etc.], whereas the title *yachid* itself indicates that there is no second to it. From this, we understand the greatness of the superiority of bringing *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*, since this is one of the things that will be innovated specifically by Mashiach—the level of *yechidah*.

13) This interpretation—that the level of *shaveha bitzedakah* is higher than the level of *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh*—is consistent with the interpretation in *Likkutei Torah* and the Arizal’s *Sefer HaLikkutim* on the verse "Zion shall be redeemed with justice" [though there it explains both levels on a lower plane]: "Zion" is the point of *Tziyon-Yesod* in the *Nukvah*. Because it is hollow and the lights are revealed there, it is the place where the *chitzonim* (external forces) take hold; therefore, it says that through "justice," etc., they cause it to be redeemed and push away the *chitzonim* from there. But all of this is only so that they should not hold onto it, and it should be recognizable there in its place, but it does not yet ascend to its original place and emerge from among them entirely. However, in order to extract it from among them, elevate it, and seat it in its original place, it is necessary for them to perform *tzedakah*, etc. This is "and those who return to her with *tzedakah*": to return it to its place requires *tzedakah*, and through the merit of *tzedakah* it will return to its original place. Thus, *shaveha bitzedakah* is higher than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh*. This is also understood simply, as stated there: *mishpat* (even though "justice is mercy") refers to the letter of the law, whereas *tzedakah* is beyond the letter of the law.

14) It is explained in other places that different interpretations of the same verse are connected to one another. From this, it is understood that the interpretation that *shaveha bitzedakah* is lower than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh* has a connection to the interpretation that *shaveha bitzedakah* is higher than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh* (this is similar to the concept of the "inverted seal"). The matter is as follows: It is known from our Sages that "study is great now, but in the days of Mashiach, action will be great." Study and action are analogous to the *tzomei'ach* (vegetative) and *domeim* (inanimate) levels. In the future, action will be great, because then the superiority of the *domeim* will be revealed. This is similar to what is explained regarding the verse "And Judah approached him," concerning the difference between the *Mishkan* (Tabernacle) and the *Beis HaMikdash* (Temple) [this topic has a special connection to Shabbos Chazon, as the Rebbe of Paritch wrote: "The depth of this matter (that on Shabbos Chazon, everyone is shown the future Temple) will be explained with what is explained in other places regarding 'And Judah approached him,' the structures of our houses, etc."]. The *Mishkan* was made of acacia wood—cedars, *tzomei'ach*—whereas the *Beis HaMikdash* was made specifically of stones and earth (and it was forbidden to have protruding wood there, as it is written, "You shall not plant for yourself an Asherah, any tree"). This is because in the *Beis HaMikdash*, there was a revelation of the superiority of the *domeim*. The primary revelation of the superiority of the *domeim* will be in the future (in the Third *Beis HaMikdash*), when Judah (the level of *domeim*) will be elevated to be higher than Joseph (the level of *tzomei'ach*), as it is written, "Behold, I am taking the wood of Joseph... and I will place them upon it, the wood of Judah... and My servant David shall be king over them... and David My servant shall be a prince for them forever". This is also why in the future, action will be great, because the essence of David is action, as explained in other places regarding the difference between David and Jonathan (who are *Malchus* and *Yesod*, analogous to Judah and Joseph), the son of Saul. Jonathan the son of Saul represents study (his service was according to intellect and reason, unlike "to obey is better than a choice sacrifice" (the *kabbalas ol* of David), and it is said "Saul from the broad rivers," where "broad rivers" refers to understanding and comprehension—study), while David is the level of action. And it is said, "Until David became great."

15) Now, even though study is great now, there are many matters (even now) in which action is superior to study. For example, one interrupts Torah study for a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others. The content of the *Iggeres HaKodesh* beginning *Ihu V'chayohi* [which the Alter Rebbe wrote in the village of Piena in the days before his passing] is the superiority of practical *mitzvos*. The reason why we emphasize the superiority of action even now is because all the revelations of the future depend on our actions and our service throughout the entire duration of the exile. Since in the future action will be great, we emphasize the superiority of action now as well, because through this, the revelation of the future—when action will be great—will be brought about. This is similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that our Sages did not say "Torah study is equal to acts of kindness" except in their time; in these times, in the footsteps of Mashiach, the primary service of Hashem is the service of *tzedakah*.

16) Based on this, the two interpretations of *shaveha bitzedakah* are reconciled: the interpretation that *shaveha bitzedakah* is lower than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh* is analogous to "study is great." However, from the perspective that in the future action will be great [and this aspect exists even now, as mentioned above], *shaveha bitzedakah* is higher than *Tziyon b'mishpat tipadeh*. Just as it is with *tzedakah*, which has a superiority over Torah from the perspective of the future, so too is it with *teshuvah* (*shaveha*), which has a superiority over Torah. As our Sages said: "They asked Torah... they asked the Holy One, Blessed be He, and He said, 'Let him do *teshuvah* and he will be forgiven.'" However, this superiority of *teshuvah* comes after the priority of Torah; that is why it says "they asked Torah... [and similarly regarding what it says, 'they asked Wisdom... they asked Prophecy...']," because first there must be the matter of [Wisdom, Prophecy, and] Torah, and from that one comes to the superiority of *teshuvah*. The true essence of the superiority of *teshuvah* will be revealed in the future, and "Mashiach comes to bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*." Our Sages said that the future redemption will be specifically through *teshuvah*, for "Israel will do *teshuvah* and immediately they will be redeemed", very soon.

## B’s”D. Shabbos Parshas Devarim, Shabbos Chazon, 4 Menachem-Av, 5736

"Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with charity." The Alter Rebbe brings in *Likutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning with the words "Zeh," at the very beginning, that which is written: "And these words which I command you this day," which refers to every single day, for "every day they should be in your eyes as new." He explains that in order to arrive at this—that every day they should be in your eyes as new—it is through contemplation of this very verse: "And these words which I command you this day." The creation of all the worlds is from the *sefirah* of *Malchus*, which is merely an illumination (*ha'arah*), whereas through the performance of *mitzvos* in this world, one draws down the *Atzmus* (the Essence). This is the meaning of "which *Anchi* (I) command you this day"—*Anchi* refers to "I, Who I am." Therefore, "better is one hour of *teshuvah* and good deeds in this world than all the life of the World to Come," because the World to Come is where one enjoys the "radiance of the *Shechinah*" (*ziv haShechinah*), a radiance alone, while through *teshuvah* and good deeds in this world, one draws down the *Atzmus*. And this is "which *Anchi* command you this day"—specifically "today," "today to do them and tomorrow to receive their reward." The reward for *mitzvos* in the World to Come ("tomorrow") is only a radiance, whereas through the performance of *mitzvos* in this world—"today to do them"—one draws down the *Atzmus*. Through contemplation of the concept of "*Anchi* command you this day"—that through the performance of *mitzvos* today (in this world) the *Atzmus* (*Anchi*) is drawn down—the *mitzvos* become for him in the manner of "today," such that every day they are truly as new in his eyes. The *maamar* continues that all this is how it ought to be, but when it is not so, and his bitterness and joy are derived from the matters of this world, then the *nitzotz Eloki* (Divine spark) within him is in exile within his *nefesh habehamis*, "like Rachel before her shearers, she was silent," and regarding this it is written, "Zion shall be redeemed with justice," etc. (as will be explained in section 9).

It is necessary to understand: seemingly, even when the *mitzvos* are like an "old decree" in his eyes, it is possible that he performs them with *chayus* (vitality), and even that this (the performance of Torah and *mitzvos*) is the primary thing for him. From what is stated in the *maamar*, "But when it is not so, etc.," it seemingly implies that when the *mitzvos* are not as new in his eyes, then certainly his bitterness and joy are from the matters of this world. Furthermore, it must be understood why the *maamar* states that in order to arrive at "every day they should be in your eyes as new," one must contemplate the concept of "*Anchi* command you this day"—that through the performance of *mitzvos* in this world (today) the *Atzmus* (*Anchi*) is drawn down, which is far loftier than the reward for *mitzvos* in the World to Come, which is only a radiance. Seemingly, since the enjoyment (and *taanug*) from the radiance of the *Shechinah* in the World to Come is an extremely great pleasure [and especially since the intent of "World to Come" here refers not only to *Gan Eden* but also to the Era of Resurrection, for the revelation that will be in the Era of Resurrection is far loftier than the revelation of *Gan Eden*], then even through contemplation of the loftiness of the reward for *mitzvos* (in the World to Come) he should have great *chayus* in the performance of *mitzvos*. Yet the *maamar* says that in order for the *mitzvos* to be in his eyes as new and not as an old decree, one must contemplate specifically the concept of "*Anchi* command you this day," the superiority of "today to do them" over "tomorrow to receive their reward."

2) This can be understood by prefacing that in order for "every day they should be in your eyes as new," it must be through the revelation of a level that is above changes. Since the definition of "world" is (place and) time, and time is change, therefore, for "every day they should be in your eyes as new," it must be through the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above enclothement in the worlds—the *Ohr HaSovev* (Surrounding Light). The light that enclothes itself in the worlds, the *Ohr HaMemaleh* (Filling Light), comes in a limited configuration to vivify the created beings according to their capacity. As our Sages said, "Just as the soul fills the body, so too the Holy One, Blessed be He, fills His world"—meaning that just as the *chayus* of the soul enclothed in the body is according to the nature of the body's limbs (in every limb the *chayus* is according to its capacity), so too is it with the *chayus* of the world drawn down by the *Ohr HaMemaleh* (that the Holy One, Blessed be He, fills His world), where the *chayus* of every created being is according to its capacity. From this it is understood *a fortiori* regarding the definition of the world in general (place and time), that from the perspective of the *Ohr HaMemaleh*, it is impossible for there to be in the world a matter that is above time and place. And even though the light that enclothes itself in the world is not grasped by the boundaries of the world—as it is written, "There is none holy like Hashem," and it is stated in the *Zohar* that the innovation in "holy like Hashem" is that even though He is enclothed in the created beings and vivifies them (from within), nevertheless He is holy and separate from them and is not grasped by them [it can be said that this is the meaning of "He is the place of the world, and the world is not His place," for "He is the place of the world" refers to the *Ohr HaMemaleh*, which vivifies the world, and nevertheless "the world is not His place," for He is not grasped by it]—this refers to the light remaining in its simplicity (even after it enclothes itself in the world) from the perspective of the light. But from the perspective of the world, the *chayus* of the world that is enclothed is measured and limited by the boundaries of the world. Therefore, in order for "every day they should be in your eyes as new" (a matter above time), it must be through the revelation of the *Ohr HaSovev*.

3) Now, since the definition of the world is place and time, it is understood that the fact that through the revelation of the *Ohr HaSovev* a matter above time and place is drawn into the world, means that the boundaries of the world are *nullified* before the revelation of the *Ohr Bli Gvul* (Infinite Light) that is above the world. This is similar to *ratzon* (will), for *ratzon* is a metaphor for *Sovev*; the fact that the will rules and dominates the limbs to act contrary to their nature is because they are nullified to the will. And since the matter of "every day they should be in your eyes as new" is that he should have *chayus* in the *mitzvos* (as in new things), and *chayus* is internal, therefore, the matter that is above time which shines upon the person (through which "they should be in your eyes as new") must be within him internally. Therefore, the empowerment for this—that every day they should be in your eyes as new—is that "*Anchi* command you today," *Anchi*—"I, Who I am"—which is above even *Sovev*. The point is that the *Ohr Bli Gvul* (the root of the *Ohr HaSovev*) is defined by the definition of *Bli Gvul* (Infinite). Therefore, the fact that it is infinite in its expansion and is found in revelation everywhere, even in this physical world, is because the light is infinite, but this does not relate to the world. There are two ways in this: either the light is not felt in the world at all, or the light is felt in it, through which a matter above time and place is drawn into it, but it is in a manner where the boundary of the world is nullified before the light. In order for the revelation of the *Ohr Bli Gvul* in the world to be internal, it is through the *Atzmus* which is not defined by any definition, neither by the definition of limitation nor by the definition of *Bli Gvul*. Therefore, through the revelation of the power of the *Atzmus*, the connection of *Bli Gvul* and *Gvul* (limitation) is made—the *yichud* (unification) of *Sovev* and *Memaleh*—and the revelation of that which is above time (which is drawn from the *Sovev*) in the world (whose *chayus* is from the *Ohr HaMemaleh*) is internal.

4) It should be added that the fact that the matter of "every day they should be in your eyes as new" is through the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* is not only so that the matter above time (*Sovev*) should be felt in the person internally, but also because within the matter of "every day as new" itself, there exist the two opposites: that which is above time, and time itself. For the matter of "new" (and the preciousness and affection in it) is the change, that at first the thing did not exist and it was renewed only now. The fact that every day they are in his eyes as new means that the renewal (the change) is in a constant manner that does not change. Thus, the fact that the matter of "every day as new" is through the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* means not only that the revelation of *Sovev* (that which is above time) is felt by him internally (through which he has *chayus* in the *mitzvos* as in new things), but more than that: that time itself (which is from the perspective of the *Ohr HaMemaleh*) is in a manner of being above time and change (the revelation of the *Sovev*).

It can be said that the fact that the performance of *mitzvos* must be in a manner of truly "as new" is not only so that through this there will be greater *chayus* in the performance of Torah and *mitzvos*, but that (also) this matter itself (that every day they should be in your eyes as new) is relevant to the performance of the *mitzvos*. For the matter of *mitzvos* is that through them the *yichud* of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and His *Shechinah* is made, the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh*. And since the service of man (*is'arusa d'letata*—arousal from below) through which the drawing down (*is'arusa d'le'eila*—arousal from above) is made must be similar to the drawing down, therefore, when the performance of *mitzvos* by man is in a manner where every day they are in his eyes as new—a connection of time with that which is above time—through this, the revelation of the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* that is made through the *mitzvos* is increased.

5) Now, the two matters of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* are the two Names of *Havayah* and *Elokim*. As is explained in many places, the Name *Elokim* is not only the shield and sheath that conceals and hides the light of the Name *Havayah*, but even the light of the Name *Havayah* as it is drawn down and contracted through the Name *Elokim* to be a source for the created beings—which in general is the *Ohr HaMemaleh*—is called *Elokim*. According to what is known, that the fact that the body conceals the soul is because the root of the soul is from *Havayah* and the root of the body is from *Elokim*, and therefore, just as *Elokim* conceals *Havayah*, so too the body conceals the soul. It can be said that it is the same regarding the matter of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* [that the *Ohr HaMemaleh* is also called *Elokim*, as above], that in order for a person to know and feel that the main thing is the matters of the soul and the matters of the body are only secondary, it is through the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh*. For in the *Ohr HaMemaleh* (as it is from its own perspective) as a source for created beings, and the created beings occupy a place relative to it, there is a place for the matters of the body. Through the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh*, where even in the light as it becomes a source for the worlds, the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above worlds shines—before which "everything is considered as naught"—through this there is the recognition that the matters of the body are only for the sake of the soul. Based on this, one can explain what is stated in *Likutei Torah* that when the matter of "every day as new" is absent, then his bitterness and pleasure are from the matters of this world, because in order for there to be the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh*, through which the matters of this world do not occupy a place for him, it is through his performance of *mitzvos* being in a manner of "every day as new."

6) Based on this, one can explain the connection of exile to forgetfulness, as it is written, "Why do You forget us forever?" etc., for the cause of forgetfulness is that the knowledge he had previously was limited, and therefore, over the course of time, it ceases. From this it is understood regarding the matter of memory and forgetfulness (so to speak) above: the matter of memory is in the *Sovev*, for since it is *Bli Gvul*, there is no possibility of cessation there. The matter of forgetfulness is in *Malchus*, for *Malchus* is the root of the created beings, *Memaleh*. Therefore, when the performance of Torah and *mitzvos* by man is in a manner where every day they are as new, through which the revelation of the *Ohr Bli Gvul* shines also in the limited light, there is no possibility of the matter of forgetfulness. But when the performance of Torah and *mitzvos* by man is with limitation, where then, when he performs that same *mitzvah* for the second and third time, he does not have the same *chayus* as he had the first time—which thereby causes also above that in the limited light there should not be the revelation of the *Ohr Bli Gvul*—from this is drawn the matter of forgetfulness. And just as in man, when his performance of Torah and *mitzvos* is in a manner of limitation, it follows from this that his pleasure is in the matters of this world, which is (pleasure in the matters of this world, even in permitted desires) the opposite of holiness, so too is it above: through the fact that *Ze'er Anpin* (*Sovev*) departs—"the Holy One, Blessed be He, ascends on high" —and only *Malchus* (*Memaleh*) remains, this causes the descent of *Malchus* to vivify the *kelipos*, the exile of the *Shechinah*.

7) It is necessary to connect this with what is written in the *Haftorah* of Shabbos Chazon: "The ox knows its owner," etc., "Israel does not know, My people does not contemplate." The *Arizal* explains [that today is the eve of his *Yahrzeit*], that "ox" refers to the calf that the *Erev Rav* made in the desert, by throwing in the plate upon which Moshe wrote "Arise, ox," in order to raise the coffin of Yosef. He explains that on this plate was written the Name *Y-L-Y* (the second Name of the Name of 72 Names), which is the one appointed over the power of the supernal ox. This is "The ox knows its owner," etc., "Israel does not know," etc.—the ox itself knew that it was from a holy Name, and "Israel does not know, My people does not contemplate," they did not know and did not contemplate this, and they said that the calf arose by itself, and therefore they strayed after it. This is why the initials of "Israel does not know, My people does not contemplate" (*Yisrael Lo Yada Ami Lo Hitbonen*) are *Y-L-Y* *Al-eh*—they did not know and did not contemplate that the fact that it arose (*Al-eh*—the ox) was through the Name *Y-L-Y*, and therefore they said it arose by itself.

It can be said that this interpretation of "Israel does not know, My people does not contemplate" is a defense of Israel. The reason they strayed after the calf was because they did not contemplate the matters (the Name *Y-L-Y*) that are above the world—meaning that even then they served *Havayah*, but since it was then before the commandment of "every day they should be in your eyes as new," therefore their service was with limitation, and therefore the revelation that shone upon them then was only the light that is enclothed in the world. From this it followed that they strayed after the calf. This is also why the sin of the calf caused the breaking of the Tablets, through which the possibility of the forgetfulness of Torah was created, meaning that even after the sin, their connection with the Torah remained, but the study of Torah after the breaking of the Tablets is with limitation, and therefore there is a possibility of cessation (forgetfulness) in it. Through this, the possibility was created that a nation and tongue would rule over them, for when the revelation is only from the level of *Malchus*, there is a place given for exile, as above.

8) This is what is written, "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us," and the *Tzemach Tzedek* explains that *Mah* (what) is the Name *Havayah* (in the *milui* of *alefin*, in *gematria* 45), and *Lanu* (us) is in *gematria* *Elokim*, and the meaning of "What has befallen us" is that *Havayah* became in the level of *Elokim*. It can be said that the matter of "what has befallen us" in the service of man is that *Havayah* is above nature, and *Elokim* is in *gematria* nature, such that even when a person has success that is above nature, he thinks it is nature. And more than that, sometimes the success that is above nature causes him to think, "My power and the might of my hand have made me this wealth," [similar to what happened with the calf, for the fact that through the Name *Y-L-Y* the rising of the ox occurred (a matter above nature) led them to think it arose by itself].

The advice for this is "Remember, Hashem," that the service should be in a manner of memory, above limitation ("every day they should be in your eyes as new"), through which the revelation of *Havayah*—the *Ohr HaSovev* that is above enclothement—shines. It is possible to connect this with the explanation of the *Baal Shem Tov* on the verse, that "what has befallen us" is the revelation of the *Mah* of the soul, for the *Mah* of the soul is the essence of the soul that is above enclothement, which is connected with the *Havayah* that is above enclothement in the world, and through this one arrives at the service of "Remember," service that is above limitation.

9) This is "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with charity," which are two levels in the soul. *Zion* is the level of the soul that is above enclothement in the body (*Mah* of the soul); regarding this level, it is impossible for it to be in captivity in the *nefesh habehamis*, that its bitterness and joy should be from the matters of this world, and it is only in exile, meaning it does not shine in revelation (in the soul that is in the body). "Those who return to her" is the level of the soul that is in enclothement; regarding this level, it is possible for it to be in captivity in the *nefesh habehamis*, that its bitterness and joy are from the matters of this world. It can be said that it is similar to what is explained regarding the interpretation of the verse, "And Zion said, 'Hashem has forsaken me, and my Master has forgotten me,'" for forgetfulness is that there is something that causes forgetting, and not just the absence of memory. This is "Hashem has forsaken me, and my Master has forgotten me": regarding *Havayah* (*Hashem*), which is the *Ohr HaSovev* that is above enclothement in the worlds, the matter of forgetfulness is impossible, Heaven forbid, only the matter of forsaking, which is that in exile "the Holy One, Blessed be He, ascends on high" and does not shine in revelation below (similar to the exile in the level of *Zion*, which does not shine in the soul that is in the body), and *Adonai* (*Malchus*), which in general is the *Ohr HaMemaleh*, the matter of forgetfulness is possible in it—the descent of *Malchus* to vivify the *kelipos* (similar to the captivity in the level of the soul that is in the state of enclothement, where its bitterness and joy can be from the matters of this world). This is "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with charity," for the redemption of the level of *Zion* from the things that cover it and prevent its revelation in the soul that is in the body is through the Torah [justice (*mishpat*) is the laws of the Torah, as it is translated in the *Targum* on the verse, "as the first justice," as the first laws], for the Torah is light ("Torah is light"), and therefore through it the revelation of the level of *Zion* is made. And the redemption of the level of the soul that is in enclothement, which is in captivity in the *nefesh habehamis* ("those who return to her"), is with charity (*tzedakah*), meaning the totality of the *mitzvos* which are called *tzedakah*, and specifically through *tzedakah* in its literal sense, for regarding *tzedakah* it is written, "Your commandment is exceedingly broad," for through the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, the revelation of the *Ohr Bli Gvul* is drawn down, and the revelation is also in the soul enclothed in the body, [and similarly above—in the *sefirah* of *Malchus*, which is called by the name *Shechinah* because it enclothes itself in the lower beings to vivify them], and in a manner of enclothement. Through this, the revelation of the essence of the soul itself is also drawn down, which is above even the level of the soul that is above enclothement, similar to what was stated above (section 3) that the *yichud* of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* is through the revelation of the power of the *Atzmus*. And since "He has also set the world in their hearts," through this it is also drawn into the world, that the revelation of that which is above nature (which is drawn from the *Sovev*) will be in revelation also in nature (which is drawn from the *Memaleh*), and through this there will also be the revelation of the *Atzmus* (which connects both of them), through which the intent of "a dwelling place for Him, blessed be He, in the lower worlds" will be completed, for Him—for His Essence. 

May it be the will that very soon the promise and the prophecy "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with charity" will be fulfilled, that a King from the house of David will arise, contemplating the Torah (justice) and occupying Himself with *mitzvos* (charity), and He will fight the war of Hashem and be victorious [it can be said that the fact that He will fight the war of Hashem is through the service in the level of the soul enclothed in the body, for the service in this level is in a manner of war with the *nefesh habehamis*], and He will build the Temple in its place [through which there will be revelation also in the entire world, for the windows of the Holy Temple were wide on the inside and narrow on the outside —or rather, "narrow on the inside and wide on the outside" —from which light goes out to the entire world] and He will gather the outcasts of Israel and will rectify the entire world to serve Hashem, and all this—very soon and in our days.

## B’ezras Hashem. Parshas Devarim, Shabbos Chazon, Erev Tishah B’Av, 5741

"Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with tzedakah." The Rebbe (Rashab) n.e. notes in his maamar beginning with these words, from the year 5664, that the term "Zion" here does not refer to the city of Zion, but rather to the totality of the Jewish people. Why, then, is it called "Zion"? Furthermore, he questions the meaning of "those who return to her" (*shaveha*)—who are they? (It should be noted that this question regarding the identity of *shaveha* is based on the preceding premise that "Zion" refers to the Jewish people as a whole. Some explain that "Zion" refers to the city of Zion and *shaveha* refers to the Jewish people. But according to the interpretation in the maamar, where "Zion" refers to the Jewish people, what are the two categories of "Zion" and "shaveha"?) Additionally, what is the significance of the redemption of Zion being through "justice" (*mishpat*), while the redemption of *shaveha* is through "tzedakah"?

2) The crux of the explanation (based on the Tzemach Tzedek’s Reshimot on the verse and the aforementioned maamar) is that "Zion" refers to those Jews who are occupied with Torah and mitzvos; they are called "Zion" because they are "marked" (*metzuyanim*) by Torah and mitzvos. As the Yerushalmi states regarding the verse, "I have placed My words in your mouth, and with the shadow of My hand I have covered you, to plant the heavens and to found the earth, and to say to Zion, 'You are My people'": We have searched the entire Scripture and found no instance where the Jewish people are called "Zion" other than this one. The explanation for this is known: this verse speaks of the three pillars upon which the world stands—Torah, avodah, and gemillus chasadim. "I have placed My words in your mouth" refers to Torah; "with the shadow of My hand I have covered you" refers to gemillus chasadim; "to plant the heavens and to found the earth" refers to the korbanos (as the Yerushalmi states there). Thus, "we have found no instance where the Jewish people are called Zion other than this one," because the Jewish people are called "Zion" specifically through their occupation with Torah, avodah, and gemillus chasadim, which encompass all the mitzvos.

*Shaveha* refers to those who are not occupied with Torah, who are literally in "captivity" (*shevi*)—in captivity within the body and the animal soul. Thus, "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with tzedakah": the redemption of those occupied with Torah is through "justice"—according to the strict letter of the law—whereas the redemption of those in "captivity" is through the quality of "tzedakah." Even though the redemption of those in captivity within the body and animal soul will also be through teshuvah—for the Jewish people are only redeemed through teshuvah, and the Torah has promised that the Jewish people will eventually do teshuvah at the end of their exile, and immediately they are redeemed (it could be said that this is the connection between the interpretation of *shaveha* as "captivity" and the interpretation of *shaveha* as "those who do teshuvah," for the redemption of those in "captivity" is achieved through their doing teshuvah)—nevertheless, the fact that teshuvah provides atonement is not according to "justice," but rather through the kindness and tzedakah of Hashem.

However, the redemption of *shaveha* is on a higher level than the redemption of "Zion," because "justice" implies measurement and limitation, whereas "tzedakah" is beyond limitation. As explained in the maamar, "justice" is the light within the boundary of the vessels, while "tzedakah" is the light of *havdalah* (differentiation) that comes only in the manner of tzedakah. Therefore, the light drawn down to the *tzaddikim*, whose redemption is through "justice," is the light within the boundary of the vessels. (This means that there are two aspects to their redemption being through "justice": first, they do not require tzedakah, as it is owed to them by law; second, the concept of "justice" *excludes* tzedakah, as it is written, "Do not show partiality in judgment," and Rashi explains: "Do not say, 'This man is poor... it is a mitzvah to support him.'") The light drawn down to the *baalei teshuvah*, whose redemption is through "tzedakah," is the light of *havdalah*.

3) There is another interpretation of *shaveha*: it comes from the word *hashavah* (returning), the return from exile. The term *hashavah* (especially when it follows the word "redeemed") indicates that even before the return, one is not in "exile," but is merely in a different place (the place of exile) and must return to his original location. According to this, *shaveha* are on a higher level than those of whom it is said "shall be redeemed." The term "redemption" applies to one who is in exile (unlike one who is merely in the location of exile) and requires redemption from that exile. We must understand how it is that the redemption of those in exile is through "justice" (according to the strict letter of the law), while the "return" of those who are only in the location of exile (who are on a higher level) is through "tzedakah." Furthermore, we must understand who these two categories are. "Shall be redeemed" is said regarding "Zion," which refers to those Jews occupied with Torah and mitzvos, yet they are in exile and require redemption; what is the merit of those called *shaveha* that they are not in exile?

4) This can be understood by prefacing what is explained in the maamar: the concept of exile and "captivity" applies only to the vessels, as they possess the status of a "thing" (*metzius*), whereas regarding the light, which is in the state of *ayin* (nothingness), exile does not apply. This concept (that exile does not apply to light) is understood even simply: a little light pushes away much darkness. This means that even after the descent and drawing down of light into a state of measurement and limitation (where it is relevant to speak of "little" or "much"), it still pushes away the darkness, to the point that even *a little* light pushes away *much* darkness. Moreover, the darkness is pushed away *automatically* by the light. (At the beginning of creation, light and darkness were mixed, but after "Hashem separated between the light and the darkness," the darkness was pushed away by the light.) From this, it is understood simply that the concept of exile does not apply to light, because the darkness (of exile) is pushed away by the light.

This is similar regarding the soul and the body, which are analogous to light and vessel. As is known from the statement of the Rebbe Rayatz, only the body is in exile, not the soul. Even though the soul is clothed in the body and the body is in exile, regarding the soul, it is not a state of exile. It is only that because the body is in exile, the soul clothed within it is found in a place where it does not belong and requires a "return." As the Sages say, "I am asleep in exile, but my heart is awake"—even when "I" am asleep in exile, the soul (my heart) is awake. Since the soul is literally a "part of Hashem from above," even when it is in the state of "literally" (*mamesh*)—meaning it is clothed in a physical body—it remains a part of Hashem from above. As the Baal Shem Tov taught, when you grasp a part of the essence, you grasp the whole. Therefore, even after its descent and clothing in the body through the "wondrous power," and even during the time of exile, it is not in exile. Accordingly, it can be said that the term *shaveha* refers not only to a specific category of Jews, but also to the soul of every Jew. Since the soul is not in exile, the term "redemption" does not apply to it. However, it still requires a "return," because since the soul is clothed in the body and is affected by the body's experiences, through the exile of the body, the soul is also found in the place of exile and therefore requires a "return."

5) It is known that the purpose of the descent of exile is for the sake of an ascent. Through the *avodah* during the time of exile, there will be a revelation in the future that is higher than the revelation that existed during the time of the Beis Hamikdash. This is like the "advantage of light from darkness"—through the darkness, an advantage is created in the light, making it higher than it was before. The lower the descent (the darkness), the higher the ascent (the advantage of light) that is achieved through it. From this, it is understood that since the descent of exile is primarily in the body, the ascent of the future (achieved through the descent of exile) that will take place in the body will be higher than the ascent that will take place in the soul. This can be understood based on what is explained elsewhere regarding the ascent of the soul achieved through its descent below: there are two aspects to this. First, by working for Hashem while below and clothed in a body and animal soul, the strength of its connection with Hashem is revealed—that even the concealment of the body and animal soul cannot nullify, or even diminish, its connection. Second, through the soul's *avodah* below, the clarification and refinement of the body, the animal soul, and one's portion in the world are achieved.

The difference between these two is that in the first, the advantage of light is *through* the darkness; the advantage is that the darkness reveals the strength of the light, which even the greatest darkness cannot conceal. In the second, the advantage of light is within the darkness itself, as the darkness (of the body, animal soul, and world) is transformed into light. The advantage is that to transform darkness into light requires the power of the Essence, which is above the categories of light and darkness; by transforming the darkness into light, the power of the Essence is revealed. Moreover, this is what completes the intent that Hashem desired: to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. As explained in Tanya, the intent of the soul's descent below is not for the soul's sake, but to refine the body, the animal soul, and one's portion in the world, for through this, the intent of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds" is completed. Just as it is with the ascent achieved through the soul's descent below, where the primary ascent is the refinement of the body, so too with the ascent of the future through the descent of exile: the primary ascent is in the body. The advantage created in the soul through the darkness of exile is the revelation of the strength of its connection, that even though it is clothed in a body and the body is in exile, the soul is not in exile. The advantage created in the body is that the darkness of the body as it is in exile (which is a greater darkness than its darkness as it is on its own) is transformed into light. Furthermore, through the fact that even its darkness as it is in exile is transformed into light, the intent of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds" is completed—in the lowest level, below which there is no lower level.

6) It is known that in the future, the soul will be nourished by the body. Accordingly, it can be said that in the future, the soul will have (not only the advantage created *through* the darkness, but) also the advantage that comes from the darkness itself. Although this advantage will be (primarily) in the body, the soul will also receive this advantage from the body. This is similar to what is known regarding the ascent achieved in the soul through its descent into the body and animal soul: in addition to the fact that the concealment of the body and animal soul awakens and reveals the hidden powers of the soul (which existed even before its descent), through the soul refining the body and animal soul, an additional advantage is created within the soul itself. As it is written, "Draw me, we will run after You"—through the Divine soul causing the animal soul to also have a love for Hashem, which is in the manner of "running," a "running" is also created in the Divine soul: "after You we will run" (in the plural). However, now, since the soul is the "giver" and the body is the "receiver," this advantage of the soul (receiving from the body) is not in its perfection. The perfection of this advantage will be in the future, when the soul will be nourished by the body.

7) This is "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with tzedakah." The fact that the Jewish people are called "Zion" is through their occupation with Torah, avodah, and gemillus chasadim—the totality of all mitzvos—which makes them like a "sign" (*tzion*), meaning that even when they are in exile, they are not lost among the nations (like an object that has a sign, through which it is returned to its owner). Moreover, through their *avodah* in Torah and mitzvos during the time of exile, an advantage and ascent are created in them that are higher than they were during the time of the Beis Hamikdash. This advantage consists of two things: first, through the *avodah* during the time of exile, the strength and limitlessness of the light are revealed (as mentioned in section 5), that even the greatest darkness (the darkness of exile, including the double and redoubled darkness of the generation of the footsteps of Mashiach) cannot conceal it. In general, this is the light that is above the vessels (the light of *havdalah*), which is limitless, yet it is still defined as "light." Second, through the transformation of darkness into light, the Essence, which is above the categories of light and darkness, is revealed (as mentioned above).

This verse, the conclusion and seal of the Haftorah of "The Vision of Yeshayahu" (the content of Yeshayahu is, as his name implies, *yeshuah*—salvation—leading to the true salvation, which is the complete redemption after which there is no exile; this is also the implication of what follows in the verse, "which he saw... in the days of... Chizkiyahu," for Hashem sought to make Chizkiyahu the Mashiach), speaks of the elevation that will be in the future redemption. Specifically, it speaks of the second elevation, which is the primary purpose of the exile. This is the meaning of "shall be redeemed" and "those who return"—this elevation is both in the body, which will be redeemed from exile ("shall be redeemed"), and in the soul, which will return from the place of exile ("those who return"). This is also why it says "redeemed with justice" and "return with tzedakah": the elevation that will be in the body ("shall be redeemed") is through "justice," for since the body was literally in exile and experienced the transformation of darkness into light, the advantage and elevation achieved through this are due to it according to the strict letter of the law, through "justice." Conversely, the fact that the soul, which was only in the location of exile ("those who return"), will be elevated to this level is (not according to the strict letter of the law, but) through "tzedakah." Seemingly, one could add that in one detail, there is an advantage in the ascent of the soul over the ascent of the body: the ascent of the body, which is through "justice" (meaning the ascent is according to a calculation of reason and logic), involves some measurement and limitation, whereas the ascent of the soul, which is through "tzedakah," is above all measurement and limitation.

"A verse does not depart from its literal meaning," to the extent that specifically through studying the literal meaning, the essence of Torah is revealed, for the literal meaning (*peshat*) is in the world of Asiyah, in which the intent of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds" is specifically completed. Seemingly, one could say this is also the reason (in the inner dimension of things) why the study with young children—the breath of which there is no sin—is specifically according to the literal meaning. It can be said that this is also the case regarding our subject: the verse "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to her with tzedakah," the primary meaning of which is the literal interpretation of the verse—the redemption and departure from exile in a simple, literal sense, in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon, in our days.

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Devarim, Tisha B’Av Nidche, 5724

### With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Devarim, Tisha B’Av Nidche, 5724

"He sets a limit to darkness". It is stated in the Midrash that a time was given to the world, a certain number of years to exist in darkness. The Tzemach Tzedek explains that this is similar to what is written in the Zohar regarding the verse "To everything there is a season, and a time to every purpose," meaning that there is a set time for the darkness of the Galus. 

One must understand: since all things in the world have a set time—"to *everything* there is a season"—what is the novelty in "He sets a limit to darkness"? Furthermore, it is difficult to understand because the language of the verse, "He *sets* a limit to darkness," implies that darkness of its own accord has no limit, but rather He "sets" a limit for it. 

The explanation is that the reason undesirable things do not exist during the fourteen times appointed for good is not that they are absent in principle, but rather that they are not present in actuality, because through the good matters present at those times, the undesirable things are nullified. This is similar to the relationship between light and darkness, where light repels darkness [to the extent that even a little light repels much darkness]. The concept of "He sets a limit to darkness" means that after its limit is reached, the matter of darkness will not be *relevant at all*. The fact that the future Geulah will be an eternal redemption after which there is no Galus means that at that time, the darkness of Galus will no longer be relevant.

2) The difference in the manner of the darkness’s nullification—whether it is merely repelled by the light, or whether its existence is not relevant at all—depends on the level of the light. To repel darkness (where, even after it is repelled, its existence remains a possibility), even a limited light suffices, and as noted, even *a little* light repels much darkness. However, for darkness to be nullified entirely, it requires an unlimited light. 

As stated in the Midrash, the reason the Geulah of Yetzias Mitzrayim (as well as the redemption from the Babylonian Galus and other exiles until the future Geulah) was a redemption after which there was Galus, while the future Geulah will be an eternal redemption after which there is no Galus, is that the Geulah of Yetzias Mitzrayim is like the light of a candle, which is subject to being extinguished, whereas the future Geulah is like the light of day, which is not subject to being extinguished. That is to say, the revelation of the future Geulah will be a revelation of unlimited light that is not subject to cessation, and therefore it will be an eternal redemption after which there is no Galus.

3) It is known that every revelation comes through Torah ("Torah is light"). From this it is understood that since the nullification of the darkness of Galus is through light, in order to draw closer and hasten the future Geulah, one must study Torah regarding the subject of light. It is worth noting that the discourse of the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e. delivered on a Shabbos Tisha B’Av Nidche discusses the subject of light. It can be said that the relevance of this subject to Tisha B’Av Nidche is that Tisha B’Av which falls on Shabbos and is deferred is auspicious for causing it to be deferred entirely, and the deferral and nullification of Galus is through light.

The maamar explains that light is *Ayin* (nothingness), *bitul*. [The difference between light and a vessel is that light is *Ayin* and a vessel is *Yesh* (existence).] There are three levels in the *bitul* of light: the *bitul* of light from its own perspective, because light is an extension of the *Maor* (the Luminary); the *bitul* within it because its source is felt within it; and its *bitul* due to the nature of *ratzo* (the desire to ascend) and its drive to be included in its source.
