One must understand: the *bitul* of light from its own perspective is (seemingly) that the light is not an independent existence and its entire purpose is the revelation of the *Maor*. What, then, is the difference between the light itself (whose purpose is the revelation of the *Maor*) and the fact that its source is felt within it? Also, one must understand what is said in the maamar—that the *bitul* in the light because its source is felt within it is the *bitul* of "as if it is nothing" (*kela chashiv*). Yet, the fact that the light is not an independent existence and its purpose is the revelation of the *Maor* is, seemingly, a greater *bitul* than the *bitul* of *kela chashiv* [because the *bitul* of *kela chashiv* relates only to its importance—that it has no value or significance relative to its source—and does not touch upon its actual existence]. Yet the maamar says that the *bitul* added to the light by the fact that its source is felt within it, over and above its *bitul* from its own perspective (whose purpose is the revelation of the *Maor*), is the *bitul* of *kela chashiv*.

The explanation for this is based on the known principle that although light is an extension of the *Maor*, since the *Maor* is distinct from the light (the *Maor* is not the source of the light, but rather the light is found from it), the fact that the light reveals the *Maor* is only the existence of the *Maor*, not its essence. Nevertheless, due to the *dveikus* of the light to the *Maor*, the essence of the *Maor* (which is distinct from the light and is not revealed within it) is also felt within it. Through this, it is nullified from its existence. The existence of the light is revelation (of the *Maor*), and by feeling that the *Maor* (the essence of the *Maor*) is above revelation, and that the revelation has no value (*kela chashiv*) relative to the *Maor*, it is nullified from its existence.

However, even the *bitul* of light because its source is felt within it is not a total *bitul*. Since the light and its source are two separate things, and the light is outside of its source, the fact that the light feels its source means it feels something outside of itself, which does not touch upon its actual existence. Therefore, the *bitul* resulting from this feeling is only in its expansion, not in its actual existence. The primary *bitul* of light (total *bitul*) is the *bitul* from the perspective of its *ratzo* to be included in its source. Since *ratzon* (will) touches upon its actual existence [as the Baal Shem Tov explains the verse "Seraphim stand above Him"—that through their desire to be included in the *Ohr Ein Sof*, they are (as it were) found (*standing*) there. Similar to human will, where a person’s will is, *he* is found, and furthermore, he is found there *entirely*], therefore, by wanting to be included in its source, it is (as it were) *included* in its source. Thus, its *bitul* from the perspective of the desire to be included in its source is a total *bitul* (similar to the *bitul* of light included in the *Maor*).

4) The maamar continues that the three levels of *bitul* in light correspond to three levels in light itself. The *bitul* of light from its own perspective is in the light that clothes itself in vessels. The *bitul* of light because its source is felt within it is in the light that is above clothing in vessels, but still within the category of clothing. And the *bitul* of light due to the nature of its *ratzo* and ascent to be included in its source is in the light that is above the category of clothing. 

These three levels of light, as they are in the *Sefiros*, are *Binah*, *Chochmah*, and *Keter*. Light that clothes itself in vessels is in *Binah*, because in *Binah* there is the connection of light with the vessel. This is why in *Binah* there is the *Havayah* with the *nikud* of *Elokim*, for in *Binah* is the connection of the light (*Havayah*) with the vessels (*Elokim*). The light that is above clothing in vessels but still within the category of clothing is in *Chochmah*. And the light that is above the category of clothing is in *Keter*. 

This is why the *bitul* of *Da’as Elyon*, that "everything before Him is as if it is nothing" (*kela chashiv*), is specifically in *Chochmah*, which is above *Binah*, because the *bitul* of *kela chashiv* is due to the fact that its source is felt within it; therefore, this *bitul* is specifically in *Chochmah*—light above clothing (but within the category of clothing). The *bitul* in *Keter* (light above the category of clothing) is a *bitul* even more exalted than the *bitul* of *Chochmah*, for the *bitul* of *Chochmah* is the *bitul* of "He alone is, and there is none else"—the *bitul* of *Ayin*—while in *Keter* it is the *bitul* of *Efess* (absolute nothingness).

It can be said that the fact that the *bitul* of light from its own perspective is in light that clothes itself in vessels, and the *bitul* of light from the feeling of its source and the *ratzo* to be included in its source is in light above clothing, is because the nature of light is revelation, and since the primary revelation in light is through its clothing in vessels, therefore, the light (as it is from its own perspective) descends and is drawn to clothe itself in vessels. Even though vessels are the opposite of light—light is *Ayin* and vessels are *Yesh* (as mentioned above in section 3 of the maamar)—nevertheless, since the *bitul* (*Ayin*) of light from its own perspective is that its purpose is the *revelation* of the *Maor*, therefore, from that very perspective it descends and is drawn to clothe itself in vessels, so that its revelation will be complete. 

However, when the light feels its source, which is distinct from revelation, it is nullified from the matter of revelation (as mentioned in section 3) and is not drawn to clothe itself in vessels. Yet, since its *bitul* because its source is felt within it is only in its expansion and not in its actual existence (as mentioned there), its *bitul* remains within its definition—the definition of revelation—and therefore it is within the category of clothing in vessels. But through the *bitul* of light from the perspective of the *ratzo* to be included in its source, since this *bitul* is in its actual existence, it is no longer (even) in the category of clothing in vessels.

5) The three levels mentioned above in the *bitul* of light also exist (analogously) in the *avodah* of man. Based on what was brought above from the maamar that the three levels in the *bitul* of light correspond to *Binah*, *Chochmah*, and *Keter*, it can be said that the three *bitulim* in the *avodah* of man are the *bitul* of intellectual understanding based on *emunah*, the *bitul* of *emunah* itself, and the *bitul* of *mesiras nefesh*.

This can be understood based on what is explained elsewhere regarding *makif* (encompassing) and *pnimi* (internal), that even when the *makif* is drawn down and clothes itself in the *pnimi*, it remains in its essence a *makif*. [Similarly regarding the clothing of light in vessels (where the light from its own perspective is a *makif*, and through its clothing in vessels it becomes *pnimi* light), even after the light clothes itself in vessels, it remains in its essence light]. This is analogous to *ratzon*, which even after it is drawn down and clothes itself in the intellect—to the point that it tilts the intellect to be in accordance with the *ratzon* and becomes the "reason" for the *ratzon*—it still remains in its essence a *ratzon* that is above "reason." 

Likewise, it is with the clothing of *emunah* in the intellect: when one contemplates in his intellect a matter he believes in (with a simple *emunah* that is above intellect) so that he may also understand the matter in his intellect, even after he understands the matter in his intellect, his *emunah* is an *emunah* that is above intellect. The difference between the two analogies is that in the analogy of the clothing of *ratzon* in the intellect, the fact that the intellect understands according to the *ratzon* is not from the side of the intellect, but from the side of the *ratzon* which *tilts* the intellect and *changes* it. And since the clothing of *ratzon* in the intellect is in a way that the intellect is nullified (changed) by the *ratzon*, the fact that the clothing does not cause a change in the *ratzon* (that even after it clothes itself in the intellect it remains in its existence) is not much of a novelty. 

But in the clothing of *emunah* in the intellect, the fact that the intellect arrives at the conclusion that the matter he believes in is true also from the perspective of the intellect is from the side of the intellect [for when he contemplates in his intellect so that his intellect, too, will be in accordance with the truth, he strives that his contemplation and logical analysis be according to the truth of the intellect], and nevertheless, the clothing does not cause a change in the *emunah*, and even after he understands the matter in his intellect (from the side of the intellect), his *emunah* is an *emunah* that is above intellect. 

Another difference between the two analogies: in the clothing of *ratzon* in the intellect, the fact that the *ratzon* clothes itself in the intellect and acts upon it so that it will be according to the *ratzon* is because the *ratzon* rules over the intellect (and it does not touch the *ratzon* itself). And since the fact that the *ratzon* rules over the intellect is (not the *ratzon* itself, but) its relationship to the other faculties, the descent of the *ratzon* and its clothing in the intellect is a true descent (a departure from *ratzon* to intellect). But in the clothing of *emunah* in the intellect, the fact that one contemplates in his intellect to understand the matter is for the sake of the *emunah*, so that his *emunah* will also be internal. Therefore, the descent of the *emunah* and its clothing in the intellect is not a true descent.

Based on the known principle that *emunah* is *bitul* and intellect is existence, it is understood that the clothing of *emunah* in the intellect means that the *bitul* is drawn into existence. And since his contemplation (and understanding) is for the sake of the *emunah* [and also the fact that the intellect remains in its existence and is not nullified relative to the *emunah* (as it is nullified relative to *ratzon*) is for the sake of the *emunah*, so that the intellect, as it is *in its existence*, will also be in accordance with the *emunah*], therefore, even after the *bitul* of *emunah* is drawn into the existence of the intellect, the *bitul* is in its full force. 

The difference between the *bitul* of *emunah* that clothes itself in the intellect and the *bitul* of *emunah* that is above intellect is that the *bitul* of *emunah* that clothes itself in the intellect comes in the form of revelation (the *bitul* is revealed in the intellect), an existence. For in addition to the fact that the *intellect* (in which the *emunah* clothes itself) is an existence, the revelation of the *emunah* (the fact that the *emunah* is in revelation in a way that it is felt in the intellect) is also an existence. The *bitul* of *emunah* that is above intellect is above the existence of revelation. [Analogous to the difference between the *bitul* of light that clothes itself in vessels and the *bitul* of light that is above clothing, for even the light that clothes itself is not an existence for itself, and its entire purpose is the revelation of the *Maor*. However, the *bitul* of the light that clothes itself is in the form of revelation, an existence. For in addition to the fact that the vessels in which the light clothes itself are an existence, the revelation of the light (that is revealed in the vessels) is also an existence. And the *bitul* of light that is above clothing is that it does not even have the existence of revelation.]

6) The *bitul* of *emunah* that is above intellect is also not a total *bitul*. For the *bitul* of *emunah* is that he believes in *Elokus* even though from the perspective of his intellect (his existence) he has no proofs for it. And since the reason for this—that he believes in *Elokus* (even though he has no proofs)—is because *Elokus* is felt in his soul [yet this feeling is above his existence (understanding)], therefore, the *bitul* of *emunah* is not a total *bitul*, since the fact that he believes is because *Elokus* is felt *within him*. 

This is analogous to the *bitul* of light because its source (the essence of the *Maor*) is felt within it; although the fact that its source is felt within it is above its existence [for the essence of the *Maor* is not revealed in the light], nevertheless, this is felt in the light as it is *in its existence*, an existence outside of the source [which is why the fact that its source is felt within it does not cause it to want to be included in its source]. The *bitul* of *mesiras nefesh*, where one gives up his soul for *Elokus* (a departure from his existence), is analogous to the *bitul* of light from the perspective of its *ratzo* to be included in its source. As is also understood from the continuation of matters in *Tanya*, that the power of *mesiras nefesh* in Israel is analogous to the desire of the *neshamah* to separate and depart from the body and cleave to its root and source, even if it will be *Ayin* and *Efess* and be nullified there in existence entirely. To add: in the desire of the *neshamah* to be included in the *Ohr Ein Sof*, there are two levels: that it wants to be included, and that it is in a state of *kilyon* (yearning/expiration) automatically. It can be said that since the *bitul* (of light) from the perspective of the desire to be included in its source is a total *bitul* (analogous to the *bitul* of light included in the *Maor*, as mentioned in section 3), therefore, the desire itself is also nullified.

7) The maamar continues that since the *ratzo* of light to be included in its source is because it is attached to its source, therefore, the *ratzo* of light [and also the *bitul* from the perspective of the *ratzo*] is in all levels of light, even in the light clothed in vessels (for the fact that the light is attached to its source is in all its levels). However, the primary *ratzo* [and the *bitul* from the perspective of the *ratzo*] is in the essence of the light that is above the category of clothing in vessels. It can be said that in the nature of the *ratzo* in light to be included in its source, there are two matters: the desire to be included in its source, and the desire not to be outside of its source. The fact that the primary *ratzo* is in the essence of the light means that in the light that clothes itself in vessels and in the category of clothing, it is the desire not to be outside of its source, and in the essence of the light, it is the desire to be included in its source.

The matter is that each of these two desires has a virtue that the other does not. The desire to be included in its source is *more exalted*, because this desire in the light is because the source is felt within it—and the revelation of the source is primarily in the essence of the light. The desire not to be outside of its source is more internal (*tiefer*) in the light, to the point that this desire is in its very existence—and therefore it is in all its levels. This is analogous to the difference between the desire of the *neshamah* to be included in the *Ohr Ein Sof* and the power of *mesiras nefesh*: the desire to be included in the *Ohr Ein Sof* is in revelation only in individuals of high standing, while the matter of *mesiras nefesh* not to be separated, Heaven forbid, from *Elokus* is in revelation in everyone.

8) Given the known great precision in the discourses of our Rebbes (also regarding the time of their delivery), it is reasonable to say that the relevance of the aforementioned maamar to Tisha B’Av Nidche is both from the perspective of the general content of the maamar—the subject of light—and also from the perspective of the details of light explained in the maamar.

The matter is that for darkness to be nullified entirely (and not just repelled by the light), it is (specifically) through the revelation of unlimited light (as mentioned in section 2). More specifically—through the revelation of light included in the *Maor*. The light that spreads outside the *Maor* has the purpose of illuminating the darkness. Like sunlight that spreads in the space of the world (outside the sun), where the space of the world is a dark place, and the purpose of the light spreading in the space of the world is to illuminate the place of darkness. The light included in the *Maor* is in a place (level) where the matter of darkness is not relevant. 

Similarly, above: one of the differences between the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum* (light included in His essence) and the light after the *Tzimtzum* (which is analogous to light spreading outside the *Maor*) is that the light drawn down after the *Tzimtzum* has the purpose of illuminating the worlds. Therefore, the revelation of *Elokus* that exists in the world through the revelation of light after the *Tzimtzum* is by way of renewal. Existence simply, and *Elokus* by way of renewal. [Analogous to sunlight spreading in the space of the world, where the space of the world from its own perspective is a dark place, and the light that illuminates it is by way of addition and renewal]. But when the revelation of *Ohr Ein Sof* that is before the *Tzimtzum* illuminates the world, *Elokus* is simply, to the point that there is no place given at all for a matter that is not *Elokus*. [Analogous to how it was before the *Tzimtzum*, when the *Ohr Ein Sof* filled the place of the space, so that there was no place then for the existence of the worlds].

This is why the nullification of darkness entirely is through the revelation of light included in the *Maor* (*Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum*). The light after the *Tzimtzum*, since its purpose is to illuminate the worlds—from which it is understood that the worlds occupy a place relative to it—is such that the concealment and hiding of the world has the capacity to conceal it. That is, in addition to the concealment of the world that exists even when the revelation shines, where the revelation of *Elokus* in the world through this light is by way of renewal (as mentioned above), it is possible that the concealment of the world will conceal even this (so that there will be no revelation of *Elokus* in the world at all, not even a revelation by way of renewal). 

In order for there to be a *nullification* of darkness, it is through the revelation of the essence of the light that is above the light that illuminates the worlds, for the world does not conceal this light. This is what is meant in the Midrash that the future Geulah is like the light of day, which is not subject to being extinguished; it can be said that the intention here is the light that is above relevance to the worlds, for which concealment is not relevant.

9) One must understand: seemingly, since from the perspective of the light that illuminates the worlds it is impossible for darkness to be nullified (only repelled by the light), and the fact that in the future Geulah the darkness of Galus will be nullified is because then there will be a revelation of a new light that is above relevance to the worlds, then the world itself (as it is from the perspective of its definitions, including also the revelations belonging to the world) would remain in Galus, Heaven forbid. 

The point of the explanation is that one of the reasons why the creation was in such a way that initially the light that is above relevance to the worlds was present, and from it specifically the light that illuminates the worlds was drawn down (even though seemingly the light belonging to the worlds should have been drawn down from the start), is so that the light belonging to the worlds would have within it (at least in concealment) the light that is above relevance to the worlds. Based on this, it is understood that although the nullification of the darkness of Galus will be through the revelation of the essence of the light that is above the light that illuminates the worlds, nevertheless, the Geulah will be (also) within the definitions of the world, because the revelation of the essence of the light that will be in the future Geulah will illuminate in revelation also in the light that illuminates the worlds, and through this—in the world.

Based on this, one can explain the relevance of the matters in the maamar to the nullification of the darkness of Galus. The fact that the maamar elaborates on the subject of the inclusion of light in its source can be said to be because the nullification of the darkness of Galus is through the revelation of light that is included (as mentioned in section 8). And the fact that it explains that the nature of *ratzo* and inclusion is also in the light that is within the category of clothing and also in the light clothed in vessels is because for the nullification of the darkness of Galus (which is from the perspective of the revelation of the included light) to be within the definition of the world, it is through the fact that the matter of the inclusion of light in its source is also in the light clothed in vessels.

10) This is "He sets a limit to darkness." It can be said that the meaning of the word *ketz* (limit) in this verse is (also) a limit (and boundary) to its beginning. That is, the matter of darkness has a place given only in the light that illuminates the worlds, and not in the essence of the light. And it is said "He *sets* a limit to darkness" (the fact that there is a limit to darkness is because He sets a limit for it, but of its own accord it has no limit), because the fact that darkness has no place given in the essence of the light *that is not* in the category of worlds is not relevant to the world. And since from the perspective of the definition of the world it has no limit at its beginning (since it has a place given in all levels belonging to the worlds), then also the limit at its end—that which in the future the darkness will be nullified—would not, Heaven forbid, be within the definition of the world. Therefore, "He sets a limit to darkness," a limit at its beginning, that the light which is not in the category of worlds, where there is no place given for darkness, will be relevant to the world. Through this, also the limit at its end, the nullification of darkness that will be in the future Geulah, will be in the world in its internality. For although the nullification of darkness that will be in the future is through the fact that there will then be a revelation of a new light that is above relevance to the worlds, nevertheless, the world will be a vessel also for this light, and through this the intention of "a dwelling place for Him in the lower worlds" will be completed, that the lower world (from the perspective of its definitions) will be a dwelling place for Him, for His essence.

**********

## B’s”d, Shabbos Parshas Devarim (Tisha B’Av, deferred), 5731.

### B’s”d, Shabbos Parshas Devarim (Tisha B’Av, deferred), 5731.

"How (*Eicha*) does she sit solitary (*badad*), the city that was full of people..." The Tzemach Tzedek explains (in *Tzemach Shmo*) that "she sits solitary" is as it is written, "Hashem alone (*badad*) shall lead him," and "So Israel dwells in safety, alone (*badad*), the fountain of Yaakov." This is accomplished through "the city that was full of people," as will be explained. We must understand: *Eicha* is an expression of wonder and astonishment. If the interpretation of "she sits solitary" is that Israel will be elevated to the level of "Hashem alone shall lead him"—the level of *badad* (outside the camp—in a positive sense) which is above *Seder Hishtalshelus*—what is the wonder and astonishment in this? Furthermore, we must understand the connection between this interpretation and the simple meaning. The simple meaning of "How does she sit solitary" refers to the magnitude of the descent, which is why we read *Eicha* on Tisha B’Av, the time of the destruction. How does the simple meaning connect with the Tzemach Tzedek’s interpretation that "she sits solitary" is a positive state?

This can be understood by first prefacing the magnitude of the elevation (according to the Tzemach Tzedek’s interpretation of the verse) in "she sits solitary," which is the concept of "So Israel dwells in safety, alone, the fountain of Yaakov." The precision of "the fountain of Yaakov" (specifically Yaakov) is as our Sages say: Not like Avraham, regarding whom it is written "a mountain," nor like Yitzchak, regarding whom it is written "a field," but like Yaakov, whom he called "a house." This means that the elevation of "So Israel dwells in safety, alone, the fountain of Yaakov," which will be in the future—and specifically in the Third Beis Hamikdash—is the concept of "like Yaakov, whom he called a house." For the inheritance of Yaakov is an inheritance without boundaries,, the level of *re'ua d're'uin*, as our Sages say: "Whoever delights in Shabbos is given an inheritance without boundaries... the inheritance of Yaakov." This elevation, which will be in the future, comes through the preceding "she sits solitary" of the exile.

This is the concept of what our Sages compared the exile to: the judgment of Adam HaRishon with expulsion. [Just as Adam HaRishon is the handiwork of the Ribono shel Olam, so too are Israel (who were judged with expulsion) the "shoot of My planting, the work of My hands," a literal "part of Elokus from above."] And just as Adam HaRishon’s judgment of expulsion was for the sake of the elevation that would follow—culminating in the elevation of *Matan Torah*, which is even higher than the elevation of "He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it" (as will be explained)—this is similar to how, at *Matan Torah*, there were the seven generations who removed the *Shechinah* from the lower realms, and then seven generations who drew the *Shechinah* down from above to below until *Matan Torah* occurred. Similarly, even after *Matan Torah*, when they needed to come to Eretz Yisrael and build the Beis Hamikdash, "the place that Hashem will choose," which is higher even than the *Mishkan* (of which it is written, "I walked in a tent"), there were many trials until the Beis Hamikdash was built. Afterwards, there was the destruction of the First Beis, and they reached the elevation of the Second Beis, which was higher than the First, as it is written: "The glory of this latter house shall be greater than the former," referring to the Second Beis, which was greater than the First in construction and in years. It is the same regarding the destruction of the Second Beis: they will reach the elevation of the Third Beis, which will be built very soon by Mashiach Tzidkeinu, which is higher than the First and the Second. And as our Sages say (cited above), not like Avraham, nor like Yitzchak, but like Yaakov, whom he called "a house." This is also the continuation in the verse, "She has become like a widow, but not a widow, Heaven forbid," for since the intention of the descent is for the sake of the ascent that follows, it is not a true descent; therefore, it is "like a widow," with the *kaf* of comparison.

2) The matter is as the Rebbe (Rashab) explains: The ultimate purpose of creation is that the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. This intention was completed through the *avodah* of the souls of Israel, as the saying goes: "With whom did He consult? With the souls of the righteous." Now, at the beginning of creation, "the world was created in its fullness," and the *ikar Shechinah* (the essence of the Divine Presence) was in the lower worlds. The *ikar Shechinah* refers to the level of *Ohr HaSovev* (the Transcendent Light). *Shechinah* refers to the level of *Ohr HaMemaleh* (the Immanent Light)—*Shechinah* because it dwells (*shochenet*) and clothes itself. But the *ikar Shechinah* is the level of *Ohr HaSovev*, and even the *Ohr HaSovev* that is above the worlds, as explained at length in the *Hemshech* of the *Maamarei HaHillula*. Although the drawing down of *Ohr HaSovev* is accomplished specifically through the *avodah* of Adam HaRishon and the souls of Israel, as mentioned, nevertheless, immediately at the beginning of creation, "the world was created in its fullness." This means (not that there was an actual drawing down of the *ikar Shechinah*, for that is accomplished only through *avodah*, but) that it was created in a way that it would be prepared and fit for the revelation of the light of the *ikar Shechinah*, and the actual drawing down is through *avodah*. This is the concept of "He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it," for through the *avodah* of Adam HaRishon, additional light was created in the Garden of Eden. The Garden of Eden itself is a level of *Ohr HaMemaleh* (and the fact that the world was created in its fullness only means that it was a place prepared for the revelation of *Ohr HaSovev*, as mentioned). However, within the level of *Ohr HaMemaleh* itself, the Garden of Eden has an advantage over the world at large in two ways: first, the light that clothes itself in the worlds is from the level of the seven lower *Sefiros*, while in the Garden of Eden, the first three *Sefiros* shine; and second, in the worlds there is only knowledge of existence, while in the Garden of Eden there is revelation of the essence. But all of this is only the level of *Ohr HaMemaleh*. "He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it"—through this he would draw down the level of *Ohr HaSovev*, the level of *ikar Shechinah*. However, even the level of "to work it" that was in the Garden of Eden is not comparable to the *avodah* after *Matan Torah*, as our Sages say regarding the *mitzvos* of the Patriarchs, that they were like "scents." Even though they said this regarding the Patriarchs, since until *Matan Torah* there was the decree that "the upper ones shall not descend below, and the lower ones shall not ascend above," this was also true regarding Adam HaRishon. And even though he was commanded (and therefore had the advantage of being "commanded and performing")—at least regarding the six *mitzvos*—the command as it exists below before *Matan Torah* is not like the command after *Matan Torah*, since the upper ones had not yet descended below. And even according to what is explained in that *maamar*, that the *avodah* of Adam HaRishon was higher than the *avodah* of the Patriarchs because Adam HaRishon was the handiwork of His hands and was in the Garden of Eden, nevertheless (as explained in that *maamar*), it is not comparable to the level of "Your name is like poured oil," the essential drawing down of *Matan Torah*. However, even the *avodah* after *Matan Torah* is not comparable to the revelation that was in the Beis Hamikdash (and specifically through "to work it and to guard it" in the Beis Hamikdash), "the place that Hashem will choose," for then specifically was a dwelling place for Him, a permanent dwelling. And within the Beis Hamikdash itself, the concept of a dwelling place for Him was greater in the Second Beis, for although five things were missing in the Second Beis, nevertheless, it was greater than the First in construction (place) and in years (time)—the definition of the lower realms—from the perspective of the world itself. However, the essential dwelling will be in the future, specifically through the *Torah* and *mitzvos* that will be fulfilled then, for then the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* will be in ultimate perfection, as the saying goes: "And there we will perform before You as the *mitzvos* of Your will," specifically there, as the Rebbe Maharash explains at length.

3) The magnitude of the elevation that will be in the future can be understood from the magnitude of the wonder of the *avodah* in this current exile—the preparation and introduction to it. It is known the saying of the Alter Rebbe in the name of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse: "So I have beheld You in the Sanctuary—would that I could behold You in the time of the Beis Hamikdash." And as is known in the interpretation of "And the man Moshe was very humble, more than any man on the face of the earth," that he was most humble when he saw the generation of the footsteps of Mashiach, that there would be a multitude of concealments and darkness, etc., and despite all this, they would study *Torah* and fulfill *mitzvos* in a manner of "increasing and going, increasing in light." This *avodah* produced humility and *bitul* in Moshe. And "Moshe is truth," and our Sages say he saw the attribute of truth. It is understood from this that it is indeed true that there is an advantage in the *avodah* of this current exile over the *avodah* of Moshe. From this, one can understand the magnitude of the elevation that will be in the future, since the revelation will be after and through such a lofty *avodah*. With this, one can also understand the reason for the length of this exile, for since this exile is an introduction to an extremely lofty revelation—higher than the "He placed him in the Garden of Eden" of Adam HaRishon, higher than *Matan Torah*, higher than the First Beis, and higher than the Second Beis—therefore the exile is of such great length, so that through the *avodah* of the Children of Israel during the time of the exile, they will arrive very soon at the Third Beis, which is an extremely lofty revelation, "So Israel dwells in safety, alone, the fountain of Yaakov," an inheritance without boundaries.

4) In order for the level of *badad* (alone) to be drawn down below and in a manner of *yishvah* (settling/dwelling), the drawing down must be through the levels of *Seder Hishtalshelus*. This is what is meant by "How (*Eicha*) does she sit solitary (*badad*)," that the drawing down of the level of *badad* below, and in a manner of *yishvah* (settling), is through *Eicha*. The *Aleph* hints at several levels, one above the other. Just as the *Aleph* of *Echad* (One)—the *Aleph* that is above the *Chet* and the *Dalet* (the seven heavens, the earth, and the four directions of the world)—is the *Alufo shel Olam* (the Master of the World), the *Aleph* of *Eicha* is an *Aleph* above the *Yud*—above the concept of the ten *Sefiros* (and one could say, above even the hidden ten *Sefiros*). And the *Aleph* is drawn into the *Yud* (in *Eicha*), which hints at the ten *Sefiros* of *Atzilus*, and afterwards into the *Kaf-Hei* (of *Eicha*), which refers to the level of *Malchus*, and specifically *Malchus* as it already belongs to, or as it has descended and clothed itself in, *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*. As is known, the difference between *zeh* (this) and *koh* (thus): *zeh* is the concept of pointing with one's finger and saying "this," and similarly there is the term *zo's* (which is also similar to the level of *zeh*, but *zo's* is the level of the *Nukvah*), which is the level of *Malchus* as it is in *Atzilus*. The level of *koh* is the level of *Malchus*, specifically as it clothes itself in *Beriah, Yetzirah, and Asiyah*, the level of "in our image." This is the concept of "How does she sit solitary," for *badad* is the level of *Yachid* (Unique One), which is even above the level of *Echad* (One), for the *Aleph* here (of *Eicha*) is "One and there is no second, also a son and a brother he has not," the level of *Atik* in which there is no division at all. As is known in Kabbalah, the *zivug* (*MaD* and *MaN*) in *Atik* is from within Himself, so in the future, the level of *badad* will also be drawn down in revelation below and in a settled manner.

5) It is known the teaching of the Maggid of Mezeritch that *badad* consists of two *Dalets*. The *Dalet* of the Giver and the *Dalet* of the Receiver. Seemingly, *Dalet* is a concept of poverty (*dalus*), "I have become impoverished," so how can there be a *Dalet* of the Giver? It is explained there that it is as our Sages say: "More than the calf wants to suck, the cow wants to nurse." That is, there is a yearning and desire in the Giver to give to the Receiver, and this is the *Dalet* of the Giver. Perhaps this can be connected with what is explained regarding "You yearn for the work of Your hands." Just as the will (the *Dalet*) of the Giver is that the lack of the Receiver be filled, so too the will (the *Dalet*) of the Receiver must be that the lack, as it were, of the Giver be filled. As is known in the interpretation of the Maggid of Mezeritch on the Mishnah "One should not stand to pray except with a heavy head (reverence)," that prayer must be for the "heavy head" above, for the *Shechinah* says, "My head is too light for Me, My arm is too light for Me." This is also the implication of the Baal Shem Tov’s interpretation of the verse: "*This* I recall to my heart, therefore I have hope"—*This* refers to the *Shechinah*.

6) This is "How does she sit solitary, the city that was full of people..." *Eicha* as an expression of wonder—that Israel, who were at the level of "a people," "glowing coals," etc., and "full of people" (literally) a multitude of divisions, etc., and "full of opinions"—a multitude of opinions, *Da’as* of the world and *Da’as* of Torah. For it is written, "For Hashem is a G-d of opinions (*de'os*)" (*de'os* is in the plural), and it is known the teaching of the Alter Rebbe that they must be unified together, and above that—that above and below are equal. "Hashem is a G-d of opinions"—He includes both opinions together. She is "full of opinions," *Da’as* of the world and *Da’as* of Torah, and in many ways. "She has become like a widow"—for her husband has gone to a distant land, the concept of her husband is in concealment. "Full of nations" is the concept of clothing oneself in the affairs of the seventy nations, etc. "She has become a princess among the provinces"—even the power of arrogance and strength is "among the provinces"—"she has become a tributary." But all this is for an elevation: *Sarati* (I have become a princess) shares the letters of *Tishrei*, for then is the building of the *Malchus* to be "a princess among the provinces." "She has become a tributary" is the *bitul* of *Kabbalas Ol*, for specifically in the time of concealment and hiding, when she is "full of people" and "a princess among the provinces," then specifically is the *bitul* of *Kabbalas Ol*, that she "has become a tributary," for she has no existence of her own and is only for the tribute. As is known, the *avodah* in this current exile, and specifically in the footsteps of Mashiach, is not through the intellect and not through the emotions, but the *avodah* of *Kabbalas Ol* (as mentioned above regarding the interpretation of "the man Moshe was very humble"). Through this specifically, "she sits solitary" is accomplished—the revelation of the level of *badad* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the Unique One, which is above even the hidden ten *Sefiros*—in a manner of *yishvah* (settling). As the Mitteler Rebbe explains in the interpretation of "You are One, but not in calculation," that He is above even the hidden ten *Sefiros*. With this, the mediation of the two interpretations of "How does she sit solitary" is understood: the simple meaning and the Tzemach Tzedek’s interpretation that it refers to the elevation and revelation of the level of *badad*. For the revelation of the level of *badad* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus* is through the *avodah* of *Kabbalas Ol* specifically during the time of exile, as mentioned. This is "How does she sit solitary..." *Eicha* as an expression of wonder and astonishment, that one will come from "full of people," "glowing coals," and "full of this," etc., to the *badad* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus*, and in a manner of *yishvah*—this is a matter of wonder. (Furthermore, one can say that the revelation and settling of the level of *badad* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus* is not according to *Seder Hishtalshelus*, above intellect and reason. Therefore, the *avodah* through which the revelation of the level of *badad* will be drawn down is the *avodah* of *Teshuvah*, for the concept of *Teshuvah* is the *avodah* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus* in the soul of man.)

7) The connection of the level of *badad*, the level of *Yachid*, specifically to Yaakov (as it is written, "So Israel dwells in safety, alone, the fountain of Yaakov") is because, as stated above, *badad* is the level of *Atik*, which is above the two lines, right and left, as it is said: "And there is no left in this *Atik*." Therefore, the revelation of this level is through the *avodah* specifically in the third line. As it is written, "Zion shall be redeemed with judgment," and the Tzemach Tzedek explains that judgment is specifically in three—that is, *Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes*. This means that the creation of a dwelling place for Him, in a manner of perfection, is through the *avodah* in all three lines specifically. As the Rebbe Rayatz explains in the Mishnah "The world stands on three things," that through the *avodah* in the three lines—*Torah*, *Avodah*, and *Gemilus Chasadim*—the world stands, for the intention of the creation of the world is completed. This is also the concept of the Third Beis, the third line, the level of the "inheritance without boundaries" of Yaakov, in which there will be (also) the inclusion of the First Beis and the Second Beis. And this will be higher even than how it was in the Garden of Eden of old, meaning even higher than how it was in the Garden of Eden before the sin, as is known regarding the concept of *Adam* and Mashiach, that *Adam* is an acronym for *Adam, David, Mashiach*. The combination is in the order of *A-D-M*—which indicates order, etc., whereas regarding Mashiach it is written: "Behold, My servant shall prosper, he shall be high and lifted up and very exalted." *Me'od* (very) has the letters of *Adam*, but in a combination that indicates something beyond limitation, the opposite of the concept of the figure of *Adam*.

8) As mentioned above, the revelation of the future is drawn down through the *avodah* of now, specifically. From this, it is understood that there is an advantage in the *avodah* of now even over the revelation of the future. As the Rebbe Maharash explains in the interpretation of the Mishnah: "One hour of *Teshuvah* and good deeds in this world is better than all the life of the World to Come," for since the *avodah* of *Teshuvah* and good deeds in this world is the cause of the life of the World to Come (including also the revelations of the future), it is necessarily the case that there is an advantage in the *avodah* of this world over the revelations of the future, for the thing that causes is stronger than the thing that is created through it. And also regarding the matter of *taanug* (delight), that the level of the "inheritance without boundaries" of Yaakov is in the time of *re'ua d're'uin* (the concept of *taanug*), there is an advantage in the *avodah* of now specifically. As he explains there before that, that the *taanug* of the future is (in general) the pleasure of the created being, and the *taanug* of *Teshuvah* and good deeds in this world is (in general) the pleasure of the Creator, "pleasure before Me" that I have spoken and My will was done.

This is that through our deeds and our *avodah* of now, we draw down that very soon the Third Beis will be built and revealed, the level of "So Israel dwells in safety, alone, the fountain of Yaakov," in which there will also be the inclusion of the First Beis and the Second Beis. And then "Hashem alone shall lead him" (each and every one of the Children of Israel), even though (and through the fact that) he finds him in a desert land and in a howling wilderness (the *avodah* in this current exile), he will come from the desert to "alone He shall lead him," in the manner of what is written before it: "Like an eagle that stirs up its nest," with mercy and compassion—that very soon the redemption will come with kindness and mercy, and then there will be the perfection of the intention that the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds.

## With the help of Heaven. Wednesday, 15th of Av, 5735

### With the help of Heaven. Wednesday, 15th of Av, 5735

"There were no better days for Israel than the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur". The Gemara asks: It is understandable that Yom Kippur is a festive day, for it contains forgiveness and pardon, and it is the day the second Tablets were given; but what is the significance of the 15th of Av? The Gemara answers that several positive events occurred on the 15th of Av (such as the day the tribes were permitted to intermarry, etc.). We must understand the magnitude of the elevation of these events, such that the festival of the 15th of Av is greater than other festivals. Especially since the plain meaning of the phrase "there were no better days for Israel than the 15th of Av, etc." implies that it is greater than all festivals, even the three *Regalim*. We must also understand why the phrasing "there were no... like the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur" implies that the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur are related to one another. Furthermore, we must explain why this statement serves as the conclusion and seal of *Maseches Taanis*, for seemingly, a *taanis* (fast) and a *yom tov* [especially a *yom tov* of such magnitude, that there were no better days than it] are opposites.

The matter is that the essence of the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av is as explained in the *maamar* regarding the 15th of Av by the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.* from *Pri Eitz Chaim*: that it is then the [perfection] of the fullness of the moon [and the events that occurred on the 15th of Av are like outcomes of the *essential* nature of this day – the perfection of the moon’s fullness]. The *maamar* explains that although the moon is full on the 15th of every month, the greatness of the moon’s fullness is its fullness and perfection *after* a diminution, for perfection after a diminution is a higher level of perfection than the perfection that exists on its own. As is known regarding the principle of ascents and descents: an ascent that follows a descent is an ascent to a level higher than the level that existed before the descent, and the greater the descent, the greater the ascent. Therefore, the essential virtue of the moon’s fullness is on the 15th of Av, because in the month of Av, the descent of the moon (for "Israel is likened to the moon") is a very great descent; therefore, the ascent of the 15th of Av (which follows the descent of the 9th of Av) is a very great ascent. And this is "there were no better days for Israel than the 15th of Av," for it is a *yom tov* greater even than the festivals of Pesach and Sukkos, even though those festivals also occur on the 15th of the month. For the ascent of the 15th of Nissan (Pesach), although it comes after the descent of the Egyptian exile, nevertheless, when Israel left Egypt, the beginning of their *avodah* was at the level of *tzaddikim*, for a convert who has converted is like a newborn child, and therefore the ascent of the 15th of Nissan is not as directly continuous with the descent that preceded it. Also, the ascent of the 15th of Tishrei (Sukkos), although the *yom tov* of Sukkos comes in continuation of the *teshuvah* and atonement of Yom Kippur, nevertheless, the ascent itself from the undesirable state that existed previously occurs on Yom Kippur, and the revelation of the matters drawn down on Yom Kippur is in Sukkos. Not so the ascent that follows the descent of the beginning of the month of Av, where the ascent itself is on the 15th of Av; therefore, the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av is greater than the *yom tov* of Pesach and Sukkos.

2) But it still requires understanding: the *yom tov* of Pesach and Sukkos (and Shavuos) is from the Torah, and how is it possible that the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av could be greater than the *yom tov* of the three *Regalim*? We must also understand that from the fact that it says "there were no better days for Israel than the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur," placing the 15th of Av before Yom Kippur [even though the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av was established (according to all the reasons in the Gemara) many years after the *yom tov* of Yom Kippur], it implies that the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av is more exalted even than the *yom tov* of Yom Kippur. This requires explanation, for on Yom Kippur, too, there is an ascent from an undesirable state; what is the virtue of the 15th of Av over Yom Kippur?

3) This can be understood based on what is explained in the *maamar* regarding the interpretation of the verse "The advantage of the land in all is a king for a cultivated field". "Land" (*eretz*) is the totality of the world, and "field" (*sadeh*—the choicest part of the land) is *Gan Eden*. This distinction between the totality of the world and *Gan Eden* (where the totality of the world is called "land" and *Gan Eden* is "field") is in their root. The formation of the world is from the aspect of the speech of *Malchus* (the external aspect of *Malchus*), which is called "land," and *Gan Eden* is from the aspect of the first three [attributes] of *Malchus* (the internal aspect of *Malchus*), which is called "field," as explained in the *maamar*. The speech of *Malchus* (the ten utterances with which the world was created) has the purpose of bringing the created beings into existence, similar to speech in a human, which is for the sake of another. The first three of *Malchus* are the internal aspect of *Malchus*, which receives from *Yesod*, which is the end of *Atzilus* (*siyuma d'gufa*), similar to the attributes in a human, which, although they relate to another, their purpose is that *the person* is aroused and affected.

The *maamar* adds that there is another advantage of *Gan Eden* over the totality of the world: the *hemshech* (drawing down) into the world is from the attributes, because the speech of *Malchus* receives from the attributes, whereas the *hemshech* into *Gan Eden* is from the *mochin* (intellect). As explained there, the fact that *Yesod* is called by the name *Kol* (All) is because of the fifty gates of *Binah* that are drawn into it (*Kol* in *gematria* is fifty). Therefore, since *Gan Eden* is from the internal aspect of *Malchus* which receives from *Yesod*, through *Yesod*, the *mochin* are also drawn into *Gan Eden*. This is "The advantage of the land in all is a king for a cultivated field"—that the advantage of the land (the totality of the world, whose formation is from the speech of *Malchus*) is in *Kol*—the *hemshech* of *Yesod*—and through this, the *hemshech* of the *mochin*, and then a revelation of *Elokus* is drawn into the totality of the world as well, just as in *Gan Eden*. And "a king for a cultivated field" is as stated in the *Zohar*: "Who is the king? This is the higher King who connects to the field when it is cultivated," for through the *avodah* in *Gan Eden* (the cultivated field), the *hemshech* of *Keter* (the higher King) is effected, which is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

The *maamar* explains that then, when the *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* shines into *Malchus*, "the moon stands in its perfection," for the light shines also into the external aspect of *Malchus* (the speech of *Malchus*, the ten utterances with which the world was created), and through this, into the world as well. For in the *hemshech* that follows the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, there is a distinction between the internal aspect of *Malchus* (field) and the external aspect of *Malchus* (land). Therefore, when the *hemshech* in *Malchus* is from the aspect of *mochin*, the revelation is only in the level of *Malchus* that receives from *Ze'er Anpin* (the internal aspect of *Malchus*), and in the level of *Malchus* that is the root of the created beings (the ten utterances), the light does not shine. Similar to the moon at the time of its diminution, where the sunlight shines only on its upper hemisphere. But when the *hemshech* is from the *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the revelation is also in the ten utterances (and through them, also in the world), similar to the moon at the time of its fullness (in the middle of the month), where the sunlight shines also on its lower hemisphere.

4) We must understand: seemingly, the matter of the diminution of the moon is that in order for the formation of the worlds to occur, a diminution and deficiency is made in *Malchus* ("You made the heavens...", "You diminished..."), such that the light of *Atzilus* that is above the root of the created beings does not shine in it. Since in *Gan Eden* the aspect of *Kol*—*Yesod* and also the *mochin*—shines, there is no deficiency in it. As explained in the *maamar*, the reason *Gan Eden* is called by the name *Kol* is because it contains everything without deficiency. Accordingly, it turns out that even in *Gan Eden*, the moon (*Malchus*) is in perfection. The *maamar* states that the matter of "the moon stands in its perfection" is specifically when "a king for a cultivated field," for through the *avodah*, the *Keter* (higher King) that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is drawn into it.

It can be said that the explanation for this is that the true meaning of "the moon stands in its perfection" is that the perfection is in a manner where it is impossible for there to be a deficiency. This perfection is specifically when the *hemshech* is from a light that is above relevance to the worlds, in which it is impossible for there to be *Tzimtzum*. For a light that relates to the worlds, even the light that is before the *Tzimtzum*, is a light in which *Tzimtzum* is possible. Therefore, the *hemshech* of the aspect of *Kol* in *Gan Eden*, although the *hemshech* is in perfection [as mentioned above from the *maamar* that the interpretation of *Kol* is "everything without deficiency"], since the *hemshech* is from a limited light (*mochin*) in which *Tzimtzum* and interruption are possible, it is not the true perfection. The true meaning of "the moon stands in its perfection" is through the *avodah* of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, through which is drawn down the light of the *Bli Gvul* (that which is above the light that relates to the worlds), in which *Tzimtzum* is impossible—"a king for a cultivated field."

5) Now, it is explained in the *maamar* that regarding "the field which Hashem has blessed", there are two interpretations: Rashi’s interpretation that it is *Gan Eden*, and the *Targum Yonasan’s* interpretation that it is the *Beis Hamikdash*. As explained in many places, the *Beis Hamikdash* is like *Gan Eden*. And just as in *Gan Eden* there are two levels—*Gan Eden* on its own, and the additional light drawn into it through *avodah*—so too is it in the *Beis Hamikdash*: in addition to the revelation that was in the *Beis Hamikdash* on its own, through the *avodah* in the *Beis Hamikdash* (the *avodah* of the sacrifices), a more exalted revelation shone in it. Based on what is written in the *maamar* that the matter of "the moon stands in its perfection" is (primarily) through the *avodah* in the field ("a king for a cultivated field"), it is understood that it is the same regarding the *Beis Hamikdash*: the matter of "the moon stands in its perfection" that was in the *Beis Hamikdash* on its own—both the place of the *Beis Hamikdash*, of which it is said "there is no place like this", and the time of the building of the *Beis Hamikdash*, which was built by Solomon, the fifteenth generation from Abraham, when "the moon stood in its perfection"—is like the revelation in *Gan Eden* on its own, the field. The essential "moon standing in its perfection" that was in the *Beis Hamikdash* is that through the *avodah* in the *Beis Hamikdash*, an additional light was drawn into it that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—"a king for a cultivated field."

Accordingly, it can be said that the revelation that was in the *Beis Hamikdash* on its own had its *hemshech* only during the time of the Temple. As explained in the *maamar*, the difference between the time of the Temple and the time of exile is like the difference between the upper hemisphere of the moon and its lower hemisphere. Therefore, since the revelation that was in the *Beis Hamikdash* on its own is a limited light that shines only in the level of *Malchus* that receives from *Ze'er Anpin* (the upper hemisphere of the moon), its *hemshech* was only during the time of the Temple. The light that was added to the *Beis Hamikdash* through *avodah* [the *avodah* of the sacrifices, and similarly the *avodah* of "and they shall make Me a sanctuary"], since this light is *Bli Gvul* in which interruption is impossible, its *hemshech* is also during the time of exile. However, due to the descent in the time of exile, the light is not felt in the world (as will be discussed in section 6).

6) The *maamar* continues that there is another interpretation in the *Zohar* for "a king for a cultivated field," which is to the negative. For "field" is the field of the *Sitra Achra* ("in the field he found her"), and "a king for a cultivated field" means that the *Malchus* of *Kedushah* is enslaved to the field of the *Sitra Achra*. It can be said that the fact that this interpretation of "a king for a cultivated field" comes after and in continuation of the interpretation that "a king for a cultivated field" is to the positive, is because the existence of the matter of "a king for a cultivated field" to the negative is so that the matter of "a king for a cultivated field" to the positive—the *hemshech* of the higher King (*Keter*)—will be in a more exalted manner. It can be said that the elevation added to the *hemshech* of the *Keter* through the descent (of "a king for a cultivated field" to the negative) relative to the *hemshech* that was before the descent is an incomparable addition. To the point that relative to the *hemshech* after the descent, the *hemshech* that was before is within the general *Seder Hishtalshelus*. This is what our Sages said: that the fact that "a lion came in the constellation of a lion and destroyed *Ariel*..." is on the condition that "a lion will come in the constellation of a lion and build *Ariel*." It is known that "a lion will come" [this is the Holy One, blessed be He, for it is written regarding Him "a lion has roared, who will not fear"] is the revelation of the *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. From the fact that in order for "a lion will come" (the revelation of the *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*) to occur, it was necessary for "a lion to come... and destroy *Ariel*," even though the matter of "a king for a cultivated field" (to the positive) existed even before, it is understood that the *hemshech* of the *Keter* (higher King) that was before, relative to the *hemshech* after the descent, is within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

It can be said that the explanation for this is based on what is known that the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* (including also the *hemshech* through *avodah*) is in the manner of *Ohr Yashar* (direct light), from above to below. That is, the revelation that shines in the world through the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* is (primarily) from above, and in order for there to be refinement and ascent also in the "below" itself, this is done (primarily) through the *avodah* of *teshuvah*. Accordingly, it is understood why the *hemshech* of the *Keter* (higher King) that was before the descent of the exile, relative to the *hemshech* after the descent, is within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. For the true meaning of "above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*" is that it does not have the limitation and distinction of "above" and "below." Since the *avodah* during the time of the Temple is (generally) the *avodah* of *tzaddikim*, where the *hemshech* through this *avodah* is (primarily) from above—meaning that even after the *hemshech* there is a distinction between the above and the below—it turns out that this *hemshech* is within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. [However, within the aspects of *Hishtalshelus* itself, the *hemshech* through the *avodah* of *Torah* and *mitzvos* is from the light of the *Bli Gvul*, which is equal in every place. Therefore, the light drawn into the *Beis Hamikdash* through *avodah* exists also during the time of exile (as mentioned above in section 5). But nevertheless, since the fact that the light is in every place is because *the light* is *Ein Sof*, therefore, in order for the light to be felt *in the world*, it is specifically when the world is in a manner that it has a connection to the light. And since during the time of exile a descent occurs in the world, therefore, during the time of exile, the revelation does not shine in the world.] But through the *avodah* during the time of exile, which is (generally) the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, the *hemshech* is from a place that does not have the distinction of above and below, the true meaning of "above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*," through which *hemshech* a refinement and ascent is effected also in the "below" itself.

7) This can be explained more deeply based on what is explained elsewhere that the revelation drawn into the world through the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*—since the intent of creation from the outset was that the *tzaddikim* ("and your people are all *tzaddikim*") through their *avodah* would add a revelation of *Elokus* in the world, "with whom did He consult? With the souls of the *tzaddikim*"—therefore, the revelation drawn into the world through the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*, even the revelation that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, including also that through the *avodah* of *Torah* and *mitzvos* a new light is drawn down that did not shine even before the *Tzimtzum*, is not a true innovation. Not so through the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, when a person has sinned and blemished and diverted from the path (the opposite of the intent of the creation of man, which was in a manner of "G-d made man upright") and afterwards repairs this through *teshuvah*—through this, an innovation is effected even relative to the intent of creation as it is at the level of "with whom did He consult." The fact that it is within the power of man to effect this innovation is because the root of the souls is in the *Atzmus* (Essence), which is above their root in the matter of "with whom did He consult." For although the "consultation" is above all revelations, even from the revelation of "desiring kindness"—for the consultation is whether to be "desiring kindness" or not—nevertheless, the consultation is regarding the revelations (whether there will be revelations or not), and the root of the souls is in the *Atzmus*.

This is the perfection of the world that will be in the future: "These are the generations of Peretz"—generations that are full (*malei*)—will be more exalted than the perfection that was at the beginning of creation: "These are the generations of the heavens and the earth when they were created (*behibaram*)"—generations that are full (*malei*)—"the world was created in its fullness". For the perfection of the world as it is from the side of creation, including also the perfection from the side of the intent of creation (the matter of "with whom did He consult"), is in measurement and limitation. The perfection of the world that will be in the future through the *avodah* of *teshuvah* [for the revelation of the future will be primarily through the *avodah* of *teshuvah*] will be above measurement and limitation: "These are the generations of Peretz," for the matter of *Peretz* [which is so named because of "you have broken forth a breach"] is that it breaks through all measurements and limitations, including also the measurement and limitation that is from the side of the intent of creation as it is in the aspect of the "consultation," meaning "new heavens and a new earth".

8) Accordingly, we can explain the differences in levels in the fullness and perfection of the moon (from section 1 above). The fullness and perfection of the moon on the 15th of every month, since it is from the side of nature that the Holy One, blessed be He, implanted in creation and is not connected with the *avodah* of Israel, is (in general) a *hemshech* according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. The fact that on the 15th of the month the light shines also on the lower half of the moon is from the virtue of the 15th day, in which even the lower half is like the upper half. The perfection of the moon on the 15th of Nissan and 15th of Tishrei, since it is connected (also) with the *avodah* of man, is (in general) a *hemshech* above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Therefore, the 15th of Nissan and 15th of Tishrei are *yomim tovim*, for the matter of *yom tov* is the *hemshech* of a light that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. The perfection of the moon on the 15th of Av, which is connected with the *avodah* of *teshuvah* (the ascent after the descent of the 9th of Av), is that the fact that it shines also on the lower half of the moon is (not only because the light is *Ein Sof* and therefore shines also below, but also) because of the ascent in *Malchus* itself. As explained in the *maamar*, on the 15th of Av, the aspect of *Atik* shines in *Malchus*, which can be said to be the revelation of the virtue and root of *Malchus* itself. This is also the connection of the 15th of Av to Yom Kippur, for on Yom Kippur, too, there is the ascent of *Malchus* into the interior of *Atik*, as explained in the *maamar*.

9) It can be said that the fact that the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av is more exalted even than Yom Kippur, although Yom Kippur is also the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, is because from the very fact that the Torah established a day of forgiveness and atonement every single year, it is understood that the descent to the undesirable things after which the ascent of Yom Kippur comes is in a manner that has a place from the side of creation. For the fact that it was established in the Torah ("He looked into the Torah and created the world") a day of forgiveness and atonement for undesirable things is because of the magnitude of the elevation in *teshuvah*—"in the place where *baalei teshuvah* stand, perfect *tzaddikim* cannot stand"—there is a place for this (also) from the side of the intent of creation as it is drawn down in revelation, at the level of "with whom did He consult," even though *the primary* intent at this level is the *avodah* of *tzaddikim*, "with whom did He consult? With the souls of the *tzaddikim*." Not so the descent of the 9th of Av, the destruction of the *Beis Hamikdash* and the exile; it is a descent such that it has no place [as is also understood from the Book of *Eichah*, that the fact that it says *Eichah* (How) in a tone of wonderment is because even from the side of the elevation in *teshuvah*, there is no place for such a descent]. The fact that in actuality this descent occurred so that there would be a more exalted ascent—"a lion came... on the condition that a lion will come"—is only from the side of the true intent (as it is in the *Atzmus*), that through the *avodah* of Israel there will be an innovation in creation, "new heavens and a new earth." Therefore, the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av is more exalted even than Yom Kippur.

This is also why the conclusion and seal of *Maseches Taanis* is "there were no better days for Israel than the 15th of Av, etc.," for this is the explanation of all the fasts. The fact that there are undesirable things that one must fast over, up to the things that occurred on the 17th of Tammuz and the 9th of Av, is for the sake of the ascent that follows the descent—the *yom tov* of the 15th of Av, which is the day of "the joy of His heart" (of the Holy One, blessed be He), which is the building of the *Beis Hamikdash* that will be built speedily in our days.

May it be His will that through our deeds and our *avodah* not to be affected by any trials, including also such trials that from the side of all calculations (also from the side of the elevation in the *avodah* of trials) there is no explanation for them, they will hasten and accelerate even more the future Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, who will fight the wars of Hashem and be victorious [for most of these wars have no place in the intellect, not even in the intellect of the warriors, and therefore the wars are with great intensity, and nevertheless he will be victorious], and he will build the *Beis Hamikdash* in its place, and gather the outcasts of Israel, including that he will gather all the sparks of *Kedushah* and also the outcasts of Israel literally—the ingathering of the exiles, very soon, in the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## With the help of Hashem. Monday, Parshas Eikev, 15 Menachem Av, 5747

### With the help of Hashem. Monday, Parshas Eikev, 15 Menachem Av, 5747

There were no better days for Yisrael than the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur. The Rebbe (Rashab) n.e. brings in his maamar explaining the concept of the 15th of Av that it is stated in Pri Etz Chaim that the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is because it is the perfection of the fullness of the moon [and the events that occurred on the 15th of Av (enumerated in the Gemara) are like results of the *primary* concept of this day – the perfection of the fullness of the moon]. The maamar notes that the moon stands in its perfection on the 15th of every month, yet it was not established as a Yom Tov except for Pesach (15th of Nissan) and Sukkos (15th of Tishrei). Furthermore, it is difficult to understand why the simple meaning of the phrase "there were no better days for Yisrael than the 15th of Av, etc." implies that it is a greater Yom Tov than all other Yomim Tovim, including Pesach and Sukkos, even though those too occur on the 15th of the month. The core explanation in the maamar is that the primary virtue of the fullness and perfection of the moon on this 15th day is that the fullness and perfection come after a deficiency. Perfection that follows a deficiency is a higher level of perfection than that which exists on its own, as is known regarding the rule of ascents and descents: an ascent that follows a descent is an ascent to a level higher than the level prior to the descent, and the greater the descent, the greater the ascent. Therefore, the primary virtue of the moon’s fullness is on the 15th of Av, because in the month of Av, the descent of the moon (and Yisrael, who are likened to the moon) is the greatest descent; thus, the ascent of the 15th of Av (which follows the descent of Tisha B’Av) is the greatest ascent.

2) It can be said that the aforementioned concept—that the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is because it is the ascent following the descent of Tisha B’Av—is also hinted at by the fact that the first event that occurred on the 15th of Av was that the generation of the desert ceased to die. The matter of the generation of the desert is connected to Tisha B’Av, for on Tisha B’Av it was decreed upon the generation of the desert that they would die in the desert and not enter the land, and the fulfillment of the decree also took place on Tisha B’Av, as every Tisha B’Av (during the last 37 years they were in the desert) they would dig their graves. The Yom Tov of the 15th of Av, on which the generation of the desert ceased to die, is the ascent following the descent of Tisha B’Av. From this, we can also understand regarding the (primary) descent of Tisha B’Av, on which the Beis Hamikdash was destroyed in the first and second instances [and specifically, the decree of the destruction also occurred on that same day (the Tisha B’Av of the first year in the desert) on which it was decreed that the generation of the desert would not enter the land, and both decrees were for the same sin (the sin of the spies)], that on the 15th of Av there shines a glimmer of the revelation of the future, the essence of which is the building of the Third Beis Hamikdash—the ascent following the descent of the destruction of the first and second Beis Hamikdash.

3) The maamar continues to explain the connection of the 15th of Av to the Third Beis Hamikdash: that in the future, the *Vav-Hei* will also be in the state of *Yud-Hei*, as it is written, "On that day, Hashem will be One" (the word *yihyeh* contains the letters *Yud-Hei* twice). Since the *yineka* of the *chitzonim* is from the level of *Vav-Hei* (*ZON*), whereas from the level of *Yud-Hei* (*Abba-Imma*) there can be no *yineka*, therefore, in the future, when *Vav-Hei* will also be like *Yud-Hei*, destruction and exile will no longer be possible. The maamar adds that one of the differences between *Yud-Hei* (*Abba-Imma*) and *Vav-Hei* (*ZON*) is that *Abba-Imma* are "two companions who never separate," while the *zivug* of *ZON* is only at times. In the future, when *Vav-Hei* will be like *Yud-Hei*, the *zivug* of *Vav-Hei* will also be constant. Therefore, the Beis Hamikdash of the future will be eternal. [For in addition to the fact that in the future Beis Hamikdash destruction will be impossible because the *yineka* of the *chitzonim* will be impossible, the Beis Hamikdash itself will be in a state where interruption is impossible, "a tent that will not be moved, its stakes will never be pulled up"]. This is the connection of *Yud-Hei* (the 15th of Av) to the Third Beis Hamikdash, because the virtue of the Third Beis Hamikdash—that interruption is impossible—is because it will be in the state of *Yud-Hei*.

The maamar continues to explain the concept of *Yud-Hei* twice, prefacing with the well-known concept regarding *Va'eschanan* having the gematria of 515 (*taktuv*): 500 (*tav-kuf*) plus 15 (*tuv*). 500 represents the five *chasadim* of *Arich* [each of which is comprised of one hundred] and higher still, the five *chasadim* of *Atik*. The concept of 515 is that the *chasadim* of *Arich* and *Atik* shine into *Yud-Hei*. This is also the meaning of "fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder"; fifteen (cubits) is *Yud-Hei*, and "shoulder" (*katef*) has the gematria of 500, and the concept of fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder is the drawing down of *Atik* into *Yud-Hei*. This is also the concept of *Yud-Hei* twice, for in the courtyard of the Mishkan there were two shoulders, and on each of them were fifteen cubits of curtains, and two times fifteen is *Yud-Hei* twice. It can be said that the connection of the fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder (the drawing down of *Atik* into *Yud-Hei*) with *Yud-Hei* twice (that *ZON* are like *Abba-Imma*) is because, according to the *seder hishtalshelus*, *ZON* are below *Abba-Imma*, and for *ZON* to be like *Abba-Imma* is through the drawing down of the *Keter* that is above the *hishtalshelus*, and within *Keter* itself—*Atik*. The difference between the two explanations (in the maamar) is that the first explanation speaks of the ascent of *ZON*, while the second explanation speaks of the drawing down of *Atik* (the root and cause for the ascent of *ZON*). The maamar continues that the 15th of Av is also connected to the second explanation of *Yud-Hei* twice, because on the 15th of Av there is a revelation of the *chasadim* of *Atik* in *Abba-Imma*, and through this, a revelation of *Atik* is drawn down into *Malchus* as well. The primary revelation of this will be in the future, but a glimmer of it shines even now on the 15th of Av, as mentioned above (section 2), that on the 15th of Av there is a glimmer of the revelation of the future.

4) The reason why this revelation shines on the 15th of Av is because the 15th of Av is the perfection of the moon following the descent of Tisha B’Av (as mentioned in section 1). One must understand that the primary "standing of the moon in its perfection" (on the 15th of the month) is only regarding its revelation. The moon itself is in perfection throughout all the days of the month, and the virtue of the 15th is that the perfection of the moon is in a state of revelation. Since all matters in the Torah are with ultimate precision, one must say that the virtue of the 15th of Av is in the matter of revelation. This requires explanation: the 15th of Av is a glimmer of the revelation of the Beis Hamikdash of the future, which will be (in addition to the revelation of the first and second houses) greater than the first and second houses. The greatness of the Third House over the first and second is a greatness beyond compare, as is also understood from what was explained above (section 3) that the Third Beis Hamikdash is connected to the concept of *Yud-Hei* twice, that *ZON* will be like *Abba-Imma* and that in *Abba-Imma* there will be a revelation of *Atik*. Yet, they connect the virtue of the 15th of Av to the fact that on the 15th is the perfection of the moon—perfection in the matter of revelation. It must also be understood that since the matter of the 15th of Av is similar to the matter of the fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder in the courtyard of the Mishkan, which existed even before the matter of the 15th of Av—even before the first event that occurred on the 15th of Av, the day the generation of the desert ceased to die [and furthermore, even before the sending of the spies, because of which the matter of the generation of the desert was decreed]—what is the magnitude of the elevation and the novelty of the 15th of Av, such that "there were no better days for Yisrael than the 15th of Av"?

This matter (that the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is connected to the matter of revelation) is also understood from the fact that one of the reasons for establishing the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is that it is the day the generation of the desert ceased to die (as mentioned in section 2). The content of the day the generation of the desert ceased to die is that it was then clarified and revealed—*it was revealed retroactively*—that *Tisha B’Av* is the day the generation of the desert ceased to die. Yet, they established the Yom Tov on the 15th of Av, on which it was clarified and revealed that the generation of the desert had ceased to die, because this Yom Tov is connected to the matter of revelation.

5) This can be understood by prefacing that just as the decree of the generation of the desert ended on Tisha B’Av, but they did not know it clearly until the moon was full on the 15th day, so too is it with the decree of the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash and the exile: the nullification of this decree is on Tisha B’Av, for on Tisha B’Av Mashiach was born, and on the night following Tisha B’Av we sanctify the moon, the concept of which (Kiddush Levanah) is that *they* are destined to be renewed like it. However, the revelation of this matter (in perfection) is on the 15th of Av, on which is the fullness and perfection of the moon.

More deeply, it can be said that the fact that on Tisha B’Av there was the beginning of the matter of the future redemption is not only at the moment after the destruction, when the savior of Yisrael was born, but even before that. For the fact that "a lion came and destroyed the Ariel" was *on the condition* that "a lion will come and build the Ariel".
