From this it is understood that the intent that "the Ariel will be built" existed before he destroyed the Ariel, but at that time, this intent and thought was in a state of concealment (in the level of thought) and was not drawn down into revelation, so that the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash could take place, through which specifically the building of the Third Beis Hamikdash—which is greater than the first and second—would occur. At the moment after the destruction, the revelation of the future redemption began—the savior of Yisrael *was born*. However, the birth on Tisha B’Av is only the beginning of the revelation [as is also understood from the matters of Tisha B’Av that exist even after the *Mincha* of Tisha B’Av and even after *Kiddush Levanah* on the night following Tisha B’Av], and the primary revelation is on the 15th of Av. According to this, the connection of the virtue of the 15th of Av to the fact that on the 15th is the perfection of the moon—which is perfection in the matter of revelation—is understood, because the concept of the 15th of Av is that on it is the revelation of the redemption that existed (in concealment, in thought and intent) on Tisha B’Av.

6) It can be said that the reason why the commandment "And they shall make Me a sanctuary," which is a commandment for all generations to make a house for Hashem [a commandment regarding all sanctuaries, including the future Beis Hamikdash], was stated (in revelation) regarding the making of the Mishkan, is because in the Mishkan, the Beis Hamikdash, which is a permanent dwelling, was also included in concealment, as was the future Beis Hamikdash, which is "a tent that will not be moved," the essence of the matter of permanence (as mentioned in section 3). This is similar to what is known regarding the redemptions: that in the redemption of the Exodus from Egypt, the conduit was opened, and all redemptions were included in it, including the future redemption. However, the revelation of the Third Beis Hamikdash and the third redemption is through the *avodah* during the time of exile, which is similar to the *avodah* of *teshuvah*. And since at the time of the Exodus from Egypt, Yisrael were at the level of *tzaddikim*, therefore, the matter of the future redemption that was included in the redemption of the Exodus from Egypt was then in concealment.

According to this, one can explain why in the courtyard of the Mishkan there were fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder, even though this matter is connected to the Third Beis Hamikdash, because in the Mishkan, both the Beis Hamikdash and the Third Beis Hamikdash were included. Yet, there were no better days for Yisrael than the 15th of Av, because before the sin of the spies, when according to the *seder hishtalshelus* there was no place for the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash and consequently not for the building of the Third Beis Hamikdash, this was in ultimate concealment. After the sin of the spies, when it was decreed upon the generation of the desert that they would not enter the land, and the beginning of the matter of the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash also occurred [for then was the beginning of the drawing down of the Third Beis Hamikdash in the level of thought], then on the 15th of Av of every year (starting from the 15th of Av on which the generation of the desert ceased to die, and all the more so after the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash) there is a revelation of the inwardness of the fifteen cubits of curtains for the shoulder in the courtyard of the Mishkan, the concept of which is the drawing down of *Atik* into *Yud-Hei* and through this also into *Malchus*, the concept of "a tent that will not be moved," the Third Beis Hamikdash in which interruption is impossible. Then, the inner intent of the weeping of the first Tisha B’Av is also revealed, "And the people wept on that night", through which weeping for generations was established, which is so that the weeping will be for the elevation of the future, "With weeping they will come," a weeping of joy due to the revelation of the high levels, similar to what our Sages said regarding Rabbi Akiva, that when he grasped the secrets of the Torah in *Shir HaShirim*, his eyes shed tears—tears of joy due to the abundance of light.

7) This is why on the 15th of Av the daughters of Yerushalayim [and some have the version—the daughters of Yisrael] would go out and dance in the vineyards. The dance of the 15th of Av is in the likeness and a glimmer of the dance of the future, when the Holy One, blessed be He, will make a dance for the *tzaddikim*, and each one will point with his finger and say, "Behold, this is our G-d, we hoped for Him and He will save us; this is Hashem, we hoped for Him, let us rejoice and be glad in His salvation." At the Exodus from Egypt, they said "this" once ("This is my G-d and I will glorify Him"), and in the future, they will say "this" twice ("Behold, this is our G-d... this is Hashem..."). At the Exodus from Egypt, when they were at the level of *tzaddikim*, they said "this" only once—the revelation of the *Havayah* of *Z'A*. In the future, when they will be at the level of *baalei teshuvah* [for *teshuvah* is "double the wisdom"], they will say "this" twice—the revelation of the *Havayah* of *Z'A* and the revelation of the *Havayah* of *Atik*. The verse continues, "let us rejoice and be glad in His salvation," and it can be said that "His salvation" (of the Holy One, blessed be He) that follows the second "this" is the inwardness of *Atik*. As is known, in the future there will be (also) the revelation of the inwardness of *Atik*.

May it be His will that all these matters will be very soon, and especially after they said in the *Haftorah* of the *Mincha* of Tisha B’Av, "My salvation is near to come," that "My salvation" (of the Holy One, blessed be He)—the salvation of which it is said "let us rejoice and be glad in His salvation"—is near to come, very soon and in our days, Amen, may it be His will.

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Eikev, 20 Menachem-Av, 5723

“He afflicted you and let you hunger, and He fed you the manna…” The Rebbe (Rashab) n”e notes in his maamar on this topic that while the Torah elsewhere speaks of the virtue of the manna, here it says, “He afflicted you and let you hunger,” which seemingly contradicts that virtue. Furthermore, we must understand the Gemara’s statement that Moshe instituted the *Birkas HaZan* for the Jewish people when the manna descended, while Yehoshua instituted the *Birkas HaAretz* when they entered the Land. The Rashba writes that this means they established the structure of the blessings, as the blessings themselves are from the Torah (as the Gemara states: “And you shall eat and be satisfied and bless” — this refers to *Birkas HaZan*; “for the land” — this refers to *Birkas HaAretz*). It is stated in *Likutei Torah* that the reason we mention “and for the eating of food” in *Birkas HaAretz* as well, and conclude the blessing with “for the land and for the food” (even though we have already recited *Birkas HaZan*), is because the text and structure of *Birkas HaZan* refers to the manna, the bread from heaven, while the food in *Birkas HaAretz* is bread from the earth. This requires explanation: *Birkas HaZan* is for the eating that satisfies (“and you shall eat *and be satisfied*”), and satisfying eating is (primarily) from bread of the earth. Yet, the blessing for the food of bread from the earth is in *Birkas HaAretz* (in which it is *not* stated “and you shall eat and be satisfied”), while the text of *Birkas HaZan* (in which “and you shall eat *and be satisfied*” is written) refers to the manna, about which it is written, “He afflicted you and let you hunger.”

We must also understand why the affliction of Yom Kippur is learned from the affliction mentioned regarding the manna. It says “affliction” here (“and you shall afflict your souls”) and “affliction” there (“He afflicted you and let you hunger”); just as there it refers to the affliction of hunger, so too here it refers to the affliction of hunger. This requires explanation, for the affliction of hunger regarding the manna means that eating the manna did not satisfy them as much as was necessary (for one who has bread in his basket is not like one who does not have bread in his basket—and the manna was a “day-by-day” thing—and one who sees and eats is not like one who does not see and eat—and with the manna, they tasted all flavors but saw only manna). From the fact that the hunger-affliction of the manna is compared to the hunger-affliction of Yom Kippur, it implies that the hunger-affliction of the manna was (not merely that the manna did not satisfy like ordinary eating, but) as if they had not eaten at all. It should be noted that this makes it even more difficult to understand why the text of *Birkas HaZan* refers to the manna. We must also understand why, now (after the manna has ceased), all the blessings of *Birkas Hamazon* seemingly refer to bread from the earth, yet the text of *Birkas HaZan* remains the text that Moshe instituted for the manna.

2. This can be understood by prefacing the Midrash’s statement that the manna was “food of hunger.” The meaning of “He let you hunger… the manna” is that “He let you hunger” refers to “the manna”—that the manna caused you hunger. The concept is that the manna alludes to *Aggadah* (as it is written, “And it was like coriander seed, white,” and it is stated in the *Mechilta* that it is like *Aggadah*, which draws a person’s heart), which is the *pnimiyus haTorah*. As explained elsewhere, bread from the earth is *nigleh d’Torah*, and bread from heaven (manna) is *pnimiyus haTorah*. Since in *pnimiyus haTorah* there is only knowledge of the existence, not the attainment of the essence, the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* is connected to hunger (similar to the “hunger to hear the word of Hashem”) to attain the essence.

More deeply, we can say that when the Midrash says the manna is “food of hunger,” it means (not only that the manna *acts* in a way that does not negate hunger in the person eating it, but also) that the manna itself is food of hunger. This can be understood by prefacing that the aforementioned explanation—that bread from the earth is *nigleh d’Torah* and bread from heaven is *pnimiyus haTorah*—is in a general sense. Specifically, however, these two matters (bread from the earth and bread from heaven) exist even within *pnimiyus haTorah*. The matter is that it is stated in *Tanya* that there are two aspects to the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*: it is a lofty and exalted *mitzvah*, and it leads to a “perfect heart.” It can be said that the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* insofar as it leads to a “perfect heart”—since it relates to the matter of *birurim* (refining the *midos*)—is similar to bread from the earth, while the essential matter of bread from heaven is the study and knowledge of *pnimiyus haTorah* for its own sake. It can be said that the distinction between these two modes of study also exists in the level of the intellect: the study and knowledge of *pnimiyus haTorah* in order to arrive at a “perfect heart” is in the *mochin* that relate to the *midos*, while the study and knowledge of *pnimiyus haTorah* for its own sake is in the *mochin* that are above the *midos*. Based on this, we can explain that the manna is “food of hunger,” because the concept of satisfaction (in the realm of intellect) is that it *grasps* the intellect. Therefore, the knowledge and attainment of the *mochin* that relate to the *midos* (bread from the earth within *pnimiyus haTorah*), which is grasped in the human intellect through actual attainment and comprehension (which is why the attainment also affects his *midos*), is food that satisfies. The knowledge and attainment of the *mochin* that are above the *midos* (bread from heaven, manna), which is in a manner of wonderment and is not (fully) grasped in the human intellect, is food of hunger.

3. It can be said that the distinction between the two interpretations of “food of hunger”—that it *acts* in a way that does not negate hunger in the person, and that the food itself is hunger that is above comprehension (even though the knowledge that causes hunger in the person is also because it is above his attainment)—is that the latter knowledge is at the level of intellect that corresponds to the *midos*, but is above them; therefore, it causes in the person (whose essence is *midos*) a hunger and thirst to attain the matter. The knowledge that is itself a state of hunger is at the level of intellect that is above the *midos* (as mentioned in section 2), which is why it is a state of hunger in essence relative to the *midos*. When this level is revealed in the *midos*, they are in a state of *bitul*. This is similar to the distinction between *Chochma* and *Binah*: through the attainment of *Binah*, when the contemplation and attainment are in the wonderment of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, one comes to *ahavah rabbah* (with longing and thirst)—there is one who loves. Through the vision of *Chochma*, one comes to *yirah*, to *bitul*. Nevertheless, even this level of manna is called “food of hunger,” because the refinement that comes through eating the manna is that the person who eats the manna is in a state of absolute *bitul*, and thereby becomes a vessel to receive vitality from a light that is not in his category. This is similar to the matter of “reviving them in hunger” of Yom Kippur, where the hunger of Yom Kippur is a state of intrinsic, unfelt *taanug* that is above eating and drinking (as is known, the reason eating and drinking are forbidden on Yom Kippur is because Yom Kippur is a revelation of intrinsic, unfelt *taanug*), and the matter of “reviving them in hunger” is that on Yom Kippur one receives vitality from this *taanug*.

4. We can connect this to the statement of the *Zohar* on the verse, “See that Hashem has given you the Shabbos.” Rabbi Chizkiyah opened with, “A song of ascents, from the depths…” The “depths” (plural) are the “depth of all” and the “depth of the well.” The Rebbe, author of the *Hillula*, wrote on the margin of his *Zohar* (which was in captivity for several years, and recently his *Zohar* and other books were redeemed and arrived here) that the connection of this interpretation of “the depths” to “See… the Shabbos” is that the “depth of all” and the “depth of the well” are *Chochma* and *Binah*, from which the *shefa* is drawn to all six *midos* of *Ze’er Anpin* (“springs issue forth and flow to bless all”). This matter relates to “See that Hashem has given you the Shabbos,” because Shabbos is the seventh day, which is *Binah* (the “depth of the well”), in which *Chochma* (the “depth of all”) is enclothed, and from it the six days and the *VAK* of *Ze’er Anpin* are blessed. The author of the *Hillula* continues that this is what is meant by “And you shall call the Shabbos a delight (*oneg*).” *Oneg* is an acronym for *Eden, Nahar, Gan*. *Eden* and *Nahar* are *Chochma* and *Binah* (the “depth of all” and the “depth of the well”), and from them the *shefa* and blessing are drawn to the *Gan* (Garden), which is *Malchus*. This is why *Malchus* is called Shabbos, for Shabbos is the letters *shin-bas* (*Sh-Bas*): *shin* (in *gematria* of “depths”) is *Eden* and *Nahar*, and *bas* (daughter) is *Malchus* (*Gan*), into which the *shefa* and blessing are drawn from *Eden* and *Nahar*, the “depths.” We must understand: at the beginning of the matter, it speaks of drawing the *shefa* from *Chochma* and *Binah* (the depths) to the six *midos* of *Ze’er Anpin*, and afterwards it explains that *this* is “And you shall call the Shabbos a delight,” the drawing from *Eden* and *Nahar* to the *Gan*, *Malchus*. The explanation for this (in the *avodah* of man) is that “depths” (plural) are the two matters mentioned above regarding “food of hunger”: the “depth of the well” (*Binah*) is the knowledge that causes hunger, and the “depth of all” (*Chochma*) is the knowledge that is hunger in essence relative to the person. The two matters of *Ze’er Anpin* and *Malchus* are two levels in the human intellect: as it is (somewhat) abstracted from its existence (*Ze’er Anpin*) and as it is in its limitations (*Malchus*). The drawing of the “depths” into the human intellect (through his *bitul*) is in both levels within him, even in his limitations, so that the matters of *pnimiyus haTorah* that are in themselves above the intellect are drawn into the intellect in actual attainment.

It should be added that the primary revelation of the “depths” is in *Malchus*. The six *midos* of *Ze’er Anpin* are (only) blessed from the seventh day, while *Malchus* (in addition to the fact that the *shefa* from *Chochma* and *Binah* is drawn into it) is itself called Shabbos. Moreover, on Shabbos (which refers primarily to *Binah*), there are also the letters *bas* (daughter), meaning that the essential matter of the *shin* (“depths”) is when it is drawn into the *bas*, *Malchus*. The explanation for this in the *avodah* of man is similar to the known concept that through the spreading of the wellsprings outward, the essence of the wellsprings is revealed.

5. Now, from the two aforementioned matters in the manna of *pnimiyus haTorah*—hunger that is above attainment, yet it is *food* of hunger—these two matters were cascaded into the manna as it was literally. The reason the manna was a “day-by-day” thing (which is why it is written, “He afflicted you and let you hunger,” for one who has bread in his basket is not like one who does not have bread in his basket) is that the nature of the world is (space and) time, and the manna was above the world, above the nature of time. Therefore, even after it was drawn into the world, it had to be renewed every day. This is the meaning of “one who has bread in his basket is not like one who does not have bread in his basket”: bread from the earth, and likewise all the influences drawn into the world, since it is not apparent in them that they are renewed every day, it seems to a person that they are in his basket. The manna, in which it was clearly apparent that it was renewed every day from above, was not in the person’s basket. Similarly, regarding the fact that they tasted all flavors in it (the second reason for the hunger of the manna): in a limited thing, it is impossible for all flavors to be present (especially since the flavors include contradictory flavors). The fact that the manna contained all flavors is because even when it was drawn below, it was bread from *heaven*, a Divine matter that is above the limitations of the world. This is “does not see and eats”: the eye of the limited person could not grasp the infinite nature of the manna, and therefore he did not see even simple food, similar to a place of light too great to bear—that vision becomes blurred.

The fact that the manna is food of hunger applies when the person is an “existence.” However, when he is in a state of *bitul* to Elokus, his primary enjoyment and *taanug* is from an influence in which he feels that it is not in the person’s basket, but is drawn *constantly* from above (like the manna, in which it was apparent that it was renewed every day). Through his *bitul*, he is a vessel to receive the unlimited *shefa*, and he “sees and eats.”

6. Based on this, we can explain that the text of *Birkas HaZan* (in which it is written, “And you shall eat *and be satisfied* and bless”) refers to the manna, because the true essence of satisfaction (and wealth) is in the manna, when one feels that the *shefa* given to him is not in (the person’s) basket, but is influenced *constantly* from above (like the manna, in which it was apparent that it was renewed every day). It is within the capacity of every Jew to arrive at this feeling. Especially according to the known concept that sustenance in this time (in the time of exile) is in the manner of the influence of the manna. Through this feeling, he becomes a vessel to receive the unlimited *shefa* of the manna. As the Sages say, “An empty vessel holds; a full vessel does not hold.” When one is an “existence,” and especially when he thinks that the *shefa* given to him is in his basket (a full vessel), he does not hold even the limited *shefa* of bread from the earth. By being an empty vessel, he holds even the satisfaction and wealth of the manna, and all the influences of children, life, and sustenance are drawn to him in a manner of abundance.

## 5727. Parshas Eikev, 20 Menachem-Av [Maamar 1]

**1.** "And it shall be, *eikev* (because) you will listen...". It is well known that there is a difficulty here : the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* depends on man's free choice, so it should have said, "And it shall be *if* you listen" [as in, "If you walk in My statutes", and "And it shall be if you listen"]. Why does it say, "And it shall be *eikev* you will listen," which implies that you will *certainly* listen? The Tzemach Tzedek explains that *eikev* refers to the time of *ikvesa d'Meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach). Thus, "And it shall be *eikev* you will listen" means you will certainly listen, for the Torah has promised that the Jewish people will ultimately do *teshuvah* at the end of their exile, and they will be redeemed immediately.

The *maamar* continues that the three terms—*tishma'un* (you will listen), *ushmartem* (and you will keep), and *va'asitem* (and you will do)—correspond to *machshava* (thought), *dibbur* (speech), and *ma'aseh* (action). *Tishma'un* is *machshava*, for the essence of hearing is in the thought (the ear is merely a vessel through which the sound enters the thought); *ushmartem* is *dibbur*, for the essence of *shemirah* (guarding/keeping) is in the mouth, as it is written, "Arranged in all things and guarded"; and *va'asitem* is *ma'aseh*. Regarding this, it continues, "And Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness which He swore..." The covenant, kindness, and oath correspond to *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* (as explained there at length). Through *tishma'un*, *ushmartem*, and *va'asitem*—the *avodah* of man's *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh*—the *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* from Above are drawn down to him: "the covenant and the kindness which He swore."

However, this matter (that the *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* from Above are drawn down to man) is not yet sufficient. For even before the soul descended below, it was in the highest level of this—the *machshava* from Above, "Israel arose in thought". The descent of the soul below is for the sake of an ascent, so that through its *avodah* below, it will ascend to a level higher than where it was before the descent, even to the level of "And You guard it within me" (which is higher even than the level of *tahorah* [purity]). This is the meaning of "And He will keep... the covenant and the kindness which He swore..." Through *eikev tishma'un*, *ushmartem*, and *va'asitem*—the *avodah* of *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* in the *eikev* of the soul, which refers to the soul within the body, and especially in *ikvesa d'Meshicha* [an addition in the descent, and consequently, also in the ascent that comes through the descent]—through the descent into the body and the *nefesh habahamit* (and especially in exile), the *avodah* of the soul's *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* is with *ratzon* (will) and in a manner of *mesiras nefesh* (higher than *hishtalshelus*). Through this, there will be "And He will keep... the covenant and the kindness which He swore" (*v'shamar* specifically), meaning that in the *machshava*, *dibbur*, and *ma'aseh* from Above, there will be the revelation of "And You guard it within me," which in general is the revelation of the *Atzmus* (the Essence).

**2.** Now, the aforementioned explanation (of the Tzemach Tzedek) regarding "And it shall be *eikev* you will listen" (that *eikev* is from the word *sof*, end, and refers to the end of days) should be connected with the teaching of the *Midrash* on this verse: "The Holy One, blessed be He, said to them... 'I give you your reward (the reward for *mitzvos*) in the *eikev* (heel)...' (as it is said) 'And it shall be *eikev* you will listen.'" However, according to the *Midrash*, which speaks of the reward for *mitzvos*, the intent of *eikev* (the end of days) is the time after the coming of Moshiach. According to the simple meaning, which speaks of the fulfillment of *mitzvos* (*tishma'un*... *ushmartem* and *va'asitem*), the intent of *eikev* (the end of days) is the end of the time of exile, *ikvesa d'Meshicha*. The connection between the two explanations is that the reward for *mitzvos* that will be in the *eikev* (in the future) is that there will then be a revelation of the *Atzmus*, as explained in *Tanya*. And since this revelation comes through the *avodah* (of Torah and *mitzvos* in a manner) of *mesiras nefesh* (as mentioned above), therefore, through *eikev tishma'un* according to the Tzemach Tzedek—the *avodah* in *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, when *mesiras nefesh* is at its greatest —through this will be the revelation of the future, "I give you your reward in the *eikev*."

**3.** This can be understood by prefacing what is written in *Tanya* that the ultimate perfection of the days of Moshiach and the resurrection of the dead depends on our deeds and our *avodah* throughout the duration of the exile. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the author of the *hillula*, wrote in his notes on the margin of his *Tanya* (which for several years was in captivity, and recently were redeemed—his *Tanya* along with other of his books—from captivity and arrived here) that the matter of the two terms, "our deeds" and "our *avodah*," will be understood from what is written later in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 12, beginning with the words "And it shall be the deed of charity...". And afterwards he continues that it is possible to say that "our deeds" refers to the days of Moshiach and "our *avodah*" refers to the resurrection of the dead.

Now, the intention of the author of the *hillula* in pointing to *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 12, beginning with "And it shall be the deed of charity..." is seemingly to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* there regarding the difference between "deed" (*ma'aseh*) and "*avodah*": "For the term 'deed' applies to something that has already been done or that is done constantly by itself, and it is a matter of the present and is always habitual... (whereas) the term '*avodah*' applies only to something that a person does with immense exertion against the nature of his soul, only that he nullifies his nature and his will before the will of the Supreme One, blessed be He." From this it is understood that this is also the meaning of the two terms, "our deeds" and "our *avodah*," in the *Tanya* here: "our deeds" refers to the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* according to nature and habit, and "our *avodah*" refers to the exertion in Torah and *mitzvos* beyond nature and habit. However, from the fact that he writes that the two terms ("our deeds" and "our *avodah*") *will be understood* from what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 12, and concludes (after pointing to the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*) "see there," it implies that his intention in pointing to the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh* is (in addition to the difference between *ma'aseh* and *avodah* in general) also to what is explained there regarding the matter of the "deed of charity", so that through studying this ("see there"), the difference between "our deeds" and "our *avodah*" will be understood more deeply.

**For it is explained** in *Iggeres HaKodesh* there regarding the matter of the "deed of charity" that this "that Israel in their nature are merciful and doers of kindness (is) because their souls are drawn from His attributes, blessed be He, in which kindness prevails over the attribute of judgment... which is why the soul is called a daughter of a *kohen*" (*kohen* being the man of kindness). He explains there that "the charity that is drawn from this level is called by the name 'deed of charity,' for the term 'deed' applies to something present and always habitual (because) the attribute of kindness and mercy was implanted in the souls of all the house of Israel long ago, from the time of their creation and their descent from His attributes, blessed be He." That is to say, even though the nature of kindness within him is (not from his *nefesh habahamit*, but) from his *nefesh elokis*, nevertheless, the charity he gives because of this nature is called by the name "deed of charity". And the *avodah* of charity is that his giving of charity is even more than the nature of his *nefesh elokis*. From this it is understood that the difference between "our deeds" and "our *avodah*" (in Torah and *mitzvos* in general) is that even when his *nefesh habahamit* conceals the nature of the *nefesh elokis*, and he must exert himself to remove the covering and concealment of the *nefesh habahamit* and reveal the nature of the *nefesh elokis*, it is still within the category of "our deeds," since his exertion is only to reveal the nature of his *nefesh elokis*. "Our *avodah*" is when his exertion is even more than the nature of his *nefesh elokis*.

**4.** This will be understood based on what is explained elsewhere that regarding the superiority of *ba'alei teshuvah* (penitents) over *tzaddikim gemurim* (perfectly righteous ones), there are two matters. First, through *teshuvah*, the strength of the connection of his soul with the Holy One, blessed be He, is revealed, that even the separation created by sins ("your iniquities separate") is only in the revelations and not in the essence of the soul, which is why, even after sins, etc., in one moment and in one instant, he becomes a *tzaddik gamur*. This elevation in the *ba'al teshuvah* relative to the *tzaddik* is that in the *ba'al teshuvah*, the strength of the connection in the soul is revealed, which exists (in concealment) also in the *tzaddik*. Second, through *teshuvah* in such a way that willful sins are transformed into merits, a new elevation is added to him that does not exist in *tzaddikim* even in concealment, as is known that these merits are higher than the merits of *tzaddikim*.

**Similarly,** this is also the case regarding the elevation of *teshuvah* that is brought about in the soul through its descent below. As is known, souls before their descent below are in the category of *tzaddikim gemurim*, and the advantage brought about in them through their descent into the body is that they become in the category of *ba'alei teshuvah*, which contains the equivalent of the two matters mentioned above. First, through the fact that the body and the *nefesh habahamit* conceal and hide the light of the soul, through this its hidden powers are awakened, even to the essential powers that are higher than the hidden powers. Second, through the *avodah* of the soul below, a new matter is created: the refinement and purification of the body and the *nefesh habahamit* and one's portion in the world. Since this matter is an innovation (and not a revelation of what was concealed), it is higher than the revelation of the hidden powers of the soul [in addition to the fact that through this specifically (the refinement and purification of the body, etc.) the purpose of the soul's descent below and the dwelling in the lower worlds is completed]. And since this elevation (the innovation of the refinement of the body and the *nefesh habahamit* and one's portion in the world) is also brought about through the *avodah* of the soul, therefore, the ascent of the soul that comes through its *avodah* below is (not only that its internal and essential powers are revealed, but) in a manner of innovation. As is explained in many places regarding the advantage of the love of Hashem that the *nefesh elokis* activates in the *nefesh habahamit* over the love of the *nefesh elokis* itself: the love of the *nefesh elokis* is in the category of existence. Even the love of the soul—that it wants to cleave to its root and source, even if it will be nothing and nullified there in existence entirely —nevertheless, since this desire is from its nature, through this desire its essential form is not nullified. Not so the love of the *nefesh habahamit*; since by its nature it is drawn to physical matters, and the love for G-dliness is the opposite of its nature, through the love for G-dliness (which is innovated within it through the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis*), its form is destroyed and it is nullified entirely—a nullification of existence. This also effects a nullification of the form of the *nefesh elokis*, so that its love will be in a category of nullification, not from the nature and existence of the lover (the soul), but rather, love from the side of the Beloved (G-dliness). Similarly, this is the case with the refinement and purification of one's portion in the world; since this causes the matters of the world to become vessels for G-dliness, it is a matter of innovation, the opposite of the nature of the world (*olam*), which comes from the word *elem* (concealment) and *hester*. Thus, this matter (that the world becomes a vessel for G-dliness) is not from the side of the world, but from the side of G-dliness, from the fact that His unity, blessed be He, has no limitation, to the point that even the existence of the world is unified with Him, blessed be He. Through this, it is also brought about in the person (who performed the refinement and purification of his portion in the world) that his *avodah* to his Creator will be in ultimate nullification, not only from the side of the existence of the person, but from the side of G-dliness.

**5.** Based on the above, one can also explain the greatness of the elevation of those who merited *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed for the sanctification of the Name [it should be noted from what is well-known "in public" that my revered father-in-law, the author of the *hillula*, was arrested and exiled to a remote town in a distant country for his *avodah* in maintaining and spreading Judaism, and he suffered there (during the imprisonment and afterwards while in exile) severe torments and tortures, etc., to the point that these torments and tortures caused (according to nature) that he passed away before his time]. Seemingly, this requires study: the matter of *mesiras nefesh* is a natural thing for every single Jew, that it is impossible at all to deny the One G-d, and he is prepared to sacrifice his soul for this and suffer tortures, etc. (and the fact that they did not have *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed is because they were not required to). What is the greatness of the elevation of those who had *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed? Even more so, it requires study what Rabbi Akiva said, "All my days I was distressed by this verse, 'With all your soul,' etc.—when will it come to my hand and I will fulfill it?" Seemingly, the very fact that all his days he yearned to fulfill this in actual deed is the revelation of his power of *mesiras nefesh* that shone within him. What was so lacking in his *mesiras nefesh* (as long as it did not come to actual deed, due to a cause not dependent on him) that he was distressed by it? The explanation for this is that the fact that every Jew is prepared to sacrifice his soul so as not to deny, G-d forbid, is from the side of the soul. And even when he awakens his power of *mesiras nefesh* in revelation (that if he were required to, G-d forbid, he would sacrifice his soul in actual deed), it is that the power of *mesiras nefesh* of the soul comes into revelation. The *mesiras nefesh* of the soul is from the side of its nature, and there is no innovation in this. Not so with *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed; a matter is innovated that was not there before. In addition to the fact that this comes through the concealment, hiding, and opposition of those who force him to deny, G-d forbid, and by sacrificing his soul and agreeing to suffer from them, he extracts the sparks that are within them and elevates them to holiness —this matter (the elevation of the sparks that fell so low) is an innovation —the innovation in *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed is also regarding the person who stands in *mesiras nefesh*. For when he sacrifices his soul in actual deed, the *mesiras nefesh* is (also) in the natural soul. Not only is there no hindrance from its side to *mesiras nefesh*, but it *wants* to sacrifice its soul in actual deed. And since the natural soul (of itself) wants to live, the *mesiras nefesh* that is activated within it (by the *nefesh elokis*) is an innovation and the opposite of its nature. This is the greatness of the elevation in *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed specifically: the *mesiras nefesh* that is from the side of the soul, since it is from the side of its nature, is in the category of existence. Not so *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed; since it is the opposite of the nature of the natural soul, through its *mesiras nefesh*, it is nullified from its existence. Through this, an elevation is also effected in the *nefesh elokis* (which activated the *mesiras nefesh* in the natural soul), that its *mesiras nefesh* also is in a category of nullification.

**6.** It can be said that similarly, this is the case, so to speak, regarding the descent of the *Tzimtzum HaRishon* (the beginning of the descent in the general *hishtalshelus*), that the purpose of the *Tzimtzum* is for the sake of the revelation [and from this it was drawn down similarly in all descents, which are for the sake of an ascent], in which there is the equivalent of the two matters mentioned above. First, through the *Tzimtzum*, it was innovated that the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* would be also in the worlds. For before the *Tzimtzum*, when the "*Ohr Ein Sof* filled the place of the void, there was no place (possibility) for the existence of the worlds", and consequently there was no revelation in the worlds. Through the *Tzimtzum*, it was innovated that the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* would be in the worlds. The innovation in this matter is only relative to the worlds, and not relative to the light, for in the levels before the *Tzimtzum*, this light was also previously in revelation. Second, through the *avodah* of the *birurim* (refinements), there will be a revelation of a new light that did not shine before the *Tzimtzum*, to the point that this revelation is higher not only than the expansion of the light, which is in a category of revelation, but also than the essence of the light, even to the revelation of the *He'elem HaAtzmi* (the Essential Concealment).

**7.** Now, it is known that these two matters—the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that shone even before the *Tzimtzum*, and the revelation of the *He'elem HaAtzmi*—will be in the time to come, except that then there will be two periods. This is the explanation of the differing *Midrashim* regarding the time to come, for they said that the Holy One, blessed be He, will make a feast for the *tzaddikim*, and they said that in the World to Come there is no eating and no drinking. The explanation is known that these two statements refer to different times. At first, there will be the revelation of the felt pleasure (the feast), which is the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that shone also before. Afterwards, there will be the revelation of the unfelt pleasure, even to the revelation of the *He'elem HaAtzmi*. In general, this is the difference between the days of Moshiach and the resurrection of the dead. For our Sages said that all the prophets prophesied only for the days of Moshiach, but for the World to Come, "No eye has seen, O G-d, except for You". It can be said that in the days of Moshiach there will be the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that shone in revelation also before the *Tzimtzum*, and in the World to Come (in the resurrection of the dead) there will be the revelation of the level of *Eden* regarding which it is said "No eye has seen," the *He'elem HaAtzmi*.

**8.** Based on this, it can be said that specifically, the revelation of the days of Moshiach depends on "our deeds," and the revelation of the resurrection of the dead depends on "our *avodah*." For since the cause of the reward for a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah* itself, the *mitzvah* (the *avodah*) must be akin to the reward (the drawing down that is effected through it). Therefore, the drawing down of the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that shone also before is effected through the exertion to reveal the nature of the soul that existed also before—"our deeds." And the drawing down of the revelation of the *He'elem HaAtzmi*, a new light, is effected through the exertion that is higher than the nature even of the *nefesh elokis* (through which a new matter is created for him that did not exist even from the side of his soul)—"our *avodah*."

**9.** This is "And it shall be *eikev* you will listen..."—*tishma'un* certainly, for it is a certain thing that the purpose for which the Holy One, blessed be He, desired to have for Himself, blessed be He, a dwelling in the lower worlds will be completed, in the two matters mentioned above: both the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that shone also before the *Tzimtzum* (the revelation of the days of Moshiach) and the revelation of the *He'elem HaAtzmi* (the revelation of the resurrection of the dead). And even though these revelations depend on "our deeds" and "our *avodah*," and permission is given to every person, we have been promised that "no one shall be cast away from Him", and every single Jew will complete the purpose through "our deeds"—the exertion in Torah and *mitzvos* beyond the nature of the *nefesh habahamit*—and also through "our *avodah*"—the exertion in Torah and *mitzvos* beyond even the nature of the *nefesh elokis*. This is "And it shall be *eikev* you will listen," for *eikev* refers (as mentioned above) to *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, for (in addition to the fact that then the promise "you will certainly listen" is fulfilled) the perfection of "our *avodah*" (the addition of a new matter even relative to the *nefesh elokis*) is (primarily) through the refinement of the darkness of the exile, and especially the darkness of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*. [And especially according to what the Tzemach Tzedek says that *eikev* is the matter of "his hand holding the heel of Esau", and he explains (in the first interpretation) that it refers to the actual heel of Esau]. And even in *tzaddikim* for whom the darkness of exile does not darken so much, and certainly they do not have the *avodah* of turning willful sins into merits, and even the elevation that is brought about through the refinement and purification of the *nefesh habahamit* is not in them so strongly (because their *nefesh habahamit* is not so material even before the *avodah*), nevertheless, through the trials, and especially through *mesiras nefesh* in actual deed, the sparks that are even in the *gai* of *kelipas nogah* are refined, as mentioned above. And after in many *tzaddikim* there was also the elevation of the refinement of the sparks in the *gai* of *kelipas nogah* through their *mesiras nefesh*, this elevation is drawn down also to their children [as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will keep for you... which He swore to your forefathers"], including also those children who are the students who learned their Torah. Therefore, they no longer need trials, and certainly not *mesiras nefesh* in its literal sense, but rather the *mesiras* (surrender) of the will. And there will be for them and for all the Jewish people "our deeds and our *avodah*" from a place of rest and expansion, in their simple and true sense, with joy and goodness of heart. And the prophecy will be fulfilled, "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," and the author of the *hillula* in their midst, and we will all go speedily and upright to our land with the coming of our righteous Moshiach, in our days, literally.

## B’ezras Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Eikev, 20 Menachem-Av (Maamar 2), 5727

"And now, O Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you, but to fear..." It is stated in the Gemara: "Is fear such a small matter?" (And it answers:) "Yes, for Moshe, it is a small matter." There is a well-known difficulty here: the verse says "What does *He* ask of *you*" (referring to every individual Jew), so how is the answer "for Moshe it is a small matter" relevant? Furthermore, we must understand the Gemara’s statement that "A person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day, as it is written: 'And now, O Israel, what (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you'—do not read it as *mah* (what), but as *meah* (one hundred)." The Maharsha explains that the reason they expound "do not read it as *mah* but as *meah*" is because the literal interpretation presents a difficulty: "Is fear such a small matter?" Therefore, they expound it as *meah*, implying that this matter (reciting one hundred blessings daily) is easy for a person to fulfill, and through this, he will come to fear Hashem. This requires clarification: what is the unique quality of the one hundred blessings that enables one to attain the fear of Hashem? We must also understand—based on the principle that all interpretations of a single verse are interconnected—what the connection is between *mah* and *meah*. Additionally, what is the connection between the two aforementioned explanations (which resolve the difficulty "Is fear such a small matter?"): that for Moshe it is a small matter, and that we should read *meah* instead of *mah*?

2) The difference between the literal interpretation (*mah*) and the interpreted reading (*meah*) is as follows: According to the literal interpretation, *mah* refers to "to fear [Hashem]," meaning that everything Hashem asks of you is to fear Him. According to the interpreted reading, *mah* (*meah*) is a subject in its own right: that which Hashem asks of you is *mah*—one hundred blessings—and through this, you will come to fear Hashem. Another difference between the two is that the word *mah* denotes that the matter is something small—in the language of the Gemara, a *milta zutrasi*—whereas *meah* is a large number, reaching the perfection of numbers, for in the letters, the largest number is hundreds. Especially according to what is explained in Chassidus, that which is added in *meah* over *mah* is the letter *Aleph*, the letters of *pela* (wonder)—the *Ohr HaSovev* that transcends the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. It must be understood that, seemingly, these two differences between the interpretations are contradictory. From the fact that the one hundred blessings are a prerequisite for fear, it is understood that fear is on a higher level than them. Yet, the obligation of one hundred blessings is learned from the exposition "do not read *mah* but *meah*," while regarding fear itself, the verse says "What (*mah*) does He ask of you," where the word *mah* denotes (as mentioned) something small.

3) It is explained in the *maamarim* of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the verse "What (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you" that *mah* represents *bitul*, as in the verse "And we are what (*mah*)." This is the essential *bitul* that transcends intellect, which stems from the essence of the soul. The meaning of "What does Hashem your G-d ask of you" is that Hashem asks of you the *bitul* of *mah*. The fact that this *bitul* of *mah* exists within every Jew due to the essence of the soul is in a state of concealment [and this concealment is not merely because the *nefesh habehamis* obscures and hides this *bitul*, but because, in its own right, it is hidden, being above revelation]. Hashem asks of you (every Jew) that the *mah* within you should be in a state of revelation. This is also the continuation of the verse, "to fear Hashem your G-d," because the root of the *bitul* of fear—even *yirah tata'ah*—is the essential *bitul* that stems from the essence of the soul, the *bitul* of *mah*. As is known, the difference between fear and love is that love, being a reality, has its root in the revelations of the soul, while fear, being *bitul*, has its root in the essence of the soul. This is what the Gemara asked: "Is fear such a small matter?" Even though the fear in this verse is the fear that leads to the fulfillment of *mitzvos* (as explicitly stated, "to fear Hashem your G-d, to walk in all His ways"), regarding the love that leads to the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, it is explained in Tanya that it is easy for every person, because love depends on comprehension; therefore, through contemplation, it is easy for every person to attain the love that leads to the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. This is not the case with fear; since it comes from the *bitul* of the essence of the soul which is above intellect, one cannot attain it through contemplation—"Is fear such a small matter?" To reveal the *mah* of the soul, the root of fear, is through the bestowal of strength from above—an *hemshech* from above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* that human *avodah* cannot reach. This is why one reaches fear through one hundred blessings, for *meah* is in *Keter* (will). Through the one hundred blessings, and especially through the *bracha* of the *mitzvos*, one draws down an *at'adalta d'le'eila* that *at'adalta d'letata* cannot reach; through this *hemshech*, the *mah* of the soul is revealed [do not read *mah* but *meah*], and through this, one comes to fear. This is why "for Moshe it is a small matter," because the *hemshech* of *at'adalta d'le'eila* that *at'adalta d'letata* cannot reach is (primarily) through Moshe. As is known, Torah—the Torah of Moshe—is an *at'adalta d'le'eila* that transcends *at'adalta d'letata*.

It should be added that there is an advantage in the *hemshech* of *at'adalta d'le'eila* that comes through Moshe, the Torah, over the *hemshech* through one hundred blessings. For Torah is of the category of *pnimiyus* (inwardness). Therefore, the *at'adalta d'le'eila* drawn down through Torah is also drawn down in a manner of *pnimiyus* (similar to the *at'adalta d'le'eila* drawn down through *avodah*). Consequently, the fear drawn down through this is a more internal feeling.

4) Based on this, it can be said that both *mah* and *meah* have their own unique quality. The fact that the *mah* is in concealment and requires the *hemshech* of the category of *meah*—a light that transcends the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—to be revealed, is due to the superiority of *meah* over *mah*. Therefore, the word *mah* denotes something small, while *meah* is the perfection of numbers (as mentioned in section 2). But on the other hand, the fact that the light transcending the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (*meah*) comes into revelation below in order to awaken and reveal the *mah* of the soul—this is due to the superiority of *mah* over *meah*. Through the *hemshech* of the category of *meah* to awaken the *mah*, an elevation is added to the category of *meah* itself (as will be explained in sections 8-9).

5) This can be understood based on what is explained in the *maamar* beginning "Zeh" in the continuation of *Torah Or* 5672, that the difference between *Ohr HaMemalei* and *Ohr HaSovev* exists even in their root before the *Tzimtzum*. The fact that the *Ohr HaKav* (*Ohr HaMemalei*) is clothed in the *keilim* is (not only because its *hemshech* is through the *Tzimtzum*, but) because even in their root before the *Tzimtzum*, it is a light of the category of *gevul* (limitation) [this is why even before the *Tzimtzum* there are the *Eser Sefiros HaGenuzos*]. However, before the *Tzimtzum*, the *gevul* within it is in a state of concealment, and after the *gevul* within it is revealed through the *Tzimtzum*, it is capable of being clothed in the *keilim*. The reason this light is in the category of *gevul*, even though the definition of light is that it is attached to the *Etzem* and is "like" the *Etzem*, is that the purpose of this light is to illuminate the worlds. This is the difference between *Ohr HaBli Gvul* (the root of *Ohr HaSovev*) and the light of the category of *gevul* (the root of *Ohr HaMemalei*): *Ohr HaBli Gvul* is (not for the purpose of illuminating, but) a revelation of the *Etzem*. Even though this revelation is also for some intent (for above, there is no such thing as necessity, *chas v'shalom*), the intent in the revelation of this light is that it should be a revelation whose nature is (not to illuminate, but) a revelation of the *Etzem*. Therefore, in this light, there is no possibility of measurement and limitation (*Eser Sefiros*) even in concealment, and even after it shines in the *keilim* and the worlds, it does not enter them through clothing; it only surrounds them—it is *sovev*. The light that illuminates the worlds, even though it too is attached to the *Etzem* and is "like" the *Etzem*, since it is for the sake of the worlds, the worlds "take up space" relative to it. Therefore, even as it is before the *Tzimtzum*, when it is not yet relevant for it to illuminate the worlds, it contains within it, in concealment, measurement and limitation (*Eser Sefiros HaGenuzos*), and after it shines in the *keilim* and the worlds, it is clothed in them.

6) The *maamar* explains that the analogy for this in the powers of the soul in man ("From my flesh I perceive G-d") is the difference between the *ratzon* (will) and the other powers. The fact that all the powers are clothed in the limbs of the body (like *Ohr HaMemalei* which is clothed in the worlds), while the *ratzon* surrounds all the limbs of the body equally (like the *sovev*), is because all the powers, even before they are clothed in the limbs of the body, are a "reality" (external to the soul), and therefore, when they are drawn into the limbs of the body, they are clothed in them. The *ratzon*, however, is not a reality unto itself, and its entire essence is the inclination and *hemshech* of the soul; therefore, even when it is drawn into the limbs of the body, it is not clothed in them, but only surrounds them. The *maamar* continues that the same applies to the analogy above: it is the difference between Torah and *mitzvos*. Torah, which is the wisdom of the Holy One, Blessed be He (a "reality," so to speak), its *hemshech* below into the person who studies it is in a manner of *pnimiyus*—"Your Torah is within my innards." The *mitzvos*, which are the *Ratzon HaElyon* (the Supreme Will), the revelation of the *Etzem*, their *hemshech* below into the person who performs the *mitzvos* is in a manner of *makif* and concealment, for the light of the *mitzvah* is not felt by the person. The fact that through the performance of *mitzvos* a refinement is effected in the person—which is why "a *mitzvah* drags along a *mitzvah*"—is only the effect of the light of the *mitzvah*, but the light itself is not felt within him, similar to the *ratzon* in the soul of man; even though the *ratzon* acts upon the limbs of the body, the *ratzon* itself is not revealed within them. The *maamar* continues [at its conclusion, in the part that explains the verse "And now, O Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you, do not read *mah* but *meah*"] that in order for the *ratzon* of the *mitzvos* itself to be revealed, it is through the *bracha* of the *mitzvos*. This is the concept of "a person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day"—*meah* is in *Keter* (will), and through the one hundred blessings, and especially through the *bracha* of the *mitzvos*, the *ratzon* is drawn down in revelation.

7) One must understand: seemingly, the matter of *makif* and *pnimiyus* explained in the *maamar*, for which the analogy of *ratzon* and intellect is used, refers to *Ohr HaMemalei* and *Ohr HaSovev*. What does this have to do with explaining the difference between Torah and *mitzvos*? The explanation for this is that the creation is for the sake of the Torah and for the sake of Israel. The intent here is not only for the creation of the world, but also for all the revelations, even the revelations before the *Tzimtzum*, and even the revelation of *Ohr HaBli Gvul*, which is a revelation of the *Etzem*. For the intent of all the revelations is so that through them there would subsequently be the creation of the world [and even the revelation that is not to illuminate the worlds, but is a revelation of the *Etzem*, is because it so arose in His will, may He be blessed, that the light relevant to the worlds should be drawn from the light that transcends relevance to the worlds]. Since the creation of the world is for the sake of the Torah and for the sake of Israel, it follows that all the revelations are also for the sake of the Torah and for the sake of Israel.

Based on this, it can be said that the inner reason why the two revelations of *sovev* and *memalei* were drawn down—the revelation of the *Etzem* and the revelation to illuminate the worlds—is because in Torah and Israel, there is an analogy to these two matters. These two matters in Torah are Torah and *mitzvos*, and in Israel, they are intellect and *ratzon* [the fact that in the soul of man there is intellect and *midos* is primarily in Israel—"You are called *Adam*"]. Based on this, it can be said that the fact that the *maamar* brings an analogy for *sovev* and *memalei* from the *ratzon* and intellect in man, and subsequently explains the difference between *mitzvos* and Torah, is (also) to hint that the root of the two revelations (the revelation of the *Etzem* and the revelation to illuminate the worlds) is (analogous to) these two matters in Torah and Israel. This adds to the understanding of the superiority of the two aforementioned revelations, that they contain not only the matter of revelation, but also an analogy to the matters of Torah and Israel, whose root is in the *Etzem*.

8) Based on this, we can explain what is known, that the *at'adalta d'le'eila* that is drawn down of its own accord to awaken *at'adalta d'letata* comes from a place that *at'adalta d'letata* cannot reach. Seemingly, this requires explanation: the fact that *at'adalta d'letata* cannot reach there is because, relative to this level, the *tata* (the lower one) does not "take up space" [it should be added that the fact that created beings do not "take up space" relative to this level is because the root of *sovev* (from which this *at'adalta d'le'eila* is drawn) is the light whose nature is not to illuminate the worlds, but a revelation of the *Etzem*]. How, then, is an *at'adalta d'le'eila* drawn from there to awaken *at'adalta d'letata*? Based on the above, it can be said that through the fact that the light which is a revelation of the *Etzem* is analogous to this matter in Israel, it is felt that the intent in it is for the sake of Israel. Therefore, an *at'adalta d'le'eila* is drawn from it to awaken *at'adalta d'letata*. It should be added that through the *hemshech* of the *at'adalta d'le'eila* to awaken the *at'adalta d'letata*, an elevation is added to the *at'adalta d'le'eila* and to the place from which the *at'adalta d'le'eila* is drawn, because through this, the intent within it is revealed even more, as is the fact that it is analogous to the matter in Israel whose root is in the *Etzem*.

9) This is the meaning of "And now, O Israel, what (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you... do not read *mah* but *meah*." The fact that the *kesiv* (written) is *mah* and the *kri* (read) is *meah*—for *kesiv* and *kri* are concealment and revelation—is because *meah* is the *sovev*, and in its root, the light of the revelation of the *Etzem*—revelation; and *mah* is the *mah* of the soul, which is in concealment. Through the soul becoming a created being, the *mah* within it is in concealment (and in order for it to come to revelation, it is through the *hemshech* of the category of *meah*, as mentioned in sections 3 and 4). Now, this concealment is below revelation. According to the principle that *kesiv* is above *kri*, it can be said that the concealment of the *mah* of the soul, which is hinted at by the fact that *mah* is the *kesiv*, is that the soul is rooted in the essential concealment of the *Etzem*. It should be added that the fact that *meah* is the *kri* of the *kesiv* of *mah* is because through the *hemshech* of *meah* to awaken the *mah*, it is felt within it (as mentioned at the end of section 8) that it is analogous to the revelation of the *mah* of Israel.

The same applies to Israel themselves: through the soul illuminating the body, in which (specifically) is the choice of the *Etzem*, an elevation is added to the soul, similar to the future time when the soul will be nourished by the body. May it be His will that very soon the prophecy will be fulfilled: "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," with the *Baal HaHillula* in their midst, and we will all walk upright to our land with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, in our days, truly.

## Parshas Eikev, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 23 Menachem-Av, 5728

"And now, O Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you, but to fear..." The Gemara states that a person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day, as it is written, "And now, O Israel, what (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you"—do not read it as *mah* (what), but as *meah* (one hundred). 

We must understand: *mah* and *meah* are two distinct concepts. Moreover, they are opposites. The term *mah* denotes something small, while *meah* is a large number, representing the perfection of a number. (This is especially true according to the explanation in Chassidus that the addition of the letter *Aleph* to *mah* to form *meah* signifies *pela*—the *Ohr HaSovev* that transcends the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.) 

Furthermore, we must understand why the Tur, in the name of Rav Natronai Gaon, states that the obligation to recite one hundred blessings daily is an ordinance of King David, as it is written, "The utterance of the man who was raised up"—*al* (on/raised) has the gematria of one hundred—and the exposition "do not read *mah* but *meah*" is merely an *asmachta* (a scriptural allusion). The reason King David instituted the one hundred blessings (as the Tur explains there) is that one hundred souls from Israel were dying every day, and they did not know why, until he investigated and understood through *Ruach HaKodesh* and instituted the one hundred blessings. 

We must understand: since the obligation to recite one hundred blessings daily is derived (as an *asmachta*) from the verse "What does Hashem your G-d ask of you," which continues, "to fear Hashem your G-d... and to love Him," it is understood that one arrives at the fear and love of Hashem through the one hundred blessings. Yet, for many generations—as long as one hundred souls were not dying every day—they did not institute the recitation of one hundred blessings daily.

### 2

This can be understood based on the explanations in the *drushim* regarding the concept of blessings, interpreting the verse "Blessed... from the world to the world." The concept of a blessing is the drawing down of influence from *Alma D'Atkasya* (the Hidden World) to *Alma D'Atgalya* (the Revealed World). In terms of the *Sefiros*, this is the drawing down from *Binah* (*Alma D'Atkasya*) to *Malchus* (*Alma D'Atgalya*). In terms of the Divine Names, it is the drawing down of the *Havayah* of above into the *Havayah* of below. 

The connection of *Binah* and *Malchus* to the two *Havayah* names is that the *Havayah* of above is *Sovev* (Surrounding), and in *Binah* is the revelation of *Keter* (*Sovev*); the *Havayah* of below is *Memaleh* (Filling), which illuminates in *Malchus*. The concept of a blessing is the drawing down of the revelation of the *Havayah* of above into the *Havayah* of below. The *drushim* explain that the drawing down of the *Havayah* of above into the *Havayah* of below, which is accomplished through the blessing, is in a manner where the two names are joined together. Even though the *Havayah* *Havayah* has a *pasiq ta'ama* (a cantillation mark of separation) between them, the *pasiq ta'ama* is not a complete separation (like other partitions). Moreover, it is stated in the *Pardes* that the *pasiq ta'ama* between the two *Havayah* names serves to unify and connect them. Through the blessing, the connection of the two names is a complete connection and unification.

### 3

According to the principle that the service of man (*is'arusa d'letata*) through which the drawing down (*is'arusa d'le'eila*) is accomplished must be akin to the drawing down itself, it can be said that the service through which the blessing and the drawing down from *Alma D'Atkasya* to *Alma D'Atgalya* is accomplished is the love of "with all your soul" (*b'chol nafshecha*). 

The meaning of "with all your soul" is with all the powers of the soul—intellect and emotions. It can be said that the superiority of the love of "with all your soul" over the love of "with all your heart" (*b'chol levavecha*) is that in the love of "with all your heart," the primary focus is the emotion (which is why it says "with all your heart," for the heart is the dwelling place of the emotions). The comprehension that gives birth to this love is in the external aspect of the intellect that pertains to the emotions; the comprehension of this level is in the brain and does not illuminate the heart. Therefore, the birth of love from the intellect is not automatic; rather, the intellect must actively produce the love. 

In the love of "with all your soul," the comprehension from which the love comes is in the internal aspect of the intellect, where the comprehension of this level illuminates the heart, and the drawing down of love from the intellect is automatic. Therefore, it says "with all your soul"—all the powers of the soul—because in this love, the intellect is also felt. [This can be connected to what is explained elsewhere, that the love of "with all your heart" is only in the heart, while the love of "with all your soul" spreads into all the powers and limbs. This means that in the love of "with all your heart," the fact that one fulfills the *mitzvos* because of his love for Hashem is in a way that the love *acts* upon his deed, whereas in the love of "with all your soul," his performance of the *mitzvos* is automatic.] 

Since the *mochin* (intellect) are hidden and the emotions are revealed, therefore, through the love of "with all your soul," where the *mochin* also illuminate in the heart, the blessing and the drawing down from *Alma D'Atkasya* to *Alma D'Atgalya* is accomplished.

### 4

There is a further explanation regarding the difference between the love of "with all your heart" and the love of "with all your soul." The love of "with all your heart" is in the category of *Memaleh Kol Almin* (Filling all worlds). Since the vitality of *Memaleh Kol Almin* is clothed within the created beings in their interior, through contemplation, this vitality is felt even in the animal soul, and the love is "with all your heart"—with both your inclinations. 

The love of "with all your soul" is in the category of *Sovev Kol Almin* (Surrounding all worlds). Since the *Ohr HaSovev* transcends clothing in the worlds, through feeling the wonder of the *Ohr Ein Sof* (*Sovev*), his love for Hashem is in a manner of *mesiras nefesh*, even if He takes your soul. Accordingly, the connection of the love of "with all your soul" to the drawing down from *Alma D'Atkasya* (the concept of the blessing) is not only regarding *Alma D'Atkasya* as it is in the *Sefiros* (*Binah*), but also regarding *Alma D'Atkasya* (*Sovev*) as it is in the totality of the revelations (*Memaleh*). It can be said that this—that through the love stemming from the feeling of the wonder of the *Ohr Ein Sof*, the drawing down from *Alma D'Atkasya* (*Sovev*) to *Alma D'Atgalya* (*Memaleh*) is accomplished—is primarily when this love, which is from the level of *Chayah* (*Makif*), is also felt in his *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah* (internal). Through this, the connection of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* is achieved.

### 5

It is known that the connection of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* is achieved through the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that transcends both *Sovev* and *Memaleh*. This is the meaning of "do not read *mah* but *meah*": *mah* is *Malchus* (*Memaleh*), and *meah* is *Arich* (*Sovev*). "Do not read *mah* but *meah*" means that even in *mah* (*Memaleh*), there should be the drawing down of *meah* (*Sovev*). The difference between *meah* and *mah* is the addition of the letter *Aleph*; *Aleph* is the level of *Atik* (the level of "One and not in calculation") which transcends *Sovev*. It can be said that the reason why adding an *Aleph* to the word *mah* creates *meah* is that *Aleph* is the level of *Atik*, through which the connection of *Sovev* (*meah*) and *Memaleh* (*mah*) is created; therefore, through the addition of *Aleph*, *mah* becomes *meah*.

Similarly, this applies to the service of man: for there to be a connection of the level of *Chayah* (*Makif*) with the level of *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah* (*internal*)—so that the love of "with all your soul" is felt also in the internal powers [and similarly, the connection of *mochin* and emotions]—it is through the service of *mesiras nefesh*, which stems from the level of *Yechidah*. One of the explanations for this is that by surrendering himself to *Elokus*, the purpose of all his powers is to fulfill the will of the Holy One, blessed be He. Since the *Makif* and the *internal* [and likewise the *mochin* and the emotions] have as their purpose not their own existence but the fulfillment of the will of the Holy One, blessed be He, they do not contradict each other; on the contrary, they connect together.

### 6

This is why the ordinance to recite one hundred blessings daily was specifically when one hundred souls were dying every day, because the revelation of the power of *mesiras nefesh* is through darkness and concealment. [According to what is known, in the time of exile, and especially in the generation of the footsteps of *Moshiach*, the power of *mesiras nefesh* is more revealed than in the time of the *Beis HaMikdash*.] Therefore, the ordinance to recite one hundred blessings was only after one hundred souls died every day, because the fact that one hundred souls died every day (for one hundred souls is the perfection of the number) was because they were then in a state of the opposite of freedom from the Angel of Death, which is the *Yetzer Hara*, and through this, their power of *mesiras nefesh* was awakened. Therefore, they instituted the recitation of one hundred blessings, through which the connection of *Sovev* and *Memaleh* is accomplished, because through the revelation (of the power of *mesiras nefesh* that stems from) *Yechidah*, the drawing down of *Atik* is accomplished—the *Aleph* of *meah*, the level of "One and not in calculation"—and through this, the connection of *mah* (*Memaleh*) and *meah* (*Sovev*) is accomplished: "do not read *mah* but *meah*."

Accordingly, we can also explain the statement of the *Midrash*: "There is no 'and now' (*ve'atah*) except an expression of *teshuvah* (repentance), as it is said, 'And now, O Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you.'" According to the principle that all interpretations of the same verse are related, it is understood that the fact that "Hashem your G-d asks of you *mah* (one hundred blessings)" is related to the concept of *teshuvah* (*ve'atah*). Since *baalei teshuvah* conquer their inclination more than the *tzaddikim*, and a person can stand against his inclination by remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*, the primary revelation of the power of *mesiras nefesh* is in *baalei teshuvah*. This is "And now... what does Hashem your G-d ask of you"—that through the revelation of *mesiras nefesh* that comes through *teshuvah* ("and now"), it is possible to achieve the matter of one hundred blessings, "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you."

### 7

We must understand: according to the above learning, for *mah* (*Malchus*, *Memaleh*) to be *meah* (*Arich*, *Sovev*) is through the *Aleph* (*Atik*) that is added to it. But *mah* in itself does not contain the concept of *meah*, not even in concealment. And from the language of our Sages, "do not read *mah* but *meah*," where *meah* is the *Kri* (the way it is read) of the *Kesiv* (the way it is written) of *mah* (for *Kesiv* and *Kri* represent concealment and revelation), it implies that in *mah* itself there is the concept of *meah*, but it is in concealment. 

We must also understand why in the first paragraph it says "with all your heart, and with all your soul, and with all your might," while in the second paragraph it says only "with all your heart and with all your soul." Seemingly, since the second paragraph speaks to those who need to be warned, "Beware for yourselves lest your heart be seduced," the matter of *mesiras nefesh* is more relevant in the second paragraph; yet, the matter of "with all your might" (which is seemingly the concept of *mesiras nefesh*) is stated specifically in the first paragraph. 

The explanation for this is that the concept of "with all your might" as it is in the configuration of love ("And you shall love... with all your might"), since the concept of love is (like all emotions) the *feeling* that one loves, but the love is without limit, is the revelation of the essence of the soul as it relates to revelation (feeling). The love that stems from the revealed powers (including the love that stems from the *Makif* of *Chayah*) is limited, while the love of "with all your might," which is without limit, is from the essence of the soul (as it relates to revelation). The revelation of the essence of the soul that transcends relation to revelation is in the matter of *mesiras nefesh*. The fact that every Jew, even the simplest, surrenders his soul for the sanctification of the Name is not from the feeling of love; for his surrendering his soul is not from his own will, but because *he cannot* be separated, G-d forbid, from His oneness. 

Similarly, this applies to the fulfillment of all 613 *mitzvos* through remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*: after he contemplates (*and feels*) that through every transgression he becomes separated from His oneness, like in idolatry, the reason he does not commit the transgression is because *he cannot* be separated, G-d forbid, from His oneness. Therefore, "with all your might" is not said in the second paragraph of *Krias Shema*, because the warning "lest your heart be seduced" is (not through the love of "with all your might," but) through remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*, because of which *he cannot* transgress the command of Hashem.

### 8

This is "And now, O Israel, what (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you." *Mah* is *bitul* (nullification), as in "and we are what (*mah*)," and it is the essential *bitul* that stems from the essence of the soul. The meaning of "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you" is that Hashem your G-d asks of you the *bitul* of *mah*. Even though this *bitul* (that stems from the essence of the soul) is always in perfection, the *bitul* of *mah* that exists in every Jew is in concealment. The concealment is not only because the animal soul conceals and hides it, but it is also concealed in itself, being above revelation. Hashem your G-d asks of you to reveal the *mah*. 

In this request (that Hashem your G-d asks to reveal the *mah*), there are two aspects: to reveal the *mah* as it is through remembering the concept of *mesiras nefesh*, and also to reveal it through one hundred blessings (as the Sages expound, "do not read *mah* but *meah*"), the connection of the level of *Chayah* with the level of *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah*, through which the *mah* of the level of *Yechidah* is revealed (for the connection of *Makif* and *internal* is specifically through the essence). 

Accordingly, we can understand why *meah* is the *Kri* of *mah*: the *bitul* of *mah* that stems from the essence of the soul is a level of concealment that transcends revelation (*Kesiv*), and *meah*—the connection of *Chayah* with *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah* that is accomplished through the revelation of the essence of the soul—is the revelation (*Kri*) of *mah*. [It should be added that even the *Aleph* of *meah*, the level of *Yechidah* through which the connection of *Chayah* with *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah* is accomplished, is below the level of *mah*. For the level of *Yechidah* through which the connection of *Chayah* with *Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah* is accomplished (*Aleph* of *meah*) is the essence as it relates to the revealed powers, while the *bitul* of *mah* is from the essence of the soul that transcends relation to revelation.]

Through Israel fulfilling the request of the Holy One, blessed be He, to reveal the *mah* of the soul in the two aforementioned ways—revealing the *mah* itself as it is above configuration, and its revelation as it is drawn into practice in the specific levels within the soul (*Nefesh, Ruach, Neshamah, Chayah*)—through this, the Holy One, blessed be He, will fulfill the request of Israel, both the general and essential request, "One thing I have asked... that I may dwell in the house of Hashem all the days of my life," and also as it is drawn into many details ("to behold the pleasantness of Hashem and to visit in His temple," etc.), and the Holy One, blessed be He, gives to every Jew a good inscription and sealing for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters, below ten handbreadths.

## 20 Menachem-Av, 5737

"And now, Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you, but to fear..." The Gemara states: "It is taught: Rabbi Meir used to say, a person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day, as it is written, 'And now, Israel, what (*mah*) does Hashem your G-d ask of you'—do not read it as *mah* (what), but as *meah* (one hundred)." It can be said that the reason for this interpretation—"do not read it as *mah*"—is that according to the literal meaning, one must ask: Why does the verse state this matter (that Hashem your G-d asks of you only to fear, etc.) in the form of a question and answer? Seemingly, it should have said, "Hashem your G-d asks nothing of you but to fear, etc." Therefore, they interpreted it as "do not read it as *mah*, but as *meah*." Now, it is known regarding the principles of the *al tikrei* (do not read) teaching that it does not negate the literal meaning of the text; rather, it adds another interpretation, and both interpretations are connected to one another. We must understand the connection and relationship between *mah* and *meah*. This is especially true given that the difference between the two interpretations is (not only in the word itself, but) in the entire verse: according to the literal meaning, He asks *nothing* but to fear, whereas according to the Gemara’s interpretation, *mah* (one hundred blessings) is the very thing that Hashem your G-d *asks* of you.

2. It is explained in many places regarding the *al tikrei* teaching that the literal meaning is understood through the content of the interpretation offered by Chazal. Based on this, we can understand the phrase "do not read," which implies that it negates the simple interpretation; the intent is that this literal meaning cannot exist except through the interpreted meaning.
