Thus, in our case—"do not read *mah*, but *meah*"—it means that through *meah* one arrives at *mah*. We must understand this, for the word *mah* indicates that the matter is something small—in the language of the Gemara, a "small thing" (*milsa zutrati*)—whereas *meah* is a large number, reaching the perfection of a number, which requires great *avodah* to attain [and this is also true regarding one hundred blessings literally, as to recite one hundred blessings every day, even on Shabbos and Yom Tov (and similarly on a fast day), requires special effort]. How, then, can it be said that in order to arrive at *mah* (a small thing), one must specifically go through *meah* (the concept of perfection attained through *avodah*)?

3. This can be understood by prefacing what is stated in Midrash Tehillim regarding the verse, "One thing I have asked of Hashem..." The Holy One, Blessed be He, said to David, "At first you say 'One thing I have asked,' and then you ask many questions: 'to gaze upon the pleasantness of Hashem and to visit His sanctuary,' etc." David replied, "From You I learned this. At first, You did not approach me with anything but 'one,' as it is written, 'And now, Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear,' and afterwards You opened up to us with many mitzvos, as it is written, 'to walk in all His ways and to cleave to Him,' etc." We must understand: seemingly, David’s answer, "From You I learned," does not resolve the fact that he said "one thing I asked"; rather, it says that the question is directed at the Holy One, Blessed be He, who initially says "but to fear" and afterwards opens with many mitzvos. The Maggid explained that David asked for only one thing, because the detailed items (to gaze upon the pleasantness of Hashem, etc.) are branches of "dwelling in the house of Hashem." Similarly, regarding "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear," the detailed items (to walk in all His ways, etc.) are branches of "fearing Hashem your G-d." However, based on this, one must understand the opposite: this concept (that there are general matters from which many details branch out) is understood simply; why must it be learned from the Holy One, Blessed be He? The point of the explanation is that the intent here by "one thing" is the essential point that is above the division of general and particular. This is what David meant by "one thing I asked"—*achas* is *yechidah*, unique in essence, which is not in the category of divided particulars (as is known, the difference between *yachid* and *echad*). Similarly, regarding "to fear Hashem"—the meaning of "to fear *es* Hashem" (the word *es* indicates something that is merely secondary) is that it has no existence of its own at all, and its entire essence is only that it is secondary and *batel* to Hashem. And even according to what is explained in Tanya that "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear Hashem your G-d" refers to *yirah tata'ah* (lower fear), it is known that all levels of fear are connected to one another. Furthermore, the *bitul* of *yirah tata'ah* is from the essence of the soul. As is known, the difference between fear and love is that love, being an existence, is from the revelations of the soul, while fear, being *bitul*, is from the essence of the soul. This is "From You I learned," for in order to connect the particulars with the essential point that is above general and particular, one requires learning and the granting of strength from the Holy One, Blessed be He. The connection of the essential point with the particulars is in two ways: First, from below to above, where through the particulars one reaches the point. As it is written, "And Hashem commanded us to do all these statutes, to fear Hashem," that through the performance of the mitzvos (the 613 particular mitzvos) one arrives at the fear of Hashem. Second, from above to below, where from the point, particulars are drawn down and branch out, in such a way that even after the particulars have been drawn down, the essential point that is above the source of the particulars shines within them.

4. Based on this, we can explain what they said: "Do not read *mah*, but *meah*." *Mah* is *bitul*, as in "And we are *mah* (what/nothingness)." [It can be said that the word *mah* indicates the smallness of the matter (as mentioned in section 2), which is similar to "You are the fewest of all the peoples," meaning they make themselves small], and this is the essential *bitul* that comes from the essence of the soul. The meaning of "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you" is that Hashem your G-d asks of you the *bitul* of *mah*. From this *bitul*, all the particulars listed later in the verse branch out, including "to fear Hashem." Although the *bitul* of fear is also from the essence of the soul, and this *bitul* is the essential point from which the subsequent particulars (to walk in all His ways, etc.) branch out, nevertheless, since the *bitul* is in the form of fear, whose essence is (like all *midos*) the *feeling* that one is afraid, it is included in the revelations of the soul. This is unlike the *bitul* of *mah*, which is *bitul* in essence, like the *bitul* of *mesiras nefesh* that is in every Jew, from the *mah* within him, which is above all powers, including the power of will. For the fact that he sacrifices his soul is not because of his will, but because he cannot, G-d forbid, be separated from His unity. This is "what (*mah*) Hashem your G-d [asks]," that the *bitul* of *mah* is because Hashem is your G-d, your strength and your life-force. Since Elokus is his life-force, it is impossible for him to be separated, G-d forbid, from Elokus.

5. **However**, the *bitul* of *mah* that exists in every Jew is in a state of concealment. This concealment is not only because the *nefesh habahamit* conceals and hides it, but it is concealed even from itself, because it is above revelation. In order for it to be in revelation, they said, "Do not read *mah*, but *meah*." *Mah* and *meah* are two extremes. *Mah* is an essential point above the category of particulars, and *meah* is a multitude of particulars, up to the greatest multitude. In the human soul, this is the ten powers, with each one included in ten. Through *avodah* in the particulars of the powers (*meah*), the point of *mah* is awakened and revealed. This is "do not read *mah*, but *meah*": *mah* by itself is above revelation—*al* (do not) read (a *kri* is a revelation), and its revelation is through the *avodah* of *meah*. Furthermore, the revelation of *mah* (which is accomplished through the *avodah* of *meah*) is in a general way and is also felt in the particular powers. It can be said that this is also hinted at in "do not read *mah*, but *meah*," for when the revelation of *mah* is only in a general sense, the revelation is only regarding *mah* (which was initially in concealment and afterwards revealed from its concealment). This is "do not read *mah*, but *meah*," meaning the reading and revelation of *mah* must be not only regarding *mah*, but also in the particular powers—*meah*.

6. **But** we still must understand: what is the connection between "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you" and one hundred blessings specifically? This will be understood by prefacing what is stated (at the beginning of the verse) "And now, Israel"—specifically "and now." The Tzemach Tzedek explains that "and now" refers to the years of our lives in this world, similar to what is stated at the end of the previous *parsha*, "which I command you today to do them," and our Sages said, "Today to do them, and not tomorrow to do them." Even though the performance of mitzvos will continue in the days of Moshiach (and on the contrary, then it will be "as the mitzvah of Your will"), nevertheless, the performance of mitzvos in the manner of "to do them"—*asiyah* from the word *kefiyah* (coercion) —is specifically today. For in the future, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," and consequently there will not be the *avodah* of *iskafya*. This is "And now, Israel" —Israel is named for "because you have struggled (*sarita*) with G-d," the mastery over all the concealments and hidings drawn from the name *Elokim*, up to the concealments and hidings of the *nefesh habahamit* and the *yetzer hara* that entice a person to do the opposite, G-d forbid. The matter of Israel is that he masters the desires of the *nefesh habahamit*, until "you have prevailed." At first they oppose him and he masters them (*iskafya*), and afterwards "you have prevailed," meaning he conquers them (*is'hapcha*). This is "And now, Israel"—that specifically now, when the existence of the *sitra achra* is present, he is called by the name Israel, for "you have struggled... and you have prevailed," *iskafya* of the *sitra achra* and *is'hapcha* of the *sitra achra*. This is not so in the future, for since "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," they will not be called by the name Israel (*sarita*), but by the name Yeshurun, or by another name that the mouth of Hashem will designate, as explained at length in the discourses of the Tzemach Tzedek. 

"And say, 'And now, Israel, what...'"—the fact that even now, when the existence of the *sitra achra* is present, and even in the time of exile and even in the footsteps of Moshiach (literally "now"), it is within the ability of every Jew to master all the preventions and obstacles and conquer them ("you have struggled... and you have prevailed"), is because of the *mah* within him, the level of *yechidah*. Since the level of *yechidah* has no opposing force, therefore, by awakening the *yechidah* within him, he has the ability now to master all the opponents and conquer them. This is what our Sages said, "Israel, even though he has sinned, is Israel" [he is not only Yaakov but also Israel, the name of the higher level], for in every Jew, even when he has sinned, the *yechidah* is in perfection [as per the well-known ruling of the Rambam, that every Jew, even when his *yetzer* forces him to nullify a mitzvah (to the point that in order for him to perform the mitzvah, he must be coerced by non-Jews), he wants to perform all the mitzvos], and therefore he is Israel, for he has the power to be "you have struggled... and you have prevailed." And what they said, "Who is a fool? One who loses what is given to him," and it is stated in *Likutei Torah* that this refers to the *mah* in the soul [for by being a fool, he does not fight against the spirit of folly that has entered him, he loses, G-d forbid, the *mah* within him], the intent is that the *mah* within him is in extreme concealment. As is also understood from the expression "Who is a fool? One who loses...", which is like something lost, that even after it is lost it is in perfection, only that one must find it, and through the proper search—he will certainly find it. This is "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you"—that Hashem your G-d asks and requests of you (from every Jew) that the *mah* within him should be in revelation. That he should not, G-d forbid, lose the *mah* that is given to him, and even if he has lost it, G-d forbid—to search until he reveals the *mah* through performing *teshuvah*. And it emphasizes "from you" (*me'imach*), that the revelation of *mah* must be through his *avodah* specifically. For even when the awakening of *teshuvah* is through the proclamations announced from above, or by bringing about various causes for this, as it is written, "And He devises thoughts so that the banished one will not be cast away from Him," this is only the preparation for *teshuvah*, but the *teshuvah* itself is accomplished through his *avodah* specifically—"from you."

7. The fact that "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you" is specifically now ("today to do them"), even though the perfection of the performance of mitzvos ("as the mitzvah of Your will") will be specifically in the days of Moshiach, is so that there will be the *avodah* of *iskafya* of the *sitra achra* and *is'hapcha* of the *sitra achra* (the meaning of Israel), for through this specifically, the intent is fulfilled that the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. And although the ultimate perfection will be specifically in the future (as mentioned above), the ultimate perfection of the future is that then there will be a revelation of the essence of *Ohr Ein Sof* in this physical world, the lowest world than which there is no lower, and this perfection is accomplished through our deeds and our *avodah* now, through the refining and purifying of the world as it is now specifically. For this reason, the soul descended below, for the main intent of this is not for the ascent of the soul that is accomplished through the descent, but to refine and purify the body, the *nefesh habahamit*, and one's portion in the world, for through this there will be the revelation in this physical world and the intent of a dwelling place in the lower worlds will be completed, as all this is explained at length in Tanya. 

8. Since the intent in the descent of the soul below is to make the world a dwelling place for Him, it is understood that this matter (making the dwelling place for Him) is a primary matter in its standing and situation. For when it does not fulfill, G-d forbid, its mission and task, even when it has the most sublime revelations, the essential is missing. Conversely, by fulfilling the intent of a dwelling place in the lower worlds, it attains a great and wondrous ascent without end. Based on this, it is understood that the *avodah* of *meah* through which the revelation of *mah* is accomplished is the one hundred blessings that pertain to the refining and purifying of the world (as follows below), even though the revelation could seemingly also be through the *avodah* in the particular powers of the soul, "to walk in all His ways," etc., because the perfection of the soul, including the *mah* within it, is specifically through fulfilling its task and mission. This is "And now, Israel, what"—that through the *mah* of the soul he performs the *avodah* of Israel ("you have struggled... and you have prevailed") now, through which he fulfills the intent for which he was created, through this specifically, is the ultimate elevation (also) of the *mah* within him.

9. This is "a person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day," for the matter of the blessings is that there should be a drawing down of the revelation of Elokus not only in Israel, but that through them, the revelation of Elokus should be drawn down into the world. As we say in the formula of the blessings, "Blessed are You, Hashem our G-d, King of the world"—that the revelation of Hashem should be drawn down (*baruch*) in Israel, "our G-d," and through this, the revelation should be drawn down into the world, "King of the world." Within the worlds themselves, the drawing down through the blessings is (primarily) in the lower worlds. As it is written, "Blessed be Hashem, the G-d of Israel, from the world to the world," that it should be drawn down from the *alma d'is-kasiya* (the world of concealment) to the *alma d'isgalya* (the world of revelation). The *alma d'is-kasiya* are the upper worlds which are *batel* to Elokus, like fish in the sea that are covered and *batel* to the water, and the *alma d'isgalya* are the lower worlds, and especially this physical world, which appear as a "yesh" and a separate thing. The matter of the blessing is that the revelation of Elokus should be drawn down even into the lower worlds, up to this physical world.

Since everything the Holy One, Blessed be He, created in His world, He did not create one thing in vain, and everything the Holy One, Blessed be He, created in His world, He created only for His glory, one must draw down the revelation of Elokus into every thing in the world, so that it should be felt within it in revelation that it was created for His glory. This is the matter of one hundred blessings, for *meah* is the greatest multitude [and as is known that the totality of the letters are in the three categories of units, tens, and hundreds], for a multitude is the matter of particulars, and the matter of one hundred blessings is that the revelation of Elokus should be drawn down into all the particulars in the world. One should add to this based on what is known regarding the numbers—units, tens, hundreds—that sometimes it is explained that the larger number is above, and the more it is drawn down below, the number diminishes (hundreds in *Keter* and units in *Malchus*). And sometimes it is explained that above is the number of units, and the more it is drawn down below, the number increases (units in *Keter* and hundreds in *Malchus*). The explanation for this is known : these two ways are in *oros* (lights) and *keilim* (vessels). In *oros*, the larger number is above, and in *keilim*, the larger number is below. Based on this, we can add an explanation to the number of one hundred blessings, for one of the differences between *alma d'is-kasiya* and *alma d'isgalya* is that in *alma d'is-kasiya* the essence is the *oros*, and in *alma d'isgalya* the essence is the *keilim*. Since the matter of the blessings is the drawing down from *alma d'is-kasiya* to *alma d'isgalya* (as mentioned above), meaning that the matters of *alma d'is-kasiya* (*oros*) should be in revelation also in *alma d'isgalya* (*keilim*), therefore one must recite one hundred blessings, to draw down the multitude of *oros* of *alma d'is-kasiya* into the *keilim* of *alma d'isgalya*. And that this should be drawn down into the multitude of creatures in this physical world, for the matter of "How great are Your works, Hashem" (the division into a multitude of particulars) is primarily in this physical world specifically.

10. This is "And now, Israel, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you—do not read *mah*, but *meah*," that in order to be able to perform the *avodah* of one hundred blessings, to draw down the multitude of *oros* from above (a multitude in quality) into the multitude of creatures below (a multitude of division into particulars), it is through the *mah* in the soul. For *mah* is an essential point above the category of number (in which the matter of multitude does not apply, not even a multitude in quality). And through the *avodah* of one hundred blessings, through this itself, the *mah* within him is revealed. And not only that, but since the intent of the descent of the soul below, including the descent of the *mah* of the soul, is to draw down the revelation of Elokus into the world [as it is now, "and now," through the *avodah* of Israel, for "you have struggled... and you have prevailed"], therefore, by the person fulfilling his task and mission, an elevation is also accomplished in the *mah* within him. 

Since we are already at the end of the time of exile, and every Jew has already completed the *avodah* of "today to do them," for the Torah promised that Israel will eventually perform *teshuvah* at the end of their exile—immediately they are redeemed, in the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when the intent of a dwelling place in the lower worlds will be completed, when there will be a revelation of Elokus in this physical world and in all the particulars within it, and Israel [who drew down the revelation into the world] will be at an even more elevated level, and all this—very soon, *b'egla d'idan*.

## Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 5726

“I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me” are the initials of *Elul*. It is explained in *Likutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning with these words that the relevance of *Elul* to “I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me” is as follows: In *Elul*, there is an *is’arusa d’lesata* (an arousal from below)—“I am to my Beloved.” On *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*, there is an *hemshech* (drawing down) from above to below (*is’arusa d’le’eila*)— “and my Beloved is to me.” The *hemshech* of *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur* is brought about by the *is’arusa d’lesata* of *Elul*. This is why *Elul* constitutes the initials of both “I am to my Beloved” and “my Beloved is to me” (for “my Beloved is to me” is also included in the initials of *Elul*): because the *is’arusa d’lesata* of *Elul* (“I am to my Beloved”) is also a prerequisite for the *hemshech* (“my Beloved is to me”) of *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*. However, this requires clarification: the fact that the letters *vav-lamed* (the initials of “my Beloved is to me”) are part of the word *Elul* itself implies that the month of *Elul* is not merely a prerequisite for “my Beloved is to me,” but that the concept of “my Beloved is to me” is also present within the month of *Elul*.

The *maamar* continues, stating that *Elul* is the time of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* (Thirteen Attributes of Mercy). Although *Elul* is “I am to my Beloved,” an *is’arusa d’lesata*, nevertheless, the *is’arusa d’lesata* of a person—especially when he is far from *Elokus*—is achieved through an arousal and a granting of strength from above. The revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul*—a revelation accessible to every single Jew, even the most distant—is the granting of strength from above for the *avodah* of “I am to my Beloved.” However, the revelation in *Elul* is primarily just a granting of strength (rather than a revelation that actively arouses the person), and the *avodah* itself comes from the person: *I* am to my Beloved. This is the advantage of *Elul* over the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*; for during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, and especially on *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*, the revelation is such that it arouses the person, and the person’s *avodah* is like a result of the revelation from above. The primary essence and advantage of a person’s *avodah*—*avodah* through one’s own strength—is in *Elul*.

To explain these two aspects regarding the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul*—that the revelation of *Elul* is for everyone, even the most distant, and that nevertheless, the revelation does not arouse the person but is only a granting of strength—the *maamar* continues that the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul* is like a “King in the field.” There are two differences between a King in the field and a King in his palace. Regarding the level of revelation, the primary revelation of the King in his beauty is in his royal palace, when he is in his royal garments and royal crown, which is not the case when he is in the field. However, the revelation itself is primarily when he is in the field. When he is in his royal palace, one may only enter with permission, and only the elite of the people and the select few may enter. When he is in the field, anyone who wishes may [and can] greet him, and the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all. The same applies to the analogy: the revelation of *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*, and similarly the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* in general, is like a King in his palace; it is in a manner where the revelation arouses the person, like a King in his palace (in royal garments and royal crown), who inspires awe and fear. But for a person to feel the revelation of *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*, it is primarily after the prerequisite of *avodah* during the month of *Elul*, through which he becomes one of the elite of the people and the select few who enter the King’s palace. The revelation of *Elul*, which is like a King in the field, is in a manner where the revelation does not arouse the person and is only a granting of strength for *avodah*; yet the granting of strength for *avodah* through this revelation is for everyone, even the most distant. It is like a King in the field, for when the King is in this state, he does not inspire awe and fear, especially to those who are in the field, who are at a low level. Furthermore, when the King is in this state, he does not even arouse a desire to greet him. This is why the *maamar* emphasizes “anyone who *wishes* to go out to greet him”—that the fact that they go out to greet the King is due to their own desire. It is just that the strength to greet the King is provided by the fact that the King is in the field, for then (while he is in the field) there is the permission and the ability for everyone to greet the King.

One must understand: seemingly, to explain that the revelation of *Elul* (and the strength provided by that revelation) is for everyone, it would suffice to say that when the King is in the field, anyone who wishes is permitted and able to greet him. Why add that the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all? Especially since the King’s receiving everyone with a pleasant countenance and showing them a smiling face is the *hemshech* and revelation from above that comes *after* the *avodah*, and it is not understood, for the *hemshech* and revelation after the *avodah* (“my Beloved is to me”) is in the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, while the analogy of the King in the field is an explanation of the revelation of *Elul*, which is (a granting of strength and) *before* the *avodah*. It is also necessary to understand the two matters: that he *receives* them with a pleasant countenance and that he *shows* them a smiling face. Also, regarding receiving them, it says with a *pleasant* countenance, and regarding showing them, it says *smiling* face.

One can explain this by prefacing that the novelty of the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul* compared to the revelation on *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur* lies in two aspects. To receive the revelation of *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur* requires elevated *avodah* (the elite of the people and the select few), whereas to receive the revelation of *Elul* requires only the act of greeting the King, which in the analogy is the arousal of accepting the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven. Another novelty in the revelation of *Elul* is that the revelation is also for those who are in the “desert” of the *sitra achra*. This is also understood from the fact that the primary revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul* is a granting of strength for *teshuvah*, for *teshuvah* in its simple sense is for undesirable matters (the category of the desert), and the essence of *teshuvah* is the casting off of the yoke. From this, it is understood that the revelation of *Elul* is also for those who are at the furthest distance. The reason the *maamar* states that the revelation of *Elul* is in the field (and not in the desert) is because the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* is (not in the desert itself, for in matters that are the opposite of Hashem’s will, there is no possibility for a revelation of *Elokus*, but rather) in the Jews who are in the desert, and the revelation within them is the granting of strength to leave the desert for the field to greet the King. Based on this, one can say that when the *maamar* says the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance, the intention in emphasizing *everyone* is that even those who only *wish* to greet the King, but are held captive by their *yetzer*, and even when a desire to do *teshuvah* and accept the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven is aroused within them, it does not come into practice—even them he receives with a pleasant countenance. This arouses within them a strong and intense desire to greet the King, and through this desire, they overcome the obstacles and hindrances.

The *maamar* adds that he shows a smiling face to all. The difference between “receives” (with a pleasant countenance) and “shows” (a smiling face) is that the term “receives” applies to something that already exists (before he received it), and he accepts that thing; whereas “shows a smiling face” means that the smiling face *of his* (which exists even before he shows it) he reveals and discloses to another. This is why, after saying the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance, it adds that he shows a smiling face to all: his receiving them with a pleasant countenance means that the desire *of the people* (to greet the King) is accepted by the King with a pleasant countenance. The addition of *showing* a smiling face is that when one is aroused with a desire to do *teshuvah*, the revelation of the smiling face from above is drawn down to him—the *taanug* (laughter) of the King himself. This *taanug* is higher than the *taanug* (of the category of a pleasant countenance) that comes from the arousal of *teshuvah*, as explained elsewhere, that the root of laughter (a *smiling* face) is in the essence of *taanug* (an intrinsic *taanug* that is not compounded) which is higher than the *taanug* that comes through a cause (a compounded *taanug*). One can say that the concept of a smiling face in the analogy is the *taanug* from above that is within the Jews themselves (which is higher than the *taanug* from the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos* of the Jews, and higher even than the *taanug* from the *avodah* of *teshuvah*), for this *taanug* is in the essence. By *showing* them a smiling face, this *taanug* is revealed to the person (who is aroused with a desire for *teshuvah*), and this arouses within him (like water reflecting a face to a face) a *taanug* in *Elokus*, until the *taanug* in *Elokus* is his own essential *taanug*, and this gives him even more strength to overcome the obstacles and hindrances and to return in complete *teshuvah*.

One must understand: from the above, it is understood that the revelation in *Elul* is not only a granting of strength for *avodah* [for when the King is in the field, there is the *permission and ability* for everyone to greet him], but it also arouses the person [for by the King receiving everyone with a pleasant countenance, and especially by showing a smiling face to all, this arouses them to return in complete *teshuvah*], and nevertheless, the *avodah* in *Elul* is *I* am to my Beloved, the *avodah* of the person.

One should add that this concept—that the revelation of *Elul* is not only a granting of strength but also arouses—is also understood from the general concept of a King in the field. When the King is in the field, there is the addition that everyone has the permission and ability to greet the King; the knowledge of the people that the King is in the field, in the very place where they are, arouses within them the desire to greet the King.

One can explain this by saying that the people’s desire to greet the King is due to their very existence. Since the King is the heart of all the people, their connection to the King is in their very existence. However, when the King and the people are at a distance, it is possible that their connection to the King, and (consequently) their desire to greet him, remains in concealment. By the King being in the field, in the same place where they are, the desire is in revelation.

The same applies to the analogy: the arousal for *teshuvah* that comes through the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul* is that through the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*, the inner desire of the Jew is revealed [as is also understood from what is explained later in the *maamar* (after the analogy of the King in the field), that the Name *Kel* is the beginning of all the Thirteen Attributes, their source, and their totality. The concept of the Name *Kel* is the *Ohr Ein Sof* itself, as it is written, “*Kel Havayah* has *shone* for us,” for light is like the essence [as explained in many places, the difference between light and flow: flow is when the source of the flow contracts itself according to the capacity of the recipient, while light is akin to the source of light]. In every Jew, this revelation shines, and furthermore, the revelation of the Name *Kel* in every Jew is the Prince and Ruler within him, for *Yisrael* are the letters *yud*—Prince of *Kel*. This is why the *bitul* to *Elokus* in every Jew is a *bitul* that is beyond reason and intellect, for in a Jew there is a revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* itself, which is beyond the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Through the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* (in *Elul*), whose beginning, source, and totality is *Kel*, the aspect of *Kel* within every Jew is aroused and revealed]. This is why the *avodah* of *Elul* is *I* am to my Beloved, even though the arousal is through the revelation from above, because the revelation from above is only a cause through which the inner desire *of the person* is revealed.

One can say that because the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* arouses and reveals the inner desire of the Jew—that the Jew’s desire for *Elokus* is because they are rooted in the Essence—an elevation is created in the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*. The matter is that the fact that creation is for the sake of the Jews refers not only to the creation of the world, but to all revelations, even the most elevated revelations. Through the descent of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* from their place (His royal palace, above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*) to the field in order to arouse and reveal the inner desire in the Jews, it is revealed within them that the intention for them is for the sake of the Jews, whose root is in the Essence. One can connect this with the statement that a King is served in the field, for even the King, above whom there is none, is served in the field, for from Him is his sustenance. According to what is written in the *Zohar*, “Who is the King? This is the Supernal King who connects to the field,” one can say that even the “sustenance,” as it were, of the Supernal King is through descending and being drawn into the field, for through this it is revealed that the intention in Him is for the sake of the Jews, whose root is in the Essence. According to what is written in the *Zohar*, “There is a field and there is a field,” a field of holiness and a field of the *sitra achra*, one can say that the concept of a King being served in the field (that through the descent and *hemshech* into the field, an elevation is created in the Supernal King) is primarily because the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* which is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (which in general is the Supernal King) is also for the Jews who are in the desert (the field of the *sitra achra*), through which their inner desire is revealed and they leave the desert (the field of the *sitra achra*) for the field of holiness to greet the King. For through the *teshuvah* of the Jews who were initially at the furthest distance, the inwardness of the Jews is revealed even more, that their true desire (even at the time of sin) is for *Elokus*, only that their *yetzer* is what overpowered them [as the *Tzemach Tzedek* interprets the verse, “For in the field he found her, the maiden cried out, and there was no one to save her,” that even when the maiden (the soul) is in the field of the *sitra achra*, and furthermore, that this caused the man of the field to seize her and lie with her, even then the desire of the soul is for holiness, and she cries out in the bitterness of her soul over the fact that the man of the field is seizing her—the maiden cried out—and through this *there is no* one to save her, for salvation is drawn to her from the aspect of *Ayin* (Nothingness) which is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*]. And since the revelation of the inner desire of the Jews (which is from their root in the Essence) is through the *teshuvah* of the Jews who were initially in the field of the *sitra achra* (the desert), therefore the elevation created in the Thirteen Attributes through their descent and *hemshech* below to arouse the person is primarily through arousing those who were initially at the furthest distance.

This is “I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me,” the initials of *Elul*. One can say that “my Beloved is to me” in the initials of *Elul* refers (primarily) to the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul*. The reason it says “and my Beloved is to me” after “I am to my Beloved” [even though the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul* is the granting of strength for the *avodah* of “I am to my Beloved”] is because, in the inwardness of things, “I am to my Beloved” (the *avodah* of the person) is higher than “my Beloved is to me” (the revelation from above), as mentioned above (sections 6 and 7), that the intention of the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* is to arouse the *avodah* of the person, and through this, an elevation is created in the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*. There are two matters in this: the elevation created in the revelation from above by its descent below to arouse the person (as mentioned in section 7), and the elevation created by the actual arousal of *teshuvah* of the person. Within this itself, there are two matters: the elevation from the *taanug* from above that is in the *avodah* of the person, and especially in the *avodah* of *teshuvah*—he receives, etc., with a pleasant countenance; and through this, the essential *taanug* that is within the Jews themselves is revealed later (for the root of the souls is higher than the root of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, even from the *mitzvos* of *teshuvah*)—a smiling face (as mentioned in section 5). One can say that since the arousal of *teshuvah* of the person (through which is the revelation of a pleasant countenance and a smiling face) comes through the revelation of “my Beloved is to me” (the revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim* in *Elul*), therefore, the effect of “I am to my Beloved” on “my Beloved is to me” is that even the revelation of “my Beloved is to me” is elevated to the *taanug* of a pleasant countenance and a smiling face. May it be His will that through our deeds and our *avodah*, and especially through the *avodah* of the month of *Elul*, we will merit immediately the future *Geulah*, when there will be the true concept of showing a smiling face, as explained in many places regarding the celebration that the Holy One, Blessed be He, will make for the righteous in the future, that they will see in revelation that the entire struggle of good and evil (in this world) is only so that there should be laughter and *taanug*, and then “our mouths will be filled with laughter,” and all this—very soon.

## Wednesday, Parshas Shoftim, Eve of Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5732

"I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me" forms the acronym for Elul. It is explained in *Likutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning with these words that Elul is the *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below)—"I am to my Beloved"—while Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur represent the *hemshech* (drawing down) from above to below (*is'arusa d'le'eila*)—"and my Beloved is to me." Seemingly, there is a difficulty: at the beginning of the *maamar*, it states that Elul is the acronym for both "I am to my Beloved" and "and my Beloved is to me," yet immediately afterward it explains that Elul is (only) "I am to my Beloved," while "and my Beloved is to me" is Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur.

The *maamar* continues, stating that Elul is the time for the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy. It explains that this revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy in Elul is for everyone, even for those who are furthest away. It is like a king who, before arriving in the city, is met by the townspeople who greet him in the field; at that time, anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted [and able] to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone. We must understand how this aligns with what the *Tur* writes : that from Rosh Chodesh Elul onward, we blow the *shofar* every day to warn the people to do *teshuvah*, as it is written, "Shall a *shofar* be blown in the city and the people not tremble?" Seemingly, since in Elul the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, the primary *avodah* of Elul is (apparently) *ahavah* (love), and the *teshuvah* of Elul should also (apparently) be *teshuvah* from love. If so, why do we blow the *shofar* to awaken *yirah* (fear) and trembling?

2) One can explain this by noting that one of the differences between *ahavah* and *yirah* is that *ahavah* comes through a revelation of light from above, whereas *yirah* comes (primarily) through the *avodah* of man. This is similar to the *yirah* of a flesh-and-blood king: the reason the citizens fear the king is because they have accepted him to be their king, for the acceptance of kingship is done by the people, as it is written, "You shall surely set a king over yourself". Therefore, since Elul is the *avodah* of "I am to my Beloved"—the *avodah* of man—there must be *yirah* at that time. Furthermore, the primary *avodah* in Elul, "I am to my Beloved," is the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven. This is what is meant in *Likutei Torah* when it says that the *avodah* of Elul is going out to the field to greet the King. The reason we blow the *shofar* (in Elul) to awaken *yirah* and trembling is that the concept of "You shall surely set a king over yourself" is that *His awe* must be upon you, and for the acceptance of kingship to be complete, it must be through the awakening of *yirah* specifically.

3) The explanation of this matter in greater detail can be understood based on what the *Tzemach Tzedek* writes in a *maamar* explaining the blowing of the *shofar* on Rosh Chodesh Elul: that the blowing of the *shofar* in the month of Elul is a preface to the blowing of the *shofar* on Rosh Hashanah. The difference between the *shofar* blowing of Elul and the *shofar* blowing of Rosh Hashanah is that the *yirah* (and trembling) that comes through the *shofar* of Elul is *yirah tata'ah* (lower fear), while the *yirah* (and trembling) that comes through the *shofar* of Rosh Hashanah is *yirah ila'ah* (higher fear). This is why they instituted blowing the *shofar* on Rosh Chodesh Elul and throughout the entire month, because in order to arrive at *yirah ila'ah*, one must first have *yirah tata'ah*. Another reason why we blow the *shofar* in the month of Elul before Rosh Hashanah is that during the Ten Days of *Teshuvah*, beginning from Rosh Hashanah, one must draw down from the *makif* (encompassing light) to rectify what was damaged throughout the entire year, and the drawing down of the *makif* is achieved specifically through *bitul*. As is explained in *Torah Or* on the verse, "The heavens are My throne and the earth is My footstool; where is the house that you will build for Me... but to this one I will look, to the poor and broken-spirited," the heavens and earth are *Torah* and *mitzvos*, for the *hemshech* through *Torah* and *mitzvos* is *ohr penimi* (internal light)—"My throne and My footstool." To draw down the *makifim*—"where is the house"—for a house is a *makif* (and among the *makifim* themselves, the distant *makif*), is through *bitul*: "poor and broken-spirited and trembling at My word." Therefore, we blow the *shofar* in Elul, because for there to be a *hemshech* of the *makif* on Rosh Hashanah, one must be "broken-spirited and trembling," and through the blowing of the *shofar* one comes to trembling.

We must understand: do we not also come to trembling through the blowing of the *shofar* on Rosh Hashanah ? On the contrary, the trembling of Rosh Hashanah is greater than the trembling of Elul, as mentioned above in the *maamar*—that the trembling coming from the *shofar* of Elul is *yirah tata'ah*, and the trembling coming from the *shofar* of Rosh Hashanah is *yirah ila'ah*. Nevertheless, the *hemshech* of the *makif* on Rosh Hashanah is through the trembling that comes from the *shofar* of Elul.

4) This will be understood by first explaining the difference between the *yirah* of Elul being *yirah tata'ah* and the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah being *yirah ila'ah*. The difference between *yirah tata'ah* and *yirah ila'ah* is, as explained in *Tanya* and elsewhere, that *yirah tata'ah* comes from His greatness in the creation and formation of the worlds. The *bitul* in this *yirah* is *bitul hayesh* (nullification of the ego). *Yirah ila'ah* comes from His greatness and transcendence, which is above the worlds, where "everything is considered as nothing before Him." The *bitul* in this *yirah* is *bitul b'metzius* (nullification of essence). This is why arriving at *yirah ila'ah* is possible only through a revelation from above, because the *Elokus* that a person can grasp through contemplation is the *Elokus* that relates to the worlds, and for the transcendence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds to be felt, it must be through a revelation from above. This is what is meant by, "And Hashem commanded us to do all these statutes to fear Hashem"—that to arrive at "fearing Hashem," *yirah ila'ah*, it is impossible to arrive at this through contemplation, but only through a revelation from above that is drawn down by the *mitzvos*. This is why the *yirah* of Elul is *yirah tata'ah* and the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah is *yirah ila'ah*: in Elul, when the King is in the field, His greatness and transcendence are not felt, and the *yirah* then is (not from a revelation from above, but) through the *avodah* of man; therefore, the *yirah* then is *yirah tata'ah*. On Rosh Hashanah, when the King is in His royal palace, His transcendence is felt, for He is exalted and separate from the people —which in the analogy is the revelation of the transcendence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds—the *yirah* on Rosh Hashanah is *yirah ila'ah*.

It can be said that the reason we must blow the *shofar* on Rosh Hashanah to arrive at *yirah ila'ah*, even though it is the time of the revelation of His kingship, is that the time of Rosh Hashanah, in and of itself, shines with the revelation of the transcendence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds. However, time is one of the parameters of the world, and therefore, the transcendence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* revealed on Rosh Hashanah due to the time of Rosh Hashanah relates to the worlds. The revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* as He is holy and separate from the worlds is primarily through the *mitzvos*, "who has sanctified us with His *mitzvos*". Since the blowing of the *shofar* on Rosh Hashanah is a *mitzvah*, the *yirah* and trembling from the sound of the *shofar* of Rosh Hashanah is *yirah* and *bitul* in the ultimate sense—*yirah ila'ah*. Based on this, we can add another explanation as to why the *yirah* coming from the sound of the *shofar* of Elul is (only) *yirah tata'ah*: because the fact that the sound of the *shofar* of Rosh Hashanah brings one to such an immense *yirah*, *bitul b'metzius* (*yirah ila'ah*), is due to the *mitzvah* of *shofar*. Since the *shofar* blowing in Elul is not a *mitzvah* (and we do not recite the blessing "who has sanctified us with His *mitzvos*"), the *yirah* (and *bitul*) coming from the sound of the *shofar* of Elul is (only) *bitul hayesh*, *yirah tata'ah*. Nevertheless, this *yirah* is a preface and preparation for the *yirah ila'ah* of Rosh Hashanah, because in order to arrive at *yirah ila'ah*, one must first have *yirah tata'ah* (as mentioned above in the *maamar*).

5) It is known that in order to go from *yirah tata'ah* to *yirah ila'ah*, one must first have *ahavah*. The order of *avodah* is *d'chilu* (fear), *r'chimu* (love), *r'chimu* and *d'chilu*. The (first) *d'chilu* is *yirah tata'ah*, followed by two levels of *r'chimu*—*ahavah zuta* (lesser love) and *ahavah rabbah* (greater love)—and afterward, *d'chilu*, *yirah ila'ah*. From this, it is understood that the reason we come from the *yirah tata'ah* of Elul to the *yirah ila'ah* of Rosh Hashanah is through the introduction of *ahavah*. This can be explained based on what is written in *Likutei Torah*—that when the King is in the field, He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all. A pleasant countenance and a smiling face are the essence of *ahavah*. Through the King *receiving* everyone with a pleasant countenance, and especially through *showing* a smiling face to everyone, this awakens in them (as "water reflects the face to the face") *ahavah* for the King. Based on this, it can be said that the details of the analogy in *Likutei Torah* hint at the four aforementioned matters: going out to meet the King to greet Him relates to *yirah tata'ah*. Afterward, the King receives them with a pleasant countenance and shows them a smiling face—the two levels of *r'chimu* (pleasant countenance—*ahavah zuta*; smiling face—*ahavah rabbah*)—and afterward comes the matter of His arrival in the royal palace—*yirah ila'ah*.

6) Although in the levels of *yirah*, the *yirah* of Elul is lower than the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah—for the *yirah* of Elul is *yirah tata'ah* and the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah is *yirah ila'ah*—nevertheless, there is a superiority in the *yirah* of Elul over the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah. The *yirah* and *bitul* on Rosh Hashanah, since it is the time of the revelation of His kingship, are not a novelty. Since "everything is considered as nothing before Him," and the more one is before Him, the more one is as nothing, the fact that the Jewish people are in the *bitul* of *yirah ila'ah* during the time of Rosh Hashanah when they are in the royal palace is not a novelty. [Similar to the *bitul* in *Atzilus*, which is not a novelty, because in *Atzilus* the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* shines. Likewise within *Atzilus* itself, the *bitul* in the *sefirah* of *Chochma*, where the primary *bitul* is, is not a novelty, because in *Chochma* is the revelation that "He is alone and there is nothing else". And all the more so the *bitul* of *Keter*, for even though it is "pure light," etc., it is "black" before the "Cause of all causes". The meaning of "black" is that *Keter* is in *bitul* (like the color black, which is not high compared to the color white) relative to the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above *Keter* (the Cause of all causes), which is not a novelty, because *Keter* perceives that it is incomparable to the *Ohr Ein Sof*]. But the *yirah* and *bitul* in Elul, when the King is in the field (where His greatness and transcendence are not felt) and nevertheless there is the *bitul* of the Jewish people, who accept upon themselves His kingship, and furthermore, they blow the *shofar* to awaken *yirah* and trembling (so that the acceptance of kingship will be complete)—this *bitul*, even though it is *bitul hayesh*, is very precious in the eyes of Hashem. It can be said that through the pleasure of the King that they go out to meet Him to greet Him (accepting His kingship) while He is in the field, there is an even greater addition in that He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all. Furthermore, the superiority of the *yirah* and *bitul* of Elul over the *yirah* and *bitul* of Rosh Hashanah is not only because of the novelty, but also regarding the matter of *bitul*. The *bitul* that comes through revelation, since the *bitul* is because one *recognizes and feels* the loftiness of the revelation (that it is incomparable to oneself), the *bitul* is connected with the person's existence (his recognition). The true essence of *bitul* is in the *avodah* of accepting the yoke, which is like a servant who, because of the yoke of the master placed upon him, is *compelled* to fulfill the master's will.

7) Based on this, we can explain what is written in the *maamar* that the *hemshech* of the *makif* of Rosh Hashanah is (primarily) through the *yirah* and trembling that comes from the *shofar* of Elul. For the fact that through trembling ("trembling at My word") there is a *hemshech* of the *makif* (house) is (primarily) when the trembling is in a manner of *bitul* and humility—"poor and broken-spirited." As explained in the *maamar*, the more a person humbles himself, the higher the *makif* that is drawn down. Therefore, the primary *hemshech* of the *makif* is through the *yirah* and trembling of Elul, because the *yirah* and trembling of Rosh Hashanah are because one feels the revelation from above, and the *bitul* that comes from feeling the revelation is not in a manner of humility. The essence of "poor and broken-spirited"—*bitul* in a manner of humility—is in the *yirah* and trembling of Elul.

We can add another explanation for the superiority of the *yirah* of Elul over the *yirah* of Rosh Hashanah: because the *yirah* and *bitul* of Elul come through the *avodah* of the Jewish people—"I am to my Beloved"—and the root of the Jewish people is in the *Atzmus* (Essence), therefore, the *hemshech* that comes through this *yirah* and *bitul* is a *hemshech* of the *Atzmus*. It can be said that this is the inner reason why one comes from the *yirah tata'ah* of Elul afterward on Rosh Hashanah to *yirah ila'ah*, because through the *yirah* of Elul there is a *hemshech* of the *Atzmus*, and through this, the revelations are (afterward) also drawn down.

8) This is also the case regarding the *teshuvah* of Elul. The fact that we blow the *shofar* in Elul is (as mentioned above from the *Tur*) to warn the Jewish people to do *teshuvah*, which has an advantage over the *teshuvah* of Rosh Hashanah. Although the *teshuvah* of Elul is for undesirable matters, as understood from what is written in the writings of the *AriZal* that Elul is an acronym for *Ane Li Yado V'samti Lach* —for the cities of refuge are a rectification for undesirable matters [it can be said that the fact that the *teshuvah* of Elul is hinted at in *Ane Li Yado V'samti Lach*, where the atonement of the cities of refuge is for one who kills unintentionally, is because through the *teshuvah* of Rosh Chodesh Elul, intentional sins become like unintentional ones, and the *teshuvah* of Elul is to rectify the unintentional ones]—and the *teshuvah* of Rosh Hashanah, which comes after the undesirable matters (even the unintentional ones) have already been rectified through the *teshuvah* of Elul, is (primarily) *teshuvah ila'ah*, nevertheless, there is an advantage in the *teshuvah* of Elul over the *teshuvah* of Rosh Hashanah. For the *teshuvah* of Rosh Hashanah is hinted at in the *mitzvah* of *shofar*, as the *Rambam* writes : "Even though the blowing of the *shofar* on Rosh Hashanah is a decree of the Torah, there is a hint in it, meaning: 'Awaken, you sleepers, from your sleep... and return in *teshuvah*.'" Even though the matter of *teshuvah* hinted at in the *shofar* is higher than the *mitzvah* of *shofar*, and as is known regarding the concept of a "hint"—that the matter being hinted at is higher than the thing that hints at it, to the point that it is not clothed in the thing and is only a hint —nevertheless, the fact that the matter is hinted at in the thing is because there is a similarity between them. Since the *shofar* blowing on Rosh Hashanah is a *mitzvah*, therefore, the *teshuvah* hinted at in it also has a connection to the *avodah* of *Torah* and *mitzvos*. The primary advantage of *teshuvah*, that it reaches the *Owner* of the will (higher than the will of the *mitzvos*), is the *teshuvah* of Elul. For the fact that *teshuvah* reaches higher than the will of the *mitzvos* is because the Jewish people preceded the *Torah*. Therefore, the advantage of *teshuvah* is primarily when the *teshuvah* comes from the person (the Jewish people) himself—the *teshuvah* of Elul, "I am to my Beloved."

9) This is "I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me," the acronym for Elul. The fact that "and my Beloved is to me" is included in the acronym for Elul is because the fact that through the *avodah* of "I am to my Beloved" (in Elul) the *hemshech* of "and my Beloved is to me" is achieved on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur is because the *avodah* of "I am to my Beloved" reaches the *Atzmus* from which all revelations are drawn (as mentioned at the end of the previous section). Thus, in the "I am to my Beloved" of Elul, the *hemshech* of "and my Beloved is to me" is also included. It can be said that this is why the *shofar* blasts of the month of Elul (according to the *Chabad* custom) are *Tekiah-Shevarim-Teruah-Tekiah*, *Tekiah-Shevarim-Tekiah*, *Tekiah-Teruah-Tekiah*—all the sounds that are blown on Rosh Hashanah—because in the blasts of Elul are all the matters that are in the blasts of Rosh Hashanah. The fact that in Elul we blow ten sounds and not one hundred sounds, perhaps it can be said that this is because the blasts of Elul (since they are the root of the matters that are drawn down on Rosh Hashanah) are above division.

10) May it be His will that through our deeds and our *avodah*, and especially through the *avodah* of Elul, we will hasten and accelerate the *Geulah* even more, as hinted at in the fact that Elul is an acronym for *LaHashem V'yomru Leimor Ashirah*, for then all the sparks will emerge from exile.

Since in Elul the King receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, surely the King will fulfill the request of every Jewish person, that they have a good writing and sealing for a good and sweet year in the revealed and apparent good—both in spiritual matters of *Torah* study and the performance of *mitzvos*, and in material matters of children, life, and abundant sustenance. And all the more so regarding the primary request—the true and complete *Geulah* through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, who will come and redeem us and lead us upright to our land, immediately.

## 1.

"I am to my beloved, and my beloved is to me" — the initial letters of which spell *Elul*. As explained in the well-known *maamar* in *Likutei Torah*, the month of *Elul* marks the beginning of the aspect of "I am to my beloved," which is the *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below), continuing until *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*, which are the aspect of drawing down the *Elokus* of the *Ribono shel Olam* below in a revealed manner. This is the meaning of "I am to my beloved"—the *is'arusa d'lesata* of the month of *Elul*—followed by "and my beloved is to me," the drawing down from above during the *Yomim Nora'im*. However, even though the essence of the month of *Elul* is the arousal from below, there must nevertheless be an arousal and a bestowal of strength from above for this. This is what is explained in the continuation of the *maamar*: that the month of *Elul* is a time for the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, which is the *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) that awakens the *is'arusa d'lesata* of "I am to my beloved".

## 2.

This is explained by way of a parable: A king, before arriving in a city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, it is permitted [and the Rebbe, *Nasi Doreinu*, adds : and they are able] for anyone who wishes to greet him to do so. He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all. When he proceeds into the city, they follow him, but once he enters his royal palace, no one may enter except by permission, and even then, only the elite of the people and the select few. The *maamar* continues that this is the case, by way of analogy, in the month of *Elul*: we go out to greet the light of His countenance in the "field." It explains that the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy is the concept of "May Hashem shine His countenance upon you". One could say that this is the concept of the King receiving everyone with a pleasant countenance and showing a smiling face, and so on, to the point that one may even make a request of the King himself. The details of this are explained regarding the *avodah* of man in the aforementioned *Likutei Torah*.

## 3.

Now, in the general collection of *Elul* *maamarim* in *Likutei Torah*, which were arranged and printed by the Tzemach Tzedek, we find a remarkable thing: these *maamarim* do not have a separate heading of "Maamarim for Elul", but are included among the *maamarim* for *Parshas Re'eh*. We must understand the connection between the *Elul* *maamarim* and *Parshas Re'eh*. Furthermore, we must understand why there are no *maamarim* printed in *Likutei Torah* for *Parshas Shoftim*, even though there is a multitude of *maamarim* from the Alter Rebbe on *Parshas Shoftim*, both on the beginning of the *parsha* ("Judges and officers") and on verses in the middle of the *parsha*. As is printed in *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, and similarly in the *maamarim* of the Mitteler Rebbe—many of which are based on the *maamarim* of the Alter Rebbe—*maamarim* were printed for *Parshas Re'eh* (which precedes *Shoftim*) and *Parshas Ki Seitzei* (which follows it), yet no *maamarim* were printed for *Parshas Shoftim* (even though the *Elul* *maamarim* pertain [also] to *Parshas Shoftim*). We must also understand that the calendar timing of *Rosh Chodesh Elul* falling in *Parshas Shoftim* necessitates that there is a connection between them, and what that connection is. It is also worth noting a wondrous point regarding the aforementioned *maamar* ("Ani L'Dodi") in *Likutei Torah*, which begins and is printed on page 32. One could say that the number 32 has a special content, as discussed elsewhere : it alludes to the fact that in Chapter 32 of *Tanya*, the concept of "Love your fellow as yourself" is explained, because the concept of *ahavas Yisrael* is the heart and the essence, as our Sages say, "This is a great principle of the Torah." Similarly, one could say regarding page 32 in the book of *Mishneh Torah* in *Likutei Torah* (which was arranged for print by the Tzemach Tzedek) that this page (and this *maamar*) is the heart of the *Likutei Torah* of *Mishneh Torah*. Even if one were to say that the fact that this *maamar* was printed on page 32 was incidental, it is still plausible to say that since this is a book of Torah—and especially according to the well-known teaching of the Baal Shem Tov —one can learn a lesson in the *avodah* of man even from such details.

## 4.

The explanation for all of this can be given based on what was stated above: that the core of the aforementioned *maamar* is that the *avodah* of the month of *Elul* is like the parable of the King in the field. Based on this, the connection between the *Elul* *maamarim* and page 32 becomes clear. When the King is in the field, the "field" makes everyone present equal, because there, everyone (without distinction) is permitted and able to greet Him, and He receives everyone, and so on (unlike when He is in His royal city, and especially in His palace, where only the elite and the select few enter to the King). Moreover, when the King is in the field, the barriers between the King and the people are nullified, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows them a smiling face. In general (and especially in *Elul*), "I" (the Jewish people) and "my beloved" (Hashem) are each, so to speak, the heart of the other. This depends on the unity of the Jewish people ("I")—the fact that when the King is in the field, everyone is equal—as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*. It can be said that this is also the connection to *Parshas Re'eh*: the concept of "seeing," the illumination of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, is that there should be "face to face"—the inner dimension of His will toward the Jewish people, and the inner dimension of the Jewish people's will toward Him (similar to the above, that each is the heart of the other). As it is written, "See, I set before you," which is the aspect of face to face. [However, the concept of "Judges and officers" is, on the contrary, the opposite of equality: to clarify the distinctions (and barriers) between one and another, between one law and another, and so on.]

## 5.

It is explained in the continuation of the *maamar* there that just as there is the aspect of a field, there is also the aspect of a desert—a "land not sown" where "no man dwells". In the parable of the month of *Elul*, the King is in the field (not the desert), for the field is superior to the desert. Simply put, the desert is a land not sown, whereas the field is a place of sowing and the growth of bread—the land from which bread comes forth. Bread is something that is refined and elevated, and "bread sustains the heart of man" ; "man does not live by bread alone, but by everything that comes from the mouth of Hashem" that is within the bread—the *Eloki* spark within the bread (as explained in the writings of the Arizal and elsewhere). Thus, the innovation of the field over the city and the desert is that the city represents the homes within the domain of holiness, the desert is outside the domain of holiness ("no man dwells there"), and the field's content is the refinement of matters outside the home and bringing them into holiness. This is the general *avodah* of man: to refine the matters of the world and elevate them to *Elokus*. It is for this reason that the sacrifices in general are called "My offering, My bread for My fire" —the concept of bread—and in the language of our Sages, "My beloved, My sustenance."

## 6.

The perfection of the *avodah* of the sacrifices ("My bread for My fire") will be specifically in the time to come. For although even during the time of *galus* there is the concept of sacrifices through engaging in the study of the laws of sacrifices, as it is written, "We will render the bulls with our lips," which also includes the concept of *n'shalamah* (we will complete/perfect), nevertheless, the essence of this will be in the time to come. As it is said in the *tefillah*, "And there we will perform before You the *mitzvos* of Your will," for it is specifically in the time to come that there will be the fulfillment of all the *mitzvos*, and especially the *mitzvah* of offering sacrifices, which is the essence of the *avodah*, in the ultimate perfection. It can be said that it is explicit in the verses that in the time to come there will also be fields (and perhaps it can be said that Jerusalem in relation to the *Beis HaMikdash* is like a field, in addition to the fields in the literal sense outside of Jerusalem). However, then the barriers that exist now between the city and the field will be nullified, and the revelation in the *Beis HaMikdash* (the city) will spread also to Jerusalem, the Holy City, and also to the fields and outskirts outside of Jerusalem, similar to the teaching of our Sages that "Jerusalem is destined to expand" throughout the entire Land of Israel, and the Land of Israel is destined to expand throughout all the lands, as it is written, "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh shall see it together," and so on.

## 7.

Based on this, one can also answer and explain the allusion in the connection of the content of this *maamar* (the concept of the nullification of barriers, everyone being equal) with *Parshas Shoftim*, which is revealed at the end of the *parsha*. The concept of "Judges and officers," and so on, is (as mentioned above) to clarify the distinctions (and barriers) between one and another, between one law and another, and so on. But when the work of the judges is completed and continues afterward in the conduct of "walking in His ways all the days", then the nullification of barriers occurs, and so on, until afterward "Hashem will expand your border" (through having previously "kept... to walk in His ways all the days"). The concept of "Hashem will expand your border" can be said to be, in a spiritual sense, the concept of the Land of Israel expanding throughout all the lands. And until there will also be the revelation of the aspect of *Chabad*, as our Sages say regarding the verse "Hashem will expand your border," that it refers to the Kenite, the Kenizzite, and the Kadmonite, and it is explained in the *maamar* "Do not distress Moab" by the Mitteler Rebbe that these are the aspects of *Chabad*. For the drawing down now is only the aspect of the seven lower *Sefiros*, and it will expand in the time to come. It can be said that this is specifically through the prior *avodah* of "spreading your springs outward" in a manner of understanding and comprehension (*yitparnesun minei*), *Chabad*. And not only that, but even the three lands (*Chabad*) will be in a manner of conquest, that one becomes the "master of the house" over them as well, until even this part of Torah is "his Torah," which is called by his name.

## 8.

May it be the will that this shall be for us: that through the prior *avodah* of spreading the springs outward and the conquest of the *Chabad* within the soul, we will come very soon to the conquest of the *Chabad* in the world, until the ultimate conquest in a manner that it is called by His name. May this be fulfilled in a manner of *achishenah* (I will hasten it) and with alacrity, so that immediately and instantly (in the language of the Rambam) the *galus* ends, and we conquer in perfection the land of the seven nations, and immediately afterward also the land of the three nations, and together the land of the ten nations. For the number ten indicates the perfection of the time to come, as our Sages say that the harp of the time to come will have ten strings, and in the time to come there will be the tenth song, the tenth heifer, and the tenth counting, for the *Ribono shel Olam* counts the Jewish people because of His great love for them. And all this speedily in our days, literally, in a simple way, in our time and place, souls in bodies, and with joy and a good heart.

## B’s”D. Shabbos Parshas Tetzei, 13 Elul, 5714.

### B’s”D. Shabbos Parshas Tetzei, 13 Elul, 5714.

"Come, my beloved, to greet the bride; let us welcome the face of Shabbos." The Rebbe Rayatz brings in his maamar "Lecha Dodi" (from the wedding discourses, based on Pirkei D’Rabbi Eliezer) that a groom is likened to a king and the bride to a queen. The groom is Hashem, and the bride is Knesses Yisrael. In terms of the Sefiros, this refers to Ze’er Anpin and Malchus, for the groom is the aspect of Ze’er Anpin and the bride is the aspect of Malchus. This is the meaning of "Come, my beloved, to greet the bride; let us welcome the face of Shabbos"—it refers to the drawing down of Ze’er Anpin into Malchus. The order of this drawing down is that, initially, there must be an external influence (from Ze’er Anpin to Malchus) which is only in the aspect of a *makif* (encompassing light), and afterward, there is the internal influence. This is the order in every instance of influence from a *mashpia* (influencer) to a *mekabel* (recipient): first, there must be an influence from the *mashpia*’s external aspect to the *mekabel*’s external aspect, which elevates the *mekabel* to be close to the level of the *mashpia*, and only then can he receive the internal influence from the *mashpia*. He brings two analogies for this [the influence of a teacher to a student, and a father playing with his young son]. It can be said that his intention in these analogies is not merely to provide examples for the *order* of the influence (that external influence is a prerequisite for internal influence), but (also) to explain the greatness of the elevation in both of these influences—that even the external influence is an extremely lofty level, to the point that it possesses an elevation relative to the internal influence. For the external influence, which is the aspect of *makif*, is above the *keli* (vessel) of the *mekabel* (whereas the internal influence is received within the *mekabel*’s *keli*). Nevertheless, it is only a prerequisite for the internal influence, because it is specifically through the internal influence that one reaches a higher elevation (which is above the aspect of *makif*). And this is "over all the honor of the chuppah", which are two aspects of honor: the honor of the groom and the honor of the bride, and higher still, the honor of Abba and the honor of Imma. Through this is the *yichud* (unification) of Abba and Imma and the *yichud* of Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah. For although both (the honor (and chuppah) of Abba and Imma, and the honor (and chuppah) of Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah) are aspects of *makif*, it is nonetheless known that it is specifically in the *yichud* of Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah (which is an internal *yichud*) that the *etzem* (essence) is drawn down.

b) The first analogy is from the influence of a teacher to a student. The order of influence is as our Sages have said: before beginning to teach the Sages, he would say a humorous remark, the Sages would laugh, and then he would sit in awe and begin the discourse. The humorous remark before the learning [which is the "idle chatter of a Torah scholar" that requires study] is external only; however, this influence is a prerequisite for the internal influence (the beginning of the discourse), because it is specifically through this that the opening of the student’s heart and mind is achieved, so that he becomes a *keli* to receive the internal influence. The source of this analogy is from the Mitteler Rebbe in *Torah Or* (Torah Chayim) [though in *Torah Chayim* it is not brought as an analogy for the matter of *Lecha Dodi*. In the *maamar* "Semuchim La’ad" (the *maamar* that the Rebbe Rashab said on his last birthday (20 Marcheshvan) in this world), he connects, by way of possibility ("and it is possible that this is the matter of..."), the matter of the humorous remark to the matter of *Lecha Dodi*. And in the *maamar* "Lecha Dodi," the Rebbe Rayatz omitted the word "possible" and writes it as a simple fact]. In *Torah Chayim* there (later on), he explains that the root of the matter of laughter is from the simple *taanug* (pleasure) that is not composite at all. From this it is understood that the root of the humorous remark (which is simple *taanug*) is higher than the influence of the intellect that follows (for the *taanug* within the intellect is a composite *taanug*). Nevertheless, it is still only an external aspect, and through the internal influence, one reaches a higher elevation. The point is that within simple *taanug* itself there are two levels: the simple *taanug* that is felt, and the essential *taanug* that is unfelt. And it is specifically through the internal influence, which the student receives in his interior, that one reaches the essential, unfelt *taanug*. And therefore our Sages said, "And from my students, more than all of them."

c) The second analogy is of a young, small child with whom his father wishes to play face-to-face. Since the infant is small, the father must lower his hands, etc., to lift his small son so that he can play with him in a face-to-face closeness. The lifting of the infant is only an external matter, and it is only a prerequisite for the internal closeness that follows (the playing, etc.). The source of this analogy is in *Or HaTorah* by the Maggid of Mezritch, and there is an addition there (which was not copied into the *maamar*) that the little one "plays with his (the father’s) beard." It can be said that this hints that the drawing down of the *makif* (which precedes the internal influence) is above the *seder hishtalshelus* (order of evolution), for the beard is the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (rectifications of the beard), the thirteen *middos* of mercy that are above the *seder hishtalshelus*. Yet, they still have some connection to the *seder hishtalshelus*, as it is written, "Remember Your mercies... for they are from of old" [which is why they are called "middos," from the word *medidah* (measurement)]. It is also known regarding the hairs that it is only an *ha’arah* (illumination). However, through the internal influence that follows (even though it is lower than the aspect of *makif*), the *etzem* (essence) that is above the *makif* is drawn down (similar to what was mentioned above in section a regarding the superiority of the *yichud* of Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah (which is an internal *yichud*) over the *yichud* of Abba and Imma, as explained by the Tzemach Tzedek in many places regarding this).

d) It is the same in *avodah* (as explained in the *maamar*): the beginning of a person’s *avodah* each day is the *avodah* of *tefillah*, as it is written, "Cease from man, in whose nostrils is a breath, for how (*bamah*) is he to be accounted?" Do not read *bamah* (how) but *bamah* (a high place/altar). The Alter Rebbe and the Rebbe Maharash explain that before *tefillah*, a person is considered like a *bamah*. *Tefillah* is a term for connection, for through *tefillah*, a person connects to *Elokus* (Divinity). The order of *tefillah* is that first there must be a general closeness (external influence) [as its matter is explained in the *maamar*], and afterward, an internal closeness is achieved, where the person connects to *Elokus* in such a way that he draws *Elokus* into all his physical affairs. This [that through *tefillah* at the beginning of the day he has the ability to connect all physical matters and make them *keilim* (vessels) for *Elokus*] can be understood based on what the Baal Shem Tov explained regarding the prohibition of greeting someone before *tefillah*. It is similar to what is written in the writings of the Arizal regarding the honoring of an older brother: it is because "the spirit remains within him," for in the firstborn son there is more of the father’s spirit than in the other sons, and all the other sons take from the father’s spirit through the firstborn. Because of the father’s spirit that is in the older brother, they are obligated to honor him just as they are obligated to honor the father [which is why they derive this law from the verse "Honor your father" specifically, for the honor of the older brother is included in the honoring of the father]. It is the same regarding a person’s thoughts, speech, and actions throughout the entire day, for they all branch out and are drawn after the first speech. Therefore, a person’s first speech [and likewise thought and action] upon waking from his sleep must be in the *avodah* of Hashem, for through this he draws holiness into all his thoughts, speech, and actions throughout the entire day. And it is specifically through this—that his internal closeness to *Elokus* (at the time of *tefillah*) is in such a way that he draws Divine light into his physical affairs until he makes them *keilim* for *Elokus*—that they reach higher, as is known regarding "much produce by the strength of the ox".

e) Likewise, this can also be understood regarding the drawing down of Ze’er Anpin into Malchus (*yichud* of Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah), where the order is (as mentioned above in section a) that first there must be an external influence and afterward an internal influence. For even the external influence is an extremely lofty influence (similar to what was mentioned above in sections b-c), which is an aspect of *makif* that is above the *seder hishtalshelus* and *keilim* (and therefore it is not absorbed into the Sefirah of Malchus in its interior, because it is above the limitation of her *keilim*). But nevertheless, this influence is an external aspect, which is only an *ha’arah* (illumination) alone. This is in contrast to the internal influence, which is received in Malchus in her interior, through which one reaches higher (than the aspect of *makif*).
