The point is that the root of Malchus is higher than the root of Ze’er Anpin. The root of Ze’er Anpin is from the exterior of Keter, and the root of Malchus is from the interior of Keter. And even though it is said regarding Ze’er Anpin that "Ze’er Anpin is attached and suspended from Atik," it is known that this does not refer to the actual Atik (only the exterior of Atik). In contrast, the root of Malchus is in the interior of Atik, *Radla* (the Unknowable Head). However, because of her descent below, her root is in concealment, and the revelation of the root of Malchus is specifically through Ze’er Anpin, and through this very thing, the Sefirah of Malchus is elevated above Ze’er Anpin. This is the matter of the order of influence: first, there must be the drawing down of Ze’er Anpin into Malchus in a way that the matter of *Ze’er Anpin* (which is above Malchus) is felt (for it is specifically through him that the root of Malchus is revealed). But nevertheless, since the influence is from the side of (the superiority of) Ze’er Anpin, it has a connection to the *seder hishtalshelus* [similar to what was mentioned above (section c) regarding the thirteen *tikkunei dikna*]. And it is specifically through the internal influence that is received in Malchus in her interior—since this influence is from the side of (the superiority of) Malchus—that one reaches the root of Malchus, which is above the root of Ze’er Anpin, to the point that Malchus influences Ze’er Anpin, "a woman of valor is the crown of her husband".

f) It can be said that this is also the explanation for what is brought (at the beginning of the *maamar*) regarding the two extremes of Shabbos. Shabbos is called "Queen," which is the Sefirah of Malchus, which is below all the Sefirot and receives from them, as the saying goes, "The moon has nothing of its own" [and as our Sages say (regarding Shabbos), that only one who toils on Erev Shabbos will eat on Shabbos]. On the other hand, "all the days are blessed from Shabbos", meaning that not only is Shabbos holier than all the days, but furthermore, it influences them. The matter is that the seven days of the week are the seven days of construction. The six days of the week are in Ze’er Anpin, as it is written, "For in six days Hashem made the heavens and the earth," and it is stated in the Zohar that each and every day does its work. Shabbos is Malchus (as mentioned above). Therefore, because Malchus descended below, and especially because of her descent into *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* where her feet descend, etc., Shabbos (Malchus) receives from the six days of the week (Ze’er Anpin), which is the matter of the *avodah* of *birurim* (the refinement of the animal soul and all physical things) of the six days of the week. However, after (and through) this *avodah*, the ascent of Malchus from *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* to her root and source occurs (on Shabbos), and then she is elevated above Ze’er Anpin to the point that she influences all six days of the week (Ze’er Anpin) as well, for "all the days are blessed from it."

g) This is "Come, my beloved, to greet the bride; let us welcome the face of Shabbos," which is the request of Knesses Yisrael that there be a drawing down of Ze’er Anpin into Malchus. The beginning of the influence is "Come, my beloved, to greet the bride"—walking only—and through this "let us welcome the face of Shabbos," which is the internal influence, the *face* of Shabbos, where the aspect of the interior of Malchus is revealed, even as she is rooted in Atik. Therefore, "let us welcome" is in the plural, for Ze’er Anpin also receives from (the root of) Malchus, "a woman of valor is the crown of her husband." And just as it is above in Ze’er Anpin and Malchus, so too is it in every influencer and recipient: that through the recipient, an addition is made in the influencer, and "from my students, more than all of them." Especially in a groom and bride below, that specifically through the internal influence, "a woman of valor is the crown of her husband," and "everything was from the dust". Through this, the power of the *Ein Sof* is drawn down, "in a generation of the upright, he shall be blessed with children and grandchildren who occupy themselves with Torah and *mitzvos*."

## B’ezras Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Teitzei, 13 Elul, 5741

### B’ezras Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Teitzei, 13 Elul, 5741

“Gladden the beloved companions as You gladdened Your creation in the Garden of Eden of old”. It is explained in the *maamar* on this subject (delivered at the time of the wedding of the Rebbe Rayatz on Friday, 13 Elul, 5657) that the “beloved companions” (*re’im ha’ahuvim*) refers to the level of Chochma and Binah, which are called “two companions who never separate” (*trin re’in d’la misparshin*). The request, “Gladden the beloved companions,” is that joy be drawn into Chochma and Binah.

We must understand this: Binah is the place of joy, as it is written, “The mother of the children is joyful” (*em habanim semechah*). It is well known that “the mother of the children” refers to Binah, which is the mother that gives birth to the *midos*. We see this experientially: when a person grasps a concept in his intellect, he experiences joy from it. Furthermore, in Chochma, where joy is not typically applicable—because joy is a product of revelation, while Chochma (like a flashing bolt of lightning) is above revelation—there shines a revelation of *taanug*. This is like the “radiance” (*tzehivu*) on the face of Rabbi Avahu when he found a new *Tosefta*; this radiance of the face comes from the revelation of *taanug*. It is known that *taanug* is higher than joy. What, then, is the request to “gladden the beloved companions,” given that there is already joy in Binah, and certainly in Chochma, which contains *taanug* that is higher than joy?

Furthermore, we must understand: “Beloved companions” (*re’im ha’ahuvim*) refers (simply) to the bride and groom, and it is known that the bride and groom are *ZON* (Ze’er Anpin and Nukvah). What is the connection between this interpretation (that “beloved companions” refers to the bride and groom, *ZON*) and the aforementioned interpretation that the “companions” are Chochma and Binah?

2. It can be said that this connection between the two interpretations is understood based on what is written in the book *Emes L’Yaakov* (cited in the aforementioned *maamar*): that *ahuvim* (beloved) has the same *gematria* as *dodim* (lovers/beloveds), and they are *ZA* and *Nukvah* (as it is known that *re’im* are Chochma and Binah, and *dodim* are *ZON*). Regarding the phrase *re’im ha’ahuvim*, where the word *ahuvim* serves as a continuation and descriptor of *re’im* (which, as stated, refers to Chochma and Binah), this can be explained in two ways.

First, based on the known manner in which the *midos* (*ZON*) are born from the *mochin* (Chochma and Binah): initially, they are included within the *mochin*, and afterwards they are drawn out into revelation. According to this, it can be said that *re’im ha’ahuvim* refers to *ZON* (*ahuvim*) as they are included within Chochma and Binah (*re’im*). By contrast, *ahuvim* (on its own) refers to *ZON* as they are drawn out into revelation—*ahuvim* in *gematria* equals *dodim*. This also explains why the concept of *ZON* (*dodim*) is hinted at in the *gematria* of *ahuvim*: *gematria* indicates a diminution of light and vitality, a diminution after a diminution, because the drawing down from the *midos* within the *mochin* (*re’im ha’ahuvim*) to the *midos* in the heart (*ahuvim* in *gematria* equals *dodim*) occurs through several *tzimtzumim*.

Second, since the *midos* are the offspring of the *mochin*—Chochma and Binah are the father and mother, and *ZON* are the son and daughter [as it is stated in Kabbalah that father and mother are *Yud-Heh* (Chochma and Binah), and son and daughter are *Vav-Heh* (*ZON*)]—they resemble the *mochin* (even after they have been drawn down and revealed). For the father bequeaths to his son, etc., to the point that the heir stands in the place of the progenitor, and the same applies to the daughter (when she inherits in the absence of a son) [specifically, the son is in the place of the father, and the daughter is in the place of the mother, as it is written, “Like her mother, her daughter”]. According to this, it can be said that even after they have been drawn down and revealed, they are called by the name *re’im ha’ahuvim* (as mentioned above, that *re’im ha’ahuvim* simply refers to the bride and groom, *ZON* in revelation), because even then (after their drawing down and revelation) they resemble Chochma and Binah.

3. It should be added that the connection between the two interpretations of *re’im ha’ahuvim* [that the primary interpretation is that *re’im ha’ahuvim* refers to Chochma and Binah, as explained at length in the *maamar*, but that there is also an interpretation that it refers (also) to *ZON*] applies also to the matter of “Gladden, gladden,” etc. For the request that joy be drawn into Chochma and Binah (the primary interpretation of *re’im ha’ahuvim*), even though they already possess joy and *taanug* in their own right, is that there be drawn into them a joy that is higher than the joy they possess from themselves (as will be explained at length below). The reason why it is necessary to draw this additional joy into them is so that through this, there will be revelation in *ZON* (the second interpretation of *re’im ha’ahuvim*).

4. The matter is as follows: The *avodah* of Hashem must be with joy, as it is written, “Serve Hashem with joy,” and it is written, “Because you did not serve Hashem your G-d with joy and goodness of heart.” Since a person must serve Hashem in all his affairs—“All your deeds should be for the sake of Heaven” and (even more so) “In all your ways know Him”—to the point that this (*avodah*) is the purpose of his entire creation, as our Sages said, “I was not created except to serve my Maker,” it follows that one must always be in a state of joy. However, there are different levels of joy. There are specific places that are places of joy, such as a building of joy. The same is true regarding time: there are specific times (Yomim Tovim) that are “appointed times for joy”. Even within these, there are levels, such as the festival of Sukkos, which is (also) “the time of our joy”. Specifically, in the *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah*, of which it is said, “Whoever has not seen the *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah* has never seen joy in his life”, where they would dance with torches of light. Torches of light are the level of Chochma, and the act of dancing (with the torches) is the drawing down (of the level of Chochma) into Binah [and even within this joy itself there are levels, for it was not performed by just anyone, but by the greatest sages of Israel, etc., while all the people came to see and hear]. Especially on Simchas Torah, where the joy of Simchas Torah is higher even than the joy of the *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah*, as is stated in *Likutei Torah*, to the point that the name of this day (for the name of everything indicates its essence and vitality) is *Simchas Torah* (Joy of Torah). From all this, it is understood that there are many, many levels of joy. Broadly, they are divided into two categories: joy that is conditioned upon something (such as joy resulting from intellectual grasp or the like), which is a joy of the revealed faculties and is within the realm of limitation; and essential joy, which is primarily in the essence of the soul, which is above the realm of limitation.

5. This can be understood based on what is explained in the *maamar* there: that the nature of joy is to break through boundaries—that is, every definition and limitation in the soul. It explains two ways this occurs. The first way is that joy breaks through the boundaries created in a person because he is accustomed to them, even though these boundaries have become like nature to him (for habit becomes second nature). The second way is that joy has the power to break through even the boundaries of one’s innate nature, to the point that joy has the power to transform and change them from one extreme to the other. That is, when joy breaks through the boundaries of one’s innate nature, it is not merely that the *midos* with which a person was born are increased and intensified beyond their measure, but that through joy, a change occurs in the very nature of his *midos*, from one extreme to the other. For example, someone who is by nature extremely stingy and miserly: at a time of joy, when he is in a state of the greatest joy, his heart is completely transformed from his previous nature, and he becomes a great spendthrift and generous person, like someone who is generous by nature, to the point that he acts kindly even toward his enemy—and it is possible to say even toward his enemy according to Torah.

Now, even regarding the first way—that joy breaks through the boundary of habit—it requires explanation. Since every habit becomes nature, even if only a second nature, seemingly it should require much time and *avodah* to change this nature gradually. How does joy have the power to change it in a single moment? And all the more so regarding the second way, where we must understand how joy has the power to break through the boundaries of one’s innate nature, to the point that it has the power to change and transform his nature from one extreme to the other. The matter is (as explained in the *maamar* there) that joy breaks through boundaries (even in the first way, and certainly in the second) only when it is a joy that reaches the essence of the soul, which is above the revealed faculties. Because the essence of the soul is above the realm of limitation (being connected with the *Atzmus*), therefore, the joy that comes from the essence of the soul breaks through all definitions and limitations.

6. This is the meaning of “Gladden, gladden the beloved companions”—that one must draw joy into Chochma and Binah. Even though the place of joy is in Binah, and in Chochma there is *taanug* that is higher than joy, the joy in Binah and the *taanug* in Chochma are (analogous to) the joy and *taanug* of the revealed faculties, and consequently, they involve measurement and limitation. And even though the interiority of Abba is the interiority of Atik—and especially since the intention is not only to the level of the interiority of Atik alone, but to the very first root of the level of the interiority and essence of the *Ein Sof*—this matter relates to the internal *yichud* of Abba and Imma, and this *yichud* must be aroused and drawn down (for the internal *yichud* of Abba and Imma occurs only at times). This is what we request: “Gladden, gladden the beloved companions”—that there be drawn into Chochma and Binah the essential joy (even from the interiority and essence of the *Ein Sof*) that is completely above the realm of limitation, for this joy breaks through all boundaries (as mentioned above). Through this, an internal *yichud* of Chochma and Binah is effected, and this *yichud* will also be a constant *yichud*.

The primary intention in this (the internal *yichud* of Chochma and Binah) is so that through it there will be a *yichud* of *ZON*, “for this is the main thing”. As explained at length in the *maamar*, it is specifically in the *yichud* of *ZON* that the essence is drawn down, which is why the *yichud* of *ZON* specifically brings about a new creation (the birth of souls). However, in order for there to be a *yichud* of *ZON*, there must first be an internal *yichud* of Chochma and Binah. This is the meaning of “Gladden, gladden the beloved companions” (*ahuvim* in *gematria* equals *dodim*, *ZON*), because the request that there be a drawing down of joy into Chochma and Binah, through which there will be an internal *yichud* of Chochma and Binah, is for the sake of the *yichud* of *ZON*.

7. According to this, the relevance of this request to the joy of a wedding is also understood. It is known that the creation of *yesh me’ayin* (something from nothing) is specifically through the power of the *Atzmus*. All lights and revelations, since they have a cause or reason, do not have the ability to bring into being something (“a *yesh*”) that (in its own perception) has no cause or reason; it is impossible for any existing thing to bestow what is not within its power. The coming into being of the *yesh* is only through the power of the *Atzmus*, whose existence is from His own essence and has no cause or reason that preceded Him, G-d forbid. Now, the “drawing down” of the *Atzmus* to create *yesh me’ayin* (during the six days of creation) was because “He desires kindness.” But after the Giving of the Torah, for this drawing down to occur, it is through the *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos*. It can be said that specifically (and openly) it is through the *mitzvos* that relate to the concept of *bli gevul* (without limit), such as the *mitzvah* of *pru u’rvu* (procreation), as it is known that the matter of procreation (to bring forth generation after generation) is a revelation of the power of the *Ein Sof*, and especially since the matter of procreation is (also) analogous to the creation of *yesh me’ayin*, which is through the power of the *Atzmus*. This is what we request at the joy of a wedding: “Gladden, gladden the beloved companions,” because the purpose of the wedding is that there be procreation, “Be fruitful and multiply and fill the earth”. Therefore, we request then: “Gladden, gladden the beloved companions,” that there be a drawing down of the essential joy of the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*. This is also why we say (in the continuation of the blessing) “as You gladdened Your creation in the Garden of Eden of old,” for the drawing down of joy in the Garden of Eden of old (at the beginning of creation) was because “He desires kindness.” This is what we request: that now, too, through our *avodah* in Torah and *mitzvos*, and especially through the joy of a wedding, this drawing down should occur.

8. Just as it was on the day of His wedding, which is the Giving of the Torah, when there was a drawing down of the essential joy, etc. (and as explained in the *maamar*, the primary joy that breaks through all boundaries is the joy of a wedding), the drawing down then was through *avodah*. For the day of His wedding, the Giving of the Torah, refers to the second Tablets, and the matter of the second Tablets is that they were given specifically through *avodah*. The same applies to the fulfillment of every *mitzvah*: through every *mitzvah*, one must intend “for the sake of the unification of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and His Presence,” as stated in *Pri Etz Chaim*. The fact that we say the *L’shem Yichud* only once before *davening* is because this statement is an act that extends throughout the entire day. Since every single Jew is the only son of the Holy One, Blessed be He, according to the well-known teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, and it is written, “My firstborn son is Israel,” in the singular, and also at the Giving of the Torah it was said to each and every Jew, “I am Hashem your G-d,” in the singular, it follows that the higher joy in the fulfillment of every *mitzvah* by each and every Jew is the joy of the Holy One, Blessed be He, at the wedding of His only son—a joy that breaks through all boundaries.

9. Especially in the month of Elul, when the King is in the field with each and every Jew, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows them a smiling face. Elul is an acronym for *Ani L’Dodi V’Dodi Li* (“I am to my beloved and my beloved is to me”). Even though *dodim* refers to *ZON*, whose union is only at times, in the month of Elul they are united in one word. From this, it is understood that in addition to the matter of the joy of a wedding (the union of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and His Presence) that exists throughout the year through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, in the month of Elul it is with greater intensity. Especially on the Shabbosos in the month of Elul. In the month of Elul, we blow the *shofar* to warn Israel to do *teshuvah*, as it is said, “If a *shofar* is blown in a city, will the people not tremble?”. Thus, in Elul there is also the matter of fear and trembling. However, this is only on weekdays; by contrast, on the Shabbosos in the month of Elul, the matter of the fear and trembling of Elul is seemingly (in revelation) not present on Shabbos, for on Shabbos we do not blow [the *shofar*], and on Shabbos there is no sadness. The primary activity of Elul on the days of Shabbos is the matter of *Ani L’Dodi V’Dodi Li*, the wedding joy of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and the Community of Israel. From this, it is understood that every addition in Torah and *mitzvos*, especially in the month of Elul, breaks through all boundaries, including the boundaries of *galus*. For every addition in Torah and *mitzvos* (whose essence is the opposite of *galus*) hastens the future Redemption. “On that day, [Hashem] will be…”, *B’fayim Yud-Heh* (two times *Yud-Heh*), meaning that the *Vav-Heh* will also be like *Yud-Heh*. Just as *Yud-Heh* are in constant union, so too will the level of *Vav-Heh* be in constant union in the future Redemption. Then there will be the matter of the wedding, as it is stated in *Shemos Rabbah* that now is the matter of the betrothal (*eirusin*), and in the future, there will be the wedding (*nissuin*), speedily in our days, truly.

## By the Grace of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Tavo, 18 Elul, 5727

### By the Grace of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Tavo, 18 Elul, 5727

"Look down from Your holy habitation, from the heavens, and bless Your people, Israel". My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, notes in his maamar on this verse—which was delivered on the first 18 Elul after his arrival in the United States for the second time to reside there, and the calendar date of 18 Elul that year fell on Shabbos Parshas Tavo, as it does this year—why it says "Your people, Israel." After all, "Your people" (Amcha) are Israel, and Israel are "the people of Hashem." Why specify both? Furthermore, it requires study: the fact that it says "Your people, *es* Israel" (rather than "Your people Israel") implies that "Your people" and "Israel" (in this verse) are two distinct matters. It must be understood (as the maamar notes) that the concept of "Israel" is higher than the concept of "Your people" [as is also understood from the fact that the term *Am* (people) sometimes denotes the opposite of praise, whereas the name *Israel* is based on "for you have struggled with Elokim and with men and have prevailed"], yet here it places "Your people" before "Israel."

2) It can be said that the explanation in the maamar—that the phrasing "Your people *es* Israel" implies they are two distinct matters—is based on what our Sages said regarding the verse, "over Saul and over Jonathan his son and over the people of Hashem and over the house of Israel": the word *al* (over) separates the concepts. Based on this, we can add that from the extra word *es*, we learn not only that "Your people" and "Israel" are two distinct matters, but also that in "bless Your people, *es* Israel," there are two distinct matters: a blessing for "Your people" and a blessing for "Israel". We must understand the difference between these two blessings, and why the blessing for "Your people" precedes the blessing for "Israel."

3) To explain this, the maamar introduces the teaching from the Yerushalmi: "Come and see how great is the power of those who perform a mitzvah, for every 'looking down' (hashkafah) mentioned in the Torah is a curse, yet this one is in the language of a blessing." Through the performance of mitzvos, they transform the curse into a blessing [and in continuation of this, it explains the verse, "But Hashem your Elokim did not want to listen to Bilaam, and Hashem your Elokim turned the curse into a blessing for you, because Hashem your Elokim loved you," which mentions "Hashem your Elokim" three times, as will be discussed in section 4]. Afterward, it explains the two categories of "Your people" and "Israel": those who are knowledgeable in Torah and sit in the tent of Torah are "Israel," while simple people who perform Torah and mitzvos with sincerity and simplicity are "the people of Hashem" ("Your people"). It places "Your people" before "Israel" because "great is study, for it leads to action", and those who perform mitzvos transform the curse into a blessing.

It can be said that the connection between "great is study, for it leads to action" and the fact that "Your people" is placed before "Israel" is that the very fact that study is "great" because it leads to action proves that action is the primary thing. However, this alone is not a sufficient explanation for why "Your people" (those who perform mitzvos) are placed before "Israel" (those who study Torah), for the statement of our Sages itself says "great is *study*." Therefore, it adds that those who perform mitzvos transform the curse into a blessing—meaning that in this specific matter (the transformation of a curse into a blessing), the superiority of action over study is revealed (similar to the future era, when action will be greater). And since the matter of "looking down... and bless" is the transformation of a curse into a blessing (as mentioned from the Yerushalmi), therefore "Your people" is placed before "Israel." We must understand the connection between the transformation of a curse into a blessing and the superiority of action.

4) Now, after the maamar explains that through the performance of mitzvos one transforms a curse into a blessing, it cites the verse, "But Hashem your Elokim did not want to listen to Bilaam, and Hashem your Elokim turned the curse into a blessing for you, because Hashem your Elokim loved you," and explains that there are three matters in this verse. In each of them, it says "Hashem your Elokim". The matter of "did not want to listen to Bilaam" is that the Ribono shel Olam does not want to hear, and does not hear, accusations against Israel. The fact that He does not hear the accusations (even though from the perspective of the attribute of judgment they have a place) is due to the attribute of mercy, "Hashem your Elokim." The matter of "turned the curse into a blessing for you" is that willful sins (zedonos) are transformed into merits (zechuyos) [it is not just that He does not listen to the accusers (while the sins remain un-erased), but that an atonement for sins occurs, and furthermore, that willful sins are transformed into merits]. It says "Hashem your Elokim" here a second time because the *Havayah* from which "did not want to listen to the accusers" is drawn is the *Havayah* of below, and in order for there to be atonement for sins, and especially the transformation of willful sins into merits, it is through the drawing down of the revelation of the *Havayah* of above. The matter of "because He loved you" is the essential love of the Ribono shel Olam for Israel, that even in the level above *Seder Hishtalshelus*, where it is said, "for Esau is a brother to Jacob", nevertheless, "and I loved Jacob" specifically. This is "Hashem your Elokim," for even though in the *Havayah* of above (the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus*) all are equal, nevertheless, through the revelation of the essential love of the Ribono shel Olam for Israel ("because He loved you"), even the *Havayah* of above is the *Elokim* of *you* (Israel) specifically. Afterward, the maamar explains the reason why "Your people" (those who perform mitzvos) are placed before "Israel" (those who study Torah), because [great is study, for it leads to action, and] those who perform mitzvos transform the curse into a blessing (as mentioned in section 3). We must understand that, seemingly, to explain why "Your people" is placed before "Israel," it should only be relevant that those who perform mitzvos transform a curse into a blessing; the fact that the maamar (also) introduces the explanation of the three matters in the verse "did not want to listen to Bilaam" implies that this adds an explanation for why "Your people" is placed before "Israel."

5) This can be understood by prefacing what the Rebbe Maharash says in his maamar titled *Shabchi Yerushalayim es Havayah, Halleli Elokayich Tzion* (from Shabbos Parshas Tavo, one hundred years ago). It needs to be understood: after all, *Tzion* is higher than *Yerushalayim* [for *Tzion* is the inwardness of *Yerushalayim*], and yet, regarding *Yerushalayim* it says *Havayah* and regarding *Tzion* it says *Elokim*. Now, Israel is called by the name *Tzion*, as it is written, "to say to *Tzion*, you are My people." Based on this, it can be said that *Tzion* and *Yerushalayim* are two levels within Israel. According to what is said in the aforementioned maamar that *Yerushalayim* is *yirah tata'ah* (lower awe), it can be said that *Tzion* is *yirah ila'ah* (higher awe). It can be said that the hint of *yirah ila'ah* is in *Tzion*, for the *bitul* of *yirah ila'ah* is a *bitul* of existence (*bitul b'metzius*), and this *bitul* is hinted at in *Tzion* (from the word *siman*—a sign), meaning it has no existence of its own and is only a sign of what is above. This is "for from *Tzion* will go forth Torah and the word of Hashem from *Yerushalayim*", for regarding *Tzion* it says Torah and regarding *Yerushalayim* it says the word of Hashem. For one of the differences between *yirah tata'ah* and *yirah ila'ah* is that *yirah tata'ah* comes from His greatness in the creation and formation of the worlds, where the *bitul* of this awe is a *bitul* of *yesh* (existence). *Yirah ila'ah* is from His greatness and exaltation that is above the worlds, where "everything before Him is considered as nothing", and the *bitul* in this awe is a *bitul b'metzius*. This is what is written, "And Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes to fear Hashem"—that in order to arrive at the fear of *es* Hashem, *yirah ila'ah*, which comes through the feeling of the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, it is through Torah and mitzvos (these statutes). For through contemplation, one can only grasp the *Elokus* that is relative to the worlds, and in order to feel the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, it is specifically through a revelation from above that is drawn down by the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos. This is the connection of *Tzion* to Torah and *Yerushalayim* to the word of Hashem, for *yirah tata'ah* (*Yerushalayim*) is from the word of Hashem that brings the worlds into being—"by the word of Hashem the heavens were made"—and *yirah ila'ah* (*Tzion*) is from the revelation of the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, which is drawn down by Torah and mitzvos. Based on this, the precision in the verse "Praise *Yerushalayim* Hashem, praise your *Elokim*, *Tzion*" (that regarding *Yerushalayim* it says *Havayah* and regarding *Tzion* it says *Elokim*) is also in the matter of *Yerushalayim* and *Tzion* in the *avodah* of man. For it is known regarding *Havayah* and *Elokim* that *Elokim* is the *Ohr HaMemalei* (the light that is relative to the worlds) and *Havayah* is the *Ohr HaSovev* (the light that is above the worlds). From this it is understood that *yirah tata'ah* belongs to *Elokim* and *yirah ila'ah* to *Havayah*, and yet, in *Yerushalayim* (*yirah tata'ah*) it says *Havayah* and in *Tzion* (*yirah ila'ah*) it says *Elokim*.

6) The explanation of the superiority of *yirah ila'ah* (*Tzion*) in greater detail will be understood by prefacing what is explained in the aforementioned maamar *Shabchi*: that in the contemplation that leads to *yirah tata'ah* (*Yerushalayim*), there are two matters. The contemplation of His greatness in creation itself, both in the matter of "How great are Your works, Hashem" and in the matter of "How great are Your works, Hashem". And the contemplation that all of existence (the multitude of created beings and the greatness of the created beings) is only from the most external aspect. As it is written, "Great is Hashem and highly praised in the city of our *Elokim*," and our Sages said, "When is He great? When He is in the city of our *Elokim*," for His greatness as it is in itself is above our comprehension, and the fact that we know His greatness through the creation of the worlds is as it is in the "city of our *Elokim*," which is the world of speech. Just as a city in the literal sense is a collection of many houses, and a house is a collection of many stones, so too is it in spirituality: letters are called stones, and words that are made from the combination of several letters are called houses [as it is in *Sefer Yetzirah*, "two stones build two houses, three stones build six houses"], and the world of speech (in its entirety) is called the city of our *Elokim*. And just as stones [and likewise the houses and the city made from the stones] are *domem* (inanimate), the most external level in the *domem, tzomei'ach, chai, medabeir* (inanimate, vegetative, animal, speaking), so too is it regarding the world of speech from which all the worlds were formed, which is the most external level. This is "and the word of Hashem from *Yerushalayim*," for the word of Hashem that brings into being, vivifies, and sustains all created beings is from *Yerushalayim*, the city of our *Elokim*, the level of *domem*. It can be said that what is explained in the maamar—that the contemplation leading to *yirah tata'ah* (*Yerushalayim*) is (not only in the greatness within creation, but also) in the fact that existence is only from the most external aspect—is because *Yerushalayim* is *yirah shalem* (complete awe), the perfection of awe. And in order for the awe (*bitul*) to be complete, it is through the contemplation that the created beings do not occupy a place. This is the connection of the two interpretations (matters) in *Yerushalayim*—that *Yerushalayim* is the world of speech and that *Yerushalayim* is the perfection of awe—that through the contemplation of "the word of Hashem from *Yerushalayim*," that the existence of all the worlds is (only) from the aspect of *Yerushalayim* (the world of speech) which is the level of *domem* relative to the levels above it, through this one will arrive at the perfection of awe.

However, even so, this is included in *yirah tata'ah*, because his primary contemplation is on the *Elokus* that is relative to the worlds, and therefore, even when he contemplates that he is only the level of *domem*, the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, where "everything before Him is considered as nothing," is not (so) felt by him. From this it is understood that when it says *yirah ila'ah* is from the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* above the worlds, the intention is that this matter itself is felt by him. Based on this, it is necessary to understand even more why regarding *Tzion* (*yirah ila'ah*) it says *Elokim*.

7) The aforementioned maamar *Shabchi* explains that the reason for what is written "Praise your *Elokim*, *Tzion*" is explained by the verse itself (in the following verse): "For He has strengthened the bars of your gates, etc." The matter is that it is in the Mishnah: "They compel him (a city dweller) to build a wall, doors, and a bar for the city." A wall is to protect from the enemy so he does not enter the city, and so that the city dwellers can go out and come in, they make an opening and a door in the wall, and they make bars for the door so that only those who are fit to enter may enter the city. So too is it above: the matter of the bars is the *gevuros* of the name *Elokim* that limit the *shefa* (flow), so that no nourishment is drawn from it to the *chitzonim* (external forces). This is "Praise your *Elokim*, *Tzion*" (and the reason the name *Elokim* is mentioned here is) "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates," for in *Tzion* is the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus* (as mentioned above), and relative to this light, all are equal, and therefore the *gevuros* of the name *Elokim* are needed to limit the *shefa* drawn from this light, so that the *chitzonim* do not derive nourishment. This is similar to what is written, "and to say to *Tzion*, you are My people," that the influence from the level of *Tzion* will be only for "My people," for Israel. This is what the verse continues, "Bless your children within you," that the blessing and influence will be only for "your children," for Israel.

The maamar continues that this matter is accomplished through the *avodah* of "Judges and officers you shall appoint for yourself in all your gates". "Your gates" are the fifty gates of *Binah* that are drawn from the *moach* (intellect) of *Binah* to the *midos* (emotional attributes) in the heart. Through the *avodah* of "Judges and officers you shall appoint for yourself in all your gates," that all seven *midos* [each of which is comprised of seven] should be for Hashem alone, through this the "bars of your gates" are made, so that the *shefa* is not drawn to the *chitzonim* but only to Israel.

8) Now, after the maamar explains *Shabchi Yerushalayim*, "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates," it explains the verse, "He makes your borders peace, etc." and its connection to "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates," and afterward it explains the verse, "He gives snow like wool, etc." It explains that snow is the aspect of "His garments were like white snow", and wool is the aspect of "the hair of His head like pure wool". This is what is written, "If your sins are like scarlet, they shall whiten like snow; if they are red like crimson, they shall become like wool." Scarlet is a white thread that was dyed red, meaning the blemish is only in the garments, and the rectification of this blemish is through the aspect of "His garments were like white snow." Crimson is red in its essence, meaning the blemish reached the essence of the soul, and to rectify this blemish is through the aspect of wool, "the hair of His head like pure wool," for the hair of the head is the drawing from the essence of the soul, as we see that when one pulls a person by the hair of his head, the entire body is drawn. The matter of "He gives snow like wool" is that even in snow, which is a garment, the aspect of wool, the essence, will be drawn. The connection between wool and snow is through a drawing from a place that is above both of them. After the maamar explains the matter of "He gives snow like wool," it explains once more (with a slight change) the matter of "Judges and officers you shall appoint for yourself in all your gates," and that through this, "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates" is accomplished. We must understand the connection of "He gives snow like wool" to "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates."

9) This will be understood by prefacing that snow and wool each have an advantage. The matter is that "His garments were like white snow" (snow) are the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (rectifications of the beard) whose root is in the *mocha stima'ah* (concealed intellect) of *Arich*, in which the *gevurah* of *Atik* is clothed, and "the hair of His head like pure wool" (wool) is in the *galgalta* (skull) of *Arich*, in which the *chesed* of *Atik* is clothed. It is explained in the *Siddur* that the matter of the *gevuros* in the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* is because they come to sweeten the judgments, and judgments are only sweetened in their root, and the hair of the head, *which do not* come to sweeten judgments (for they are above the thirteen attributes of mercy), are the aspect of *chesed*. From this it is understood that the sweetening of judgments through the thirteen *tikkunei dikna*, since they come to sweeten the judgments, therefore the sweetening belongs *to the below* (to those upon whom judgments were aroused), and the sweetening through the hair of the head, which are above the matter of sweetening judgments, is from the *chasadim* within them, a revelation *from above*. This is why the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* are mercy (the thirteen attributes of mercy) and the hair of the head is *chesed*, for mercy is (generally) from the fact that one feels the pain of the other, and *chesed* is from itself.

Now, from what is explained in the maamar (cited above in section 8) that the rectification of the blemishes through the revelation of the hair of the head is analogous to how when one pulls a person by the hair of his head, the entire body is drawn, it is proven that the aspect of the hair of the head that is above is the essence of Israel [for since the hair of the head is the essentiality of above that is above the aspect of garments, this is also the essentiality of Israel, for Israel and the *Kudsha Brich Hu* are one]. Based on this, it must be said that what was brought above—that the hair of the head is *chesed* (and the sweetening of judgments is through a revelation from above)—is regarding the revealed powers of the soul, through which the rectification and revelation of the blemishes occur. The matter is that the thirteen *tikkunei dikna*, despite being above *Seder Hishtalshelus*, nevertheless, since they come to sweeten the judgments (that are in *Seder Hishtalshelus*), they belong to *Seder Hishtalshelus*. It can be said that their matter in man is the essence of the revealed powers. Therefore, the revelation of the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* *acts* upon the revealed powers of the soul. The aspect of the hair of the head is the essentiality of above that is above the essence of the revealed powers [and this is what is said in the maamar (cited above in section 8) that the revelation of the aspect of the hair of the head is effective even when the blemish has reached the essence of the soul, for the essence in which the blemish reached is the essence that belongs to the revelations, and the aspect of the hair of the head is the essence of the soul itself, in which no blemish is possible]. And since the essence is distinct from the revelations, it is not possible *that it should act* upon them. The rectification of the blemishes in the revealed powers through the revelation of the aspect of the hair of the head is that it is revealed in them that from the perspective of the essence of the soul, no blemish is possible, for even at the time of the sin, it is "in faith with Him", and since the essence of the soul is *their* essence, therefore the blemishes in them are only in the externality. That is to say, the rectification of the blemishes through the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* is that the essence belonging to the revealed powers *acts* upon them, *upon their configuration*. And the rectification of the blemishes through the aspect of the hair of the head is that it is revealed in them that from the perspective of *the essence* (of theirs), no blemish is possible in them, but this does not belong so much to the matter of the revealed powers themselves, to their configuration.

10) This is "He gives snow like wool," for in each of them there is an advantage. The advantage of snow is that the rectification and filling of the blemishes through the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (snow) is in the inwardness (*in the configuration* of the revealed powers), but it is in measure and limitation, for since it is by way of action [that the essence belonging to the revealed powers acts upon them], there are several levels of difference in this. The advantage of wool is that the rectification of the blemishes through the hair of the head is that it is revealed in them that in the inwardness (from the perspective of their essence) *it is not possible at all* that there should be a blemish in them. The matter of "He gives snow like wool," that even in snow the aspect of wool, the essence, will be drawn, is that there should be both advantages. That is, that which from the perspective of the essence *it is not possible* for there to be a blemish in them, will also act upon their configuration.

In order for there to be the connection of wool and snow, it is through a drawing from a place that is higher than both of them [as brought above (section 8) from the maamar]. It can be said that the explanation for this is that the fact that the essence of the soul and the configuration of the powers are (analogous to) two matters is because even the essence of the soul is defined within a definition, and its definition is above the configuration of the powers. But from the perspective of the essence of the soul as it is rooted in the *Atzmus* (the Essence), the simplicity of the soul and the configuration of the intellect and *midos* within it are all one. Through the revelation of this aspect of the soul, even the powers of the soul (the configuration of the powers) are in a manner *that it is not possible* for them to be contrary to the intention. And through the drawing down of the essence of the soul (wool) into the specific powers (snow), an elevation is also made in the essence of the soul, for through this, its root is revealed as it is rooted in the *Atzmus*.

Based on this, the connection of the matter of "He gives snow like wool" to the matter of "for He has strengthened the bars of your gates" can be explained, for wool and snow are analogous to *makif* (encompassing) and *penimi* (internal). Through the connection of wool and snow, that the essence of the soul that is above the revealed powers (wool, *makif*) is drawn into the revealed powers (snow, *penimi*), through this, the same occurs in the revelations of above, that even the *makifim* are drawn into the *penimi*.

11) It should be added that the matter of "He gives snow like wool" also belongs to the matter of *Yerushalayim* and *Tzion* at the beginning of the maamar. *Yerushalayim* and *Tzion* (*yirah tata'ah* and *yirah ila'ah*) are analogous to snow and wool. *Yirah tata'ah*, since the awe is from His greatness in the creation of the world, belongs also to the *nefesh habehamis* (animal soul)—analogous to the level of snow that acts upon the revealed powers. And *yirah ila'ah*, since it is from the exaltation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the worlds, therefore, even though regarding the *nefesh elokis* (divine soul) it is a greater awe, it is in a manner that the awe of the soul does not act upon the *nefesh habehamis*—analogous to the level of wool, which does not act upon the revealed powers. And just as the aspect of wool, despite being above the aspect of snow, nevertheless, through its drawing into the aspect of snow, an elevation is made in it, so too is it in *yirah ila'ah* (*Tzion*), that through the fact that strength is drawn from it into *yirah tata'ah* (*Yerushalayim*) to act upon the refinement of the body, the *nefesh habehamis*, and one's portion in the world, an elevation is made in it [analogous to "great is study, for it leads to action," that through the fact that study leads to action, a greatness is made in the study]. However, in *Tzion* and *Yerushalayim*, the drawing of *Tzion* and *Yerushalayim* is only that from *Tzion* strength is drawn into *Yerushalayim* [analogous to study *that leads* to action], and in wool and snow, the aspect of wool itself is drawn into the aspect of snow, as explained above (section 10) regarding the matter of "He gives snow like wool." Therefore, the elevation that is made in wool through its drawing into snow is a greater elevation than the elevation that is made in *Tzion* through its drawing into *Yerushalayim*, as mentioned above (there), that through the connection of wool and snow, the root of the soul is revealed as it is rooted in the *Atzmus*. It should be added that the elevation that is made in the higher through its drawing into the lower is also in the drawing of the aspect of snow and the aspect of wool into the revealed powers. For through the drawing of the soul that is above the internal powers (the aspect of snow or the aspect of wool) into the internal powers to rectify and fill the blemishes, an elevation is made in it. And so too is it in the internal powers (intellect and *midos*), that through their drawing into thought, speech, and action, an elevation is made in them. However, the primary matter of this (the elevation that is made in the higher through its descent into the lower) is when the higher acts to *change* the lower, for through this, even the action of the lower upon the higher is in a manner of change, that the elevation made in it through its descent into the lower is an incomparable elevation. Therefore, the primary matter of the superiority of the lower and the elevation that is made through it in the higher is in the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, for through the drawing of the essence of the soul (the aspect of snow or the aspect of wool) into the internal powers, a change is made in them, even to the transformation of willful sins into merits. Therefore, even the elevation that is made through this in the essence of the soul is an incomparable elevation.

12) This is "Look down from Your holy habitation, from the heavens, and bless Your people, Israel," and the maamar explains that the reason "Your people" is placed before "Israel" is because the primary revelation is in action, for "great is study, for it leads to action," and those who perform mitzvos transform the curse into a blessing, for the primary superiority of action is in the *avodah* of *teshuvah* that transforms willful sins (curse) into merits (blessing). It can be said that the three matters of "Hashem your Elokim" in the verse "did not want to listen to Bilaam, etc." explained in the maamar are the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* (the *avodah* of Torah and mitzvos), the *avodah* of *teshuvah* of the aspect of snow, and the *avodah* of *teshuvah* of the aspect of wool. The matter of "But Hashem your Elokim did not want to listen to Bilaam," that He does not want from the outset to listen to the accusers, is analogous to the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*. The matter of "and Hashem your Elokim turned the curse into a blessing for you," the transformation of willful sins into merits through the revelation of the *Havayah* of above that is above *Seder Hishtalshelus*, is analogous to the *avodah* of *teshuvah* of the aspect of snow—above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* that is in man. And the matter of "because Hashem your Elokim loved you," the essential love of the Ribono shel Olam for Israel, that even in a place where "Esau is a brother to Jacob," nevertheless, "and I loved Jacob" specifically, is analogous to the *teshuvah* of the aspect of wool—the rectification of the blemishes through the revelation of the essence of the soul, which even at the time of the sin (when he is like Esau) is "in faith with Him."

The maamar brings the three matters, including the matter of "did not want to listen," which is analogous to the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*, even though the primary matter of the superiority of the lower ("Your people") is in the *avodah* of *teshuvah* (as mentioned above), because the matter and the elevation in *teshuvah* (that it acts to change) is also in the performance of mitzvos (of the *tzaddikim*), as brought in the ma

## 18 Elul, 5730

"You have exalted Hashem today... and Hashem has exalted you today." The Gemara relates that the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to the Jewish people: "You have made Me a single entity in the world, as it is written, 'Hear O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One,' and I will make you a single entity in the world, as it is written, 'And who is like Your people Israel, a single nation on earth.'" We must understand the statement, "You have made Me a single entity." The meaning of "you have made Me" is that the fact that Hashem is "One" (a single entity) is brought about by the Jewish people. This is also understood from the comparison between "I will make you" and "you have made Me" (especially according to the version, "I, too, will make you"). Just as the meaning of "I will make you" is that the fact that the Jewish people are a "single nation" is brought about by the Holy One, Blessed be He—as the verse continues (after saying, "And who is like Your people Israel, a single nation on earth"), "that G-d went Himself to redeem for Himself a people," and Rashi explains, "And how are they distinguished from all the nations? By the fact that G-d went Himself to redeem for Himself a people"—so too is the meaning of "you have made Me," that the matter of "Hashem is One" is brought about by the Jewish people.

2) The aforementioned explanation of "exalted" (that "you have made Me a single entity in the world, and I will make you a single entity in the world") follows what is stated in the Gemara (earlier): "What is written in the tefillin of the Master of the World? ... 'And who is like Your people Israel, a single nation on earth.' Does the Holy One, Blessed be He, take pride in the praise of Israel? Yes, for it is written, 'You have exalted Hashem today,' and it is written, 'And Hashem has exalted you today.' The Holy One, Blessed be He, said to Israel: 'You have made Me a single entity in the world, and I will make you a single entity in the world.'" The explanation of this (the Gemara's question, "Does the Holy One, Blessed be He, take pride in the praise of Israel?") is that tefillin are called *pe'er* (glory), as it is written, "Bind your glory upon yourself," for tefillin bring glory and praise to the person who wears them. Likewise, the tefillin of the Master of the World bring Him, as it were, glory and praise. From this it is understood that "And who is like Your people Israel," which is written in the tefillin of the Master of the World, is the glory and praise of the Holy One, Blessed be He. This is why the Gemara asks, "Does the Holy One, Blessed be He, take pride in the praise of Israel?"—for this verse is the praise of Israel, so how can it be the glory and praise of the Holy One, Blessed be He? It answers, "Yes, for it is written, 'You have exalted Hashem,'" where *ha'amarta* (exalted) denotes importance and praise, meaning that Israel creates importance and praise in Hashem. We must understand: the proof from the verse "You have exalted Hashem" is (seemingly) only that Hashem is praised through the praises that Israel offers Him (Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One). Even though all created beings are of no value at all compared to Him, it arose in His will that through the praises Israel offers Him, importance and praise are brought into Him (as it were). How does this prove that the Holy One, Blessed be He, takes pride in the praise of Israel—specifically in the praise of Israel's own merit, that they are "a single nation on earth"? It must be said that through "You have exalted Hashem," where Israel praises Hashem and Hashem takes pride in this, it comes about that Hashem takes pride in the praise of Israel itself. Furthermore, the fact that the verse written in the tefillin of the Master of the World is (not "Hear O Israel... Hashem is One," as in our tefillin, but) "And who is like Your people Israel, a single nation on earth," proves that this praise of Hashem—that He takes pride in the praise of Israel—is a greater praise than the praise of "You have exalted Hashem" (the praise of Hashem through Israel's praising Him). Indeed, this praise (that He takes pride in the praise of Israel itself) is His *pe'er* (tefillin). We must also understand why the Tzemach Tzedek brings (in his maamar *Es Hashem He'emarta Hayom*) that there are two opinions regarding *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha*. The Rashba writes that *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha* are like "My beloved is mine and I am his," while the Maharsha writes that it is like "I am my beloved's and my beloved is mine." We must understand: the order of *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha* (*ha'amarta* and then *he'emircha*) is like "I am my beloved's" (and then) "and my beloved is mine." What is the Rashba's reasoning that *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha* are like "My beloved is mine and I am his"?

3) All of this will be understood by prefacing what the Tzemach Tzedek brings (in the aforementioned maamar) from the Bachya, that in the verse "You have exalted Hashem," there are fifteen words, corresponding to the fifteen items that were in the Mishkan. The Bachya states there that the Mishkan is a likeness of the creation of the world, and the reason for this in the creation of the world and in the Mishkan is to hint at what is written, "For in *Y-H* Hashem is the Rock of worlds." That is, the fifteen items in the Mishkan hint at *Y-H* (which has the numerical value of fifteen). From this, it is understood regarding the fifteen words in the verse "You have exalted Hashem" that they hint at *Y-H*. The Bachya continues there that corresponding to them (the fifteen items in the Mishkan) are fifteen instances of *tav-kuf* (500) in the seven heavens. The maamar explains that this is also the meaning of *va'eschanan* (and I pleaded), which has the numerical value of 515 (*tav-kuf-tet-vav*), fifteen times 500. According to what is explained elsewhere, the matter of *va'eschanan* in gematria 515 (where 500 and 15 are in one word) is the connection and unification of the level of 15 (*Y-H*) with the level of 500 (as follows). It can be said that the fact that there are fifteen words in the verse "You have exalted Hashem" (and likewise that there were fifteen items in the Mishkan) which hint at *Y-H* (as above), the intention is (not for the level of *Y-H* as it is by itself, but) for the level of *Y-H* as it is connected and unified with the level of 500. This will be understood according to the Sages (brought above) that the matter of "You have exalted Hashem" is "You have made Me a single entity," meaning "Hashem is One," for which there are two interpretations. The first interpretation is that "Hashem is One" is as the Arizal writes regarding the verse, "On that day Hashem will be One," that *Y-H* and *V-H* will be "bound in one unity," a connection of *mochin* and *midos*. The second interpretation is that "Hashem is One" is like "I am Hashem," where "I"—the essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof*—and the Name *Havayah* are absolutely one. This is what the fifteen words (gematria *Y-H*) in the verse "You have exalted Hashem" hint at: the level of *Y-H* as it is connected and unified with the level of 500. For even in the connection and unification of 15 with 500 (in the word *va'eschanan*) there are two interpretations, similar to the two interpretations above regarding "Hashem is One." The first interpretation is that 500 refers to the *midos* that are below the *mochin*. For the primary *midos* are the five *midos* from *Chesed* to *Hod*, and each one is comprised of ten, and ten of ten, in gematria 500. This is also why the matters in the world are in the number 500, for the root of created beings is from the *midos*. Accordingly, the matter of *va'eschanan* in gematria 515 (where 500 and 15 are in one word) is the connection of the *mochin* (15) with the *midos* (500), like the first interpretation of "Hashem is One." The second interpretation is that 500 refers to the *midos* of *Arich* that are above the *mochin*. The matter of 515 is to link and connect *Chochmah* and *Binah* (15) with the *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, similar to the second interpretation of "Hashem is One," that *Havayah* and "I" (the essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*) are absolutely one.

4) Accordingly, the connection of "You have exalted Hashem" to the tefillin of the Master of the World is also understood (for even though in the tefillin of the Master of the World it is written, "And who is like Your people Israel," which is the matter of "And Hashem has exalted you," the two matters of *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha* are connected to each other), for in the tefillin of the Master of the World there are also these two matters. Tefillin are four *mochin*, and the fact that the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin has two interpretations. First, that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is *Ze'er Anpin*, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, wearing tefillin is the drawing down of *mochin* into *Ze'er Anpin* (meaning, the essence of the *mochin* is drawn into *Ze'er Anpin*. For that which is drawn into the *midos* of *Ze'er Anpin* from the *mochin* as they are according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is only from the level of *mochin* that belong to the *midos*, and even this is through many, many *tzimtzumim*, until in their enclothement in the *midos* of *Ze'er Anpin* they are transformed into the essence of *midos*; for the *mochin* within the *midos* are, relative to the *mochin* themselves, the essence of *midos*. The matter of the Holy One, Blessed be He, wearing tefillin is that the essence of the *mochin* is drawn into the *midos* (*Ze'er Anpin*). This is why tefillin are called *pe'er*, that the Holy One, Blessed be He (*Ze'er Anpin*), is glorified by them, for *tiferes* is a matter of that which is incomparable). Second, that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is the essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above *Atzilus*, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, wearing tefillin is the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* into the *mochin*. (According to this interpretation, the matter of the *pe'er* of tefillin is understood even more, for the addition of light drawn into the *mochin* from the essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above *Atzilus* is completely incomparable). This is "You have exalted Hashem"—*ha'amarta* denotes importance and praise—for the fact that the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin (His glory and praise) is brought about by the *avodah* of Israel. This is "You have made Me a single entity" (*asitani*—specifically "you have made Me"), for from the perspective of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, as it is measured by the line of measure, the drawing down from above to below (from the *Matzil* to *Atzilus*, and likewise within *Atzilus* from the *mochin* to the *midos*) is limited according to the vessel of the lower one. In order for the Holy One, Blessed be He, to wear tefillin in the two interpretations above, which are similar to the two interpretations above regarding "Hashem is One"—the unification of *V-H* with *Y-H* and the unification of *Havayah* with "I"—this is brought about by the *avodah* of Israel: "You have made Me."

5) This should be connected with the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe (whose birthday is 18 Elul) on the verse, "And You are holy, enthroned upon the praises of Israel," that the Holy One, Blessed be He, from His own perspective is holy and separate, and through the praises of Israel—the fact that Israel praises and extols Him—He is "enthroned" and drawn down below. This is "You have exalted Hashem," that through Israel praising Him (the praises of Israel), it comes about that the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin, whereby light (from above *Atzilus* into *Atzilus*, and within *Atzilus* itself from the *mochin* into the *midos*) is drawn down not according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, and through this He is "enthroned" and drawn down below as well. For in the drawing down according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, when the light is drawn down and descends, it is diminished and contracted, until in this physical world it becomes a total concealment and hiding. This is not the case when the drawing down is not according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (for the root of this drawing down is from the inwardness and essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is above connection to the worlds, and this drawing down is specifically through the *avodah* of Israel, because the root of the souls of Israel is in the essence of the *Ohr Ein Sof*), for then the revelation is drawn down below as well.

6) This drawing down (that the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin) is (primarily) through the fulfillment of the mitzvah of tefillin. As the Sages say regarding the verse, "He declares His words to Jacob, His statutes and His judgments to Israel," what He does, He tells Israel to do. The explanation of this is known: that through Israel doing and fulfilling the mitzvot, they cause the Holy One, Blessed be He, to do these mitzvot. (Similar to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "Hashem is your shadow," that just as a shadow does what a person does, so too the Creator, Blessed be He, as it were, does what a person does). From this, it is understood regarding the mitzvah of tefillin—and the entire Torah (the mitzvot) is compared to tefillin—that the fact that the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin is brought about by the tefillin of Israel. This will be understood according to what is known, that the intention of the mitzvah of tefillin (and this intention is part of the mitzvah) is to subjugate the heart and the brain. The matter of subjugation—that one subjugates himself to *Elokus*—is like the mitzvah of *Krias Shema*, whose matter is the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven (the first paragraph) and the acceptance of the yoke of the mitzvot (the second paragraph). The matter of subjugation and the acceptance of the yoke is above intellect and emotion, and together with this, the subjugation of tefillin concerns specific powers (unlike the acceptance of the yoke of *Krias Shema*, which is general), for one subjugates his four *mochin* (*Chochmah*, *Binah*, and *Da'as* which is divided into *Chesed* and *Gevurah*), and this is drawn down into the *midos* in the heart as well—the subjugation of the heart. It can be said that by subjugating his *mochin* in the manner of the acceptance of the yoke, which is a drawing down from the essence of the soul (for the matter of the acceptance of the yoke is from the essence of the soul that is above *Hishtalshelus*) into the power of his intellect, through this the second matter (interpretation) of the Holy One, Blessed be He, wearing tefillin is brought about: the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* into the *mochin* above. And through this being drawn from the brain to the heart, the first matter (interpretation) of the Holy One, Blessed be He, wearing tefillin is brought about: the drawing down of *mochin* into *Ze'er Anpin*.

7) It should be added that through the drawing down of the acceptance of the yoke (above the *Hishtalshelus* that is in man) into the brain and heart, this is drawn down into all the powers, even into the lower powers. This is why the straps of the *tefillin shel rosh* must reach (below) the navel, so that even the matters of man that are "from the middle and below" will be subjugated to *Elokus*. Through this, one acts likewise in the world, that even in the lower matters (from the middle and below) there will be a revelation of *Elokus*. In addition to the fact that in tefillin the revelation of "One" is drawn down even into the physical parchment, etc.—for in *Krias Shema* the revelation of "Hashem is One" is in the person who recites *Krias Shema*, whereas in tefillin the drawing down is also into the physical parchment, etc. (and this is why the entire Torah is compared to tefillin, for the matter of Torah and mitzvot is to draw *Elokus* down below specifically, to be for Him a dwelling place in the lower worlds)—the revelation of tefillin acts even upon those who, by their own nature, are opposed to holiness. As it is written, "And all the peoples of the earth will see that the Name of Hashem is called upon you, and they will fear you," and the Sages say, "These are the tefillin of the head," for the drawing down through wearing tefillin acts even upon those in whom one must instill "and they will fear you" (because they are opposed). And not only that, but "they will see... that the Name of Hashem is called upon you." For the nations of the world (even those who acknowledge *Elokus*), their knowledge is only in the name *Elokim* (in gematria, *hateva*—nature), but they do not know the Name *Havayah* (which is above nature), just as Pharaoh said, "I do not know Hashem." Through Israel wearing tefillin, the revelation of *Havayah* (that is in the Jew who wears tefillin) is in such a way that even the peoples of the earth (and more than that, *all* the peoples of the earth, which includes those who by their own nature do not acknowledge *Elokus*, not even the name *Elokim*) see that the Name of Hashem is called upon you, and this sight acts upon them so that "they will fear you."

8) This should be connected with the revelation of the teachings of Chassidus, for 18 Elul is the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov, founder of the general teachings of Chassidus, and of the Alter Rebbe, founder of the teachings of Chabad Chassidus. One of the primary emphases in the teachings of Chassidus is that all matters should be drawn down below in revelation. As the Alter Rebbe writes in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* at the beginning, "It is written, 'Forever, Hashem, Your word stands in the heavens,' and the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, explained that 'Your word' which You said, 'Let there be a firmament in the midst of the waters,' etc.—these words and letters stand and remain forever within the firmament of the heavens, etc." Although this explanation is found in *Midrash Tehillim* on the verse (as brought in *Likutei Torah*), the Alter Rebbe writes, "And the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, explained it," for one of the explanations of this is that the Baal Shem Tov spread out and revealed this so that it would be known to all. The Alter Rebbe continued this with intellect, so that it would be for praise, for a name, and for glory—referring to Chabad—until it would be grasped even in the intellect of the animal soul, and even in the intellect of those who were (before they learned this matter) heretics, "to make you supreme over all the nations."

9) This is "You have exalted Hashem," "You have made Me a single entity in the world, as it is written, 'Hear O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One,'" for through Israel saying "Hashem is One" in *Krias Shema*, and especially in tefillin, where they draw "Hashem is One" down even into the physical parchment, through this the Holy One, Blessed be He, wears tefillin, which are (the tefillin) His glory and praise (as above)—*ha'amarta* denotes importance and praise. The reason for this—that it is in the power of Israel that through their fulfillment of the mitzvot there will be the fulfillment of the mitzvot of the Holy One, Blessed be He—continues in the verse, "And Hashem has exalted you... to be for Him a treasured people." This is why it concludes (in the verse "And Hashem has exalted you") "and to keep all His mitzvot" (even though, seemingly, this belongs to the verse "You have exalted Hashem," for the praise that Israel praises Hashem is that they accepted upon themselves to be for Him a G-d, etc., and to keep His statutes and His mitzvot, etc.), for keeping all His mitzvot of Israel brings about His mitzvot, that the Holy One, Blessed be He, will do the mitzvot. Therefore, this is said in the verse "And Hashem has exalted you" (in the praise that the Holy One, Blessed be He, praises Israel), for the fact that it is in the power of Israel to cause (through their fulfillment of the mitzvot) that there will be the mitzvot of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is a great praise for Israel. It can be said that this is what the Rashba meant, that the matter of *ha'amarta* and *he'emircha* is like "My beloved is mine and I am his" (at first "My beloved is mine" and then "I am his"), for the power in Israel to be "You have exalted Hashem," to add (as it were) importance and praise to Hashem, is through the fact that "Hashem has exalted you."

10) The fact that "Hashem has exalted you... to be for Him a treasured people" is not because of the reason, because of the merit of Israel, their fulfillment of Torah and mitzvot, and the like, but rather that this is how the Holy One, Blessed be He, chose in His (free) choice, as it is written, "For Hashem has chosen Jacob for Himself, Israel for His treasure." The fact that Israel is His treasure is because of His choice, and therefore, this is in the essence of Israel. For every single Jew (even before he fulfills Torah and mitzvot) is His treasure. Through this, a merit is also created in them (regarding the matter of revelations), for through their fulfillment of the mitzvot, the mitzvot of the Holy One, Blessed be He, are created. This is why in the tefillin of the Master of the World it is written (not the verse "Hear O Israel... Hashem is One," but) "And who is like Your people Israel," for the primary glory and praise of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is not the addition of light that is created above (the mitzvot of the Holy One, Blessed be He) that is created through the fulfillment of the mitzvot of Israel, but rather the praise of Israel itself, which specifically reaches the (choice of the) essence.

11) This should (also) be connected with 18 Elul, for in addition to the fact that (also) this matter (the greatness of the elevation of Israel and the love of Israel) is one of the primary matters of the teachings of Chassidus, 18 Elul is the day of the beginning of the *avodah* of the coming year, beginning from Rosh Hashanah, when Israel crowns the Holy One, Blessed be He, as King. The power that Israel has to crown Him as King is because they are connected and unified with His essence (which is above the level of King), and the Holy One, Blessed be He, accepts the coronation and becomes King of Israel, and through this and by them—(also) King over all the earth, "Hashem, G-d of Israel, is King, and His kingdom rules over all," and it is drawn down in revelation that He will be King of Israel *and their Redeemer*, through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, who will fight the wars of Hashem and be victorious and build the Temple in its place and gather the dispersed of Israel, and "the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem," the entire world, in the true and complete Redemption, very soon.

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Tavo, 18 Elul 5733

### B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Tavo, 18 Elul 5733

"Arise, shine, for your light has come..." The phrase "for your light has come" serves as the reason for "Arise, shine." Hashem is saying to Yisrael that since your light—the light of Yisrael—has already come, you must therefore arise and shine. We must understand the nature of these two lights: the light of Yisrael themselves, and the light they are required to shine. This can be understood based on the Yalkut, which states: Yisrael said before Hashem, "We made a Menorah for You in the days of Moshe and it was extinguished; in the days of Shlomo and it was extinguished. From here on, we wait only for Your light, as it is said, 'For with You is the source of life; in Your light we see light.'" And so Hashem said, "Arise, shine, for your light has come." From the fact that "Arise, shine, for your light has come" is compared to "In Your light we see light," it is understood that the two matters in the verse "Arise, shine, for your light has come" are analogous to the two matters in the verse "In Your light we see light."

2) This can be understood by prefacing what the Rebbe Rayatz explains in his maamar titled *Ki Imcha Mekor Chaim, B'Orcha Nireh Or*, that this verse contains four levels: *Chaim* (life), *Mekor Chaim* (source of life), *Orcha* (your light), and *Or* (light). These four levels are in order from below to above. *Chaim* is the Elokus vitality that is enclothed within the worlds, *Memalei Kol Almin* (filling all worlds). [It should be added that it is called *Chaim* in the plural because the vitality enclothed in the worlds and creations is in a state of manifold division, each creation according to its nature.] *Mekor Chaim* is the light of *Sovev Kol Almin* (surrounding all worlds). *Orcha* is Torah—"Torah is light"—which is even higher than *Sovev*. And the *Or* that is seen through *Orcha* is higher even than *Orcha*, to the point that *Orcha* is merely a preparation for the *Or* that is seen through it.

3) Now, in order to explain the superiority of *Orcha*, through which we will understand the greatness of the *Or* seen through *Orcha* (which is higher than *Orcha* itself), we must first explain the concept of *Mekor Chaim*, which has two interpretations. The reason it is called *Mekor Chaim* is that even the light of *Sovev*, being merely an illumination, is (at least) a source for the light of *Memalei* and, through it, for the vitality enclothed in the worlds. And *Mekor Chaim* refers to the light that is above the level of being a source for the vitality of *Memalei Kol Almin*. It is called *Mekor Chaim* because the vitality is found from it. [Similar to what is written in *Likkutei Torah* regarding Hashem being called *Tzur Chayeinu* (the Rock of our lives), where *Tzur* means the source and root of all roots of existence. The intent is not that He is a source, Heaven forbid, for existence, but that all the roots of existence are found from Him.] This is the meaning of "For with You is the source of life," where the word *Imcha* (with You) has two interpretations. The emphasis in *Imcha* can be that it is only *with You* and not *You*—something secondary and nullified to You. Or, the emphasis can be that it is not a separate entity, but rather *Imcha*—unified with Him, blessed be He. This is similar to what is said in the Midrash on the verse, "If you lend money to My people..."—"If you lend money... to My people; just as I am [merciful], so too you shall be [merciful]." It can be said that these two interpretations correspond to the two interpretations (above) of *Mekor Chaim*. According to the interpretation that *Mekor Chaim* is a source for life, the meaning of "For with You is the source of life" is that the matter of *Mekor Chaim* is only *with You* and not *You*—secondary and nullified to You. According to the interpretation that life is found from Him (but He is not in the category of a "source"), the meaning of "For with You is the source of life" is that the drawing down of life is only from *Imcha*—from the level of light that is unified with Him, blessed be He.

4) Now, even according to the interpretation that the intent of *Mekor Chaim* is that life is found from Him (and not that He is a source for them), the fact that it is called *Mekor Chaim* (the vitality of the worlds) proves that it has a connection to the worlds. This is why, after saying "For with You is the source of life," it adds "in Your light..." (as the order of the verse is from below to above, as mentioned). *Orcha* is above connection to the worlds. Therefore, it is called *Or* (light), for the nature of light is that it is attached to the *Maor* (the luminary) and is a derivative of the *Maor*. That is, it is not in the category of an independent existence, and consequently, it is not appropriate for it to be a source for anything; its entire essence is that it is a revelation of the *Maor*. The verse specifies *Orcha*—"Your light"—because in addition to the fact that light in general (even as it spreads outside the *Maor*) is entirely the spreading and revelation of the *Maor*, *Orcha* is specifically "your light"—the light of Yisrael, light that is included in His Essence. In general, this is the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum* (as explained in many places that the general light before the *Tzimtzum* is light included in His Essence).
