This light is above connection to the worlds, and therefore, for the worlds to come into existence, there had to be a withdrawal of the light. Regarding this, our Sages said, "Before the world was created, He and His Name alone existed." The light before the *Tzimtzum* (as the beginning of creation is the *Tzimtzum*, and before the world was created is before the *Tzimtzum*) is called "His Name." Just as a person's name is not an existence at all (not even like the existence of light) and its entire essence is that *the person* turns to those who call him by his name, so too is it with the light before the *Tzimtzum*: it is not in the category of an existence, and its entire essence is only that it is "His Name"—He and His Name alone.

5) It is known that in the *Ohr Ein Sof* before the *Tzimtzum* there are (in general) two levels: the essence of the light and the spreading of the light. Within the spreading of the light itself, there are two general levels: the revelation to Himself, which is the root of *Ohr Sovev*, and the revelation that pertains to the worlds (for although the general light before the *Tzimtzum* is included in His Essence, within His Essence itself there is a revelation that pertains to the worlds), which is the root of *Ohr Memalei*. According to the principle that the drawing down of light from above is not by way of necessity, Heaven forbid, and even the drawing down of the light before the *Tzimtzum* (even the revelation to Himself, which is above the revelation pertaining to the worlds) is for the sake of some intent for the worlds, it follows that the two levels of *Sovev* and *Memalei* after the *Tzimtzum* are drawn from the two revelations (revelation to Himself and revelation pertaining to the worlds) before the *Tzimtzum* in such a way that the revelations before the *Tzimtzum* *pertain* to the levels after the *Tzimtzum*. From this it is understood that even the light before the *Tzimtzum* is included in *Mekor Chaim*, and *Orcha* (which is above *Mekor Chaim*) is even more exalted than the light before the *Tzimtzum*. It can be said that this is what is explained in the maamar, that *Orcha* refers to Torah ("Torah is light"), for the Torah is not for the sake of the worlds; on the contrary, the existence of all the worlds (including the revelations before the *Tzimtzum*, which are for the sake of the worlds) is for the sake of the Torah.

6) The verse continues, "In Your light we see light," which is higher even than *Orcha*, to the point that *Orcha* is merely a preparation for the *Or* that is seen through it (as mentioned from the maamar). The explanation for this can be given based on what is known regarding Torah and the souls of Yisrael: the root of Yisrael is higher than the root of the Torah. As it is stated in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu*: "Two things preceded the world: Torah and Yisrael. I do not know which of them preceded the other. When it says, 'Command the Children of Yisrael,' 'Speak to the Children of Yisrael,' I say that Yisrael preceded." However, the souls of Yisrael were drawn down and descended into the category of a separate existence, like a son ("You are children to Hashem your G-d") who, despite being from the essence of the father, is a separate existence, whereas the Torah, even as it is drawn down below, is unified with Him, blessed be He—"The Torah and the Holy One, blessed be He, are all one." This is the reason why the superiority of Yisrael (who preceded the Torah) is revealed through the Torah (for in the Torah it says "Command the Children of Yisrael," "Speak to the Children of Yisrael"), because the souls, as they are in themselves, being a separate existence, have their root in concealment. Not so the Torah, which is one with Hashem; it is in a category of revelation ("Torah is light"), and through the Torah, the root of Yisrael is (also) revealed.

7) This is "Arise, shine, for your light has come"—these two matters (*Ori* and *Orcha*) are analogous to the two matters in "In Your light we see light" (as mentioned at the beginning of the maamar). *Orcha*—the light of Yisrael themselves—is like "In Your light" (your light), and "Arise, shine"—the light that Yisrael shine—is like the light that is seen through *Orcha* (which is higher than *Orcha*). This can be understood based on what is explained in other places regarding the soul and the body: regarding souls, it is written, "You are children to Hashem your G-d," and therefore, the love and connection of Hashem to Yisrael due to their souls is like a *natural* love, so to speak (like the love of a father for his son). That is, the root of this love is from a level where there is a perception of the place of the beloved, and it is not from His Essence truly. Not so the love and connection of Hashem to Yisrael due to their bodies; it is (not due to the superiority of the body, nor the superiority of being a "son"—an essential superiority—but) due to the fact that Hashem *chose* the body of Yisrael with His free choice, and this choice is from His Essence truly. However, the superiority of the soul (which is a son to Hashem) is in revelation, whereas the superiority of the body (in which is the choice of the Essence) is in concealment. By the soul working with the body, its superiority—the choice of the Essence—is revealed.

Based on this, one can explain "Arise, shine, for your light has come": *Orcha* is the light of the soul, and "Arise, shine" means that through the light of the soul ("for your light has come"), it must work within the body and illuminate it, through which a matter higher than the light of the soul (*Orcha*) is revealed, similar to what was stated above (Section 2) regarding "In Your light we see light," that the light seen through *Orcha* is higher than *Orcha*.

8) The Rebbe Rayatz explains in his maamar *Ki Imcha Mekor Chaim* mentioned above that the verse "For with You is the source of life..." is a statement of the Community of Yisrael to Hashem during the time of exile. During the time of exile, the thirst for Elokus is greater than during the time of the Beis Hamikdash, as per the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov (whose birthday is 18 Elul) on the verse, "My soul thirsts for You, my flesh longs for You in a dry and weary land without water; so I have gazed upon You in the Sanctuary." "My soul thirsts for You" is during the time of exile (in a dry and weary land without water), and regarding this it says, "So I have gazed upon You in the Sanctuary"—would that I could gaze upon You in the Sanctuary. During the time of exile, the Community of Yisrael says to Hashem, "Master of the Universe, 'For with You is the source of life; in Your light we see light'—with You, Master of the Universe, is the source of life; with Your light we see light." Based on what was explained above in Section 1 (based on the Yalkut) that "Arise, shine, for your light has come" is like "In Your light we see light," it can be said that Hashem's statement to the Community of Yisrael, "Arise, shine, for your light has come" [even though the plain meaning of "for your light has come" (that it has already come) implies that it speaks of the time of the Redemption], is (also) for the time of exile. That is, even during the time of exile, and especially in the final days of the exile, the matter of "Arise, shine, for your light has come" is possible and necessary, both regarding the light of the soul (*Orcha*) and regarding the soul illuminating the body ("Arise, shine"). Through our deeds and our *avodah* during the time of exile, and especially through the matter of "Arise, shine, for your light has come," we bring closer and hasten even more the future Redemption, when "Arise, shine, for your light has come" will be fulfilled literally (that it has already come), and in a manner of swiftness, as the conclusion and seal of the Haftorah—"I will hasten it."

## By the Grace of Hashem. Eve of the second day of Parshas Nitzavim-Vayelech, 18 Elul, 5739 

(Draft)
**You** are standing today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d: your heads, your tribes, etc., to enter into the covenant of Hashem your G-d, etc. And afterwards it continues (in the second portion, the Chumash lesson for this day): "And not with you alone do I make this covenant, etc., but with [those who are here] and with [those] who are not here with us today," and Hashem your G-d will return, etc. Now, this parsha is always read before Rosh Hashanah (as stated by the Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah). The teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is well known: that "You are standing" is the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, with which He blesses His people, the Children of Israel, on Shabbos Mevarchim—the final Shabbos of the month of Elul—with the blessing of the month of Tishrei. Through this power, Israel blesses the months of the entire year; from this it is understood that this matter ("You are standing," etc.) is a general, all-encompassing concept. The matter is as follows: the verse explains that the fact that "you are standing today, all of you," all ten levels —from your heads, your tribes, down to your woodchoppers and your water-drawers—"as one", is in order "to enter into the covenant of Hashem your G-d," etc. Before they entered the Land (when this parsha was first stated), there was a covenant made regarding the acceptance of the Torah, in addition to the covenant He made with them at Chorev. That is to say, this refers to a special covenant made before entering the Land. And since "not with you alone do I make this covenant" (but also with those who are not here with us today), it is understood that this matter of the covenant before entering the Land is relevant to the avodah of every single individual.

2) This can be understood by first explaining the concept of entering the Land in terms of avodah. It is written (in the parsha of last week, from which all subsequent days are blessed, including this day, 18 Elul): "And it shall be, when you come into the Land which Hashem your G-d gives you," etc. The Baal Shem Tov explains (in the Torah discourse delivered by the Rebbe Rayatz, who heard it from his father, the Rebbe Rashab, who heard it from the Baal Shem Tov): "And it shall be, when you come into the Land"—when you reach the [Supernal] *ratzon* (will) and *merutza* (running/desire); "which Hashem your G-d gives you as an inheritance and you possess it"—this is a *matana* (gift) from above as an inheritance to every Jew, and there must be avodah within it; "and you dwell therein"—this must be with *hityashvus* (settledness); "and you shall take, etc., and put it in a basket"—this is the *malbish* (clothing) of the *oros* (lights) into *keilim* (vessels); "and you shall go to the place"—this is the concept of *hashgacha pratis* (Divine Providence); "which Hashem your G-d shall choose"—when a Jew goes to a place, it is not that he is going on his own, but rather he is being led by Supernal Providence. So, when he arrives at a place, the *kavanah* (intention) is "to cause His name to dwell there"—to publicize *Elokus* in the world. Afterwards, the Baal Shem Tov repeated the previous Torah discourse and added that the matter of "causing His name to dwell there" is "with a blessing and a verse of Tehillim." The Maggid explained: "And it shall be, when you come into the Land"—this means when you desire to come to the Supernal Land (the World to Come) "which Hashem your G-d gives you," for all Israel has a share in the World to Come, "and you possess it"—to possess it as an eternal inheritance so that one will not need to be reincarnated (G-d forbid), but rather "and you dwell therein" in an eternal and everlasting dwelling. Thus you shall conduct yourself and merit: "And you shall take from the first," etc.—meaning, the first of your taking from the pleasures of this world should be from the "first," which is *Chochma*, as it is said, "The beginning (*reishis*) is *Chochma*," etc. This means that all matters of this world have a holy spark mixed within them, which is *Chochma*. Therefore, all your taking and your actions should have as their primary focus and goal the "first" within them, which is the holy *Chochma* therein. That is why it says "from the first" and not "all the first", because the whole of it is physicality, only that it contains a bit of holiness, which is the *reishis*. And that is what it says, "from the first of all the fruit of the ground," which are the sparks within the vegetation. And it is not only that you must seek to clarify [the sparks] from the vegetation, but even "which you bring from your land"—meaning, even from a thing that is complete earthliness, which is the *domem* (inanimate), which is more physical than vegetation. The sparks within animals are not mentioned here because they can be easily elevated to holiness, as is explained in the writings of the AriZal. Furthermore, do not say that I am warning you only regarding physical things, which are inanimate, vegetation (and animal), but even regarding spiritual things, which are words of Torah. And that is what it says, "which Hashem your G-d gives you," etc.—your *kavanah* should be desirable, your thought pure, and your speech complete, so that in every word that comes out of your mouth, every letter, its vowels, and its cantillation marks should be evident. And that is what it says, "and you shall put it in a basket (*tana*)," for *tana* is an acronym for *te'amim* (cantillation marks), *nekudos* (vowels), *osiyos* (letters). It does not mention *tagin* (crowns) here, because they are not articulated. And when you conduct yourself thus—meaning, that in all these matters there will be the concept of "taking from the first," the level of *Chochma*—then "you shall go to the place," etc., and you will elevate everything to holiness. This is "which Hashem your G-d shall choose," and this is "to cause His name to dwell there." And this is why the verse opens with the word *v'hayah* ("and it shall be"), which is an expression of joy. The Alter Rebbe explained (in Likutei Torah, Parshas Ki Savo) that just as there is a level of Eretz Yisrael in the world, so too is there in the year, and that is on Rosh Hashanah; and prior to this, there must be a covenant, etc.

3) To understand all this, it is known that the source of all things in the world is in the Torah, and so it is regarding Eretz Yisrael (and the entry into Eretz Yisrael), that this level exists in the Torah. As the Alter Rebbe explains at length (in Torah Or, at the beginning, and in Likutei Torah there), Eretz Yisrael is the level of the Oral Torah. For *eretz* (land) is a term for *ratzon* (will) and *merutza* (running/desire) (as brought in the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov mentioned above), and as the saying goes, "Why is it called *eretz*? Because it desired (*ratzta*) to do the will of its Creator." And the revelation of the Supernal Will is specifically through the Oral Torah. For in order to fulfill the Supernal Will, study of the Written Torah is not sufficient; for although "there is nothing that is not hinted at in the Torah", this is only by way of a hint, and there can be two opinions from it, for "both these and those are the words of the living G-d". It is specifically through the *halacha pesuka* (decided law) and clear legal ruling in the Oral Torah that one can know and fulfill the Supernal Will.

4) With this, we can understand the matter of the covenant made before entering Eretz Yisrael, which is the Oral Torah. For the concept of the Oral Torah is the connection of the highest of the high with the lowest of the low. The *halacha* originates from the Supernal Will, which is far above the level of *Chochma* (which is the Torah in its simple sense), and it is the level of "and Hashem was with him", that the *halacha* follows him (which is above not only the level of *Elokim*, but even above the level of "both these and those are the words of the living G-d," for "living G-d" is the level of *Binah*, as explained in the discourses of the Tzemach Tzedek and the Rebbe Maharash, and the subsequent Nesi'im, their successors, who explain the concept of "living G-d"). From there, it is drawn down into a legal ruling for practical *halacha* in this world. As the Alter Rebbe explains in Iggeres HaKodesh, the parable of the fulfillment of *mitzvos* is like a pillar connecting the roof to the floor. In the language of Kabbalah and Chassidus, this is the connection of *sovev kol almin* (that which encompasses all worlds) and *memalei kol almin* (that which fills all worlds). It is known that for this connection, there must be an *hemshech* (drawing down) from a place that is above both of them, and this is the concept of the covenant.

5) From this, we can understand the concept of the covenant on the level of the *nefesh*. Just as the concept of the covenant, in its simple sense, is that it draws down from a matter that is above *ta'am* (reason) and *da'as* (intellect)—which is why no change can ever occur in it, and so it shall stand, and through this, opposites are unified, as explained in Likutei Torah that by passing between the pieces, they become "as one" —similarly, one can understand the covenant in the *nefesh*: that for the sake of unifying the hidden and the revealed within the *nefesh*, there must be the concept of the covenant, which is the *hemshech* from the highest place in the *nefesh* (similar to the above regarding Torah).

6) This is also the concept of the covenant on the level of the world before the entry into the Land in its literal sense, for "you shall come into the Land," etc., "and you shall possess it and dwell therein." It is explained in many places that the entry into Eretz Yisrael was the descent from the world of thought or the world of speech to the world of action—a descent down to the "land that consumes its inhabitants". And since there needed to be the connection of the highest of the high with the lowest of the low, there had to be, prior to this, a special covenant, separate from the covenant He made with them at Chorev. For even after the covenant at Chorev, they were still a "generation of knowledge" (a level of thought or a level of speech). Not so here; there had to be the descent to the lowest of the low, until they brought it about that the Land was "very, very good". For this, there had to be a special covenant.

7) Now, just as there is the concept of a covenant in the *nefesh* and in the world, so too is it in the year. For Rosh Hashanah is the level of entry into Eretz Yisrael in the year, and every year before Rosh Hashanah, there must be a renewal of the covenant. The matter is that Rosh Hashanah is the perfection of man's avodah, for then the Holy One, Blessed be He, says, "Make Me King over you" (for the decision regarding the creation of the world is through the souls of Israel, as the saying goes, "With whom did He consult? With the souls of the righteous," and "Your people are all righteous", as explained at length in the teachings of the Maggid in *Ohr Torah* and in the beginning of *Likutei Amarim*, that because the *taanug* (delight) from the avodah of the righteous ascended before Him, etc., like the parable of a father who pictures his young son, etc. And so it is every Rosh Hashanah, that the coronation is specifically through Israel), and through this comes the decision to be King over the entire world. And from the decision on Rosh Hashanah, it is drawn down to all the days of the year. That is why it is called *Rosh* (Head) Hashanah and not the *beginning* of the year, as explained at length in *Ateres Rosh* at the beginning, that it is like the head which includes all the limbs, and even afterwards, when the limbs are each in their place, the head is what leads them. So it is on Rosh Hashanah, which leads all the days of the year, until it is drawn down into actual deed. This is the concept of an *hemshech* from the extremity to the extremity. And also, the general matter of the decision to be King is drawn down through the crowning by the souls of Israel, who are themselves rooted above even the Torah, and from there it is drawn down below specifically through a legal ruling in the Torah—that is, the instructions in the Torah regarding practical action. For in order to arrive at a true legal ruling, one must toil to arrive at the truth of truth (as explained in the *hemshech* of Yom Tov of Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos, by the Rebbe [Rashab], and in the discourses of the Rebbe Rayatz, his successor). All of this is an *hemshech* from the highest extremity to the lowest extremity. Therefore, there must be, prior to this, the matter of a special covenant, for through the covenant, all the Children of Israel (and "Your people are all righteous") become one with the *Atzmus* (Essence) and *Mahus* (Being), similar to the covenant in its simple, physical sense.

8) From the covenant in general, good resolutions are drawn down regarding Torah study, the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and the avodah of *tefillah*, for through this, Israel and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are all one. And from this comes a good writing and sealing for a good and sweet year. Its beginning is beforehand, in the month of preparation, which is the month of Elul—the acronym for *Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li* ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"). Especially from 18 Elul, which is the birthday of the two great luminaries, when their *mazal* (fortune/influence) is strengthened. Their purpose and intention was that "your springs be spread outward," even to the furthest "outside," beyond which there is no "outside." And through this, *ati mar* —the King Moshiach will come, very soon, in our days.

## Shabbos Parshas Nitzavim-Vayelech, 23 Elul 5739

"You are standing today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d: your heads, your tribes, your elders, and your officers, all the men of Israel, your young children, your wives, and your convert who is within your camp, from the hewer of your wood to the drawer of your water." It is stated in *Likutei Torah* that we always read this parsha before Rosh Hashanah. This is hinted at by the word "today," which refers to Rosh Hashanah, for this is "the beginning of Your works, a remembrance of the first day." This is the meaning of "You are standing today, *all of you*": that all the children of Israel—from your heads and tribes down to the hewer of wood and drawer of water—unite together to become one. For the vessel for the blessings and the *hemshech* (drawings down) from Above is the concept of unity, as it is written, "Bless us, our Father, [as] we are all as one." (This is explained at length in *Tanya*, Chapter 32; *Likutei Torah*, *d'h* "Hachalzu"; and in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvas Ahavas Yisrael*). Since Rosh Hashanah is the time for the *hemshech* of *chayus* (vitality) for the entire year—as is known (and explained at length in *Etz Chaim*, and hinted at in *Likutei Torah*)—it is called *Rosh* Hashanah (Head of the Year) rather than the "beginning of the year." Just as the head contains all the limbs of the body, and just as the limbs are in their places while the head is present within them and leads them (for all the limbs obey its will), so too is it with the "today" of Rosh Hashanah. On this day, the entire *chayus* for all the days of the year is drawn down, and the subsequent conduct of the year is according to the manner in which it was drawn down on Rosh Hashanah. (The same applies to a person’s *avodah*: one’s conduct throughout the year is according to the resolutions made on Rosh Hashanah). This is "You are standing today, all of you": the preparation and the vessel for this *hemshech* is "all of you"—the unity of the children of Israel becoming one, through which they become vessels for the indwelling of His *yichud* (oneness).

The verse details ten levels ("your heads, your tribes... from the hewer of your wood to the drawer of your water"). Just as there are ten levels in the human soul—the three *sechalim* (intellects) and seven *midos* (emotions)—so too are all of Israel one complete *komah* (stature) divided into ten levels. The point is that the unity of the children of Israel—where they unite to become one, thereby becoming vessels for the indwelling of His *yichud*—is not in a way that lacks distinctions between levels (nor does it mean that they lose their sense of self due to the revelation of the level of *Yachid*). Rather, even while they are in a state of existence and divided into ten levels, they are nevertheless united in a complete unity. This unity (the unity of particulars) is like the unity of the level of *Echad* (One), which is lower than the level of *Yachid* (Unique/Single). As is known, the difference between *Echad* and *Yachid* is that *Yachid* is above division, whereas *Echad* implies that there are distinct things that are united. This is hinted at in the letters of the word *Echad*: the *Chet* and *Dalet* point to the seven heavens, the earth, and the four directions of the world, all of which are *batel* (nullified) to the *Aleph*. The *Aleph* does not negate the existence of the world; rather, the *Aleph* itself means *Alufo shel Olam* (the Master/Champion of the world). The *Aleph* is the head of the word *Echad*, which includes (as mentioned regarding the "head") the *Chet* (seven heavens and earth) and the *Dalet* (four directions). Through this unity of the children of Israel—who are in a state of existence and divided into ten levels, yet together are "one"—they become a *reshus hayachid* (a private domain) for His *yichud*, meaning for the level of *Yachid* (which is above the level of *Echad*). This is the revelation of the level of *Yachid* that is drawn down into the level of *Chai HaOlamim Melech* (Life of the Worlds, King), reaching even into the existence and division of the levels, down to the level of the "hewer of wood and drawer of water." On the contrary, through the unity of the children of Israel—even as they are divided into ten levels down to the hewer of wood and drawer of water—they become one with His *Atzmus* (Essence).

This is what the verse continues: "to enter into the covenant." ("To enter into the covenant" is an explanation of what was written previously: "You are standing today, all of you," and as it is stated in *Likutei Torah*, this explains the path of *yichud*, the meaning of *teshuvah*, and why it is specifically on Rosh Hashanah). As explained in *Likutei Torah*, it is like two lovers who make a covenant between them, binding themselves to one another as if they had become one flesh. This is the manner of the covenant-making, as it is written, "who cut the calf and passed between its parts"—the fact that both pass through one body indicates that they have become one flesh. *Likutei Torah* emphasizes that they became "one *flesh*," and that they both pass through "one *body*," because the *yichud* of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with the children of Israel is also through the physical body. On the contrary, from the perspective of the intent of *dirah b'tachtonim* (a dwelling in the lower realms)—a dwelling for His *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (Essence and Being)—it is specifically in the lower realms. As it is written, "I have come into My garden," and our Sages say, "into My *ginuni* (bridal chamber)..." The essence of the *Shechinah* was in the lower realms; it is specifically in the lower realms that there is the level of *gan* (garden) and *ginuni* (bridal chamber). The concept of a garden points to His pleasure and delight, so to speak, and this pleasure and delight is specifically in the lower realms. The matter is as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, *d'h* "Ihu V'chayohi Chad," that the creation of the *yesh nivra* (created existence) is through the power of the *Atzmus*, whose existence is from His *Atzmus* and is not caused by any prior cause, *chas v'shalom*. Therefore, the revelation of the *Atzmus* is specifically in the *yesh nivra* (not in His *chayohi* or *grumohi*). As explained in *Beurei HaZohar*, the true existence of the *yesh nivra* (what appears as *yesh*) is the *Yesh HaAmiti* (True Existence). Therefore, the covenant and the bonding of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with Israel is primarily in the body of the Jew, as explained in the well-known *sicha* regarding the connection of the *Atzmus* specifically to the physical body.

This is the meaning of saying before the *Malchiyos* (Kingship verses), "Make Me King over you." His *Atzmus* *be'et zich* (so to speak) in all Jews and in every single Jew, that "you shall make Me King over you." Even though He "consulted" with the souls of the *tzaddikim*—meaning the pleasure that He would have, so to speak, in the *avodah* of the souls ascended before Him, and this pleasure existed even before the creation, as taught by the Maggid in *Likkutei Amarim* and *Or Torah* at their beginning—nevertheless, He asks, "Make Me King over you." For although He consulted with the souls of the *tzaddikim*, the ultimate intent is the *avodah* of the souls within bodies. Through this, "Make Me King over you" is accomplished, to awaken the revelation of the inner aspect of His *Malchus* from His *Atzmus* and *Mahus*.

This is "to enter into the covenant," that every year before Rosh Hashanah there must be a renewal of the covenant regarding the acceptance of the Torah, which is similar to the covenant that existed before entering the Land of Israel for the first time, in addition to the covenant He made with them at Chorev. For at the time of the covenant at Chorev, the Israelites were *tzaddikim*, but after the descent (caused by sin), there was a need to "enter into the covenant of Hashem your G-d," which is the level of *teshuvah*. This covenant (of "entering into the covenant") that comes after the descent—and "a descent is for the sake of an ascent"—is loftier than the covenant made at Chorev. For "to enter into the covenant" is that those making the covenant pass between the parts "within one body," which is the concept of the connection of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with Israel, where they become truly one. This reaches the point where even the body of the Jew is unified with His *Atzmus* (as mentioned above), and from this connection comes "My heart said to You, 'Seek My face'; Your face, Hashem, I will seek" (in such a way that my face—the Jew's—and Your face, Hashem, become one), which is the *avodah* of *teshuvah* (which is higher than the *avodah* of *tzaddikim*). The concept of *teshuvah* is above measurement and limitation, above the limitation of time—which is why *teshuvah* can happen in a single hour and a single moment—and above the limitation of place (including the limitation of spiritual place, where "place" in spirituality means a level or rank). Therefore, even when one is at the lowest level (due to sins, etc.), *teshuvah* is effective. This is what the verse continues: "And Hashem your G-d will return your captivity." It does not say "He will return" (*v'heshiv*), but "He will return" (*v'shav*—He will return with them). For because of the covenant of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with Israel, where they have become truly one, and also because of the body of the Jew, which is a "holy nation" and in the ultimate state of holiness, wherever a Jew is—even if he is "at the ends of the heavens"—His *Atzmus* and *Mahus* are there, since they are truly one. Therefore, it does not say *v'heshiv*, but *v'shav*.

This is "You are standing today, all of you," that all the sparks of the souls (from your heads and tribes down to the hewer of wood and drawer of water) are standing and ascending to their original source, "before Hashem," until they become truly one with the "before Hashem" (as mentioned regarding "entering into the covenant")—"Israel and the King are one." Through this, they are also "standing" (as the Baal Shem Tov explains), meaning they are enduring and firm, which means they are victorious in judgment. This applies not only to spiritual matters ("the judgment of the G-d of Yaakov") but also to physical matters ("the portion of Israel"). On the contrary, the essence of the judgment on Rosh Hashanah (and the victory in judgment) is regarding physical matters, so that every Jew will have a good and sweet writing and sealing for a good year, in the revealed and manifest good, with children, life, and sustenance, and in all of them, in abundance.

## B’s”d. The Night of the Third Day of Selichos, 5720

### B’s”d. The Night of the Third Day of Selichos, 5720

"To You, my heart has said, 'Seek My face,' etc." The Rebbe Rayatz brings in his maamar, *Zeh*, Rashi’s commentary on this verse, noting that there are two interpretations of the word *Lecha* (To You): "For You" (in Your service) and "In Your place." The maamar continues that there are also two interpretations of *Bakshu Panai* (Seek My face): *Bakshu* as a request and supplication, and *Bakshu* as a request and search. It explains that these two matters (request/supplication and request/search) are both found in tefillah. Tefillah is a request and supplication, while the "search" is the request that one succeed in his avodah to search for and find ways to rectify all his affairs. This is the meaning of "To You, my heart has said, 'Seek My face'"—specifically the *heart*, because both aspects of "Seek My face" are in tefillah (as above), and tefillah is "avodah of the heart." The maamar adds that there are two aspects to avodah of the heart: avodah *within* the heart and avodah *with* the heart. It can be said that these two aspects correspond to the two interpretations of "Seek My face." The request and supplication in tefillah come through avodah *within* the heart; for one’s request and supplication to be genuine, he must stir his heart—this is avodah within the heart itself. The "search" in tefillah (how to rectify all his affairs) is avodah *with* the heart. That is, the avodah is not *in* the heart, but in all his affairs, yet this avodah is performed *by means of* the heart.

2) To explain this, the maamar introduces the verse, "And from my flesh I shall see Elokah." One must understand: the essence is the soul, so why say "from my *flesh*"? It explains that there are two modes of vision: intellectual vision and sensory vision. Intellectual vision relates more to the soul, while sensory vision relates more to the body. This distinction applies also to the object being seen, for every thing has a body and a soul—even physical things have a soul within them, and even spiritual things have a body within them. Therefore, it says "from my *flesh* I shall see Elokah," because the intent of "seeing Elokah" is sensory vision in Elokus; there are matters of Elokus, such as Divine Providence, that can be seen tangibly. The maamar continues in its interpretation of "from my flesh I shall see Elokah," that the powers of the human soul are drawn down from the Sefiros above, as it is written, "Let Us make man in Our image, after Our likeness," and therefore, from the powers of the human soul, one can understand the Sefiros above.

The maamar continues (after explaining at length the matter of "from my flesh I shall see Elokah") that for there to be an arousal of the emotions in the heart, there must be preparation for it. Even though the arousal of the emotions in the heart comes through contemplation, nevertheless, for the light of the intellect to shine into the heart and arouse the emotions, there must be preparation for this from the side of the heart as well. The preparation is the bitterness felt before tefillah. When one contemplates the ultimate purpose of his soul’s descent below—which is a descent for the sake of an ascent, so that through its avodah in Torah and mitzvos it will ascend to a higher level than it was before its descent—and then considers how he actually conducts himself, that not only is he not engaging in Torah and mitzvos as he should (so the ascent of the soul through the descent is not complete), but through his undesirable actions he lowers his soul even further below; and especially when he contemplates the parable of one holding the king’s head, etc., he will come to great bitterness. Through this bitterness, the "plowing" of the soil of his heart is accomplished, making it ready for a genuine arousal (through contemplation) of the emotions in the heart.

The maamar continues that this applies throughout the entire year, and especially in the month of Elul, which is the time of the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy,. The revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy in Elul is for everyone, even for those who are furthest away. This is like the parable of the King in the field, when everyone who wishes is permitted and able to greet Him (and present their requests to Him), and He receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all. [It should be added that although the explanation in the maamar regarding the virtue of Elul follows the subject of bitterness—that since Elul is the time of the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy even for the distant, it is a most auspicious time to plow the soil of one’s heart through bitterness—the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy in Elul should also add to the matter of joy. Since in Elul the King shows a smiling face to all, this should arouse (like water reflecting a face) additional joy in the service of the King.] The maamar concludes that the interpretation of "To You, my heart has said" as "For You and in Your service" means that the heart is for Him, may He be blessed, to fulfill His will to make the lower world a dwelling place for Him. And the interpretation of "To You, my heart has said" as "In Your place" refers to the point of Yiddishkeit that exists in every single Jew, which is connected to the Essence.

3) To understand the explanation of the two interpretations of "To You, my heart has said" and their connection to the matters explained in the maamar (the matter of "from my flesh I shall see Elokah," and that for there to be an arousal of emotions in the heart there must be preparation, etc.), we must preface what the Maggid said in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: that in every word of the words of tefillah, there are three levels: Worlds, Souls, and Elokus. Based on this, it can be said regarding "Seek My face" that the avodah of "Seek My face" is in tefillah, which consists of these three levels. In the word *Panai* (My face) in this verse, there are three interpretations. According to Rashi’s interpretation of "To You, my heart has said," that the heart speaks in His service or in His place, *Panai* refers to His face, the inwardness of Elokus. The Alter Rebbe explains that the heart saying "Seek My face" refers to one’s own inwardness, the inwardness of the heart, the inwardness of the souls. And there is another interpretation of "Seek My face," that *Panai* refers to Atzilus, because the four levels—Face and Back, Right and Left—are the four worlds of ABYA [Back – Asiyah, Left – Yetzirah, Right – Beriah, and Face – Atzilus], the inwardness of the worlds.

4) Now, regarding the matter of *Panai* (Face), in each of these three levels there are two general degrees: an inwardness that has a connection to the outwardness, and an inwardness that is truly distinct from the outwardness. Regarding the Worlds, this is Atzilus and that which is above Atzilus. As the Tzemach Tzedek writes in explanation of the verse, "Seek My face; Your face, Hashem, I will seek," "Seek My face" is to draw down Chochma, Atzilus, and "Your face, Hashem, I will seek" is to draw down the Face of Hashem, the lights of Arich and Atik. The difference between Atzilus and that which is above Atzilus is that Atzilus is included in the four worlds, yet it is their "Face," an inwardness that belongs to the outwardness; whereas that which is above Atzilus is above the worlds, an inwardness that is distinct from the outwardness. The same applies to the inwardness of the heart, the "face" of the souls, which contains the equivalent of these two degrees. As explained in *Likutei Torah* on the maamar *Ki Seitzei LaMilchama Al Oyvecha* (When you go out to war against your enemies), there are two degrees in the inwardness of the heart: the illumination of the point of the heart and the essence of the point of the heart. Both degrees are from Atzilus [this is the difference between the outwardness of the heart and the inwardness of the heart: the outwardness of the heart is from BYA, and the inwardness of the heart is from Atzilus. This is why the outwardness of the heart is according to reason and knowledge, while the inwardness of the heart is above reason and knowledge, for in Beriah there is the matter of comprehension, "Imma nests in the Throne," and Atzilus in general is Chochma, for the true essence of Chochma is above intellect]. However, the illumination of the point of the heart is from the Atzilus that is within BYA, and the essence of the point of the heart is from Atzilus itself. Just as above, the aspect of Atzilus that is in BYA is only an *illumination* of Atzilus, so too in the human soul, this level is only an *illumination* of the point of the heart. Thus, the illumination of the point of the heart is what shines from the inwardness of the heart to the outwardness of the heart (analogous to the illumination of Atzilus in BYA), and the essence of the point of the heart is the inwardness as it is in its own place.

The same applies to the inwardness of Elokus, which contains the equivalent of the two degrees mentioned above. This can be understood based on what is written in *Tanya* regarding the two names *Havayah* and *Elokim*: *Elokim* is outwardness, and *Havayah* is inwardness. [This can be connected with what is explained in *Likutei Torah* there, that the love in the outwardness of the heart comes through contemplation of the "Filling Light," and the love (the longing that is above reason and knowledge) in the inwardness of the heart is drawn from the "Surrounding Light," for *Havayah* and *Elokim* are (generally) Surrounding and Filling. Therefore, the Filling Light (*Elokim*), the outwardness, is the root for the love of the outwardness of the heart, and the Surrounding Light (*Havayah*), the inwardness, is the root for the love of the inwardness of the heart.] Based on this, it can be said that the interpretation of "Your face, Hashem" is the Essence of *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim*. For the fact that *Havayah* (in general) is inwardness is true even after it is clothed in *Elokim*, but "Your face, Hashem" is the Essence of *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim*.

5) It can be said that the level of "Your face, Hashem"—the inwardness of *Havayah*—is higher even than the *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim*. [Analogous to what is explained elsewhere regarding the verse, "And the truth of Hashem is forever," that even the name *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim* is *Havayah* (in general), while "the truth of Hashem" (the true *Havayah*) is the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above the name *Havayah*, above even the *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim*.] This can be understood based on the known principle that the inwardness of every thing is the thing itself, and that which serves as a source for some other matter is its outwardness. Based on this, we can explain the difference between the two degrees in the inwardness above (*Havayah* and the *Ein Sof* above *Havayah*): *Havayah* is from the root *mehoveh* (bringing into being), but the creation from the name *Havayah* is in a manner of "automatically." As is known, the creation from the name *Elokim* is in a manner of "clothing" ("In the beginning *Elokim* created"), while the creation from the name *Havayah* is in a manner of "automatically" ("Let them praise the name of Hashem, for He commanded and they were created"). Therefore, in general, the name *Havayah* is inwardness, because the fact that creation from it is in a manner of "automatically" indicates that it is removed from the matter of creation (and is not truly a source). But specifically, the fact that creation occurs from the name *Havayah* is because it is a source for creation, and therefore, the true essence of inwardness is in the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*.

Based on this, it can be said that the same applies to the two degrees of the inwardness of the heart: the fact that the illumination of the point of the heart is not as inward as the inwardness of the essence of the point of the heart is true even as it is in its essence, before it shines into the outwardness of the heart. For the fact that it draws down to shine into the outwardness of the heart proves that it is not the true essence of inwardness. The true essence of inwardness is in the essence of the point of the heart, which is distinct from the outwardness of the heart. This is analogous to what was stated above (end of section 4) regarding "Your face, Hashem," which is higher even than the *Havayah* that is above being clothed in *Elokim*.

6) We must add an explanation regarding the connection of the two degrees in the inwardness of the heart (the illumination of the point of the heart and the essence of the point of the heart) to the two degrees in the inwardness above (*Havayah* and the *Ein Sof* above *Havayah*), based on what is explained in *Likutei Torah* there regarding the verse, "When you go out to war against your enemies," that "When you go out to war" refers to the war of the Divine soul with the animal soul, and this war is in the powers of the soul that are clothed in the body (intellect and emotions). In contrast, the inwardness of the heart (the illumination of the point of the heart) is "against your enemies"—above your enemies—where the enemy has no control or hold. Through the revelation of the illumination of the point of the heart, "against your enemies," through this "you shall capture its captives," turning the evil into good. However, the turning of evil into good through the revelation of the illumination of the point of the heart is only in the "garments" (thought, speech, and action), and to turn the emotions from evil to good is through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart. This is "And you shall see among the captives a woman of beautiful form." The "woman of beautiful form" is the soul clothed in the body, and to extract her [her essence and being, i.e., her intellect and emotions] from captivity is through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart. It can be said that the reason why regarding the transformation of the garments (through the revelation of the illumination of the point of the heart) it is written "you shall capture its captives," and regarding the transformation of the emotions (through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart) it is written "and you shall see among the captives," is because regarding the illumination of the point of the heart, there is an adversary. This is why regarding this level it is written "against your enemies," because regarding the illumination of the point of the heart, the existence of the enemy is present; it is just that it is in a manner of "against your enemies," above your enemies, where the enemy has no control or hold. Therefore, the extraction of the matters of holiness (thought, speech, and action of the soul) from captivity, which is through the revelation of the illumination of the point of the heart, is in a manner of action: "you shall capture its captives" [though the action is not in a manner of war, because regarding this level the enemy has no control]. In contrast, the essence of the point of the heart is [analogous to] the level of *Yechidah*, against which there is no "opposite side," for the "reflection of a reflection" has no [power]. Therefore, the nullification of the "other side" through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart is (not that through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart the nullification *is accomplished*, but rather) that through this revelation, there is no place from the outset for the existence of the "other side." This is "And you shall see among the captives a woman of beautiful form," for when there is the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart, then the level of the soul (the woman of beautiful form) that was previously in captivity is revealed of its own accord, "and you shall see" (and there is no need to *extract* her from captivity).

The same applies above: in the name *Elokim*, there can be (through a multitude of *Tzimtzumim*) a source of nourishment for the *Chitzonim*, and even to "other gods." According to what is explained in many places that the name *Elokim* is not only the shield and sheath that conceals and hides the light of the name *Havayah*, but that even the light of the name *Havayah* as it is drawn down and constricted by the name *Elokim* to be a source for the created beings—which in general is the Filling Light, called *Elokim*—it can be said that the same applies to the Filling Light. Since the creation from the name *Elokim* (the Filling Light) is in a manner of "clothing," the created beings that are formed from it occupy space, and their nullification is only the nullification of "somethingness," and therefore it is possible for "existence" to evolve from this, and even the existence of idolatry ("other gods"). For there to be no place given to existence and the "other side," it must be specifically through the revelation of the name *Havayah* (the Surrounding Light), for creation from it is in a manner of "automatically," and the created beings do not occupy space relative to it—they are in a state of nullification of existence. And based on what was explained above (section 5) that even the name *Havayah* is a source for creation, it is necessary that even relative to the name *Havayah* there is some occupation of space by the created beings, and the true nullification is specifically relative to the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*, which is not in the category of a source for worlds. Based on this, it can be said that to negate *completely* the possibility of giving place to existence, it must be specifically through the revelation of the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*. This is the meaning of the verse, "You shall have no other gods before Me," for in order that there be no place given to other gods, it is through "before Me" (*Al Panai*), for the true meaning of *Panai* (My face) is the Essence of the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*.

7) It can be said that the two interpretations of "To You, my heart has said, 'Seek My face'" (that "To You" is "For You and in Your service," and "To You" is "In Your place"), and also the two interpretations (in the maamar) of "Seek" (request and supplication, request and search), correspond to the two degrees of *Panai* (Face). In the inwardness of the name *Havayah* (which is the level of inwardness relative to the name *Elokim*), the equivalent of which in man is the illumination of the point of the heart, the interpretation of "To You" is "For You and in Your service." That is, the heart is the messenger of the Holy One, blessed be He, for the essence of a messenger is that he is sent *to do* something. The mission at this level of the inwardness of the heart is to illuminate the outwardness of the heart in order to win the war against the animal soul, for the main victory (through the revelation of this level) is in the garments—thought, speech, and action—but for the thought, speech, and action to be complete, it is through the emotions in the heart, avodah *with* the heart. Based on this, the interpretation of "Seek My face" is a request and search, to search in all his affairs that they be in accordance with the level of *Panai* (the Face of *Havayah*). And in the inwardness of the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*, the equivalent of which in man is the essence of the point of the heart, the interpretation of "To You" is "In Your place," as brought above (end of section 2) from the maamar, that it is the point of Yiddishkeit in every Jew that is connected to the Essence (in Your place). At this level, the matter of a mission is not applicable, because the point of Yiddishkeit is not a means to another end (fulfilling a mission), and the purpose is in itself. The avodah regarding this level is avodah in the heart itself, that it be in a state of revelation. For the inwardness of the heart as it is in itself is in a state of concealment, and the avodah regarding it is to arouse it so that it will be in a state of revelation. Based on this, the interpretation of "Seek My face" is a request and supplication, for a request and supplication is (as the language in the maamar states) in a state of great arousal.

8) It is explained elsewhere that in the ascent of the soul through its descent below, there are two matters. Through the fact that even while it is clothed in the body and animal soul it serves Hashem, the strength of its connection with the Holy One, blessed be He, is revealed—that even the concealment and hiding of the body and animal soul cannot cause a deficiency in its connection. And through its avodah below, a new matter is accomplished: the clarification and refinement of the body and animal soul and its portion in the world. And since this matter (the clarification and refinement of the body, etc.) is an innovation (and not the revelation of a concealment), it is higher than the revelation of the strength of the soul’s connection. And based on the known principle that the clarification and refinement of the body and animal soul (for which the soul descended below) is specifically through love and fear in the revealed heart, the outwardness of the heart, it can be said that there is an advantage in the mission of the illumination of the point of the heart to the outwardness of the heart, over the avodah of the revelation of the point of Yiddishkeit.

9) It can be said that this is what the maamar explains regarding the verse "And from my flesh I shall see Elokah"—specifically "from my *flesh*," that the intent is sensory vision (in Elokus) that relates to the body, because the ultimate intent of the soul’s descent below is (not that the matters of the soul be in a state of revelation while it is clothed in the body, but rather) *that the body* should see Elokus. [It should be noted that there is another interpretation of "from my flesh I shall see Elokah," that in the flesh itself one sees the Elokus within it. As in the teaching of the Alter Rebbe on the verse "And from my flesh I shall see Elokah," that one must "remove the flesh" so that one can see Divinity. From the fact that he says one must "remove the flesh" (the things that cover), it is understood that through this one sees the Elokus that is in the flesh itself. As is also understood from the maamar of the Rebbe (Rashab) n”e on the verse "And from my flesh I shall see Elokah": "Do not look at the fact that he is a *golem* (a physical body); the *golem* was brought into being by the Essence of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, for He alone has the power and ability to create something from nothing and absolute nothingness." It can be said that the fact that the maamar explains that the interpretation of "from my flesh I shall see Elokah" is sensory vision, even though seeing the Elokus that is in the flesh itself is seemingly a higher matter (especially according to the interpretation of the Rebbe n”e that it refers to the power of the Essence that is in the body), is because seeing the Elokus that is in the flesh (the power of the Essence that is in it) is an intellectual vision that relates to the soul, and the ultimate intent of the soul’s descent below is *that the body* should see Elokus.]

10) It is known that just as the descent of the soul below is for the sake of an ascent, so too is it regarding the descent of the Divine light to bring into being and sustain the created beings, which is a descent for the sake of an ascent. Based on this, it can be said that through the name *Havayah* descending and clothing itself in the name *Elokim* (in order to bring into being and sustain the created beings), an ascent is accomplished in the light, higher even than as it is in its root in the *Ein Sof* above *Havayah*. The ascent is that a new matter is accomplished in it—the revelation of Elokus in this physical world. As brought above (section 2) from the maamar, there are matters of Elokus, such as Divine Providence, that are in a state of actual revelation, to the point that it is possible to see them tangibly. It can be said that this is what is said in the maamar, that the fact that sensory vision relates to the body is both regarding the person who sees and regarding the thing that is seen; that the advantage of the inwardness that belongs to the outwardness and its descent into the outwardness is both regarding the person, *that the body* sees Elokus (as above, section 9), and regarding the light above, that its revelation is in this physical world.

11) The same applies to the avodah of man, that through the descent of the intellect [the highest in man, for the nature of the intellect is to ascend above] into the emotions [the lowest in man, for the nature of the emotions is to descend below], an ascent is accomplished in the intellect. And the main ascent is not that the light of the intellect shines in the heart as well, but that through this a new matter is accomplished—the arousal of the *emotions*. It can be said that this is the reason why for there to be an arousal of the emotions in the heart there must be preparation from the side of the heart as well, because the *main* innovation in the arousal of the emotions is when the arousal is (also) from the side of the matter of the emotions.

It can be said that the same applies to the "King in the field" (Elul), for although this is a descent relative to how He is in His royal palace (Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur), for when He is in His royal palace He is in the crown of royalty and royal garments, whereas when He is in the field He is not, nevertheless, through this an ascent is accomplished, as it were, in the King, because through His descent to the field a new matter is accomplished—that even those who are furthest away come to greet Him. However, since regarding the matter of revelations, the fact that He is in the field is a descent relative to how He is in His royal palace, the avodah in the field must be in a manner of going (afterwards) after the King to His royal palace, as stated in the maamar that the avodah of Elul is a preparation for the avodah of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. This is also the connection of the two interpretations of "To You, my heart has said, 'Seek My face,'" that the avodah of "To You, my heart has said" according to the interpretation of "For You and in Your service," to fulfill His will to make the lower world a dwelling place for Him, must be in a manner that through this they will reach the interpretation of "In Your place," the revelation of the point of Yiddishkeit that is connected to the Essence.

12) The maamar continues (at the conclusion and seal of the maamar) that through the arousal of the point of the heart, one becomes a pure vessel to receive the blessing of abundance for the entire year. It can be said that in this there are two virtues: the virtue of "For You and in Your service" and the virtue of "In Your place." When the drawing down of abundance is according to the order of *Hishtalshelus*, they examine in the Heavenly Court if one is worthy of it, and there are accusers who accuse and say that he is not worthy of it. It can be said that this matter is true even when the drawing down is from the name *Havayah* (since even the name *Havayah* is a source for creation, as above, section 5), as it is written, "And the sons of Elokim came to stand before Hashem." The fact that an abundance of blessing is drawn down (in great profusion) is because through the revelation of the essence of the point of the heart, the drawing down is from the *Ein Sof* that is above *Havayah*, and the accusation of the "sons of Elokim" is not applicable there (as above, end of section 6, in the explanation of the verse "You shall have no other gods before Me"), and furthermore, there are not even the measurements and limitations of the name *Elokim* (of holiness), and therefore the abundance drawn down from there is in great profusion. The fact that the drawing down of abundance is in physical matters, and all the more so the fact that the drawing down of abundance is not only from above but (as above from the maamar) that the person becomes a suitable vessel to receive the abundance, is because through the avodah in the illumination of the point of the heart and the outwardness of the heart to make the *lower world* a dwelling place for Him, the virtue of physicality is felt (as above, section 10, regarding "from my flesh I shall see Elokah") and the virtue of the Jewish people who make the dwelling place.

Since in the avodah of Elul there are two matters—that the avodah (itself) is in the field and in a manner of going after the King to His royal palace (as above, section 11)—therefore, also in the drawing down of the abundance there are two matters: that "much good" is drawn down (in abundance) that is above measurement and limitation, and this comes in good that is visible and revealed (also) in physical matters, for a good and sweet year, in children, life, and sustenance in their literal sense, and in all of them—abundantly.

## B's"d. Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5713

(Unedited transcript)

"These are the journeys of the Bnei Yisrael who went out from the land of Mitzrayim... and Moshe wrote their departures for their journeys... and these are their journeys for their departures." It is well known that there are precise difficulties here: the verse says "These are the journeys" (in the plural), yet concludes "who went out from the land of Mitzrayim"—and the exodus from Mitzrayim was only the first departure and journey. Furthermore, it is not understood why it says "and Moshe wrote," for Moshe Rabbeinu wrote the entire Torah; what does this come to teach us? Also, what is the meaning of the doubling: "their departures for their journeys" and "their journeys for their departures," and why is the order reversed from the beginning to the end? In general, one must understand what the narrative and knowledge of the order of the journeys has to do with us. Even though the Midrash explains this for that generation with a parable of a king and his son who traveled, and upon returning they counted all the journeys and the events that occurred in them, the Torah is eternal. Therefore, this narrative must be relevant to all times and all places.

2) To understand all this, we must first explain the request of Knesses Yisrael: "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us; look and see our disgrace." The Baal Shem Tov explains this as: "Remember, G-d, what has become of our *Mah* (the level of self-nullification) within the soul; look closely and make us see our own shame." This is the request of Knesses Yisrael to the Ribono shel Olam. Likewise, there is a request for remembrance from the Ribono shel Olam to Yisrael, as is stated in the Zohar at the beginning of Parshas Bechukosai regarding this verse. The request from Above to Knesses Yisrael is also in the language of "remember," as it is written: "My people, remember now what Balak king of Moav counseled and what Bilam the son of Beor answered him..." and it concludes: "What does Hashem ask of you... but to do justice, love kindness, and walk humbly with your G-d." And it is written: "Remember your Creator in the days of your youth... before the sun darkens..." The Midrash states: The prophet said to Yisrael, "Remember your Creator while the Beis HaMikdash still exists, which is called the 'House of Choice' (Beis HaBechirah); while the covenant of Kehunah exists, as it is said: 'And He chose him from all the tribes of Yisrael for Me to be a Kohen'; while the covenant of Levi exists, as it is said: 'For Hashem your G-d has chosen him from all your tribes.'" This is the meaning of "before the sun darkens," for "the sun darkens" refers to the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash. Thus, it must mean "Remember your Creator in the days of your youth"—in the time of the Temple, which is called the House of Choice. Since in the time of the Temple, Bnei Yisrael did not fulfill the request from Above to "Remember your Creator... do justice, love kindness, and walk humbly with your G-d," this was the cause of the destruction. Because of this, we ask in the time of Galus: "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us; look and see our disgrace."

We must understand what the concept of "remembrance" Above is, for which we ask "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us." Remembrance and forgetfulness are matters of "without limit" and "limit." Forgetfulness is from the side of limitation; since a person is limited, all his affairs are in limitation. Therefore, the impression made upon him by something he saw or heard is also limited, and for this reason, it eventually ceases—this is the concept of forgetfulness. Conversely, the concept of remembrance is without limit. We see this even in a human being: a matter that touches him to his core and the interior of his soul—meaning, it is above his limitations—he remembers always. According to this, the content of the request "Remember, Hashem..." is not understood, for Above is without limit; why is it necessary to ask for the concept of remembrance Above?

3) However, the matter is that remembrance and forgetfulness are the concepts of *Panim* (face/inner) and *Achor* (back/outer), interiority and exteriority. Just as it is in a person below, where he remembers always what touches him internally, whereas something that touches him only externally (which is the concept of *Achor*) is subject to forgetfulness. Likewise, there are also Above the levels of *Panim*, right, left, and *Achor*, as stated in the *Remez* that they correspond to the four worlds of *ABY"A*. The world of *Atzilus* is called *Panim*, for just as in the face of a person there is the interiority of the life-force, so too in *Atzilus* is the interiority of the *Ohr Ein Sof*, to the point that "He, His life, and His essence are one." This means that although *Atzilus* is after the *Tzimtzum*, and the general light after the *Tzimtzum* is in the state of a short and constricted *Kav*, nevertheless, it is the same essence of light. This is the difference between *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* and *Atzilus*: the formation of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* is through the *Parsa*, whereas the formation of *Atzilus* is not through the *Parsa* but only through the *Tzimtzum*, as stated in *Etz Chaim*. The difference between *Tzimtzum* and *Parsa* is like the difference we see below between light shining through a window or a hole; even though the light is in a state of diminution and constriction—shining only to the extent that the window or hole can contain—it is still the same essence of light. Conversely, when light shines through a screen (*masach*), the light undergoes a change of essence, to the point that the light that comes after the screen is called "derivative light." Similarly, it is Above: the formation of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* through the *Parsa* is a change of essence, whereas the formation of *Atzilus* through *Tzimtzum*, although the light there is in constriction, is the same essence of light as before the *Tzimtzum*. And although there are also *Parsa'os* in *Atzilus*—as is known that there is a *Parsa* between *Keter* and *Chochmah*, between *Binah* and *Ze'er Anpin*, and between *Ze'er Anpin* and *Malchus*—nevertheless, the *Parsa* in *Atzilus* is not like the *Parsa'os* of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*. The *Parsa'os* of *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* serve to conceal and they do hide the light, whereas the *Parsa'os* in *Atzilus* reveal the light. A *Parsa* is like skin, and our Sages said, "Those whose skins are like their flesh—the skin of a person..." (which is not like the skin of an animal, which is coarse skin). Its counterpart Above is the *Parsa'os* that reveal the light. This is the difference between the letters of *Mah* and the letters of *Ban* (and their meaning in *avodah* is the difference between the letters of Torah and the letters of *Tefillah*). The letters of *Ban* conceal the light, and because of this, the created beings are formed as a state of "existence" and a separate thing. Conversely, the letters of *Mah* do not conceal the light; on the contrary, they reveal the light, and therefore they effect *bitul* (nullification) in the created beings. This is "their skins are like their flesh—the skin of a person," for *Adam* (man) in *gematria* is *Mah*, and this is the concept of the *Parsa'os* that reveal the light—the *Parsa'os* in *Atzilus* which are called by the name *Mah*, as stated in *Pachach Eliyahu*: "The name *Mah* is the path of *Atzilus*." This is why *Atzilus* is called *Panim*, because the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* shines there. The essence of the level of *Panim* is the level of *Chochmah*, similar to what is written: "A man's wisdom illuminates his face." This means that in *Atzilus* shines the light of *Chochmah*, as the saying goes, "The supernal *Abba* nests in *Atzilus*," and in *Chochmah* shines the *Ohr Ein Sof*, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Tanya* in the name of his teacher, the Maggid, that the level of *Chochmah* is that "He alone is He, and there is nothing else." And higher than that, in *Atzilus* shines the light of *Keter*, which is the concept of the name *Mah* in the *milui* (spelling) of *alaphim*, and *Aleph* is the *Sefirah* of *Keter*. Since *Atzilus* is the level of *Panim*, the concept of forgetfulness does not apply there, whereas in *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, which is the level of *Achor*, the concept of forgetfulness does apply. Now, all this is the difference in the worlds. However, the souls of Yisrael, even as they are below, are in a state of interiority, for the souls of Yisrael "arose in the thought," meaning in the highest level of thought, and it is written: "Face to face Hashem spoke with you." Through this, that Hashem spoke with you, the interiority of Yisrael became the interiority of Above. However, all this is from the perspective of the soul itself, but from the perspective of its descent below and its enclothement in the body and the animal soul, and especially in the time of Galus—in the time of Galus it is written: "And I will surely hide My face." This means that since "they turned their backs to Me and not their faces," meaning the *avodah* was in a state of *Achor*, therefore there was also created Above a "hiding of the face," and because of this, we must ask for the concept of remembrance: "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us."

4) To understand more deeply why the souls of Yisrael are in a state of interiority: it is written, "And now, Yisrael, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear..." and our Sages said, "Is fear a small thing? Yes, for Moshe it is a small thing." What is written, "but to fear," refers to *yirah tata'ah* (lower fear), which is why it says "but to fear"—it is the lowest form of fear, and therefore for Moshe it is a small thing. The matter is that it is written: "For Hashem is a G-d of knowledge (de'os)," two *de'os*: *da'as elyon* (supernal knowledge) and *da'as tachton* (lower knowledge). *Da'as elyon* is that Above there is existence and below there is none—meaning, one sees with sensory vision that Above is the true existence and below there is none. *Da'as tachton* is that creation is "something from nothing," meaning that below there is existence and Above there is none, for since he sees only the created existence, he calls the below "existence" and the Above "nothing." Because of the difference between these two *de'os*, there is also a difference in their *bitul*. The *bitul* from *da'as tachton* is only *bitul hayesh* (nullification of the existence), for since he sees the existence, he is in a state of reality, yet he still has the concept of *bitul*—the nullification of the existence. Conversely, the *bitul* from *da'as elyon* is *bitul b'metzius* (nullification of reality), for since he sees that below is "nothing," the *bitul* is a nullification of reality. This is why for Moshe, *yirah tata'ah* is a small thing, for Moshe is in the state of *da'as elyon*, as our Sages said: "All the prophets prophesied with *koh* (thus), and Moshe prophesied with *zeh* (this)." *Zeh* is the vision of the essence, the level of *da'as elyon*, and because of this he was in a state of *bitul b'metzius*. Therefore, for Moshe, who is in the state of *da'as elyon*—*bitul b'metzius*—*yirah tata'ah*, which is only *bitul hayesh*, is a small thing. Now, although *yirah tata'ah* is a lower level—a small thing—about which they said "but to fear," nevertheless, they demand (*mont men*) *yirah tata'ah* specifically, because the ultimate intent and the primary *taanug* (delight) is in *yirah tata'ah* more than in *yirah ila'ah* (higher fear). As it is written: "G-d has made laughter for me," for specifically through effecting the *bitul* in the things that come from the name *Elokim*—specifically that they are in a state of existence, the nullification of existence into nothingness—then the primary concept of laughter and delight is created Above. Likewise, it is written: "Leviathan, which You created to play with," for *Leviathan* is from the word *chibur* (connection), as it is written: "My husband will join (yiloveh) with me." The concept of connection applies specifically when there are two things distinct from one another, and this concept is in the *avodah* of *bitul hayesh* specifically, where the existence and the nothingness are two things distinct from one another, and yet they effect the nullification of the existence into nothingness. Specifically through this is the concept of laughter created—"to play with." This means that although the *avodah* of *is'hapcha* (transformation) is higher than the *avodah* of *iskafya* (subjugation), that is only in the matter of revelations, but the primary *taanug* is in the *avodah* of *iskafya* specifically.

However, we still need to understand what is meant by "for Moshe it is a small thing," for seemingly it is not understood; it is written "He asks of you." But the matter is, as explained in *Tanya*, that every soul from the House of Yisrael has within it a spark of Moshe Rabbeinu—a spark from the soul of Moshe. This is the level of *Mah* that is in every one of Yisrael, which is the concept of *bitul b'metzius* (as mentioned above). This is because the root of the souls is from the level of *Chochmah*, as it is written: "You are children to Hashem your G-d," and it is written: "Yisrael is My firstborn son." Just as a son is drawn from the essence of the father's brain, so too the souls are from the essence of the level of *Chochmah*, which is the level of *Mah*. Therefore, the souls are in ultimate *bitul*—*bitul b'metzius*—as it is written: "As Hashem the G-d of Yisrael lives, before whom I have stood," which refers to all the souls, that they are in a manner of "standing," which is the concept of *bitul*. This is "And now, Yisrael, what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear," for since all of Yisrael are in the state of *Mah* due to the spark of Moshe in every one of Yisrael, then "what does Hashem your G-d ask of you but to fear," for fear is a small thing for the spark of Moshe in every one of Yisrael. In order to reveal the level of *Mah* in the soul, they instituted the one hundred blessings, as our Sages said: "Do not read *Mah* (what) but *me'ah* (one hundred)," from which they learned that a person is obligated to recite one hundred blessings every day. One hundred blessings is similar to what is written: "And Yitzchak sowed in that land and found... one hundred gates (sha'arim), and Hashem blessed him." This means that through the *avodah* of *tzedakah*—"sowing righteousness"—the blessing and the drawing down from Above is created, and the level of *Mah* in the soul is revealed.

However, in the time of Galus, the *avodah* is not in the state of *Mah*, which is the interiority of the soul, but only in the state of exteriority and "backs." Therefore, there is also created Above a "hiding of the face" (as mentioned above), and therefore we ask: "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us"—what has become of our *Mah*—for that *Mah* is in concealment and hiding. And despite it being in concealment, the concept of remembrance still applies, for ultimately its essence, root, and the soul itself are in the state of *Mah*. And the verse continues: "Look..." The difference between *re'iyah* (seeing) and *habitah* (looking) is that *re'iyah* is in proximity, as it is written: "And he saw that he could not overcome him," and *habitah* is in distance, as it is written: "Look (habet) from heaven and see." Therefore, the concept of *re'iyah* which is in proximity cannot be in the time of Galus, and for this we ask *habitah*, which is the revelation in the state of *makif* (encompassing light). And despite it being in the state of *makif*, it also acts within the interiority, especially regarding the action upon the *kelipos*, for *ohr makif* blinds the eyes of the external forces.

5) The explanation of the matter: just as there is the level of *Mah* in *Kedushah*, so too there is the level of *Mah* in the *sitra achra*, and this is the concept of "and his concubine, whose name was Re'umah"—they saw (*ra'u*) *Mah*. The matter is that the possibility for the affairs of the *sitra achra* is because they have a "giving of place" in *Kedushah*. As we see in the *avodah* in the soul: when one performs his *avodah* in *bitul*, but in a way that he *feels* the *bitul*, this is a giving of place for it to come from this to a state of *yeshus* (self-centeredness). This means that first the *bitul* will be in a manner of *yeshus*—which is the concept of the *kelipah* of *Re'umah*, "they saw *Mah*"—and afterwards he will come to *yeshus* entirely, which is absolute evil. Likewise, it is also in the *hishtalshelus* (chain of progression) of the worlds: through the *kelipah* of *Re'umah*, which is opposite the world of *Atzilus*, in the multiplicity of the *hishtalshelus*, absolute evil branches out from this—the level of *Mah* of the *sitra achra*. And regarding this it is written: "He who sheds the blood of man, by man"—for *Adam* in *gematria* is *Mah*—through sins, he sheds the blood of the *Adam* of *Kedushah*, the level of *Mah* of *Kedushah*, into the "man of Belial," which is the level of *Mah* of the *sitra achra*. The matter is that the 248 positive commandments and 365 negative commandments correspond to the 248 limbs and 365 sinews. The concept of the limbs is that they draw the life-force and limit the life-force so it is not drawn outward. When one cuts the limb, the life-force is drawn outward, and similarly regarding the sinews through which the blood flows. Likewise, when one transgresses a positive or negative commandment, he causes the life-force and the blood of *Kedushah* to be drawn outward.
