This is what is meant by "and he who curses (nokev) the name of Hashem," for all the *mitzvos* depend on the name of Hashem, and when he sins and blemishes and diverts the path by transgressing one of the *mitzvos* of Hashem, he "pierces" the name of Hashem, and through this he sheds the blood of the *Adam* of *Kedushah* into the "man of Belial." This is also what our Sages said: "Titus pierced the curtain and blood came out of it." This means they showed him how the destruction could happen—that it is not by its own power, but only through the blemish created by shedding the blood, the interiority of the life-force of the *Adam* of *Kedushah*, into the "man of Belial." Based on this, we can explain another interpretation of "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us"—that our *Mah* has become the *Mah* of the *sitra achra*. This matter is brought about by the first interpretation of "what has befallen us," that the level of *Mah* of *Kedushah* is in concealment and hiding, and from this it descended further below, so that the level of *Mah* of *Kedushah* became the level of *Mah* of the *sitra achra*, similar to the matter of "he who sheds the blood of man, by man."

6) And the verse continues: "Look and see our disgrace." The matter is that it is written: "The disgrace of your widowhood you shall not remember anymore," for in the time of Galus, Knesses Yisrael is called by the name "widow," as it is written: "She has become like a widow," and our Sages said: "Like a widow, but not a widow in truth—like a woman whose husband went to a distant country." A woman is Knesses Yisrael, and her husband is the Ribono shel Olam, and a woman whose husband went to a distant country means that the union of Knesses Yisrael with the Ribono shel Olam is missing. In the matter of the *Sefiros*, it is the union of *ZON* (*Ze'er Anpin* and *Nukvah*); the woman is the level of *Malchus*, and her husband is the level of *Ze'er Anpin*. A woman whose husband went to a distant country means that the level of *Ze'er Anpin* (is not drawn to *Malchus*, but) has ascended to the "sea of *Chochmah*." This is why in the time of Galus, the Holy One, blessed be He, ascends higher and higher; the Holy One, blessed be He, is the level of *Ze'er Anpin*, and in the time of Galus, He ascends higher and higher—higher to the level of *Binah* and higher to the level of *Chochmah*. This is the concept of "widow," as stated in *Pardes* that "widow" (*almanah*) is *al maneh* (for a *maneh*). A *maneh* is one hundred *zuzim*, two times *nun* (50+50), and this is the fifty gates of *Binah* as they are from below to above and from above to below, through which the elevation of the *Midos* and the drawing down of the *Ohr Ein Sof* into the *Midos* is effected, through which it will be drawn below into the level of *Malchus*. This is also the concept of the journeys, "their departures for their journeys... their journeys for their departures," which is the concept of elevation and drawing down. But in the time of Galus, it is *al maneh*, for the concept of elevation and drawing down through the fifty gates is missing, and therefore it is not drawn from the level of *Ze'er Anpin* to *Malchus* to be a union of *ZON*, which is the concept of "widow." Another interpretation of "widow" is as stated in *Sefer HaShorashim* that "widow" is from the word *ilem* (mute/silence). For the interpretation that "widow" is from *al maneh*—that her *kesubah* is a *maneh*—it is not understood why a male is also called a widower (*alman*); it must be that because a woman is called a widow, therefore a male is also called a widower. But for the interpretation that "widow" is from the word *ilem*, it is well-understood that a male is also called a widower, because the joy of the union of the husband with his wife is missing. The matter is that when the revelation of the voice shines in the speech, then the speech shines in revelation, and when the speech shines in revelation, then "He will subdue peoples under us" (for through *yidaber*—from the word *dibbur*—is also created *yidaber*—from the word *hanhagah*—that Yisrael are in the highest level, etc.). But when the voice is not in revelation, then the speech is in concealment in Galus, and this is the concept of "widow" from the word *ilem*. Regarding this we ask: "Look and see our disgrace," for although *habitah* is the level of *makif*, nevertheless, it is effective also in the interiority, as it is written: "For Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you..." "To save you" means to be a shade over your head, which is the level of *makif*, and nevertheless, through this, "to save you" is effected in its literal sense, from the word *hatzalah* (rescue), and especially regarding the action upon the *kelipos*, for *ohr makif* blinds the eyes of the external forces (as mentioned above).

This is what is meant by "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us..." The Ribono shel Olam demands from Yisrael: "Remember your Creator in the days of your youth," while the Beis HaMikdash still exists, which is called the House of Choice, while the covenant of Kehunah exists, and while the covenant of Levi exists. The demand is "do justice, love kindness, and walk humbly with your G-d." But when the *avodah* of "walking humbly" is missing, which is the opposite of the concept of "they saw *Mah*," then the *Mah* of the *sitra achra* is created. For this we ask: "Remember, Hashem, what has befallen us," that the *Mah* of *Kedushah* is in concealment and hiding, and to the point that through this the *Mah* of the *sitra achra* is created. Therefore, "Look and see our disgrace," until "the disgrace of your widowhood you shall not remember anymore."

7) This is what is written: "And these are the journeys of the Bnei Yisrael who went out from the land of Mitzrayim." All the exiles are called *Mitzrayim*—*Mitzrayim* is from the word *meitzar* (strait) and *gevul* (limit). And until they come to the Yarden and Yericho—*Yericho* is from the word *rei'ach* (scent), an *avodah* that is above reason and knowledge—this is still a state of *meitzar* and *gevul*. In the future redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, this level will be revealed, as it is written: "He will not judge by what his ears hear, and not by what his eyes see... but he will smell with the fear of Hashem"—that he smells and judges, *makifim* that are above *Chochmah* and *Binah*. And that they come to this is the concept of the journeys. The *avodah* in the journeys is the descent of the soul and its enclothement in the *meitzar* of the body in general, and especially in the time of the *meitzarim* (straits), the concealments and hidings that are in the exiles. The empowerment for this is from the level of "their departures," from the word "like a spring of water whose waters do not fail"—the root and essence of the soul, the *Mah* in the soul. And through the drawing down from "their departures for their journeys," which is effected through the level of Moshe in every one of Yisrael—"and Moshe wrote"—the level of *Mah* is revealed also in the soul that is in the body, and through this he performs his *avodah*. The *avodah* is the traveling and the elevation from below to above—"their journeys for their departures." And no verse loses its literal meaning: the journeys of the generation of the desert in the desert of the nations. For what a person has the ability to draw down—the *Mah* in the soul in revelation and to overcome his body and animal soul, especially in the time of Galus and the generation of the footsteps of Mashiach, a darkness double and redoubled, the time of trials, etc. (as mentioned above)—is through the deeds of the fathers who subdued the source of the *kelipos* by traveling and camping in the desert of the nations, the serpent, the fiery serpent, and the scorpion. "And it was when the ark traveled... and Moshe said... and Your enemies were scattered and those who hate You fled before You." Therefore, the branches will also be subdued afterwards by the person throughout all the generations, through that "and Moshe wrote" which is in every one of us, "their departures for their journeys and these are their journeys for their departures." This is in the manner of general and particular, until they come to the Yarden and Yericho—he smells and judges in his *avodah* in particular—and afterwards to the general redemption, the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, "who will not judge by what his ears hear and not by what his eyes see, but he will smell with the fear of Hashem," he smells and judges, in the redemption that is destined to come speedily in our days.

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5716

(Unedited transcript)

"Sing to Hashem a new song, His praise in the assembly of the Chassidim," and "the exaltations of El are in their throat, and a two-edged sword in their hand." In the verses that follow, it explains what they will do with the sword, etc. Now, it is stated in the Midrash Tehillim on this passage that this psalm speaks of the future redemption. Who are the "Chassidim"? These are Yisrael. Whenever they see the Ribono shel Olam, they become Chassidim; they saw Him at the sea and became Chassidim and sang a song, as it is said, "Then Moshe sang," and when they see Him in the time to come, they will become Chassidim, as it is said, "His praise in the assembly of the Chassidim." Similarly, it is stated in the Mechilta and Yalkut on Parshas Beshalach that this song is for the future to come. This is why it says "a new song" (*shir chadash*) in the masculine, whereas everywhere else it says "a new song" (*shirah chadashah*) in the feminine—even regarding the redemption from Mitzrayim, it calls it "this song" (*hashirah hazos*) in the feminine. As explained in Shir HaShirim Rabbah (on the verse "I am black and beautiful"), the feminine form takes a tenth of the assets, etc.; thus, Yisrael inherited the land of the seven nations, which is a tenth of the seventy nations, so they sang the song in the feminine. But in the future to come, they are destined to inherit like a son who inherits all his father's assets, so they will sing in the masculine. 

We must understand the statement, "the exaltations of El are in their throat, and a two-edged sword in their hand." Since it speaks of the future redemption, what is the purpose of the sword? For regarding the future, it is written, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares... nation shall not lift up sword against nation."

2) To understand this, we must first preface what is stated in the Mishnah (Shabbos 6:4): "A man may not go out (on Shabbos) with a sword, nor with a bow, nor with a shield, nor with a club, nor with a spear..." Rabbi Eliezer says these are ornaments for him, while the Sages say they are nothing but [a disgrace], as it is said, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares." This Mishnah lists five weapons: the *sayaf* is a sword, which is a weapon; likewise the bow; the shield, which is meant to protect against arrows and catapults, is also included in the category of weapons; and the club—the Gemara explains that "club" means a *kulpa*, a staff with a thick head used for striking, which is also a weapon. It is stated in the Yerushalmi on the verse, "And the Bnei Yisrael went up armed (*chamushim*) from the land of Mitzrayim," that the word *chamushim* has two interpretations: "five" and "armed," meaning they were armed with the five weapons listed in the Mishnah (this is the correct version in the Yerushalmi). We must understand the difference between the redemption from Mitzrayim and the future redemption: in the future redemption it is written, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares," whereas in the redemption from Mitzrayim, weapons were necessary. Seemingly, since it is a matter of redemption, why are weapons necessary at all?

3) To understand this, we must first preface the concept of the "sword" in spirituality. Our Sages said, "Whoever recites the Shema... it is as if he holds a two-edged sword," which implies that there is a specific virtue in a two-edged sword. The matter is as stated in the Zohar: "This sword is Havayah; the head of the sword is the *Yud* of Havayah, the body of the sword is the *Vav*, the *Heh* and *Heh* are its two edges, and the sheath of the sword is the name *Ad-nai*." The concept is that it is written, "Havayah, may Your enemies perish"—meaning, there are those who fight against Havayah, and the victory in the war is through the name Havayah itself, for "this sword is Havayah," and through the sword of Havayah, one defeats those who fight against Havayah.

The matter is that the *yineka* (sustenance) of the *chitzonim* (external forces) can come from two sources. The first way is from the "multiplicity of *tzimtzumim*." When the *Ohr Ein Sof* shines in a revealed manner, they cannot receive it, because the *Ohr Ein Sof* only dwells where there is *bitul*. But where there is *yesh* (existence), the *Ohr Ein Sof* cannot be revealed, for "I and He cannot dwell together." Therefore, the *kelipos*, which are *yesh* and a separate entity, cannot receive from the revelation. But when it is contracted through the "multiplicity of *tzimtzumim*," they can receive *yineka*, because they possess at least a small amount of *bitul*—they call Him "the G-d of gods"—even though they also hold onto their own existence. Because they have a small amount of *bitul*, they can receive *yineka* from the multiplicity of *tzimtzumim*. 

The second way is that they receive their *yineka* from "height and haughtiness"—from the world of *Tohu* that preceded *Tikkun*, where [the *yesh*] does not occupy any space at all, and darkness is like light. As it is written, "The lizard you can catch with your hands, yet it is in the king's palaces"—since it is in the king's palaces, where it occupies no space at all, therefore even a lizard can be caught with one's hands. This is what is meant by, "If you exalt yourself like an eagle," for they exalt themselves very high, like the way of an eagle in the heavens.

This very matter—that they can receive *yineka* through these two ways—depends on the *avodah* of man. It is written, "Yaakov is the cord of His inheritance," and just like a cord whose one end is tied above and one end below, when the bottom end is moved, the top end also moves. So too in the *avodah* of the *neshamos* of Yisrael: according to the way of man's *avodah* below, it is likewise effected above. When a person lowers himself into material things—instead of his inner desire being for *Elokus* through Torah and *tefillah*—he causes, above, a multiplicity of *tzimtzumim* to the point that the *chitzonim* can receive *yineka* from it. And when a person exalts himself in haughtiness and arrogance—even though he knows his own lowliness well, he still exalts himself without reason or knowledge—"a spirit brings a spirit," causing the *chitzonim* to receive *yineka* from a very high place. This is the concept of *Paroh* (Pharaoh), which consists of the letters of *oref* (nape), for he receives from the "nape" of *Arich*, which is a very high level. This matter depends on *avodah*: when they "turned their back to Me and not their face," this draws forth the aspect of *Paroh*, who draws *yineka* from the nape of *Arich Anpin*, where "darkness is like light." This is the concept of the "two-edged sword," to cut off their *yineka* from both ways.

4) To understand this in detail: it is explained in the books of Kabbalah and Chassidus, in the discourses regarding Mitzrayim and the exodus from Mitzrayim, that Mitzrayim is the "narrowness of the throat" (*meitzar hagaron*). In the throat, there are three aspects: the trachea, the esophagus, and the veins, which are the three ministers of *Paroh*: the chief cupbearer, the chief executioner, and the chief baker. Just as there is a Mitzrayim and three ministers of *Paroh* in the realm of *sitra achra*, so too there is a Mitzrayim and three ministers in the realm of *kedushah*. 

The "chief cupbearer" is the drawing forth of *taanug* (delight), for water causes all kinds of delight to grow, and this is the drawing forth of Divine *taanug* throughout the entire *Seder Hishtalshelus*. In the human body, this is the trachea, for in the trachea there are the nerves of the brain, and through these nerves, *taanug* is drawn from the brain into the entire body. As our Sages said, "There are three tubes: one goes to the heart, one to the lungs, and one to the liver," which are the general organs; this is the trachea, which draws the *taanug* from the brain through the nerves into the entire body. In *avodah*, this is the study of Torah with *taanug*, for *taanug* is the inwardness of Torah, and likewise the *taanug* in *tefillah*. This is the role of the chief cupbearer. 

The "chief executioner" in *avodah* is the boiling of the blood in *kedushah*, which is the aspect of love like "flashes of fire." The chief cupbearer is love in delights, which is love that flows like water, while the chief executioner is love like flashes of fire. 

The "chief baker" is Torah. Although we said that the chief cupbearer is Torah, that refers to the *taanug* of Torah, whereas Torah in general is the aspect of the chief baker. Torah is called "wheat," which has the numerical value of 22—the 22 letters of the Torah. From wheat, one must make bread, as it is written, "Come, eat of my bread." For wheat to become bread, it must be baked, as it is written, "Ten women shall bake your bread in one oven." The "oven" is the warmth of love like flashes of fire, and "one" is the "Unique One of the world." "One oven" means the *koch* (fervor) and flashes of fire regarding the Unique One of the world. Thus, there are two matters here: the oven, which is the flashes of fire, and the Unique One of the world, which is the most exalted. This is the role of the chief baker, which is the Torah, serving as an intermediary between the two lines of the chief cupbearer and the chief executioner.

These three ministers of *kedushah* cut off the vitality from the three ministers of *sitra achra*. In *sitra achra* as well, there are three ministers of *Paroh*: the chief cupbearer is the *taanug* in material matters; even if it is permissible desire, the fact that one is immersed in them causes him to have no connection at all to Divine matters. The chief executioner is the boiling of the blood in material and physical things. The chief baker is one whose general state is not placed in Torah but in materialism. Through the three ministers as they are in *kedushah*, one cuts off the *yineka* from the three ministers of *Paroh*. Through the chief cupbearer in *kedushah*—which is the *avodah* of love in delights, whose purpose is the drawing forth of *taanug* in the *hishtalshelus* through the *Sefirah* of *Chochma* (this is the trachea, "Acquire *Chochma*, acquire *Binah*")—one cuts off the *yineka* that they draw from a high place. When the drawing forth is through *Chochma*, whose essence is *bitul*, they cannot receive it, because the *yineka* from a high place is only possible when it is in the aspect of a *makif* (surrounding light), but when it is drawn into the *pnimiyus* (inwardness), they cannot receive it. This is the chief cupbearer, who cuts off the *yineka* from the high place. 

Through the chief executioner in *kedushah*, one cuts off the *yineka* from the "multiplicity of *tzimtzumim*," which is caused by a person lowering himself into material things. Through the love like flashes of fire and the boiling of the blood in *kedushah*, the boiling of the blood in *sitra achra* is consumed. This is what the Targum translates as "chief executioner" (*rav katuliya*), whose meaning is as stated in the Gemara on the verse, "He who sacrifices a thanksgiving offering honors Me"—everyone who sacrifices his *yetzer* [is as if he sacrificed an offering]. Through the boiling of the blood in *kedushah*, he consumes the boiling of the blood in *sitra achra*, and consequently, the *yineka* from the multiplicity of *tzimtzumim* is nullified.

This is the "two-edged sword," which is the *avodah* of love in delights and love like flashes of fire. In general, this is the difference between Torah and *tefillah*: Torah is from above to below, through which one cuts off the *yineka* from the *makif*; *tefillah* is from below to above, by way of war, for "the time of prayer is a time of war," and through this, one cuts off the *yineka* from the multiplicity of *tzimtzumim*. This is the "sword of Havayah," for both ways of *yineka* of the *kelipos* are cut off specifically by Havayah. The *yineka* from the *makif* is cut off by Havayah, as it is written, "If you exalt yourself like an eagle... from there I will bring you down, says Havayah." And the *yineka* from the multiplicity of *tzimtzumim* is also cut off by the name Havayah, for the *yineka* of the *kelipos* is specifically from the multiplicity of *tzimtzumim* of the name *Elokim*. In that itself, it is not from the aspect of *El-ha*, but from the aspect of *Yam* (sea)—from these combinations the "land of the sons of Cham" draws its *yineka*. But through the revelation of the name Havayah, the *yineka* is nullified. This is the "sword of Havayah," a two-edged sword to cut off their *yineka* in both ways. In *avodah*, this is the *avodah* of Torah and the *avodah* of *tefillah*. There is a virtue in *tefillah*, which is from below to above, over Torah, which is from above to below, similar to the virtue of *iskafya* (subjugation) over *is'hapcha* (transformation), and the virtue of a *baal teshuvah* over a *tzaddik*, which is why Mashiach comes to "bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*." This is "Whoever recites the Shema... it is as if he holds a two-edged sword," for the Shema is called a two-edged sword to cut off the *yineka* from the three ministers of *Paroh*, through which one exits Mitzrayim. Therefore, the Shema concludes with, "I am Havayah your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim."

5) The explanation of the five weapons in the *avodah* of "service of the heart, which is *tefillah*": The *sayaf* (sword) refers to the *Pesukei D'Zimra*, from the expression "to sing (*lezamer*) to the tyrants," meaning that through contemplation of "He spoke and it came to be," he "sings" to the tyrants. The bow is the *Shemoneh Esrei*, as it is written, "With my sword and with my bow," which the Targum translates as "with my prayer and with my supplication." The virtue of the bow is that it acts even from a distance, and this is by pulling the string—the more one pulls the string downward, the further the arrow will reach. The bow has another advantage over the sword: it kills even an enemy one does not see. So too in the *avodah* of *Shemoneh Esrei*, which is a request: the more one feels the deficiency, the deeper the request and the fulfillment of the request will be. The more one is embittered by his distance from *Elokus*—which is pulling the string downward—the deeper the fulfillment of the request will be. Furthermore, it kills an enemy one does not see, which is the subtlety of evil. Before *tefillah*, "a man's way is right in his own eyes," for he has not transgressed a positive or negative commandment, and especially if he has studied some Torah and performs *mitzvos*, he is a *tzaddik* in his own eyes. However, when he reaches the *avodah* of *Shemoneh Esrei*, he "catches himself" that there is evil within him and regrets it; this is the request in *Shemoneh Esrei*, "Forgive us." After *Shemoneh Esrei*, we say *Ashamnu, Bagadnu*, etc., in all the details of the 22 letters, through which we extract the vitality from the 22 letters from which the *sitra achra* draws its *yineka*. All this is because the revelation is greater; in *Shemoneh Esrei* we say "Blessed are You, Havayah," which is the drawing forth of Havayah that is above the *hishtalshelus*, and the drawing forth is in "our G-d, King of the world." Therefore, because of the abundance of light, we also remove the subtlety of evil, as it is written, "And also the hornet... for He is a great and awesome G-d," and because He is a great G-d, even the subtlety of evil is cut off. The club, which is "easy to rule," in *avodah* is as our Sages said: "A person should always incite the good inclination against the evil inclination." "Always" is because the root of evil and good is from the aspect of *Gevuros* and *Chasadim*, and from the *Gevuros*, there must always be the matter of "incitement." The spear is the Shema, for the spear (*romach*) corresponds to the 248 (*ramach*) words of the Shema, and the *Vav* hints at the six words of *Shema* and *Baruch Shem*. The difference between the club and the spear is that through the spear, the vitality is taken away completely, whereas the club is only a striking. In *avodah*, in the *midos* (character traits), there are two aspects: *midos* of the permissible and *midos* of the forbidden. The *midos* of the forbidden must be completely eradicated through the spear, whereas for the *midos* of the permissible, one needs the club—to strike them and use them in *kedushah*. The shield, which is meant to protect against arrows and catapults, in *avodah* is the wearing of *Tallis* and *Tefillin* before and during *tefillah*. During *tefillah*, there is an intensification of the *sitra achra* to distract him from his *avodah*, as stated in Tanya, that it is like the parable of the uncircumcised one standing before him to distract him. For this is the purpose of wearing *Tallis* and *Tefillin*, which become garments for the soul to protect against the arrows.

From this, we can understand why they said that on Shabbos a man may not go out with a sword. In the *avodah* of the six days of the week, the time of prayer is a time of war to fight the evil in one's soul. However, on Erev Shabbos at twilight, the evil is separated from the good, as it is said, "All judgments are removed from her, and there is no dominion... and she is separated." Therefore, on Shabbos, the aforementioned matter of war does not apply; this is why they said a man may not go out with the five weapons, because Shabbos is not the time for that war. But Rabbi Eliezer says that they are nevertheless ornaments for him, meaning that the *birurim* (refinements) of the six days of the week are also ornaments on Shabbos to adorn oneself with; the prayers of the weekdays are elevated in the prayer of Shabbos, and it is an adornment for the person who was victorious during the weekdays. The Sages say they are not ornaments, and the proof is that for the future it is written, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares"; if they were ornaments, they would adorn themselves with them in the future. Rather, they are not ornaments at all, and on the contrary... the reason is that "whoever wrestles with a filthy person becomes filthy himself," and therefore it is not an ornament at all. 

Based on this, we can understand the difference between the redemption from Mitzrayim and the future redemption. Although for the future redemption it is written, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares," in the redemption from Mitzrayim it is written, "And the Bnei Yisrael went up armed." This is because for the future it is written, "And the spirit of impurity I will remove from the earth," whereas in the redemption from Mitzrayim, the evil was still in its strength, as explained in Tanya regarding "for the people fled," which is because the evil was in its strength. But since the redemption had to be "in the blink of an eye," they did not want to "bother" with it. Since there was still evil, they needed weapons. This is not the case for the future, when "the spirit of impurity I will remove from the earth," then "they shall beat their swords into plowshares."

In the future redemption, there will be, in general, two levels, in time and also in the soul. For the *amei ha'aretz* (common people), or as stated in *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding the *Erev Rav*, and at the beginning of the time of redemption, it will be like this for all of Yisrael, similar to what our Sages said, "There is no difference between this world and the days of Mashiach except for the subjugation of the kingdoms," and there will be a need for a sword. However, for the *talmidei chachamim*—and as stated in *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding Yisrael who are not from the *Erev Rav*—and afterwards it will be so for everyone, that "the spirit of impurity I will remove from the earth," they will not need a sword. This is what is meant by "They shall beat their swords into plowshares... nation shall not lift up sword against nation." This is the meaning of "the exaltations of El are in their throat, and a two-edged sword in their hand"—although it speaks of the future to come, as stated at the beginning of the psalm, "Sing to Hashem a new song, His praise in the assembly of the Chassidim," nevertheless, at the beginning of the time of redemption, there will be a need for weapons. Regarding this, it says that "the exaltations of El will be in their throat, and a two-edged sword in their hand," to take vengeance on the nations, for the nations will still exist before they are refined to "serve Him with one shoulder." Also, according to what is explained in *Likutei Torah* on the verse, "All nations surrounded me," that this is "the nation that is within you"—the body and the *nefesh habahamit*—they will need a two-edged sword in their hand. Afterwards, in the perfection of the redemption, "They shall beat their swords into plowshares... nation shall not lift up sword against nation," for "the spirit of impurity I will remove from the earth," and "I will grant peace in the land" through the "Prince of Peace," Dovid, King Mashiach, in the future redemption, speedily in our days.

## Wednesday, 15 Menachem Av, 5735

"There were no better days for the Jewish people than the fifteenth of Av and Yom Kippur." We must understand the reason for this comparison and the common denominator between the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur. We must also understand why this statement ("There were no better days...") appears as the conclusion and seal of Tractate Taanis, given that "better days" (Yomim Tovim) are a matter of joy, the opposite of the concept of fasting. This is especially true since the phrasing "There were no better days for the Jewish people than the fifteenth of Av..." implies that the joy of the 15th of Av (and Yom Kippur) is greater than the joy of the Yomim Tovim that are a positive commandment from the Torah, as it is written, "And you shall rejoice in your festivals." According to this, the connection of this subject to the conclusion of Tractate Taanis is even more difficult to explain.

The connection between the 15th of Av and the concept of fasting is also proven by the fact that the Mishnah links the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur. Yom Kippur is the only fast day mandated by the Torah, and this fast is unique and distinct from other fasts, including the fact that the four fasts (as well as the fasts enumerated in Megillas Taanis, many of which are brought in the Tur) will be transformed into joy and gladness, whereas the fast of Yom Kippur will continue even in the future. From the fact that the Mishnah links the 15th of Av with Yom Kippur, it is evident that the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is relevant not only to the subject of fasting in Tractate Taanis—which is why the statement "There were no better days for the Jewish people than the 15th of Av" is the conclusion of Tractate Taanis—but also to the fast of Yom Kippur.

The reason why the 15th of Av is a Yom Tov—which, on the face of it, is not understood, as the Gemara asks: "Yom Kippur is understandable because it contains forgiveness and atonement, and it is the day the second Tablets were given, but what is the 15th of Av?"—is brought in the *derushim* from *Pri Etz Chaim*, because it is then that the moon is full. The *derushim* raise a difficulty: every month has a 15th day (when the moon is full), so what is the specific superiority of the 15th of Av? Furthermore, the statement "There were no better days... than the 15th of Av" implies that it is even higher than the 15th of Nissan (Pesach) and the 15th of Tishrei (Sukkos).

One of the reasons given in the Gemara there for why the 15th of Av is a Yom Tov is that it is when the strength of the sun wanes. This is difficult to understand: the waning of the sun's strength is a phenomenon of the celestial luminaries and does not relate to the affairs and actions of man (unlike the other reasons mentioned in the Gemara there). If so, what is the Yom Tov when the sun's strength wanes? Even though the waning of the sun's strength (despite being a celestial phenomenon) has consequences regarding affairs and actions on earth—as the Gemara states there, "they would no longer cut wood for the arrangement [of the altar]," etc.—the language of the Gemara ("From the fifteenth of Av onwards, the strength of the sun wanes") implies that the Yom Tov and joy of the 15th of Av is due to this fact itself, and not merely due to the consequences resulting from it. Therefore, it must be that this waning of the sun's strength is also related to the *avodah* of man. This is the equivalence between the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur: just as the atonement of Yom Kippur is achieved through the *avodah* of man—for even though "the essence of the day atones," the atonement is achieved with greater intensity and power through man's *avodah*; and furthermore, even the atonement that comes from the essence of the day is only when man "holds on" to the essence of the day, for "the atonement of the day of Yom Kippur does not atone [for one who does not repent]"—so too, regarding the waning of the sun's strength on the 15th of Av (for even after it wanes, the sun still has strength; it is only that its strength has diminished), it is a matter that relates to the *avodah* of man.

The point of the explanation regarding the superiority of the 15th of Av, even though every 15th of the month is the fullness of the moon, is explained in the *derushim* as being because the ascent of the 15th of Av comes after the descent of Tisha B'Av. The matter is as follows: it is stated in the *Yalkut*, "A lion came in the sign of the lion and destroyed Ariel... in order that a lion [this is the Ribono shel Olam, as it is written, 'A lion has roared, who will not fear?'] should come in the sign of the lion [and I will turn their mourning into joy], and build Ariel," etc. This means that the exile and destruction that occurred in the sign of the lion (in the fifth month) was only in order that the "Lion" should come and build Ariel, the Third Beis Hamikdash, which is higher than the First and Second. For the elevation of the Third Beis Hamikdash (which is higher than the First and Second) comes specifically through the preceding exile. This is the superiority of the 15th of Av over the 15th of every month, including the 15th of Nissan (Pesach) and the 15th of Tishrei (Sukkos). Since the ascent of the 15th of Av comes after the great descent of Tisha B'Av ("A lion came... and destroyed Ariel"), it is a much greater ascent. As is known, the rule regarding ascents and descents is that the ascent corresponds to the depth of the descent. Although the ascent of the 15th of Nissan (Pesach) also comes after the descent of the exile in Egypt, the Jewish people were then in a state of *tzaddikim*. And the ascent of the 15th of Tishrei (Sukkos), although it comes as a continuation of the *teshuvah* of Yom Kippur, since the general *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos* is a spiritual *avodah*—for even though the *mitzvos* are clothed in physical objects, *tzitzis* in physical wool and *tefillin* in physical parchment, the essence of the *mitzvos* is to introduce spirituality into physicality—the descent caused by sins and iniquities (the opposite of the *mitzvos*) relates to physicality only as it relates to spirituality. Consequently, this is not yet the ultimate descent, and therefore the ascent of Sukkos, which comes through *teshuvah*, is not the ultimate ascent. In contrast, the descent of Tisha B'Av, where "He poured out His wrath upon wood and stones" (physical wood and stones), means that the descent (due to sins) affected the physicality of the world, than which there is nothing lower. Since the descent of Tisha B'Av is a descent than which there is nothing lower, the ascent of the 15th of Av that follows this descent is a much greater ascent, corresponding to the intensity of the descent. This is the concept of "double comfort," "I, even I, am He who comforts you," a double "I." Based on this, it is understood that the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is higher even than the Yom Tov of Yom Kippur. This is why they said, "There were no better days for the Jewish people than the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur," placing the 15th of Av before Yom Kippur, even though the matter of the 15th of Av (according to all the reasons in the Gemara) was innovated many years after Yom Kippur, and even in the times of the year (every year), Yom Kippur (which is in the month of Tishrei) precedes the 15th of Av, because the Yom Tov of the 15th of Av is higher (precedes in superiority) than the Yom Tov of Yom Kippur.

However, it still needs to be understood: "And you shall rejoice in your festivals" is a positive commandment from the Torah, unlike the Yom Tov (and joy) of the 15th of Av. Furthermore, the Yom Tov of Yom Kippur is not from the Torah (for there is no obligation to rejoice on Yom Kippur; on the contrary, the commandment of Yom Kippur is "You shall afflict your souls." It is only that since it is a day of forgiveness and atonement, the matter of joy follows as a natural consequence). If so, how can the Yom Tov (and joy) of the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur be greater than the Yom Tovim that one is commanded by the Torah to rejoice in? The matter is that in the elevation of "the moon standing in its fullness," there are two general categories. The category of "the moon standing in its fullness" as it is according to the order and law of the Torah (from which the order of the moon's changes according to nature was derived), and the category of "the moon standing in its fullness" as it is according to the *avodah* of man, as it is above the level of the law of the Torah. For the Jewish people are above the Torah, which is why the Jewish people are called "groom" and the Torah is called "bride," because the Jewish people influence the Torah. This is the concept of "Blessing the Torah first," that the Jewish people bless and draw down into the Torah from the level of the Giver of the Torah, similar to how David would "connect the Torah to the Holy One, blessed be He." This is the superiority of the 15th of Av over the 15th of Nissan and the 15th of Tishrei, because the fullness of the moon on the 15th of Nissan and the 15th of Tishrei is the "moon standing in its fullness" that comes from the order of the Torah—that is, from the *avodah* of man as it is measured according to the Torah. Even though this *avodah* brings about an elevation in the world, the elevation is measured and limited. In contrast, the fullness of the moon on the 15th of Av is the "moon standing in its fullness" as it is from the *avodah* of the souls of the Jewish people that is above the Torah—the *avodah* of "with all your might."

In order to explain these three matters (the world as it is in itself, for the world was created in its fullness; what is added to the world through the *avodah* of man as it is according to the measure of the Torah; and the innovation achieved through the *avodah* of "with all your might" that is above measure, even above the measure of the Torah), the *derushim* bring the interpretation of the verse, "And the profit of the earth is in all; the king is served by the field," that there are three levels in this. The level of "earth" as it is in itself; the "profit of the earth" through the level of "all"; and the level of "the king is served by the field," which is higher even than the "profit of the earth." The "profit of the earth" is the level of "field" (as it is in itself) [for a field is part of the earth, but because it is of the choicest of the earth, suitable for sowing and growth, it is the "profit of the earth"]. However, "the king is served by the field" (the elevation achieved in the field through *avodah*) is higher than the "profit of the earth." The matter is that "field" refers to Gan Eden. Just as a field is of the choicest of the earth, suitable for sowing and growth (as above), so too Gan Eden is the choicest of the world, suitable for the revelation of light—that is, for a level of light that is higher than the light that shines in the world in general. The light that shines in the world in general is from the level of the *Midos*, which is why existence is from the level of the six days of creation or the seven days of creation. And even though the world was created with ten utterances (which include the three *mochin*), this is the *mochin* as they are within the *Midos*. But the light that shines in Gan Eden is (also) from the level of *Gimmel Rishonos*. For this reason, there is another superiority of Gan Eden over the world in general: the revelation in the world is in the category of "knowledge of existence," while in Gan Eden it is the revelation of the essence. This is what "the profit of the earth" is—the level of Gan Eden (as the profit of the earth is the level of field), because Gan Eden is the level of the world as it is a complete structure in all ten *Sefiros*, *Zayin Tachtonos* and *Gimmel Rishonos*, the level of "the world was created in its fullness." And this is also what is meant by "And the profit of the earth is in all"—the profit (and superiority) in Gan Eden over the world in general is through "all." "All" refers to the *Sefirah* of *Yesod*, which is called "all" after the fifty gates of *Binah* ("all" in *gematria* is fifty) that are drawn into it, and through this, there is also drawn into it from the level of *Chochmah*, for *Chochmah* and *Binah* are the general *mochin*. The aforementioned elevation in Gan Eden, which is the "profit of the earth" [that the level of *Gimmel Rishonos* shines in it, and from this it also has the revelation of the essence], is the level of "field" in itself. However, through *avodah*—"the king is served by the field"—an elevation is achieved that is higher than the level of "profit of the earth." As it is stated in the *Zohar*, "The king is served by the field—who is the King? This is the Supreme King." This level is above the world (even as it is in its perfection, the "profit of the earth"). For the entire matter of the creation of the world is only from the ten utterances, whose beginning is *Chochmah*, and the "Supreme King" is the level of *Keter* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

Since the level of *Keter* (the Supreme King) is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the *avodah* in man that draws down this level must also be above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* of his own powers, in the category of "with all your might." For through the *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos* as it is in the category of measure and limitation (the *Hishtalshelus* in man), the light that is in the category of *Hishtalshelus* is drawn down. And even though through the *avodah* of Torah and *mitzvos* (even when the *avodah* is in measure and limitation) a light higher than the level of Gan Eden is drawn down—as is proven from what is written, "And He placed him in Gan Eden to work it and to guard it," "to work it" refers to the 248 positive commandments and "to guard it" refers to the 365 negative commandments; meaning that Gan Eden for Adam HaRishon was not a place of receiving reward, but rather Gan Eden was the place of his *avodah*, and through his *avodah* in Gan Eden he drew down lights higher than the level of Gan Eden—nevertheless, what is drawn down through *avodah* as it is in measure according to the Torah is only what relates to the world, and it is what causes the existence of the world through the Torah, as it is stated in the Gemara, "If the Jewish people accept the Torah, you [the world] will exist." But the drawing down of the light that is above *Hishtalshelus* is specifically through the *avodah* of "with all your might."

Based on the above, it is understood why the *maamar* begins with the interpretation of "the king is served by the field" before explaining the superiority of the 15th of Av over the 15th of Nissan and the 15th of Tishrei. For the superiority of the 15th of Av over the 15th of Nissan and the 15th of Tishrei is like the superiority of "the king is served by the field" over the level of "field" as it is in itself. The superiority of Gan Eden (field), which is the level of "profit of the earth"—that is, that the world is in its perfection (as above)—is like "the moon standing in its fullness." However, this perfection is only the perfection of the world, and even what is added to Gan Eden through the *avodah* of "to work it and to guard it" (as it is in the measure of the Torah) is only what relates to the world. The same applies to the fullness of the moon of the 15th of Nissan and the 15th of Tishrei, which is from the matter of the Torah. In contrast, the fullness of the moon of the 15th of Av, since it comes after the descent of Tisha B'Av—which descent awakens the *avodah* of "with all your might" (as will be explained later)—is like "the king is served by the field," a light that is above *Hishtalshelus*.

In order to arrive at the *avodah* of "with all your might" that is above measure and limitation, one must contemplate the constraints and boundaries of the world. For by feeling the constraints and boundaries of the world, this itself awakens him to exit the constraints and boundaries, and for his *avodah* to be above measure and limitation. And the more he feels the constraints and boundaries—that in addition to the constraints and boundaries of the world in general, there are also things that prevent and distract from the *avodah* of Hashem, such as hunger and illness [for when a person is hungry and ill, it is impossible for him to understand and contemplate, etc., and he cannot serve Hashem (meaning that in order to serve Hashem when he is ill, a special effort is required)], and even more so the concealments and darkness during the time of exile—the more he feels the constraints and boundaries, the more it brings him to the *avodah* of "with all your might," the exit from constraint and boundary. In this, it is understood why the aforementioned *derush* brings the second interpretation in the *Zohar*, that "the king is served by the field" is for the worse, that "field" is the level of the field of the "other side" ("in the field she found him"), and "the king is served by the field" is that the *Sefirah* of *Malchus* descends, etc., and is hidden in the field of the "other side." For the contemplation of the matter of "the king is served by the field" as it is for the worse—which is the concept of the exile of the *Shechinah* [for the reason for this, that the *Shechinah* is in exile, is the exile of the Jewish people, that we were exiled because of our sins]—this contemplation awakens him so that his *avodah* will be above measure and limitation, and through this, a light that is above *Hishtalshelus* is drawn down, "the king is served by the field" for the better.

This is "A lion came in the sign of the lion and destroyed Ariel... in order that a lion [this is the Ribono shel Olam, as it is written, 'A lion has roared, who will not fear?'] should come in the sign of the lion and build Ariel," the Third Beis Hamikdash. For the "Lion" [the Ribono shel Olam] is the concept of the revelation of *Keter* that is above *Hishtalshelus*. Since the revelation that is above *Hishtalshelus* is through the *avodah* that is above measure and limitation, therefore, in order for the "Lion" to come, there had to be "a lion came," etc., for the bitterness and pain that comes from the constraint of exile is what awakens the *avodah* that is above limitation, as above. Therefore, specifically through the preceding exile, the "Lion" will come and build Ariel, the Third Beis Hamikdash. This is also the superiority of the Beis Hamikdash of the future over the First and Second Temples: that specifically in the Third Beis Hamikdash (because it is after the preceding final exile) there will be (the essence of) the revelation of the level of *Ein Sof* that is above *Hishtalshelus* ("the Lion will come"). This is the reason why the Beis Hamikdash of the future will be in the category of eternity (whereas the First and Second Temples were in the category of interruption), for from the perspective of the revelation of *Ein Sof* that is above *Hishtalshelus*, the concept of interruption does not apply. This is what is written, "The sanctuary, O Lord, which Your hands have established; the Lord shall reign forever and ever," the interpretation of which is (as written in *Emek HaMelech* in the aforementioned *derush*) that because "The sanctuary... which Your hands have established"—meaning that the Beis Hamikdash of the future will be by the hands of the Ribono shel Olam Himself [the level of *Ein Sof* that is above *Hishtalshelus*]—therefore "the Lord shall reign forever and ever," that it will be in the category of eternity.

The power that exists during the time of exile for the *avodah* of "with all your might," through which the Beis Hamikdash of the future will be, is from the revelations of the First and Second Temples that were before the exile. These revelations give the power to illuminate the darkness of the exile with "the candle of the mitzvah and the light of the Torah," until through this "the night will shine as the day" in the future redemption. The reason for this (why the First and Second Temples give the power for the *avodah* of "with all your might" through which the Third Beis Hamikdash will be) is because even in the First and Second Temples (although there was an interruption in them) there was a "miniature" of the Third Beis Hamikdash. The same applies to the *Mishkan*, which was a "miniature" of the Beis Hamikdash of the future. Even though the *Mishkan* is called *ohel* (tent), a temporary dwelling (unlike the Temple which is called *bayis* (house), a permanent dwelling), the *Mishkan* specifically, because it was the work of the hands of Moshe, exists forever. In this, it is understood why, after bringing in the aforementioned *derush* the interpretation of *Emek HaMelech* that "The sanctuary, O Lord, which Your hands have established" refers to the Beis Hamikdash of the future, he adds that the implication from the Gemara and Midrashim is that it refers to the *Mishkan* and the Temple (even though this interpretation does not seemingly relate to the content of the matter explained in this *derush*). For the fact that in "The sanctuary, O Lord, which Your hands have established" there are these two interpretations (that it refers to the Beis Hamikdash of the future, and that it refers to the *Mishkan* and the Temple) is because in the First and Second Temples (and also in the *Mishkan*) there was a "miniature" of the Beis Hamikdash of the future, as above. Therefore, the *maamar* also brings the interpretation that "The sanctuary, O Lord, which Your hands have established" refers to the *Mishkan* and the Temple, for in this he explains that the power in this time of exile for the *avodah* to draw down the Third Beis Hamikdash is from the First and Second Temples (and also from the *Mishkan*).

However, the essence of the matter of "The sanctuary, O Lord, which Your hands have established" is specifically in the Beis Hamikdash of the future. In contrast, in the *Mishkan* and the Temple (First and Second), it is only a "miniature" of the Beis Hamikdash of the future. For the interpretation of "Your hands have established" is that it is made by the hands of the Ribono shel Olam Himself—the level of *Keter* that is above *Hishtalshelus*—and the revelation of this level will be in the Beis Hamikdash of the future, when specifically there will be the true matter of "the moon standing in its fullness," the level of perfection that is above *Hishtalshelus*. For the level of "the moon standing in its fullness" that was in the First Temple [as our Sages said, that the Beis Hamikdash was built by Shlomo, because Shlomo was in the fifteenth generation from Avraham, and then the disk of the moon was filled] is like the level of "profit of the earth," whereas the perfection in the Beis Hamikdash of the future is the concept of "the king is served by the field." In order to draw down the level of "the king is served by the field" as it is for the better, there had to be the exile first, the level of "the king is served by the field" as it is for the worse. Through the descent of *Malchus* to the lowest extremity, until it is served by the field of the "other side," there will be the ascent of *Malchus* to the highest level, until the level of *Atik* shines in it. The reason for this—that Yerushalayim, which is the level of *Malchus*, is called *naveh sha'anan* (a tranquil abode), which refers to the level of *Atik*—is because the level of *Atik* will shine in *Malchus*.

This is also the connection of the 15th of Av to Yom Kippur. For on Yom Kippur is the ascent of *Malchus*. This is why Yom Kippur is a day on which one is obligated in five prayers, in each of which *Malchus* ascends to a higher level, until in the prayer of *Ne'ilah* it ascends to the level of the interior of *Atik*. This is why we say then "The Lord is the God" seven times, "Blessed be the name" three times, and "Hear O Israel" once, which is from the perspective of the ascent of *Malchus* into *Atika*, as explained in many places. This is the connection of the 15th of Av to Yom Kippur, for on the 15th of Av *Malchus* ascends to the level of the interior of *Atik*. On the contrary, since the ascent of the 15th of Av is after the descent of Tisha B'Av, the ascent of *Malchus* of the 15th of Av is higher than the ascent of Yom Kippur. It is, as it were, like the ascent that will be in the future redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, who will fight the wars of Hashem and be victorious [meaning he will have to fight with opponents who stand in strength, etc., and he will be victorious] and build the Beis Hamikdash in its place and gather the outcasts of Israel, who will gather all the sparks of holiness, and the outcasts of Israel literally—the matter of the ingathering of the exiles, very soon in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## 15 Av, 5738

"And you shall teach them to your children and speak of them." Following this, it is written, "And you shall bind them as a sign upon your hand..."—the mitzvah of Tefillin. Regarding this, our Sages said that the entire Torah is compared to Tefillin, meaning that the intent here is to the mitzvos of the Torah. Thus, the verse prioritizes the matter of Torah over the matter of mitzvos. It is a well-known point of precision raised by our Rebbes that in the second paragraph of Shema, it is written: "And you shall bind them as a sign upon your hand... and you shall teach them to your children..." This verse follows the reverse order, prioritizing the matter of mitzvos (the mitzvah of Tefillin) over the matter of Torah.

Furthermore, one must understand why the order where Torah precedes mitzvos is found in the first paragraph of Shema, while the order where mitzvos precede Torah is found specifically in the second paragraph. One must also understand the precision of the language regarding Torah: in the first paragraph, it says "And you shall teach them" (*v'shinantam*), which Rashi (based on the Midrash of our Sages) explains as a term of sharpness—that they should be "sharp in your mouth," so that if a person asks you a matter (of halacha), you will not need to stutter, but can answer him immediately (and only afterwards is it written "and you shall speak of them"). In the second paragraph, however, it says "And you shall teach them" (*v'limadtem*), a term that includes all modes of study (even if the study is not in a manner of being "sharp in your mouth").

2. This can be explained by first clarifying the concept of the fifteenth of Av (which is a matter of *hazman gerama*—determined by the time). The Mishnah states: "There were no festivals for Israel like the fifteenth of Av and Yom Kippur" (as the Gemara explains the details at length). It is explained in the discourses of our Rebbes that the phrasing of our Sages, "there were no festivals," implies that 15 Av is even higher than the festivals of Pesach, Shavuos, and Sukkos. Seemingly, even if one were to explain the superiority of 15 Av over Shavuos as being due to the elevation of the fifteenth day of the month, when the moon is in its fullness, one still needs an explanation for the superiority of 15 Av over 15 Nissan (Pesach) and 15 Tishrei (Sukkos), even though all three share the elevation of the fifteenth day of the month when the moon is in its fullness.

The well-known explanation for this is that the superiority of 15 Av lies in the fact that it occurs in the month of Av, which begins with a great descent—a descent after a descent—which is the concept of "having been punished doubly" due to the spiritual decline in which they "sinned doubly." Therefore, the subsequent ascent—which comes after the avodah of teshuvah in a manner of "weeping," a double weeping—is also in a manner of double consolation, reaching an ascent so sublime that it is incomparable to the ascent of 15 Nissan or 15 Tishrei.

3. More specifically, 15 Tishrei is also an ascent that follows a descent. As is known, the difference between Nissan and Tishrei is that the essence of Nissan is the avodah of *tzaddikim*. When Bnei Yisrael left Egypt, they were on the level of *tzaddikim*, for a convert who has converted is like a newborn child. Thus, the festival of Pesach corresponds to Avraham Avinu, whose attribute is *Chesed*, and whose avodah was in a manner of influence from above to below, as it is written, "And he called there in the name of Hashem, the G-d of the world." This means he drew Elokus into the world so that the Ribono shel Olam would have a dwelling place in the lower realms—not merely in the sense that Hashem is the G-d *of* the world, but in a way that Elokus and the world become one, which is the general concept of the avodah of *tzaddikim*.

In contrast, Tishrei: the name "Tishrei" itself follows the order of *Tashrak* (reverse order), which is from below to above. Also, the avodah of the month of Tishrei is the avodah of teshuvah, which is why it comes after the preparatory avodah of the month of Elul, with regret for the past and then a good resolution for the future, until one arrives at 15 Tishrei, when the moon is in its fullness, which is the festival of Sukkos, culminating in Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah.

However, this concept—that the month of Tishrei is also an ascent following a descent due to the avodah of teshuvah within it—is only relative to the month of Nissan. Relative to the month of Av (where the descent was incomparable—the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, exile, etc., in all details), the avodah of the month of Tishrei, which is the avodah of teshuvah, is akin to the avodah of *tzaddikim*. The point is that the avodah of teshuvah in Tishrei is a process of going step by step, which is why there must be the preparation of "a month of days," as explained in *Likutei Torah* of the Arizal and the Alter Rebbe, referring to the avodah of Elul, through which one progresses step by step until reaching the level of Rosh Hashanah, and subsequently to the perfection of the full moon during Sukkos.

In the month of Av, by contrast, it is not a process of going from step to step. Rather, the ascent occurs immediately after the ultimate descent of Tisha B'Av, from one extreme to the other. The concept of consolation is already present on Tisha B'Av itself, which is why we say in the Mincha prayer, "Comfort Zion and build Jerusalem," because that is when Mashiach, the savior of Israel, is born—whose essence is the point, the core, and the reality of teshuvah. This means that the birth of Mashiach begins on that very day and at that very moment of the ultimate descent, in a manner that is drawn down openly in several matters that begin after midday of Tisha B'Av, the reason for which is that it is the time of Mashiach's birth. And only so that the revelation may be complete, one must wait until 15 Av.

This is similar to what we find regarding the reason for the festival of 15 Av being the day the "dying of the desert" ceased; until 15 Av there was doubt, and when the moon reached its fullness, it was clarified that the "dying of the desert" had already ceased on Tisha B'Av, and they were a complete congregation, of whom it is written, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are alive, all of you, today," standing ready to enter the land in the true and complete Geulah through the first redeemer, which is connected to the Geulah through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, the final redeemer. (It is known that all exiles are named after Egypt, because they contain the essence of the Egyptian exile, and similarly, the redemption from Egypt exists in all redemptions, and all redemptions are named after it, until the final redemption—the true and complete Geulah from this last exile, after which there is no further exile, regarding which it is said, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders.")

It should be noted that this is also the case regarding the weekly parsha: Tisha B'Av and the elevation within it occur in Parshas Va'eschanan (and in many years, 15 Av also falls in Parshas Va'eschanan), which comes "in a single moment" after Parshas Devarim and Chazon. This is the superiority of the month of Av even over the avodah of the month of Tishrei (and certainly over the avodah of the month of Nissan), because the avodah of Tishrei is in a manner of going from step to step, a movement belonging to the avodah of *tzaddikim*, whereas the ascent of the month of Av is from one extreme to the other, which is the movement of the avodah of *baalei teshuvah*, for the essence of teshuvah is "in a single hour and in a single moment."

This is also the precision in the statement of our Sages, "There were no festivals for Israel like the fifteenth of Av and Yom Kippur"—first 15 Av is mentioned, and then Yom Kippur, to teach that the superiority of 15 Av is greater than that of Yom Kippur. For although regarding Yom Kippur it is explained in the Gemara that its superiority is "because it contains forgiveness and atonement," which is the matter of the avodah of teshuvah (and from this we learn that the essence of 15 Av is also the matter of teshuvah), nevertheless, the superiority of 15 Av is greater than that of Yom Kippur, because in it, the avodah of teshuvah is emphasized "in a single hour and in a single moment," from one extreme to the other, whereas in Yom Kippur, the avodah of teshuvah comes after a long avodah with many details and sub-details, starting from Rosh Chodesh Elul, as mentioned above.

4. The explanation of the general concept, as brought in the discourses, is the rule that the ascent is proportional to the descent. Therefore, when the descent is to the lowest possible depths, then "according to the pain is the reward," and it is precisely then that the ascent reaches the highest possible heights. This is similar to what is explained in many places: when a spark of holiness is found at the very bottom, this itself indicates that its root is at the very highest level, for everything that is highest descends and is found at the lowest. As it is brought in the writings of the Arizal and in the discourses of our Rebbes regarding the verse, "For man does not live by bread alone, but by everything that proceeds from the mouth of Hashem does man live"—that even though the "word of Hashem" exists within man, nevertheless, it is precisely through the "word of Hashem" that is in the bread, which is below man, that man lives with the "word of Hashem" that is within him. This is because the "word of Hashem" that is in the animate (and below that, in the vegetative and inanimate), which is below man, has its root in a higher place. Therefore, precisely through man's avodah in the "word of Hashem" that is in the inanimate, vegetative, and animate, to elevate them to their root and source (which is above the root of man), an elevation is also effected in man—"man shall live"—similar to the statement of our Sages, "The Ark carries those who carry it."

This is the same regarding the general concept of descents, starting from the descent of the *Seder Hishtalshelus* down to the descent of the exile, which is the essence of the month of Av and Tisha B'Av. Through this, the exile is realized in its simplest form, in the lowest manner—and through all this, one arrives at the greatest ascent. This is the purpose of the entire concept of exile; it is not for the sake of punishment, G-d forbid, but so that they may arrive at purity, and purity leads to holiness, and from holiness, one proceeds to the ultimate ascent—the coming of Eliyahu Hanavi and the resurrection of the dead. This begins with the resurrection of the dead as it is "the smallest of them," which in general is the avodah of *birurim* (refining), to refine the sparks of holiness that have fallen below, for "one who falls from his level is called dead," and by refining them, one revives them, and subsequently purifies and elevates them to the ultimate perfection, "as the mitzvah of Your will."

As mentioned above, this elevation (after the descent of exile) occurs openly already on Tisha B'Av at the beginning of the time (and prayer) of Mincha, when He "poured out His wrath," as it were, upon the wood and the stones—which showed openly the greatness of the love of Hashem, that He poured out all His wrath—completely, so that nothing remained of it, and immediately Mashiach, the savior of Israel, was born. And as stated, this matter comes to revelation in the manner of the conduct of Tisha B'Av after midday. But this is not yet the ultimate perfection of the revelation; it continues to be revealed from day to day, as the moon approaches the state of "the moon in its fullness," until the perfection of the revelation on the fifteenth of Av, which becomes a great festival, to the extent that "there were no festivals for Israel like the fifteenth of Av."

5. Now, based on what was stated above—that precisely through descending to the lowest depths can one effect an ascent to the highest heights, to a place higher than the place from which the descent occurred—we can also understand the superiority of the matter of *maaseh* (action/deed) over the matter of *talmud* (study), which is the general difference between mitzvos (action) and Torah (study). Torah's essence is an influence from above to below, and together with this, "Are not My words like fire," which is why words of Torah do not contract impurity—meaning that even when they are below, and even with someone who is in a state contrary to purity, even there they do not contract impurity. Mitzvos, by contrast, their essence is precisely in physical things, to the extent that even those mitzvos whose essence is understanding and comprehension in the mind or emotion in the heart are connected to physical limbs, the physical brain and the physical heart. Especially according to what is explained in many places, that the perfection of the avodah in the performance of these mitzvos is when a change is also effected in the physicality of the vessels of the mind and the vessels of the heart (contraction, expansion, and diffusion). And since in mitzvos there is the matter of descending lower (into physicality), therefore through them one reaches the highest of the high.

6. The explanation of this matter: there are two opinions (and both are the words of the living G-d) as to whether study is greater or action is greater. This is also the difference between the two orders in the verses (as mentioned, both are the words of the living G-d): the order in the first paragraph of Shema, where *v'shinantam* (study) is said first and then *v'kashartem* (action), follows the opinion that study is greater (for priority in Torah indicates priority in stature); and the order in the second paragraph of Shema, where *v'kashartem* is said first and then *v'limadtem* (study), follows the opinion that action is greater.

The point is that the essence of study is simply to know "the action that they shall do and those that they shall not do" (which is the general concept of mitzvos, positive and negative), and only afterwards can there be the performance of mitzvos in practice. This is the reason that study is greater, because study leads to action. This means that the matter of study is connected to the head of a person, which is called "head" because it is prior in stature and rules and governs the entire body. Its counterpart is the matter of mitzvos: the 248 positive mitzvos correspond to the 248 limbs, and the 365 negative mitzvos correspond to the 365 sinews, which are below the head; therefore, the decision of the head must come first as to how the conduct of the body will be. And only when both matters of Torah and mitzvos already exist is there room for two opinions as to what comes first, study or action, and even for the second opinion that action is greater, due to the elevation that comes precisely through the descent below (which is similar to the general elevation of the month of Av, as mentioned above).

Nevertheless, it is said *v'shinantam* before *v'kashartem*—study before action—because even though the superiority of action is great, in order for the matter of action to be possible, there must first be the matter of study that leads to action. Just as it is in the general avodah of man: although it was stated above that man's vitality is precisely through the "word of Hashem" that is in the bread which is below man (due to the superiority of the descent below), nevertheless, in order for man to live through eating the bread, he must first prepare the bread so that it is fit for human consumption, as it is stated in the Gemara: "Does a man bring wheat and chew wheat? Rather, he must make the wheat into human food (with the help of his 'help-mate')." Likewise, it is regarding the matter of study and action: although action is greater (due to the superiority of the descent below), nevertheless, in order for the matter of action to be possible, there must be the precedence of study. And through this, the elevation of action is also added to the study, just as it is added to man through the eating of bread, as mentioned above.

7. This is also the explanation (in the inner dimension of Torah) for the order of the two paragraphs of Shema and the differences between them. Our Sages said: (Why) does the paragraph of Shema precede the paragraph of *V'hayah Im Shamoa*? The priority in the order of the verses is because that is the order of avodah. Since the order of avodah is that first there must be the study of Torah, and then the study leads to action, therefore in the first paragraph the order is *v'shinantam* and then *v'kashartem*, for through the study (*v'shinantam*) one knows how to perform the mitzvos (*v'kashartem*) and performs them in their perfection (and this serves as a preparation for the performance of mitzvos in the time to come, "as the mitzvah of Your will"). This is also the precision of the language "v'shinantam"—that they should be sharp in your mouth so that if a person asks you a matter of halacha, etc.—because in order for study to lead to action, it must be in a manner of "concluding the halacha in practice."

However, after the paragraph of Shema has preceded, so that the study (*v'shinantam*) and the action that comes through it (*v'kashartem*) already exist, then comes the second paragraph, where the order is first *v'kashartem* and afterwards the study of Torah. And since the study to "conclude the halacha in practice" already exists beforehand (which is what is stated in the first paragraph, *v'shinantam*... *v'kashartem*), therefore it says here *v'limadtem* simply, which includes all modes of study (even the mode of "study and receive reward").

There is another point here: it is known that in the time to come, action will be greater. Therefore, the order *v'kashartem* and then *v'limadtem* (action is greater) is said specifically in the second paragraph, because among the differences between the first and second paragraphs is that the first is in the language of command (in the past and present), while the second is in the language of command and also in the language of narrative (in the future). The narrative is that "you will turn aside and serve," etc., and afterwards there will be the matter of teshuvah, which is what is meant by "And you shall place these My words," etc. And therefore it says afterwards *v'kashartem* and *v'limadtem*, because in the time to come, action will be greater.

8. This is the general concept of "the day that causes it"—the fifteenth of Av—which is the perfection of the ascent after the descent of Tisha B'Av, as it was drawn down in revelation at the time the Beis Hamikdash existed. To the extent that even in the time of exile, there are several customs on 15 Av because in the time of the Beis Hamikdash it was a great festival for many reasons stated in the Gemara, and in *Pri Etz Chaim* (cited in the discourses of our Rebbes, *D'H Nechamu*), it lists seven good qualities of that day, which is called "Yesod," which is the seventh. Through all this, 15 Av attains its superiority and level as it will be in the time to come, when the greatness of the elevation that was in the descent of the exile will be revealed, and then there will also be "action is greater."

And so it will be for us, very soon: through the avodah of teshuvah during the time of exile (as hinted at in the second paragraph of Shema in the future tense), the verse will be fulfilled: "And Hashem your G-d will return your captivity and have mercy on you, and He will return and gather you from all the nations," etc. This means that the *Shechinah* that is in exile will return from exile together with Bnei Yisrael, and in a manner that "you will be gathered one by one, Bnei Yisrael," that the Ribono shel Olam gathers each and every one of Israel—through the "one" that is within him—and leads him to greet Mashiach Tzidkeinu, with our youth and our elders, with our sons and our daughters, and their silver and their gold with them, with all the *birurim* and all the sparks of holiness, until "you shall empty out," etc., that they will refine everything, "and I will remove the spirit of impurity from the land," and they will see openly that "there were no festivals for Israel like the fifteenth of Av," below ten handbreadths, in Jerusalem the holy city and in the Holy Land in general, very soon, with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

## B's"d. Shabbos Parshas Eikev, 20 Menachem-Av, 5716

### B's"d. Shabbos Parshas Eikev, 20 Menachem-Av, 5716

(Unedited transcript)

"And it shall come to pass, because (*eikev*) you hearken to these ordinances, and keep and perform them, that Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness which He swore...". It is well known that there is a precise point to be made here: the word *tishme'un* (you shall hearken) implies a certainty—*tishme'un* definitely. This is because *eikev* refers to the time of *ikvesa d'meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach). Since this is the very last generation, therefore *tishme'un* definitely, because it is the final generation and it is impossible to wait any longer; there is no more time to delay the *birurim* (refinements), and therefore *tishme'un* definitely.

Now, there are three interpretations of the word *tishme'un*: *Tishme'un* as in understanding, as it is written, "Speak, for your servant understands (*shomei'a*)." *Tishme'un* as in gathering, as it is written, "And Shaul gathered (*vayishma*) the people." And *tishme'un* in its literal sense, as in hearing. The concept of hearing pertains to thought, for the ear is merely the vessel through which one hears, but the hearing itself takes place in the thought. Furthermore, the concept of hearing also pertains to speech, for one hears what is being spoken.

This is the meaning of "you shall hearken (*tishme'un*), and keep (*veshamartem*), and perform (*va'asitem*)." *Tishme'un* is thought, as mentioned above that hearing is in the thought. *Veshamartem* is speech, as the saying goes, "Keep (*shamor*) refers to the Mishnah." This is the halachic ruling as it is expressed in speech. When the intellect is in the thought, it is still in a state of concealment, where there are arguments for what is permitted and pure, and arguments for the opposite. This is not the case when the intellect comes into the open through speech; then the halachic ruling is established. At that point, there is no nourishment for the *chitzonim* (external forces); when it is still in concealment, there is a possibility for nourishment, but when it is revealed, they have no nourishment. This is why "Keep refers to the Mishnah"—the Mishnah, whose essence is the revelation of intellect through speech, acts as a guard so that there will be no nourishment, etc. And *va'asitem* is action. Thus, *tishme'un*, *veshamartem*, and *va'asitem* correspond to thought, speech, and action.

The beginning of this is from the aspect of *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* (thought, speech, and action) within the thought itself. This corresponds to the three interpretations of the word *tishme'un*: hearing as understanding is the thought within the thought; hearing as gathering is the action within the thought; and hearing in its literal sense is the speech within the thought, where one hears what is being spoken. This is the meaning of "And it shall come to pass, because (*eikev*) you hearken...": when you hearken in the aspect of *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* within the thought, and subsequently *tishme'un*, *veshamartem*, and *va'asitem* in actual *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh*, then "Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness which He swore." These three matters—covenant, kindness, and oath—are the *hemshech* (drawing down) from above.

*Covenant* is action, for the concept of making a covenant is that one cuts a whole thing into two and passes between them, which ensures that the love between them will be constant, even in a situation where there is no logical reason for the love—not from the aspect of speech, and not even from the aspect of thought. Nevertheless, the love remains due to the *krisus bris* (cutting of the covenant), which is a matter of actual deed. *Kindness* is thought, for kindness is a feeling of the heart and mind, and therefore it is included in thought. Specifically, it is stated here "He will keep the kindness," as explained regarding the difference between "doing kindness" and "preserving kindness": "doing kindness" is the act of kindness, while "preserving kindness" is keeping the kindness in one's heart and thought. And *oath* is speech.
