Thus, "And it shall come to pass, because..." means that when the *avodah* (service) from below to above is in thought, speech, and action, then there will be a drawing down of thought, speech, and action from above to below.

One must understand the reason for the change in order: in the *avodah* from below to above, the *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* are stated in their order—first thought, then speech and action—whereas in the drawing down from above to below, action is stated first, followed by thought and speech. Seemingly, since the drawing down from above comes about through the *avodah* of man, the order of the drawing down from above should follow the order of the *avodah*. What is the reason that in the *avodah* the order is that action comes after thought and speech, while in the drawing down from above, action comes before thought and speech?

2) The matter is as follows: The entirety of man's *avodah* comes through *hisbonenus* (contemplation). The point of *avodah* is as our Sages said, "Which is the *avodah* in the heart? This is prayer." Before this is the contemplation of *Krias Shema* and its blessings, etc. It is written, "Hear, O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One." The *Aleph* of *Echad* (One) points to the *Ein Sof*, the Master of the world; the *Ches* points to the seven heavens and the earth; and the *Dalet* points to the four directions. Now, the *Dalet* is a large *Dalet* (*dalet rabati*), which is the aspect of the greatness of speech. *Dalet* is the aspect of speech, and the large *Dalet* is the greatness of speech, which is the aspect of speech as it exists in thought.

The matter is, for example, as we see in a human being below: all the details of speech are included first in his thought, in one thought. This one thought is the source of all the individual speeches. Not only is the thought their source, but the thought includes within it all the details of speech even after they have been drawn forth from it. Similarly, one can understand this above: all the details of the ten utterances are included first in the aspect of one thought that includes them all. This is the aspect of the utterance of *Bereishis*, as our Sages said, "Bereishis is also an utterance." From this phrasing, two opposites are understood: on one hand, it is understood that the utterance of *Bereishis* is included among the utterances; on the other hand, it is understood that it is above them, for it needs to be made known that it is "also" an utterance, because the utterance of *Bereishis* is above the other utterances, and it is the aspect of the utterances as they are included in the thought. This is what they said, "Could it not have been created with one utterance?"—"one utterance" refers to the utterance of *Bereishis*, which includes within it all the other utterances; therefore, from the one utterance of *Bereishis*, the entire creation could be created. This is the aspect of the large *Dalet*, which is the matter of the details of the utterances as they are included in the one thought that includes them, which is the greatness of speech. For this is not the true essence of thought, but rather the matter of speech, yet it is speech as it is still included in the thought; this is the aspect of the greatness of speech. This is the matter of "Hashem is One," which is the *bitul* (nullification) as it is from the aspect of the large *Dalet*, the greatness of speech.

However, who are those who contemplate and work with this *bitul*? It is written, "Hear, O Israel," for "Israel arose in the thought". "Israel arose in the thought" refers to the *machshava ila'ah* (supernal thought), which is above the aspect of thought as it comes in a limited configuration. This means that it is not only higher in level than the aspect of thought in speech and speech in thought, but it is also above the aspect of thought within thought. Thought in speech is when one thinks how to speak—that is, how to explain in the details of the modes of speech—and this is not the true essence of thought, for this is the aspect of thought as it is enclothed in the matter of speech, thinking how to speak. Speech in thought is the thought itself that is above the matter of speech, but it still includes speech, as mentioned above regarding the greatness of speech, which is the one thought that includes the details of speech. The true essence of thought is the aspect of thought within thought, which is when one thinks the essence of the intellect before it is enclothed in letters; this is higher in level than the aspect of the intellect's thought after it is enclothed in letters.

The superiority of the intellect before it is enclothed in letters over the intellect after it is enclothed in letters is in two respects: First, the intellect that is enclothed in letters is configured in the details of the modes of explanation, which are the letters in which it is enclothed; the letters are the details of the modes of explaining the intellect. This is not the case before it is enclothed in letters, for it is not yet configured in the details of the modes of explanation, and therefore it is possible to explain it in several different ways. Second, the intellect before it is enclothed in letters is not only not configured in the details of the modes of explanation, but furthermore, the intellect itself is in a state of simplicity, for it is still abstracted from the details of the intellect itself (not just from the modes of explanation). However, the aspect of "Israel arose in the thought" is the aspect of *machshava ila'ah*, which is above even the aspect of thought within thought, for the aspect of thought within thought is in a state of configuration; even though it is abstracted from the modes and details, it is still, at the very least, in the configuration of intellect. This is not the case with *machshava ila'ah*, which is in a state of absolute simplicity.

3) But according to this, one must understand why the *neshamah* (soul) descended below. This is a descent from a high mountain to a deep pit in the literal sense, for since the root of the souls is in *machshava ila'ah*, to what purpose did it descend below? The matter is that this descent is for the sake of an ascent, and the ascent is higher even than the aspect of *machshava ila'ah*.

The matter is as follows: It is stated in the Gemara, "One verse says, 'And you shall gather your grain,' and another verse says, 'And strangers shall stand and feed your flocks'—this is when Israel does the will of the Omnipresent, and this is when they do not do the will of the Omnipresent." The well-known difficulty here is: the verse "And you shall gather your grain" is stated in the parsha of *Vehaya im shamo'a*, in which it is said, "And it shall come to pass, if you hearken... with all your heart and with all your soul." How can it be said of this that it is a time when they do not do the will of the Omnipresent? The Maggid of Mezritch explained that since the *avodah* is only "with all your heart and with all your soul," but the *avodah* of "with all your might" (*b'chol me'odecha*) is missing, it is called "not doing the will of the Omnipresent."

The matter is that the meaning of "doing the will of the Omnipresent" is that one must "make" (create) the will in the *makom* (place). *Makom* refers to the *seder hishtalshelus* (order of evolution), and the *Ohr Ein Sof* itself is above the aspect of *makom*, as it is stated in the Midrash on the verse, "Behold, there is a place (*makom*) with Me"—He is the place of the world, but the world is not His place. Therefore, one must "make" the will in the *makom*. This means that not only is the will in the aspect of *makom* a novelty, but the matter of the will itself is a novelty, for the *Ohr Ein Sof* is "not among all these attributes at all", for He is above all the *Sefiros* and above even the aspect of will within them. For there to be a will, this is a novelty, as it is written "Let there be will" (*yehi ratzon*), meaning that the aspect of will should be created. For there to be the aspect of will, this is through the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, as the saying goes, "There is pleasure before Me that I spoke and My will was done." By causing pleasure before Him, may He be blessed, through the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, then "My will is done," meaning the aspect of will is created. All this is the creation of will in general, which is done through the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* in general. However, in order to "do the will of the Omnipresent"—that is, to create the will in the *makom*—the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* alone is not enough; for this, one needs the love of "with all your might." To do the will in general, the *avodah* as it is from the aspect of "with all your heart and with all your soul" is sufficient, but to create the will in the *makom*, one needs the *avodah* specifically as it is from the aspect of "with all your might." This is why the second paragraph of *Krias Shema* is the aspect of "not doing the will of the Omnipresent," because the *avodah* of "with all your might" is missing in it; and through the *avodah* of "with all your might" specifically, one does the will of the Omnipresent.

4) The matter is that there are two levels of will: the lower will and the higher will. Both these aspects of will exist in the animal soul, and from this one can understand them in the divine soul, and similarly one can understand them above. The lower will in the animal soul is like the desire for business; this will is born from the intellect. When one understands how the matter of business is good for him, he desires it, and because of this will, he thinks about the business, speaks about it, and acts in it. This will is the lower will, since it is born from the intellect. The higher will is a will that is above the intellect, such as the desire to live, the desire for one's existence; this will is not from the intellect and reason. From this aspect of will—the desire to live—the will to engage in business is also found; the desire to live is configured by the intellect into specific desires according to the modes of the intellect that he has reasoned are good for him. All specific desires are the desire to live as it has been configured by the intellect.

The difference between the lower will and the higher will is that the lower will is limited, for since it is born from the intellect, it is limited according to the limitation of the intellect. Also, this will is only in the externality of the soul; because it is only from contemplation, it reaches only that place in the soul that the intellect reaches. This is not the case with the higher will, which is above the intellect; it is without limit, and it is the will that comes from the internality of the soul. From this, one can also understand in the divine soul that it has a lower will and a higher will. The lower will is the desire for *Elokus* (Divinity) from contemplation, and the higher will is the aspect of "to love Hashem your G-d, for He is your life", which is not from reason, but because this is his life. Like (in the animal soul) the desire to live, this is the aspect of the higher will, the "desire of all desires".

Similarly, one can understand this above: the lower will is the will as it comes into the *hishtalshelus* through *Chochma*, and the higher will is the will that is above reason, from which all wills are drawn (as mentioned above regarding the animal soul, that all wills are drawn from the desire to live), the "desire of all desires." This is the concept of "doing the will of the Omnipresent"—that is, the creation of the will that is above the *hishtalshelus*, the higher will, in the *makom*, in the *hishtalshelus*. By drawing the will that is above the *hishtalshelus* into the *hishtalshelus*, there will be a conduct of "without limit" below, because even within the limitation of the *hishtalshelus*, the "without limit" shines. Therefore, at the time when they do the will of the Omnipresent, "strangers shall stand and feed your flocks," because even below there will be a conduct of "without limit." This is like what is said, "On that day, Hashem will be One"—now, "I am not as I am written, I am not as I am read", meaning that now Hashem is in concealment, whereas in the future, Hashem will be in revelation below. This drawing down is through the love of "with all your might," for in order to reach the aspect of "without limit" that is above, this is through the *avodah* in the "without limit" that is in the soul. Even though this is not the true "without limit"—for it is only "your might"—nevertheless, since in man it is at least "without limit," and it is the higher will that is in man, through this he draws down also the higher will from above, which is the concept of "doing the will of the Omnipresent."

5) This is "Hear, O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One." "Hashem our G-d" is the Hashem that is above the *hishtalshelus* as our strength and our life, which is the aspect of the higher Hashem. "Hashem is One" is the lower Hashem, for Hashem is *tzimtzum* and expansion, drawing down and expansion, through which (the lower Hashem) it is possible to be "one," meaning the creation of the seven heavens, the earth, and the four directions. This is "Hear, O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One": "Hear, O Israel" is the contemplation; "Hashem our G-d" is the higher Hashem as our strength and our life; and through this, "Hashem (the lower) is One," meaning the *bitul*. This is the concept of the descent of the *neshamah* below, because through the contemplation below specifically, the *avodah* of *teshuvah* is accomplished in it, which is the *avodah* of "with all your might," through which one does the will of the Omnipresent—that is, the drawing down of the higher will, which is above even the aspect of *machshava ila'ah*, the root of the souls.

6) This is "And it shall come to pass, because (*eikev*) you hearken... and keep and perform," which is the *avodah* of *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* as it is from the aspect of the love of "with all your might." Through this *avodah*, then "Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness and the oath." Covenant, kindness, and oath are the drawings down from above the *hishtalshelus*, and they are the concept of "doing the will of the Omnipresent." This is what is meant by "He will keep the kindness," which is intended in the manner of what is said in the *Zohar* on the verse, "And if a man takes his sister, it is kindness (*chesed*)." "Man" is the Holy One, blessed be He; "his sister" is the Community of Israel (this is the union of the Holy One, blessed be He, and the Community of Israel, the union of the Holy One, blessed be He, and His *Shechinah*). And why is it called *chesed*? It is *chesed* definitely. This means that for the drawing down to be below, it is through the *chesed* from Him, may He be blessed. As it is written, "Remember Your mercies and Your kindnesses, for they are from of old (*me'olam*)." The concept of "remembering" is only appropriate to say regarding something to which the concept of forgetting applies. This means that since the entirety of the *hishtalshelus* does not occupy a place before Him, may He be blessed, we therefore ask, "Remember Your mercies and Your kindnesses." "Your mercies" is the aspect of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy that are above the *hishtalshelus*, as it is written, "And Hashem passed before him and called, 'Hashem'..."—"And Hashem passed" is the higher Hashem that is above the *hishtalshelus*. "And Your kindnesses" is the aspect of "abundant in kindness" that is above the *hishtalshelus*, "for they are from of old (*me'olam*)." *Olam* is from the word *he'elem* (concealment), meaning that they are in concealment in their root, like the concept of the "hidden *Sefiros*," the *Sefiros* of *Akudim*. One must draw this aspect into the world in its literal sense—meaning that even below there will be the drawing down of "without limit"—and through this, "strangers shall stand and feed your flocks."

This drawing down is through the love of "with all your might" specifically. This means that the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* in *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* alone is not enough, for *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* are only garments that are incomparable to the powers of the soul, and certainly to the aspect of will. As is known, thought and speech are like cause and effect—thought is the cause relative to speech, and likewise speech relative to action—whereas *machshava, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* relative to the powers of the soul, and especially relative to the will, are incomparable. Therefore, there must be the *avodah* of "with all your might" specifically, through which there will be the drawing down of the higher will. However, for the love of "with all your might" to effect the drawing down of the higher will from above, one needs the cutting of a covenant, for since the created beings do not occupy a place at all, how can they draw down through their *avodah*? Rather, it is through the *krisus bris* that the *avodah* from below will draw down the revelations from above. Therefore, the verse places the covenant before the kindness and the oath, because the entirety of the drawing down is through the covenant. This is "And it shall come to pass, because (*eikev*) you hearken...": in the time of *ikvesa d'meshicha*, *tishme'un* definitely, because it is the final generation, and "none shall be cast away from Him". Therefore, *tishme'un* definitely, in the aspect of "with all your might," and through this, "He will keep the covenant," etc., that the redemption from exile will be with a high hand, through Moshiach our righteous one, speedily in our days.

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 5716

### B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 5716

(Unedited transcript)

"And I will make your suns *kadkod* [rubies/agates]". Our Sages, of blessed memory, say: One said they are *sheham* [onyx], and one said they are *yashfeh* [jasper]. The Holy One, blessed be He, said: "Let it be both this and that." This verse is one of the prophecies regarding the future Redemption that will come through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days. There are two modes here—*sheham* and *yashfeh*—and the Holy One, blessed be He, said, "Let it be both this and that." To understand these two modes in terms of spirituality—that is, the revelation of Elokus that will be in the future—we can understand it from the fact that these two stones were among the twelve precious stones in the Choshen of the Kohen Gadol, corresponding to the tribes of Bnei Yisrael; *sheham* corresponds to Yosef, and *yashfeh* corresponds to Binyamin.

Yosef and Binyamin are the *tzaddik elyon* (upper tzaddik) and *tzaddik tachton* (lower tzaddik). The aspect of Yosef is the drawing down of Elokus from above to below; Yosef is the "provider of grain", who draws Elokus from above to below. This means that even when the world has not yet been refined to the point where it can receive a lofty revelation of light within itself, the light is nevertheless drawn down from above to below. The aspect of Binyamin is refinement and ascent from below to above; that is, he effects the clarification, refinement, ascent, and connection of the souls of Yisrael and their portion in the world—and consequently, in the entirety of creation—so that they are able to receive the light. By way of analogy: just as the brain of an animal is not a vessel for intellect, while the human brain is a vessel for intellect because it is more refined, the *avodah* of Binyamin is the ascent from below to above, which effects refinement in the human brain and intellect until it becomes a vessel for lofty Divine light.

Each of these two modes possesses a unique advantage. The advantage in the *avodah* of Binyamin, which is the aspect of *yashfeh*, is that the lower entity becomes more unified with the Divine light; since the drawing down is due to the refinement that made it a vessel for the light, it is in complete unity with the light. The advantage in the *avodah* of Yosef, which is the aspect of *sheham*, is that a light is drawn down that is extremely lofty, not according to the mode of the lower entity, but as it is from the perspective of the Higher. Regarding this, the Holy One, blessed be He, said, "Let it be both this and that," meaning that in the future, both advantages will exist. All of this is explained at length in *Likutei Torah* in the discourses on "And I will make your suns *kadkod*".

It is known that all the revelations that will be in the future depend on our deeds and our *avodah* throughout the duration of the exile. Since in the future there will be the modes of "from above to below" and "from below to above," it must be said that these modes also exist in our *avodah* during the duration of the exile. We must understand what these two modes of *sheham* and *yashfeh* are in *avodah*.

To understand this, we must first preface what was explained previously that "And it shall be, because (*eikev*) you listen" refers to the time of the footsteps of Mashiach (*ikvesa d'meshicha*). At that time, "you will surely listen," because it is the final generation, and "none of the banished will be cast away," and therefore, in this generation, you will surely listen. The general *avodah* is "you listen, and you keep, and you do," which is thought, speech, and action. When one's thought, speech, and action are solely those of the *nefesh habahamit*, and specifically those of Torah and *mitzvos*, then "Hashem, your G-d, will keep for you the covenant and the kindness and the oath," and the thought, speech, and action from above will be drawn down to him. In general, this is that through his *avodah*, a union is effected between the worker and the One worked for—a union of the souls of Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, a face-to-face union. Through the love of "with all your might", one draws down revelations that are above *seder hishtalshelus*. However, this drawing down of the revelation from above through his *avodah* is only by virtue of the covenant alone, for "He is not included in any of these attributes at all," and for the deeds of created beings to hold a place, it is only by virtue of the covenant.

2) The matter of the covenant is the Torah, as it is written, "The covenant which He made with us at Chorev". In the *Yalkut* on the verse "These are the words of the covenant," it is stated that "covenant" refers only to Torah. This means that the Torah is the covenant that unites the souls of Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, as it is written, "I stand between Hashem and you." "I" refers to "I am who I am," which is not hinted at by any letter or any *kotz* (serif)—in general, this is *Keter*—and it connects Yisrael and the Holy One, blessed be He, through the Torah.

The explanation of this is based on the principle that every intermediary connecting two things possesses two aspects: one aspect belonging to the higher, and one aspect belonging to the lower. Through these two aspects within it, it becomes a connecting intermediary. Similarly, this can be understood regarding the Torah, which is the intermediary connecting the souls of Yisrael and the Holy One, blessed be He: the Torah contains an aspect belonging to created beings, and an aspect belonging to the Holy One, blessed be He, and through this, it connects the souls of Yisrael and the Holy One, blessed be He. The Torah is enclothed in physical matters, etc., and from this perspective, it belongs to created beings—this is, in general, the *galya* (revealed) aspect of Torah. There is also an aspect in the Torah as it exists in spiritual matters, which is the *satim* (hidden) aspect of Torah, which speaks of matters of Elokus. This is why it is hidden (from us), for the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He. Through these two aspects, the Torah is the intermediary connecting *Ohr Ein Sof* and the souls of Yisrael.

To explain these two aspects in the Torah more deeply: it is known that the statement "The Torah emanates from *Chochma*" does not refer only to *Chochma Tachtah* (lower wisdom) and *Chochma Ila'ah* (higher wisdom), but to *Chochma Setimah* (hidden wisdom), for *Chochma Setimah* is the true intermediary. The entirety of *Keter* is an intermediary between *Ohr Ein Sof* (the Emanator) and the emanated beings, and this is through the two aspects within *Keter*: the lower aspect of the Emanator and the first aspect of *Atzilus*. Through these two aspects (the lower aspect of the Emanator and the root and source of the emanated beings), *Keter* becomes an intermediary to connect *Ohr Ein Sof* with *Atzilus*. However, these two aspects as they are in *Keter* are two distinct levels, and this is not the true essence of an intermediary. The true intermediary is the aspect of *Chochma Setimah*, because in *Chochma Setimah*, these two aspects (belonging to the Emanator and belonging to *Atzilus*) are not two distinct levels, but are as one; therefore, it is the true intermediary.

This can be understood by way of analogy to what we see below in the human soul: the power of *Chochma* contains two opposing matters: the power of abstraction and wonder, and the power of descent and enclothement. The matter of "wonder" in *Chochma* is its ability to abstract the intellect from material images, and even from physical images, and even from spiritual images—meaning it abstracts the intellect from all images within it, length, breadth, and depth, leaving only the "point." This is the aspect of the "point" in *Chochma*. The matter of "descent and enclothement" in *Chochma* is the power of *Chochma* to bring the intellectual concept down to the lowest levels, as in "And he spoke three thousand parables" and even lower. These two matters in *Chochma* are not two separate things, but one thing. The power of descent is due to the power of "wonder"; the reason it has the power to bring the intellectual concept down to the lowest levels is because it grasps the very point of the intellect, abstracted from all images, and precisely for this reason, it has the ability to bring the intellect down to the lowest levels.

Similarly, this can be understood above regarding the aspect of *Chochma Setimah*: the two aspects in *Chochma Setimah*—the aspect belonging to the Emanator and the aspect belonging to *Atzilus*—are not two separate things, but one thing, and therefore *Chochma Setimah* is the true intermediary. Likewise, this can be understood in the Torah: the two matters in the Torah—that it is the wisdom of the Holy One, blessed be He, and that it is enclothed in physical matters—are not two separate aspects, *galya* of Torah and *satim* of Torah, but rather, because the Torah emanates from *Chochma* (Setimah), it is precisely because of the higher aspect in the Torah that it descended below and was enclothed in physical matters. Therefore, the Torah is called a "covenant," which is the true intermediary between the souls of Yisrael and *Ohr Ein Sof*.

Similarly, the *mitzvos* are called a "covenant," because the *mitzvos* also contain two aspects: they themselves are made of physical things, and within them is the drawing down of the Higher Will, for "will" is higher than "wisdom." These two aspects in the *mitzvos* are not two separate things, but one thing, for the *mitzvos* that are enclothed in physical things are themselves the Higher Will, for it so arose in His will to fulfill the *mitzvos* specifically in physicality. And because it is the Higher Will, which is even higher than *Chochma*, it descends below specifically into physical things. However, this very fact—that through Torah and *mitzvos* it becomes possible for there to be a union of the souls of Yisrael with *Ohr Ein Sof*—is seemingly difficult: since *Ohr Ein Sof* "is not included in any of these attributes at all," how can the deeds of the lower beings hold a place such that there is a face-to-face union? Since He is not included in any of these attributes at all, it is impossible for there to be a face-to-face union, neither from the perspective of *Ohr Ein Sof* nor from the perspective of the souls of Yisrael. Regarding this, it is said, "I stand between Hashem and you to tell you the word of Hashem." "I am who I am" is the aspect of *Keter*, which is above both of them, and by the power of *Keter*, the union is effected through the Torah.

3) This is "And it shall be, because (*eikev*) you listen to these judgments." The translation of "judgment" (*mishpat*) is *halacha*, which refers to the laws of the Torah. This means that since this verse explains the union of the souls of Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, as mentioned above, it says "these judgments," for the union is through the laws of the Torah. "You listen" (*tishme'un*) is a term of gathering, as in "And Shaul gathered...". The matter is to gather and collect all the scattered sparks of his Divine soul that became attached to foreign desires through the multitude of thoughts and the dissipation of the soul. Even though it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," specifically—that the action must be in physicality—nevertheless, the thought does not need to be immersed in this, as it is written, "The labor of your hands you shall eat," meaning there must be labor of the hands only, but not labor of the brain and heart. Therefore, one must gather the sparks that were scattered in the dissipation of the soul, as it is written, "If your outcasts are at the ends of the heavens, from there will He gather you."

Just as one must gather the scattered sparks of his soul, so too must there be a gathering in the laws of the Torah. For from the dissipation that occurred in his soul, there is also a concealment and hiding for him in the Torah, such that he cannot clarify and rule on the *halacha* according to its truth. Regarding this, it says, "You listen to the judgments," these are the *halachos*, for "listen" is a gathering; there must be a gathering in his soul and a gathering in the laws of the Torah. This is also what is written, "And you shall gather your grain, and your wine, and your oil." The souls of Yisrael are called by the names "your grain," "your wine," and "your oil," which are three distinct levels among the souls of Yisrael: Kohanim, Leviim, and Yisraelim. "Your grain" refers to the Yisraelim, for just as in physicality bread is the essence—"and bread sustains the heart of man"—and other foods are only additions to the bread, so too among the souls of Yisrael, the essence is the Yisraelim; even Kohanim and Leviim are Yisraelim, but they have the additional advantage of Kohanim and Leviim. Therefore, Yisraelim are called "your grain." "Your wine" refers to the Leviim, for the *avodah* of the Leviim is in the recitation of song, and "song is recited only over wine". "Your oil" refers to the Kohanim, whose *avodah* is in the aspect of oil, in silence and with the desire of the heart (*re'uta d'liba*). This is "And you shall gather your grain, and your wine, and your oil," which is the matter of gathering the scattered sparks in all three types of souls of Yisrael.

Also, the interpretation of "And you shall gather your grain, and your wine, and your oil" is the matter of the gathering that must be in the Torah, for the Torah is also called by the names "your grain," "your wine," and "your oil," which are the distinct levels that exist in the Torah. "Your grain" is the *galya* of Torah; "your wine" is the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of Torah, the secrets of the Torah; and "your oil" is the "secrets of secrets," like oil that floats on top of wine, as explained at length in *Imrei Binah*. This is "And you shall gather your grain, etc.," which is the matter of the gathering that must be in all parts of the Torah. This is "And it shall be, because you listen to these judgments," that when there will be the gathering of the scattered sparks of his soul and the gathering in the Torah—and in general, it is the *avodah* of "you listen, and you keep, and you do," which are thought, speech, and action—through this, the thought, speech, and action from above will also be drawn down from above to below, so that there will be a face-to-face union of the souls of Yisrael and *Ohr Ein Sof*.

4) However, all this is in the *avodah* of thought, speech, and action as it is from the perspective of the lower will that is born from the intellect. But in the *avodah* as it is from the perspective of the Higher Will—that is, the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba* (desire of the heart) which is above reason and knowledge, which in general is the love of "with all your might" stated in the first paragraph of the *Shema*—in this paragraph, the verse "And you shall gather your grain, and your wine, and your oil" (which is done by virtue of the matter of "If your outcasts are, etc.") is not mentioned as it is in the second paragraph of the *Shema*. This is because from the perspective of the love of "with all your might," which is the matter of "doing the will of the Place," as mentioned above in the name of the Maggid, that it is the drawing down of the Higher Will that is above *seder hishtalshelus*, from the perspective of drawing down this aspect, there is no need for the *avodah* of "gathering." Rather, as it is written, "And He will bless, etc., your grain, your wine, and your oil," so that there will not be in them the aspect of the dissipation of the soul into foreign desires, etc. This matter applies specifically within *seder hishtalshelus*, but from the perspective of the love of "with all your might," through which one draws down the Will that is above *seder hishtalshelus*, this matter does not apply. This is the true essence of the covenant of Torah: the Torah's essence is the drawing down from above to below—that is, the drawing down of the Higher Light as it is (not according to the measure of created beings), which is the light that is above *seder hishtalshelus*. *Tefillah* is the ascent from below to above, "and you shall gather your grain, etc.," but the Torah is the drawing down from above to below, the drawing down of the light that is above *seder hishtalshelus*. This is through the preface of the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba*, the aspect of "with all your might," at which time the light that is above *seder hishtalshelus* is drawn down through the Torah. This is the true essence of the covenant of Torah, that the Torah is what connects and unites the souls of Yisrael with the aspect that is above *seder hishtalshelus*.

5) The root of the difference between these two aspects: it is known that regarding a covenant, there are two modes. The first mode is like the covenant that Avraham Avinu made with Avimelech through seven ewes, where both of them participated in the ewes, and each of them had a part in it, and through this, they are united. The second mode is that they take one whole thing and cut it in two, and those who make the covenant pass between the pieces. Now, when one cuts a single thing in two, this is seemingly the opposite of wholeness and is a separation, etc., but in truth, this is the true union—meaning that each one by itself is only half a thing, and is no existence at all without the other. Similarly, this can be understood above: the aspect of the covenant of Torah in the *avodah* of "gathering your grain, etc.," even though the drawing down of the light is effected through it, is nevertheless an existence unto itself. However, the Torah after the preface of the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba* and *teshuvah*—for *teshuvah* is also a covenant, as it is written, "To pass into the covenant of Hashem"—is in a much loftier mode, where it is no existence at all unto itself, etc., and through this is the drawing down of the light that is above *seder hishtalshelus*. In this, one can also understand the matter of the covenant of Rosh Hashanah, as it is written, "You are standing today, etc., to pass into the covenant." Seemingly, this is not understood; after all, even throughout the year there is a covenant of *Ohr Ein Sof* and the souls of Yisrael, so what is the matter of the covenant of Rosh Hashanah? But the matter is that the covenant of the entire year is like the covenant of the seven ewes; however, on Rosh Hashanah, there is the *avodah* of *teshuvah*, where it is no existence at all unto itself, etc., and it is the union in *Ohr Ein Sof* Himself, the Possessor of the Will.

6) In this, one can also understand what Rashi explains on the verse "And it shall be, because (*eikev*) you listen": "If the minor *mitzvos* that a person tramples with his heels (*eikev*) you listen." This matter is as it is written in the *Zohar* on the verse, "Why should I fear in days of evil, the sin of my heels (*eikev*) surrounds me," which refers to the minor sins that a person tramples with his heels. Now, regarding Yaakov, it is written, "And his hand was holding the heel (*eikev*) of Esav." Yaakov means *Yud-Eikev*, for he illuminates all levels down to the aspect of the "heels," and this is the matter of being careful in all matters, even in the most minor of the minor, for this is *Yud-Eikev*. The root of the drawing down of Yaakov, *Yud-Eikev*, that there should be in him the carefulness even in the most minor of the minor, is as it is written, "The voice is the voice of Yaakov." The first voice is lacking, and the last voice is full. The last voice is full—this is the Torah. The first voice is lacking—this is the voice that is not heard, and this is the matter of the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba*. When "the voice is the voice of Yaakov"—the first voice and the last voice—and this is the Torah after the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba*, then there is the matter of Yaakov, *Yud-Eikev*, which is the matter of being careful even in the most minor of the minor. This means that when his *avodah* is according to reason and knowledge, then there is a difference between the most minor and the most severe; but when he has the drawing down of the Torah after the preface of the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba* which is above reason and knowledge, then there is no difference at all between minor and severe. This is "The voice is the voice of Yaakov," and when "the voice is the voice of Yaakov," then "the hands are not the hands of Esav" that rule. This is what is meant by "Why should I fear in days of evil, the sin of my heels surrounds me"—because he lacks the aspect of Yaakov, *Yud-Eikev*, "and his hand was holding, etc." This is what Rashi explains on the verse "And it shall be, because (*eikev*) you listen": "If the minor *mitzvos* that a person tramples with his heels you listen," because this verse explains the matter of the drawing down that is above *seder hishtalshelus*, which is through the Torah after the preface of the *avodah* of *re'uta d'liba*. Therefore, Rashi explains that there must be carefulness even in minor *mitzvos*, for this is an indication that his *avodah* is above reason and knowledge, which is why he is careful in the minor just as in the severe. And since his *avodah* is above reason and knowledge, then "Hashem, your G-d, will keep for you the covenant and the kindness and the oath," and the light that is above *seder hishtalshelus* will be drawn down.

7) These two modes in *avodah*—the *avodah* of "the voice," *tefillah* and Torah—are the *avodah* in the way of "from below to above" and in the way of "from above to below," as explained at length in many places. And since in holiness there is inclusion and unification, there are also these two modes in the *avodah* of *tefillah* itself: the *avodah* of the night and the *avodah* of the day. It can be said that similarly, this is also the difference between the *avodah* of "with all your heart and with all your soul" and the *avodah* of "with all your might," and even in the *avodah* of "with all your might" there are these two modes, for "with all your might" has an aspect of will and an aspect of *taanug*. Likewise, in the Torah itself there are the two modes: the Written Torah and the Oral Torah, as explained in other places. Through these two modes in our *avodah* during the duration of the exile, there will be in the future the two modes of *sheham* and *yashfeh*. For now, in the time of exile, it is in concealment—both the ascent that is effected in the world and the drawing down of the light in the world are in concealment—and in the future, it will be revealed what they effected in the *avodah* during the time of exile: "And I will make your suns *kadkod*," which are *sheham* and *yashfeh*, and "let it be both this and that."

## B’s”d, Shabbos Parshas Nitzavim-Vayeilech, 25 Elul, 5716

### B’s”d, Shabbos Parshas Nitzavim-Vayeilech, 25 Elul, 5716

(Unedited transcript)

"You are standing today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d: your heads, your tribes... from your woodchopper to your water-drawer". This parsha is always read before Rosh Hashanah. The word "today" (hayom) alludes to Rosh Hashanah, as our Rebbe received from his teacher, the Maggid, and his teacher from his teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, that "today" refers to Rosh Hashanah, which is the Day of Judgment. This is as it is written, "And it was the day," which the Targum renders as "the day of the great judgment." Since Rosh Hashanah is the day of judgment and trial, this is the blessing: "You are standing today, all of you"—that all of you, from your heads and tribes down to the woodchopper and water-drawer, are *nitzavim*, standing firm and established, meaning that you are victorious in the judgment.

2) It is stated in the Midrash regarding the verse, "And you shall take for yourselves on the first day," that this is what is meant by the verse, "Let the field exult (*ya'aloz sadai*) and all that is in it." "The field" refers to the world, and "all that is in it" refers to the creatures. Before whom? Before Hashem. Why? Because He comes on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur. To do what? "He will judge the world with righteousness and the peoples with equity". We must understand what the joy of "the field and all that is in it" exulting over the judgment is—after all, this is judgment and trial, and seemingly it would be better to have no judgment at all. It is even more puzzling, for our Sages said that even if the whole world tells you that you are a tzaddik, you should consider yourself a rasha. And our Sages said that three books are opened on Rosh Hashanah: tzaddikim are inscribed immediately for life, resha'im [are inscribed for death], and so on. If so, how can one be in a state of joy? Furthermore, we must understand: is it not written that "the judgment belongs to Hashem," and regarding the Jewish people it is said "for which G-d is close to them," as it is written "you are children to Hashem your G-d," and "for the sake of my brothers and friends"—and a relative is disqualified from judging? We must also understand the phrase "He will judge the world (*teivel*) with righteousness"—what is the concept of "righteousness" (*tzedek*), and why is the specific term *teivel* used?

The matter is as our Sages said in the Midrash: "All seventh [units] are beloved." Among days, the seventh is beloved—Shabbos, as it is written, "And G-d blessed the seventh day and sanctified it" (and our Sages said He blessed it with the manna and sanctified it with the manna; they also said He sanctified it with the light of a person's countenance, for a person's countenance on a weekday is not the same as on Shabbos). Among months, the seventh is beloved—the seventh month, which is "sworn" (*mushba*) with blessings in both the physical and spiritual realms, as our Sages said, "winepresses within it, blessings within it," for it is the time of ingathering. Likewise in the spiritual realm, it contains many mitzvos: the shofar of Rosh Hashanah, Yom Kippur, Sukkos, the Four Species, and Shemini Atzeres. Therefore, the seventh [level] of the earth is also beloved. Just as there are seven heavens—*shamayim*, *shemei hashamayim*, *raki'a*, *shechakim*, *zevul*, *ma'on*, and *aravos*—and it is written, "Extol Him who rides upon the *aravos* (*b'aravos*), in His name *Y-ah*," meaning that *aravos*, which is the seventh, is the beloved one because the souls of the tzaddikim are found there, and therefore it is beloved to the Holy One, blessed be He, to "ride" upon them. So too with the earth, which has seven names—*eretz*, *adamah*, *arka*, *gai*, *tziyah*, *neshiyah*, *teivel*—*teivel*, which is the seventh, is the beloved one. And regarding this it is said, "He will judge *teivel* with righteousness"—*teivel* specifically.

3) To understand this, we must first preface the concept of judgment, which concerns the totality of one's avodah over the past year in fulfilling Torah and mitzvos, across the three pillars of Torah, avodah, and gemillus chasadim, which are the three things upon which the world stands. Their totality is the concept of *tzedakah*. For even Torah is a matter of *tzedakah*, since Torah in itself is of an incomparable nature, and its drawing down into the world is an act of *tzedakah*. The Jewish people effect this connection (that Torah be drawn into the world) through their avodah, because the thought of Israel preceded even the thought of Torah. Likewise, avodah—which is the concept of the sacrificial service, and in our time, the concept of tefillah—is connected with *tzedakah*, as our Sages said, "Rabbi Elazar would give a coin to a pauper and then pray," as it is written, "I, with righteousness (*b'tzedek*), will behold Your face." This means that through *tzedakah*, the concept of "beholding Your face" is achieved in tefillah—"Your face" specifically, the aspect of the inwardness of Elokus that is revealed through the inwardness of the soul. Therefore, tefillah is directed toward *Havayah* ("And Chana prayed to *Havayah*"), above the name *Havayah*. This is the meaning of "He will judge *teivel* with *tzedek*": two *tzedeks*, representing the two aspects of *tzedek*—the *tzedek* of gemillus chasadim and tefillah, which is the *tzedakah* that involves limitation, and the *tzedek* of Torah, which is the *tzedakah* without limitation.

4) To understand more specifically the virtue of the *tzedakah* for which "Rabbi Elazar would give a coin to a pauper and then pray, as it is written 'I, with righteousness, will behold Your face,'" we must note that the concept of *tzedakah* is to "revive the spirit of the lowly"—the pauper who has nothing. When one gives him *tzedakah*, one revives him, and thereby awakens above a similar concept of reviving the spirit of the lowly, which are the three worlds of *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*. They are called "lowly" because the source of their existence is only from the aspect of *Malchus*, which is merely an illumination, as it is written, "His name alone is exalted; His splendor (*hod*)—[merely] a radiance and illumination—is upon earth and heaven." Therefore, one must "revive the spirit of the lowly," meaning that the light of *Atzilus* should be felt even in *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*. This is the concept of *tzedakah* above, which is effected by *tzedakah* below. Through this, a revelation of light that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* is subsequently drawn down in tefillah—the concept of the illumination of the *Ohr Ein Sof* from the aspect of "face," as in "behold Your face."

More specifically, regarding *tzedakah* itself, there are two modes of avodah. Our Sages said, "He who gives a coin to a pauper is blessed with six blessings, and he who appeases him is blessed with eleven blessings." The reason for this is that giving a coin to a pauper is for the sake of his body, and since he thereby revives only his body, his action in the realm of *tzedakah* above is only to draw the light of *Atzilus* into *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*. This is also alluded to in the word *prutah* (coin), which is a *prat* (detail) of the *Heh*—meaning to draw down and "detail" the aspect of the *Vav* into the *Heh*. As explained in the Siddur in the discourse *Adonai Sefatai Tiftach* regarding "voice" and "speech": the voice is the aspect of the *klal* (general), and the speech is the aspect of the *prat* (detail) that specifies what is in the general, for the voice is the general aspect of all the letters, and the letters are the aspect of the details. This is the concept of *prutah*—to detail the aspect of the *Vav* into the *Heh*. Therefore, he is blessed with six blessings, corresponding to the letter *Vav* of the name *Havayah*. However, appeasing the pauper is not a matter needed for his body alone, but a matter of setting his mind at ease. The pauper, in himself, is in a state of bitterness because he has a grievance regarding his poverty, as it is written, "A prayer for the pauper when he is faint," for his prayer is about the very fact of his being a pauper. Although the order of creation is such that there must be the distinction of rich and poor, he still argues: why must *he* be the poor one? When one speaks to the pauper's heart and sets his mind at ease, this is a higher matter than merely giving a coin for his physical needs. Therefore, through this, one effects (not only the drawing down of the light of *Atzilus* into *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*, but also) the drawing down of the inwardness of Elokus. This is why he who appeases him is blessed with eleven blessings, for it is known that the number eleven points to the aspect that is above the ten *Sefiros*, similar to "before *Havayah*," above *Havayah*. This is also the concept of "appeasing" (*piyus*), which shares the same letters as *Yosef*. Regarding Yosef, it is written, "These are the generations of Yaakov: Yosef." Yaakov's domain is in *Atzilus*, but the purpose is for it to be drawn down into *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah* as well. This is the role of Yosef, who is the "provider of grain for all the land"—the concept of drawing down below. In order for it to be drawn down below, the drawing must come from a most exalted level. This is the concept of "giving a coin to a pauper and then praying"—first one must give the coin, and through this, one subsequently attains "beholding Your face," an inward drawing, just as through the act of appeasement.

5) These two modes of avodah in *tzedakah* (giving a coin to a pauper and appeasing him) must take place before tefillah. The reason is that regarding tefillah, our Sages said, "The Patriarchs instituted the prayers," and they also said that the three festivals correspond to the three Patriarchs: Pesach to Avraham, Shavuos to Yitzchak, and Sukkos to Yaakov. Thus, the concept of tefillah and the concept of the festivals are on the same level. Regarding the festivals, it is written, "Three times a year, all your males shall appear before Hashem your G-d in the place He will choose." This means that in the Beis Hamikdash, which was aligned with the *Heichalos* (Palaces), there was a revelation of "the face of Hashem your G-d." Likewise, in tefillah, which was structured to correspond to the *Heichalos*, there is the revelation of "the face of Hashem your G-d." The revelation of "the face of Hashem your G-d" in the Beis Hamikdash was effected through the act of prostration, as it is written, "to see and to prostrate," etc. There are two aspects to prostration: external prostration, which is like the prostration of a servant to a master—by way of coercion and necessity, where it is possible that he has no desire for it at all, but prostrates himself out of fear of the master, in a manner of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke); and internal prostration, which is in a state of desire and will, in a manner where all his powers are nullified. These two aspects of prostration correspond to the two aspects of "hearing" and "seeing"—that is, when the avodah is merely in the aspect of "hearing," it effects only external prostration, but when the avodah is in the aspect of "seeing," it effects internal prostration. Likewise, there are these two matters in tefillah. Tefillah is "a ladder set upon the earth," meaning that the beginning of tefillah is in the manner of "After Hashem your G-d shall you walk"—"after Hashem" means below *Havayah*, in the aspect of "back" and externality only, which is avodah in the manner of *kabbalas ol*. However, the conclusion and purpose of the avodah is to be "beholding Your face," in the aspect of inwardness, "before *Havayah*," meaning above *Havayah*. These two matters in tefillah, whose totality is *kabbalas ol* and *hasagah* (intellectual grasp), come through the two modes of avodah in *tzedakah*: giving a coin to a pauper and appeasing him.

6) With this, we can understand "He will judge *teivel* with righteousness." It is explained in *Likkutei Torah* that *teivel* is the numerical equivalent of *aryeh* (lion) twice over. This means that in the mode of avodah of the "lion"—which is the avodah of love (the totality of avodah, as the saying goes, "There is no service like the service of love")—there are two aspects. In general, this is the difference between the *serafim* and the *ofanim*: the *serafim* say "Holy" because they grasp how He, blessed be He, is holy and distinct from the category of worlds, and therefore they desire to be included and nullified to Him; this is due to the taste and grasp of the greatness of the *Ohr Ein Sof*. But the *ofanim* are in great tumult due to the lack of grasp. Likewise, these two aspects exist among the Jewish people: there are those of knowledge who grasp the greatness of the Creator, and they desire to be included due to their grasp (this is avodah in the aspect of "seeing"), and there is the aspect of the "multitude" who do not grasp at all, yet they still desire to be included, like the *ofanim* (this is avodah in the aspect of "hearing," *kabbalas ol*). For every Jew can reach the level of the "lion." Therefore, it is said "He will judge *teivel* specifically," for in the aspect of *teivel*, both aspects of the Jewish people are alluded to. This is also the meaning of "He will judge *teivel* with *tzedek*," two *tzedeks*—the *tzedek* of *tzedakah* and tefillah, and the *tzedek* of Torah (as mentioned above).

7) However, the matter of judgment ("He will judge *teivel* with righteousness") is not a matter of judgment alone; rather, the intent is that through it, a revelation of a most exalted light will be drawn down. The matter is that the entire concept of judgment above is so that through it there will be a revelation of a more exalted light. As we find regarding Rosh Hashanah and Sukkos (which are alluded to in the word *aryeh*—which is the concept of *teivel*, *aryeh* twice over—for it is known that *aryeh* is an acronym for *Elul*, *Rosh Hashanah*, *Yom Kippur*, *Hoshana Rabbah*), regarding which it is said, "His left hand is under my head, and His right hand embraces me." This means that the aspect of "His left," which is the judgment of Rosh Hashanah, is only so that there will be the revelation of "His right hand embraces me" on the festival of Sukkos. Furthermore, not only is the judgment for the sake of a more exalted light, but from the outset, it is not a matter of judgment at all. It is similar to what is explained in the Zohar on the verse, "The heavens were not pure in His eyes"—that this is actually a positive thing, for it is because of their preciousness that they were not pure in His eyes, like the parable of a person who has a fine vessel or a fine building: the more precious the vessel is to him, the more he refines it, and it seems to him that it is not yet perfectly refined and still needs refinement.

This is also the meaning of "And *He* (*Hu*) will judge *teivel* with righteousness"—*Hu* specifically. It is known from our Sages that the five instances of "He" (*Hu*) are for the good, and we have one "He" that is better than all of them: "He is Hashem our G-d," for His attribute of mercy is eternal. The matter is that the concept of judgment and trial is from the side of the name *Elokim*, as it is written, "for the judgment belongs to *Elokim*." Nevertheless, it is said here, "before *Havayah* for He comes to judge." The matter is, as is known, that there are two aspects of the name *Elokim*: the first, as it is written, "And you shall know... that *Havayah* is the *Elokim*"; and the second, that the name *Havayah* when it ascends to *Atik* is considered as *Elokim*. This is the meaning of "before *Havayah* for He comes to judge"—above the name *Havayah*, meaning because the name *Havayah* ascends to *Atik*, therefore it is considered as *Elokim*, where the concept of judgment and trial resides. This is also the meaning of "And *He* will judge *teivel* with righteousness"—*He* specifically, *Hu* refers to *Atik*. In this aspect, even the judgment is a matter of mercy, meaning its purpose is the polishing of the vessel.

8) This is the meaning of "Let the field exult (*ya'aloz sadai*) and all that is in it," because through the judgment and trial of Rosh Hashanah, a most exalted light is drawn down. This is also what they said in the Midrash, brought in the Tur, Laws of Rosh Hashanah: "This nation knows the character of their G-d; all the nations wrap themselves in black and wear black, but Israel wears white and wraps themselves in white, because they know that the Holy One, blessed be He, will perform a miracle for them." Seemingly, it is not understood what the joy of wearing white is—even if they know He will perform a miracle, it would still be better if there were no judgment at all. But the matter is that the judgment of Rosh Hashanah is for the sake of drawing down a more exalted light, and for this is the joy. This is the meaning of "He will perform a miracle for them," for a miracle is above nature, meaning a light that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. For this day is the beginning of Your works, because the *Malchus* is included in the aspect of the King who is exalted alone from of old, the aspect of His name in the aspect of "He alone is He," and from there it must be drawn down. However, because a most exalted light is being drawn down, there are accusers who do not want the light to be drawn down. Therefore, it says, "You are standing today, all of you, before *Havayah*." All the levels among the Jewish people—"your heads, your tribes," meaning those of grasp whose avodah is like the avodah of the *serafim*; "from your woodchopper to your water-drawer," whose avodah is in *kabbalas ol* like the avodah of the *ofanim*—all levels are *nitzavim*, standing firm and established, and are victorious in the judgment, so that the exalted light will be drawn down for them, "before *Havayah*," above the name *Havayah*. And this is drawn down below, down to this world, in all the matters of judgment and trial of Rosh Hashanah, so that there will be a healthy year, a lively year, and a joyful year in all details, and with abundant children, life, and sustenance.
